# Igros Kodesh

## Volume 6

## 1529

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Ephraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Peace and blessing!

I received your letters of the 27th of Nissan and the eve of Rosh Chodesh Iyar in due time and with pleasure. As you requested, I read your *petka* at the holy *tziyon* when I was there on the eve of Rosh Chodesh Iyar. Surely, the Rebbe, my father-in-law, will arouse [mercy] regarding the matters written in the *petka*, as well as that which is "between the lines," and that which is hinted at in the whiteness of the paper—as brought in the *maamar* on *Bechukosai* in *Likutei Torah*, and in *Shir HaShirim*, in the *maamar* beginning *Simeni KeChosam*, Chapter 3, and in many other places in *Chassidus* regarding the superiority of the whiteness surrounding the letters over the letters written upon the parchment.

Thank you, thank you for beginning to participate in the support of the *Ahalei Yosef Yitzchak* institutions. The greatness of the reward is as brought in the *Mishnah*: "The reward of a *mitzvah* is a *mitzvah*"—*mitzvah* [shares the root] with *tzavsa* (connection) and *hiskashrus* to the Master of the Will of the *mitzvah*. Likewise, this is also a matter of *hiskashrus* with the one after whom the institutions are named, and *keriah* (calling) [shares the root] with *keriah* (drawing down/summoning). Even though this amount is not a "stone with which one struggles," surely for you as well, it is only a matter of a beginning and an opening, like the "point of a needle." Especially in this time of *Sefirah*, it is known that the fiftieth gate is higher than *Chochma* and *Binah*, even though it is called the fiftieth gate of *Binah*, as is explained at length in the *maamar* on *Sefirah*, and especially in *Likutei Torah*. See also *Sefer HaMaamarim 5700*, the *maamar* beginning *BaLailah HaHu*, and the *maamar* there beginning *Ki Yishalcha Bincha*, and it is noted there in the footnotes.

As per your instruction, I am enclosing my letter to Mr. Nachman Perlstein in the holy tongue, as you requested. I rely on you that if the aforementioned requires explanation, you will provide what is necessary.

With blessing.

***

#### 1529

Most of the letters are from the secretariat's copies, and some are from photocopies of the original letters. They are not marked unless the source is different or they have already been printed.

**Rabbi Ephraim Eliezer, may he live:** Yales. Additional letters to him: above, Vol. 5, 1517, and where noted in the footnotes there. Below: 1561, 1808, 1862, 1944.

**Ahalei Yitzchak:** Ahalei Yosef Yitzchak.

## 1,730

1,730

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

Through the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and energetic, who engages in communal needs, R' Ephraim Eliezer HaKohen Yalles, may he live, we have received your contribution for the benefit of the Oholei Yosef Yitzchak institutions, which are named after my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and are conducted in his spirit.

The magnitude of the merit in supporting such institutions is understood and explained. It should be added that, especially in our era—after the horrific destructions in which tens of thousands of Jewish sons and daughters were taken from us—the responsibility of every single person among the *she'eris hapeleitah* (the surviving remnant) is immense. For upon their shoulders rests a portion of the *avodah* that was previously carried out by those who ascended through *kiddush Hashem*. If the value of every individual's responsibility is many times greater than it was in the period preceding this one, then this is all the more true regarding the youth. Every boy and girl is a seed and a fresh tree that, in time, will bear fruit and the fruit of fruit, for generations upon generations. Consequently, their education and the safeguarding of them to walk in the path of Torah and *mitzvos*, and to be permeated with the spirit of *Yisrael Sava*, is of an immeasurable value. Anyone who assists in this receives a reward that is also without limit, for he takes a part in the existence and flourishing of Jewish sons and daughters, and their connection to the Living G-d through the Torah of life, the eternal life—that is, a living Torah and a luminous Torah.

With blessings for success, and may you merit to give *tzedakah* with an open hand for every matter conducted in the purity of holiness.

#### ***1,730***

R' Nachman Perelstein. See the previous letter.

## 1,531

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was happy to receive your letter, in which you share the good news of the birth of a son, mazal tov. I hereby express my blessing of mazal tov; may you merit to bring him into the covenant of Avraham Avinu at a good and auspicious time, and may you and your wife, may they live, raise him to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, with peace of mind and physical well-being.

Regarding the order of his studies, you should consult locally with those who know him.

Awaiting good news regarding his health, with blessings of mazal tov and proper health for all.

P.S. Regarding what you wrote concerning the name—that the name of your wife’s father, may she live, was... etc., and whether one must also give the additional name Chaim or not—it is known what my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, said regarding matters of names: "Such things I do not say; may Hashem grant that it be for long life."

One could possibly explain this based on what is elucidated in the writings of the Arizal and his holy disciples: that when a child is born, etc., and his father and mother name him, etc., it is not by chance, etc., but rather Hashem places that name in their mouths which is necessary for that soul, etc. This name is inscribed Above on the Kisei HaKavod, as is known (Shaar HaGilgulim, Introduction 23; see also Emek HaMelech, Shaar 1, end of Chapter 4). Consequently, you should consult with your wife, may she live, and your decision will surely be, as mentioned above, appropriate both physically and spiritually.

#### ***1,531***

**And his father and mother name him:** See also Igros Kodesh, Vol. 1, letter 195.

## 1,732

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter regarding Mr. ... which is full of dissatisfaction. But what can I do? One cannot argue with everyone individually. When Mr. ... showed me the blueprint of the machine he was planning to set up several months ago, I told him right then and there that he needed to incorporate hollow tubes **inside** the machine so that the disinfectant material would penetrate not only from the sides but also from within. I also gave him my reasons and rationale: since this is a large mass of sacks, it is difficult for the airflow to penetrate from one end to the other. Naturally, he heard everything I proposed to him, but afterwards, he did it differently—that is, without the aforementioned hollow tubes. Now he is complaining that the matter is not perfect. **I am** not, G-d forbid, upset with him, for since he heard this from an older man and then his engineer told him otherwise, perhaps he had no choice. But in any case, the situation is as stated above, and now there is distress over it. However, after all this, I have seen greater things from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and my hope is strong that despite all the aforementioned, in the end, all his affairs will be successful, and he will see this with his own physical eyes and be able to count it off on his fingers...

## 1,733

B”H, Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of the Lod Yeshivah,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

My previous letters were surely received in due time, and I await your response.

Regarding the matter of a vocational training school, I spoke yesterday, Erev Rosh Chodesh Iyar, with the representative of the Joint [Distribution Committee] here... It is to be hoped that they, too, will urge the administration in the Holy Land—may it be built and established—to assist as much as possible.

It is understood that what I wrote in my previous letter remains in full force, as I also stated orally to the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing man, involved in communal needs, etc., Rabbi A. Wolf, shlita: that the aforementioned school must be **not in Lod**, but in the village, etc., and it should not be in the field of electricity, radio, and the like, but rather printing, carpentry, etc. This is as I explained my reasons and rationale to Rabbi A. Wolf, shlita, as mentioned above.

With blessings for success in your holy work,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***1,733***

**Vocational training school:** See above, letter 1,297. Below, 1,449; 1,607.

## 1,734

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your brief letter, in which you inform me that you held a farbrengen in... However, you were brief where you should have been lengthy; you did not mention anything regarding one of the intentions I had for these farbrengens—namely, that you, may you live and be well, should also repeat a maamar of Chassidus at them. I hope that you will surely fulfill this request of mine as well. It would be best if you would write to me explicitly regarding this, and if it was out of misplaced humility that you did not do so, you should at least do so now. Surely those who attend the farbrengen will not be upset that you are not satisfied with one farbrengen and wish to hold at least one additional farbrengen as mentioned above.

This is consistent with what I told you at the farbrengen here: that the physical administrators of the institutions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, are also spiritual administrators, for this was the will of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. This does not mean that they should have the final say in spiritual matters—which would naturally cause a disruption of order—but rather that they should know that the physicality of the institutions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is also spirituality. Consequently, everything that one can demand of a spiritual administrator of an institution of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the physical administrator must demand of himself, and so on. Further elaboration is unnecessary.

With blessings.

## 1531

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, involved in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Eliezer, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

Enclosed is a copy of my letter to the administration of the Yeshiva in Lod, which requires no explanation.

Furthermore, I am very surprised that I have, at this time, no information regarding what is being done concerning the arrangement of the "non-stream" [independent] stream. I recently received word that registration for the coming school year begins in the month of Sivan; if so, the time is very, very short. May it be His will that this, too, be hastened in its time.

Sent to your address are two letters for S.Z.R., one letter for R.A., and one thousand [units of currency] from Agudas Israel. Please confirm their receipt.

With blessings for proper health for you, your wife, and your entire household, may they live.

**M. Schneerson**

## 1536

1536

B”H, 3 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the Directorate of Agudas Chassidei Chabad in the Holy Land, may they live,

Shalom u’vracha!

In response to your letter of 26 Nissan, regarding your request to be notified by telegram, I sent a telegram today which reads as follows: “I am alarmed by the proposal to jeopardize the support for Lod. A letter is on its way. My signature.”

Although the explanation may seem superfluous, I will clarify the matter. As stated in the letter, it has been decided by the Agency to support the Yeshiva in Lod with the sum of 5,000 pounds for the construction of facilities for children of the age and category of Aliyah HaNoar. This is part of the 100,000-pound sum that was allocated after much negotiation, difficulties, and delays, specifically for buildings for orphaned children of Aliyah HaNoar, as this was the demand of the Coordinated Committee here—that a sum be allocated specifically for this purpose. Consequently, I see no prospect of succeeding in changing the purpose for which this sum was allocated. Furthermore, even if you were to succeed in changing it, it is liable to cause damage and loss—whether immediately or subsequently—as well as justified resentment from other parties and yeshivos that are also hoping to receive support from this sum. As for those who suggested to you that you should lobby for this, it is certain that they either do not know the history of these funds, or they do not care if there is resentment, or they assume it will only be verbal resentment and will not lead to any practical consequences. As mentioned above, regarding all three points, there is reason to fear that the situation is not so.

2) Since there is already a promise **following the visit** to Lod to support them, and given the tactics the Agency has used for the past two years—employing all sorts of pretexts to evade the matter or at least to delay it for as long as possible—I fear that if you begin making changes, they will be happy for this opportunity and will begin a new round of negotiations with you. In the meantime, it is unknown what will be done with the money, etc. Therefore, it is my clear opinion that first and foremost, one must secure the sum that has already been allocated for the specific purpose without changing it. Simultaneously, one should exert all efforts in two areas: a) That from this sum of 100,000 itself, they should allocate a sum larger than 5,000; b) Since they are promising to lobby on your behalf, it is appropriate to lobby for the Agency to provide funds from its other coffers as well for the construction of Chabad buildings, and not only from the 100,000-pound sum that came about through the efforts of the Coordinated Committee here. If you present the matter with appropriate arguments, there is a chance you will succeed, especially since, until now, there have not yet been detailed plans on how to divide the 100,000, and it seems the reason for this is that the other parties did not have concrete plans regarding the actual implementation.

3) If you succeed in having them give you some additional sum, there is the option of whether it should be in Lod or in Kfar Chabad. However, if it is from the 100,000-pound sum, then it is best that they use the money for buildings for Aliyah HaNoar children, as mentioned above. If it is from other coffers, then it is possible to use it for a different purpose, as you suggest in your letter.

4) Based on the demands of the Coordinated Committee here, as well as the lack of denial from those arguing against them (the Agency representatives), there is a chance that over time there will be additional sums beyond the aforementioned 100,000, provided that there are requests from places where there are Aliyah HaNoar children and a lack of suitable buildings for them. Consequently, if it aligns with my previous letters regarding the appropriate efforts to absorb immigrant children into our institutions in the Holy Land, there is room to immediately prepare a detailed plan and the necessary buildings for this, and you should certainly send a copy of the plan to me as well.

5) Regarding what you wrote that they are giving this as a loan: to my regret, due to the weakness of the party representatives here—and apparently also in the Holy Land—they agreed to this, despite my vigorous protest and their previous promise that they would demand the Agency fulfill its promise to give the money as a grant. However, in any case, even regarding the loan, there are two levels: generally, the **commencement** of the loan repayment is five years from the day of receipt. But if the Agency is convinced that it is difficult for the institution to begin repayments after five years, they have promised to allow such an institution to begin repayments after ten years. Therefore, since Anash have come from places behind the Iron Curtain and consequently could not bring their property with them, etc., my hope is that through this, you will be able to demand that their loan repayments begin after ten years.

6) I am very surprised that I do not hear from you regarding what is being done about the Shmittah fund money for Anash. Especially since, according to my letter to them, they know that Mr. Goldman sent a telegram from here several weeks ago (to Mr. Eshkol) regarding this. But if you act with negligence on the spot, they will certainly not be the ones to initiate it.

7) I am somewhat surprised that nothing positive has yet materialized regarding the "Zerem Bilti Zeramim" (the non-affiliated stream). For in a letter I received, it is stated that the start of registration for the upcoming school year is in the month of Sivan...

Awaiting good news,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1737

B"H, 3 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing men, engaged in communal needs:
Mr. Yehuda Fogel
Mr. Chaim Boruch Fogel
Mr. Moshe Schiffman
And Mr. Eliezer Bernstein.

Peace and Blessing!

I was pleased to learn through the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, of noble lineage, who is engaged in communal needs and possesses great energy, etc., Rabbi Chaim Menachem Ben-Tzion Blumenkrantz, of your fine efforts in general, and in particular regarding the great mitzvah of building a mikveh in the camp of Bogota, for which you have joined the committee overseeing its construction.

Surely it is unnecessary to elaborate on the immense value of this matter. Beyond the fact that it is one of the fundamental mitzvos of our holy Torah, the purity of the family and all matters connected to it are one of the central pillars. It is in their merit and through them that the Jewish people have the strength to endure all the hardships and the yoke of galus, and to remain healthy in body and soul. Furthermore, the fulfillment of this mitzvah is not merely a matter for those who observe it—the husband and wife alone—but it affects the children who are born, and their children, and their children’s children, until the end of all generations. When parents observe the laws of family purity, their sons and daughters are kosher children; if, G-d forbid, the parents are not careful in this, it creates a blemish in the soul and body of the children, their offspring, and their offspring’s offspring, and so on. Moreover, this is not a private matter concerning only these parents and their children, but a general matter for the entire Jewish people. As is explained in many places in the words of our Sages, it is through purity that the Shechinah dwells among Israel. For all these reasons, expediting the construction of the mikveh in a beautiful manner, and the advocacy to ensure that this mitzvah is observed, is of the utmost necessity. Every effort is worthwhile to bring this matter to a successful conclusion and to hasten it as much as possible. The measure of the Holy One, blessed be He, is measure for measure, but with an addition—and an addition that far exceeds the primary matter.

May it be the will of Hashem that for all those who are involved and participating in this great mitzvah, Hashem should bestow upon each and every one of them what they need for their specific circumstances, and in particular, an abundance of nachas and pleasure from their children, may they live, in all respects.

As my own participation in this great mitzvah, I am enclosing a check for 18 shekel. May it be His will that you succeed in raising many times this amount, to complete the mikveh as soon as possible, and to increase holiness and purity in every place, with the help of Hashem upon you.

With blessings for success and goodness in both material and spiritual matters.

## 1,538

B"H, 3 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 26 Nissan, in which you write regarding those you invited to your Sedarim and also for Shevi’i Shel Pesach. Great is your merit, and the merit of your wife—may they live—for you are assisting in drawing the hearts of the sons and daughters of Yisrael to their Father in Heaven. Especially regarding matters such as these—invitations to Sedarim and the like—even though on the face of it this is not a matter of formal study, but rather instruction by way of incidental influence, it is precisely because of this that the message is absorbed more readily and leaves a greater impression. And although this is only by way of *makif* (encompassing influence), when one adds, at the time or shortly thereafter, an appropriate explanation in the appropriate terms, then the *makif* enters into the *pnimiyus* (internal dimension), and one may hope for great benefit.

I was also pleased by what you mention in your letter regarding the work at the college in Boston. I do not know the basis for the doubt you express in your letter as to whether it is desirable, for it is certainly desirable and favored. Regarding your uncertainty as to what to focus on, I have already said several times during the visits of people such as yourself that the essential point in our religion and our Torah is *asiyah* (action) in actual practice. As is well known, this is also the general manner of receiving the Torah: first and foremost they said "we will do" (*na'aseh*), and only afterwards "we will hear" (*nishma*). I have already shared a parable **now** regarding this: when there is a fire, there is no time to explain to the onlookers, or even to those working to extinguish the fire, how the firefighting equipment operates, why it must be positioned in a certain way, or why it must be turned in a certain direction. The same applies to the situation of the Jewish people now, for as the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, goes: "The walls of *galus* are burning." We must save the souls of the children of Yisrael from this fire so that they may all merit the complete *Geulah* speedily in our days. Anyone who is present at the scene and closes his eyes, refusing to see the fire, or who sits at ease waiting until someone explains to him all the details of the fire, all the details of how the firefighting equipment is made, and all the reasons for how and why they extinguish the fire, is taking upon himself the matter of *pikuach nefesh* (saving a life) in actual practice. Conversely, the very act of engaging in extinguishing the fire prepares and readies one well to understand afterwards where the fire came from, upon what foundation the machines were built, and how they extinguish the fire.

The analogy from all this is understood and simple, though it must be explained to each person according to their intellect and their particular circumstances.

It has been a while since I heard anything regarding the health of your family—may they live—and I am certain you will inform me of good news in this regard as well.

With blessings.

## 1539

1539

B"H, 3 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the distinguished avreich, G-d-fearing, etc.,
R' Avraham Mordechai, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 25 Nissan, in which you inform me that your engagement (tenaim) to Mrs. Leah Raizel, may she live, has taken place, and that you have both agreed to live in Sefaria and have set the wedding date for this summer:

May it be the will of Hashem that it be in a good hour and a successful time, and may you build a home in Yisrael upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, as they are explained and illuminated by the "Light of Torah"—which is the teachings of Chassidus.

Regarding what you wrote, that the age of the bride, may she live, is approximately one year older than yours, and that her name is Leah Raizel but she is called only Raizel, and that his mother’s name is Miriam Leah: according to the language of the Tzemach Tzedek (Responsa Even HaEzer, sec. 43; see also Piskei Din, sec. 16, and all the more so in this case), there is **no room for concern whatsoever**.

Regarding your question as to whether you must be called by others by the name Avraham Mordechai, or if it is sufficient to be called by both names only when being called to the Torah or when signing a document: there are no set rules for this, nor have I heard any specific instructions regarding it. Consequently, you should continue to conduct yourself as you have until now. However, I notice a contradiction in your letter between the beginning and the end, for at the beginning you write that your name is Avraham Mordechai **Shmuel**, and afterwards you write Avraham Mordechai alone.

Regarding your setting of times for Torah study in addition to the shiurim that are standard for everyone: I have written long ago that every member of anash should have two shiurim in Nigleh and two shiurim in Chassidus every day—one for *iyun* (in-depth study) and one for *girsa* (review/fluency). At the very least, one should arrange for *girsa* and *iyun* a few times a week, and if possible, organize it so that three days do not pass without a shiur for *iyun*. Specifically, regarding which sefer or kuntres maamarim you should set your shiur in, you should consult with the elders of anash, may they live.

And you should act according to their instruction.

With blessings for mazal tov and success in all your affairs, both spiritual and material.

## 1,540

1,540

B"H, 3 Iyar, 5712

Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter regarding your son... *sheyichyeh*, who wishes to travel to study at the Tomchei Temimim here, and you add that in the coming month of Tammuz he will turn twenty years old—may he have long, good days and years.

Your aforementioned son *sheyichyeh* should utilize the summer months to increase his diligence in the study of Nigleh and the study of Chassidus (it is understood that this does not mean he should weaken his health; as is known from the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov and the teachings of Chabad Chassidus in particular, one must be healthy in *gashmius* and healthy in *ruchnius*). During the summer months, he should also correspond with the administration of Tomchei Temimim here, and they will surely come to an understanding. If he utilizes the time during the summer months for the study mentioned above, then it is appropriate that he come here to study by the coming Rosh Hashanah. May Hashem merit you to receive *nachas* from him and from your other children *shichyu*—*Yiddishe nachas*, *Chassidishe nachas*—with tranquility and abundance.

With blessings.

## 1541

B"H, 3 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 12 Nissan, with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed therein: the *pidyon nefesh* was read at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, at a time of favor (*eis ratzon*), and he will surely arouse Divine mercy for each of those mentioned in the *pidyon nefesh* for whatever they require.

Regarding what you wrote concerning *tikkun* for the past, that you do not have the strength to fast, etc.: you should examine the *Sefer Toldos Maharash*, page 72, where the saying of the Rebbe Maharash is recorded: "Fasting does not mean not eating from sunrise to sunset; that is merely 'drying out.' A *taanit* is *avodah*. Think for 15 minutes every day about yourself." The Rebbe Maharash concluded that through this, the Chassid is transformed—not only in his soul-powers, but in a change from one essence to another. My father-in-law, the Rebbe, concluded that from this story, everyone must take the lesson that "everyone needs to think for 15 minutes every day about themselves."

In my opinion, the above is in addition to the general instruction that you should endeavor not to dwell on the past and on your failings, for it seems that for you, this is a tactic of the *yetzer* to cause you to stumble into sadness and melancholy. Rather, you should hold onto the path of *simchah*. "Serve Hashem with *simchah*"—this must encompass two aspects: the *avodah* of a servant, as explained in *Torah Or*, beginning of *Parshas Mishpatim*, which also includes the category of a *eved kenaani*, whose nature is that he prefers license, yet nevertheless he serves Hashem, and specifically with *simchah*. For with even a slight amount of *hisbonenus*, one will come to the realization that "happy is my portion, and good and beautiful is my lot," that I have merited to be a Chassid. Consequently, no matter what happens, you can be certain that the Rebbe will place you in a position of true light. However, you must be strong in your *hiskashrus* through studying *Torah d'Chassidus* and through matters of *ahavas Yisrael*. The Alter Rebbe has already ruled that "love your fellow as yourself" is the vessel for "love Hashem your G-d."

#### ***1541***

**The ruling of the Alter Rebbe:** See also above, Vol. 4, Letter 1035, and the references in the notes there. Vol. 5, Letter 1527.

## 1542

5 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad
in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established
May they live

Peace and blessing!

1) I received your letter of 26 Nissan with pleasure, in which you write of your activities from the beginning of Teves until now. May it be the will of Hashem to instill in your hearts the correct recognition that aligns with the demand of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. We heard from his holy mouth, not once but twice, that one must be extremely cautious regarding the trait of self-satisfaction with the work already accomplished. One must be careful not to let the *yetzer hara* use this to pour a spirit of slumber and weakness upon the work that must be done henceforth. Sometimes, it goes even further, and he uses this to inflate one’s *yeshus* and sense of self—especially when he has something to hold onto, namely, that the activities are indeed good, visible, and tangible. In such a case, he comes with a very strong argument, and even greater caution is required. As is known, this is the matter regarding which the spies said "truth" at the beginning, which gave them a foothold to weaken the hearts of *Bnei Yisrael* from being in the category of "dwellers of Eretz Yisrael"—*yoshvei* (settled and permanent), *Eretz* (which desired to do the will of its Creator), *Yisrael* (who merit to become *Li*—for Hashem—a head). (See *Likutei Torah*, *Shelach*, the discourse beginning *Ani Hashem Elokeichem* regarding the Sages' statement that whenever one answers *Amen*, Hashem nods His head. *D'rachim* of Chassidus).

2) Following the above introduction, I reveal that I am satisfied (though not completely) with the specifics of your good activities (for I have no fear that I will say "Rejoice, my children, my inner parts" regarding activities in which others have labored). The reason I write that it is not in the measure of perfection is that, as you describe in your letter, it is clearly evident that given the current situation, one can see the fruits of every single activity, provided that the activity is performed with sincerity. Consequently, it should be done in a manner that is appropriate and without being deterred by those who prevent and hinder at the initial stage. Accordingly, this could have been accomplished during these months, Shevat and Nissan, many times over. If in any period time is something that does not return, then all the more so in our era—the era of the *ikvesa d'meshicha*—where every single moment is extremely precious and can be filled to accomplish great and hidden things, fruits and the fruits of fruits, until the end of the world (*olam*, from the word *elem*—concealment).

3) Surely, in those places where you write that you are still in the midst of the work or where tangible results have not yet been seen, you will again establish contact to clarify the situation. Surely, in the end, you will succeed, as per the promise of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, that by virtue of his *mesiras nefesh*, those who follow in his footsteps will succeed in their activities in Torah and *mitzvos*.

4) Regarding activities in the circles of yeshiva students, one of the ways that should have been adopted is to search within these circles for *bochurim* and *avreichim* from the lineage of *anash* and to prove to them—naturally, not in public—that their fathers and forefathers bequeathed to them the strengths of generations of Chassidim. If they do not use these strengths in accordance with the will of their fathers and forefathers, it is the opposite of the matter of honoring one's father, a disregard for their will, and a waste of the strengths given from Above without using them, etc. Who knows, perhaps this is one of the primary intentions of why they were rolled into a particular yeshiva—so that they would be the conduit through which the *Maor* (the Luminary) in Torah will shine there. This is the *pnimiyus haTorah* which, in our generation, has been revealed in the teachings of Chassidus. Surely you will find the appropriate words to add to this, according to the spirit and the state of mind of the individual *avreich* or *bochur* with whom you speak.

5) You mention in your letter regarding the group in... Some time ago, there was an *avreich* there... who studied for some years at the Tomchei Temimim yeshiva here (his father is a native of the Holy Land and studied at the Toras Emes yeshiva). It is appropriate to convey my regards to him and to arouse him and demand of him that he must be among the first in spreading the *maayanos* in his surroundings.

6) Regarding what you wrote about detailed instructions for your work: it is difficult to give detailed instructions from such a distance. As is known, the ruling of our Sages is that everything depends on the conditions of the place and the time, provided that the core point is preserved. In every single activity, you must keep before your eyes the primary intention: the drawing close of the hearts of *Bnei Yisrael* to our Father in Heaven, especially through the general teachings of Chassidus and the teachings of Chabad Chassidus, the ways of Chassidus, and the customs of Chassidim.

7) Regarding what you wrote that you might be able to obtain assistance for your work from..., but that then you would need to indicate the partnership in every announcement and publication, etc.: it is obvious that under such a condition, you cannot accept any support. I am **greatly** astonished that they demand such a condition from you. It is understood that when one receives financial assistance, it is only right to provide a report that the money was spent for the purpose for which it was given, but it should not be used as pressure to force you to publicize in every announcement—whatever it may be, whether about studying Chassidus, a gathering, a *farbrengen*, etc.—the partnership of...

8) I was pleased to read in your letter that you publicized the content of my general letter for the festival of Pesach and that you also printed it in the *chareidi* press. Surely you will send copies of the above here (both what you printed and the clippings from the press). In the future, it would be good of you to send two copies of any printed material here. Many thanks for the trouble. Surely my general letter to the yeshiva students has already arrived; as its conclusion states, even though it was written in connection with the festival of Pesach, the content stated therein is timely all year round.

9) I wrote some time ago that I am astonished that the number of members in Tzeirei Agudas Chabad is not increasing. You must explain to all the young people from the lineage of *anash* that although becoming a member of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad is not a matter of status, but rather a matter of responsibility, on the other hand, even if they do not join, the responsibility still rests upon their shoulders. By joining and becoming part of the collective, the merit of the collective assists them. As mentioned above, every single person from *anash* and their lineage—which is surely in accordance with the ruling that a father bequeaths to his son with wisdom, etc.—possesses the strengths that their fathers bequeathed to them, Chassidic strengths. Those who do not use these strengths—and who can say what happens to them when they pass them by with disdain—it is a grave sin, especially in this era of ours, as mentioned above. Elaborating on this is superfluous.

10) Regarding the question of the matter of broadcasting via radio: you did not write to me the contradictory part of this, which surely also exists, even though to my eyes here, the damage is negligible compared to the profit that can be hoped for from such broadcasts, provided that the broadcast is prepared with the proper preparation by the one who is to broadcast. The text of the broadcast should have the approval of a committee specifically for this purpose, so that it is appropriate and you can be certain that it aligns with the intention.

11) It is very correct that you decided to find, wherever possible, some people on the spot who will be the supervisors to ensure that all matters are consistent with the goal. Surely Hashem will succeed in finding the appropriate ways to bring this into reality.

12) I was pleased to read in your letter that you elected the additional representative from your side to the administration of Agudas Chabad and called a joint meeting together with Agudas Chabad. May it be the will that from now on, the connection between Tzeirei Agudas Chabad and Agudas Chabad will be strengthened, until the *kesher* (which, as explained in *D'rachim* of Chassidus, are two matters that have only been connected) becomes *dveikus*—that they become one block to do the will of our Father in Heaven.

With a blessing for success in your holy work, and regards to all the members of the administration and all the members of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad.

P.S. Enclosed is a check as my participation in the expenses of your holy work.

## 1743

1743

B"H, 5 Iyar, 5712

To the honored children of the late, G-d-fearing man, who occupied himself with communal needs, etc., R' Moshe Eliezer, of blessed memory, and Mrs. Rachel Elka, of blessed memory, Kreimer,
May Hashem preserve them and grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

I learned from the letter of the G-d-fearing man, who occupies himself with communal needs, a man of many accomplishments, etc., R' Avraham Dober, may he live, that tonight is the yahrtzeit of your late father, of blessed memory, and that 22 Iyar is the yahrtzeit of your late mother, of blessed memory. I would like to take this opportunity to express to you all my wish and blessing that the memory of your parents, of blessed memory, remain alive within you for long, good days and years.

In general, a yahrtzeit is associated with two movements. On one hand, as explained in the sefarim, on this day the soul of the departed experiences an aliyah, an elevation, passing into a higher spiritual world. This is, of course, a joy for the soul, and consequently, for all those close to it as well, for long, good days and years.

On the other hand, here below, the yahrtzeit refreshes the memory of the passing, which evokes a movement that is the opposite of joy.

In truth, however, the yahrtzeit should not evoke here below a movement that is the opposite of joy, but rather a movement of serious reflection, introspection, and cheshbon hanefesh: to align one’s own life here in this world with the life-path of the soul above—going from strength to strength (mechil el chayil). That is to say, just as the soul above is elevated more and more each year, going from strength to strength, so too must all those here below who are connected to that soul also go from strength to strength by ascending in Torah, avodah, and gemilus chasadim.

And through this, one also provides the departed with the greatest possible nachas ruach.

This also underscores the fundamental outlook of our faith: that in truth, the concept of death does not exist in holiness at all—and among Yidden in particular. There is only a transition from one world to another. And for those who, during their lifetime here below, were always connected to holiness, Torah, and mitzvos, the transition is in one direction—ever higher and higher, from strength to strength—first in this physical world, and then in the World to Come, in an ascent after ascent (be'aliyah achar aliyah).

With blessing.

## 1544

1544

B”H, 6 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter in due time, and in recent days the *pidyon nefesh* and the contents of your letter to the distinguished Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, engaged in communal needs, etc., R’ Yosef Halevi Weinberg, were also conveyed to me. Surely, during this time, all the *kuntresim*, my general letters, and the telegram have reached him as well, and surely he has publicized them as they are, or at the very least, their content in an appropriate manner.

2) It is surely unnecessary to remind you (as you have undoubtedly done so yourself) to provide your daughter, *tichyeh*, who is visiting Eretz Yisrael, *tizkeh l’mitzvos*, with the addresses of our *anash* and our institutions there, so that she may visit them. There is reason to hope that this will influence her for the good, in accordance with the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *n.e.*: “If good is good, is better not better?” I would appreciate it if you would inform me of the details regarding this—which places she visited and the impression the visit made upon her, etc.

3) I was very pleased with the content of your remarks at the Board of Deputies meeting regarding Chabad and Lubavitch, etc. Even though our Sages of blessed memory state that the *kelipah* mimics the side of holiness (like a monkey before a human), nevertheless, to our sorrow and pain, there are many things we must learn from the opposing side. We see clearly, especially in recent times, that their *chutzpah* succeeds. If such *chutzpah*, which has no foundation, etc., succeeds, then how much more so will true expansion—*v’eshalecha b’rachavah*—in matters of holiness, without fear of the *he'elem* and *hester*, surely and simply succeed and accomplish its purpose. Proof of this in your own case is the fact that you illuminated the spark that exists in the interior of... This is proof in two ways: as per the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukl”l, n.b.g.m., z.y.e.*: “Before truth, everything becomes *batel*,” and as the old Chassidim used to say: “A Chassidishe spark is never lost.” The meaning is: not only is it not lost—not only does it break through in matters of *tzedakah* and *gemilas chasadim*—but in the end, it breaks through in matters of Chassidus, as mentioned above. May Hashem grant you to have the “true breadth,” and consequently, may it bring you only *nachas ruach* and satisfaction from your good deeds, without any heartache, *chas v’shalom*.

With blessings for success in your *avodah* with joy and expansion.

1546

B”H, 6 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn

He will be able to stay in Morocco for the time necessary for this, provided that the required preparation—if it takes time—is done beforehand.

The telegram regarding R’ Shalom surely arrived on time.

With blessings for success in your holy work, and for all good, both revealed and hidden, for you and your entire family, may they live.

**M. Schneerson**

## 1747

1747

B”H, 6 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, refined, and diligent in his holy work, etc., R’ Michael, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter from Thursday of last week, as well as those preceding it. Regarding what you wrote about having sent the list of students—they have not yet been received, but they will surely arrive in the coming days.

2) Regarding your question about the proposed study schedule, where the older classes would study Chassidus for an hour and a half before davening and two hours of Chassidus in the evening:

In my opinion, it seems too early to implement a schedule of three and a half hours of Chassidus study every single day for the Sephardic students. While I also agree that it is necessary to establish the practice of studying Chassidus before davening, as well as in the evening and at night, one must take into account the duration of the study time—both morning and evening. This is a new location, and consequently, one should not demand the maximum at the very beginning. Perhaps it would be worthwhile to have a set time for Chassidus study that everyone is **obligated** to attend, while providing the opportunity for those who wish to do so on their own initiative to add more time, but without it being mandated by the Yeshiva. In my opinion, for the time being, the requirement from the Yeshiva should be from half an hour to forty-five minutes in the morning before davening, and about an hour and a half in the evening. You should encourage the students that on Shabbos they ought to add to this, even those students who are not within the walls of the Yeshiva but are at home.

3) I was pleased to read in your letter about the baking of the shmurah matzah and the surrounding atmosphere of the baking. As my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, explained several times: "Sometimes the *arum* (the surrounding atmosphere) accomplishes more than the *inyan* (the matter) itself." Even though this is in the manner of a *makif* (encompassing light), when one adds an explanation of the matters during or in close proximity to the act, the *makif* enters into the *pnim* (internal), which then provides a twofold benefit—both that of the *makif* and that of the *pnim*.

5) It goes without saying that during an *eis ratzon*, when I am at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, I will mention you and your family, may they live, for success in your holy work and in your personal matters as you require. Great is the merit of your involvement in spreading the light of the Torah of our holy Nasiim [in Morocco], to draw down and receive the blessings of Hashem from above, *da anten*—below ten tefachim.

6) Regarding what you wrote some time ago about the incident in the mikveh, where you later saw that the water did not reach the connecting aperture through which the *hashakah* (connection) is effected: It is almost certain that prior to this, there had been at least one instance of connection and *hashakah*, for it is unbelievable that when they filled the mikveh, they did not ensure that this aperture was covered by water. It is known that once there has been a *hashakah*, even for a moment, according to many Acharonim, one need not be stringent at all, and the mikveh is kosher even *lechatchilah*. In many responsa, including those of the Chasam Sofer, it is noted that there was a time when they would initially set up mikvaos in such a way that they would have a *hashakah* once, and thereafter use them for immersion. Furthermore, they would use this mikveh to render another mikveh of drawn water kosher through *hashakah*. Our custom is known, based on the mikveh that was in Rostov, where they wanted the *hashakah* to be present for the entire duration of the immersion. However, in any case, this is not a matter of the essential law, etc.

With blessings for success in your holy work and all the best to you and your entire family, may they live, in both material and spiritual matters.

B"H, 6 Iyar, 5712

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your notification that your birthday is... surely on the upcoming Shabbos Kodesh you will endeavor to receive an aliyah to the Torah and repeat a maamar of Chassidus at Seudah Shlishis (and if the listeners are not yet accustomed to hearing Chassidus, you are not obligated to disclose that you are saying Chassidus, as long as the matter is accomplished). ## 1549

B"H, 6 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished chossid, who toils in the needs of the community, etc.,
Rabbi Shmaryahu, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 27th of Nissan, as well as the two previous ones. Surely it is superfluous to dwell on expressing thanks, for as the Mishnah rules, "the reward of a mitzvah is the mitzvah itself." This means that in performing a good deed, the greatest reward is the good deed itself, for through it one connects with the Mitzvah—the Source of the Will—which is above the reward of Gan Eden, Olam HaBa, etc. This is in line with the saying of the Alter Rebbe regarding the verse, "Whom have I in heaven but You..." (Tehillim 73:25): "I want nothing more than You alone" (Shaar Mitzvos HaTefillah, Chapter 4).

3) It is my hope that in a few weeks, the young scholar, the esteemed and distinguished chossid, Rabbi Shalom Haskind, may he live, will visit Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. I am writing regarding this—in continuation of the conversation we had when you were here, and as a response to his letter to Rabbi R. M. A., may he live.

4) It is somewhat surprising that regarding what I prompted you concerning the Chassidic booklets (bichlech) located in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, there has thus far been no visible effect, etc.

5) During the length of time that you were here, we spoke about many matters, but not about the primary issue: the question, "Ayeka?" ("Where are you?"). It is well known how the Alter Rebbe answered the minister who asked him for the meaning of these words; he explained that this is the question Hashem asks every person: "Where are you? What is happening with you?" Surely all the good activities—whether in the affairs of Agudas Chassidei Chabad, the yeshivos, the village, etc.—are present, but after all that, the verse commands, "And do not hide yourself from your own flesh," meaning that everyone must also remember themselves. And the question is: Ayeka? Reb Shmaryahu (with all the titles mentioned above at the beginning of the letter, and if more titles are due to you, then all the more so, etc. But after all that, the question is): Ayeka? What is happening with your learning of Chassidus, Nigleh, etc., etc.?

With blessings for proper health for your wife, may she live, for you, and for all your household, may they live, and for an abundance of Chassidic nachas from yourself and from all your household, may they live.

**M. Schneerson**

## 1550

1550

B"H, 6 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter (without the date of writing):

1) Regarding what you wrote—that there are those who say not all the *baalei batim* in your congregation are satisfied with you, etc., and consequently you are asking for my opinion as to whether you should look for a position in another city:

In my opinion, this is not the right course of action. The energy you would need to invest in searching elsewhere would be better spent—for several reasons—in increasing your circle of friends and acquaintances within your current congregation by becoming more involved with the people (it goes without saying that this involvement must not come at the expense of compromising on matters of Torah and *mitzvos*). As is well known from our Sages, whoever possesses *yiras shamayim*, his words are heeded. Furthermore, you should show them that you are a person of action regarding communal affairs as well—even those matters for which you receive no salary. Through this, you will become beloved to the people, and consequently, beloved to the *Makom* (the Almighty), as our Sages say: "Anyone in whom the spirit of his fellow creatures takes pleasure, in him the spirit of the *Makom* takes pleasure" (*Pirkei Avos*, Chapter 3, Mishnah 10). See also *Sefer HaMaamarim Yiddish*, page 172, *d.h. Hu Hayah Omer*.

2) In response to your notification that your wife, *tichyeh*, has entered the ninth month of her pregnancy: May it be the will of *Hashem* that the pregnancy be completed with ease, and that the birth take place at its proper time, easily, with a healthy and viable child. You should make an effort (without making a spectacle of the matter) to open the *Aron* during the days of the Torah reading until after the birth, in a good and auspicious hour.

With blessings,

## 1551

1551

B"H, 6 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...I was pleased by what you wrote in your letter regarding the fixed times you have for studying Chassidus. However, I am pained that after the many years that you and the family... etc., have been living in..., you have not managed to gather at least a minyan of people who would also participate in the study of Chassidus with you. Is it possible that you and your family were brought to... solely for the sake of material livelihood or for the work of supporting the Yeshiva?! While supporting Torah is a most exalted matter—as the Zohar explains, and as is explained in the maamar of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *zatzukal-lah-h, nbg-m, zya*, titled *Etz Chaim Hi Lamachazikim Bah* (Simchas Torah, 5699), that "those who support it" is interpreted as "those who are fortunate," and not just fortunate, but "from its beginning"—nevertheless, after all this, one must not forget the Torah itself. It is impossible to fulfill one’s obligation merely by supporting others so that they may learn (see *Kesuvos* 111b regarding one whose involvement is limited to such work, for whom this may suffice; but for those who have merited to be educated in the tent of Torah, and especially in Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, it is) obvious and clear that one must also study oneself, and also see to it that others study this Torah to which one has merited to be connected.

Consequently, it must be clear to you and to the family... etc., that your being in... is not merely a matter connected to the material (even if it is the most exalted of the material), but also to the spiritual—meaning that you must be the *mashpia* and the conduit through which the light of the teachings of Chassidus will illuminate... and its surroundings. And since this is demanded of you, surely you have been given the strength to bring this from potential into action, and when you exert effort in this, then, as per the promise of the Alter Rebbe, you will succeed.

With blessings for general and personal success.

## 1552

B"H, 6 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter (though it was undated) informing me that your wife, may she live and be well, has agreed to wear a sheitel. May it be the will of Hashem that she does so with a joyful heart, and may you speedily see with your own eyes an increase in blessing and success in all your affairs—both general and specific—with good health and livelihood for yourself and for your entire household, may they live.

I was also pleased to read in your letter that you have established a regular study session with the esteemed Chossid, our teacher R' [Name], may he live, and that you are finding more satisfaction in your private studies. Surely, from time to time, you will continue to increase this satisfaction, in accordance with the ruling of our holy Torah that "we elevate in matters of holiness"—which is an obligation upon a person. And since the attribute of the Ribono shel Olam is "measure for measure," He, too, elevates him from level to level in holiness from Above. Consequently, the limitations of this world naturally diminish, until even physical matters occur without such great Tzimtzum and restriction, and it becomes possible to engage in Torah, avodah, and acts of kindness with an expanded soul and bodily tranquility.

With blessings for success in your holy work.

P.S. I will read the pidyon nefesh, as you requested, at the holy gravesite of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

## 1553

B"H, 6 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to read in your letter about the positive developments in your situation, and I am certain that by the time you receive my letter, the health of your wife, tichyeh, has already returned to its proper state.

Regarding what you wrote about the possibility of arranging for your placement in the Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim in your camp, I have inquired into this, and according to the information I have received, at this time, such an arrangement does not appear possible. However, regarding what you write in your letter about the "broken heart" you feel due to your current situation—evidently referring to your material livelihood—I am very surprised. After you and your wife, shichyu, and all those in your surroundings have witnessed the wonders of Hashem over the past years, and as each one of us from the *she'eris hapeleitah* whom Hashem has saved in a miraculous way—for "it is not because you are more numerous," etc.—there is no room for a broken heart. This is especially true since you have only been in a new country for a short time. It is proper that your heart be confident in the One who sustains and provides for all, that He will provide your livelihood in its proper time and season. Then, you will wonder at yourself for having felt there was any reason for a broken heart, even if it was only a passing matter, etc.

May it be the will of Hashem that you hold fast to the path of the Baal Shem Tov, according to the verse, "Serve Hashem with joy." This means that even regarding the *avodah* of "In **all** your ways know Him" (*Rambam, Hilchos Deos, Chapter 3; Tur Shulchan Aruch, Siman 231*), this *avodah* too must be done with joy. In time, I am confident that this joy will not be for you merely a matter of *kabalas ol*, but that it will also be settled and absorbed in your intellect, such that you will realize there is reason to be joyful—not only from the perspective of the *nefesh elokis*, but even from the perspective of the body and the *nefesh habahamis*.

With blessings for a good settlement in all respects.

## 1554

B"H, 10 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Manhattan Chapter for "Beis Rivkah"
May Hashem grant them life

Blessings and peace!

On the occasion of the 7th annual banquet of your Manhattan women’s division for the Beis Rivkah schools, which is taking place tomorrow, G-d willing, Tuesday, 11 Iyar, 5712, I send you my greetings and blessing.

Our Sages, of blessed memory, tell us that it was in the merit of the righteous women that the Jewish people were redeemed from Mitzrayim. This merit consisted of the fact that, despite the harsh decrees and the suffering of the galus, they raised a generation of loyal Jewish children who were devoted to Hashem, the G-d of their fathers.

Hashem Yisbarach has promised us that the future Geulah Shleimah, speedily in our days, will be similar to the Geulah of Yetzias Mitzrayim.

This means that just as it was then, so too today, the redemption of the Jewish people is dependent upon Jewish women, in whose hands lies the education of Jewish children.

I hope, therefore, that you will continue your work—both in the education of your own children and in helping the education of other children—and that you will, in particular, make every effort to strengthen your activities on behalf of the Beis Rivkah schools, where the future Jewish mothers are being educated, who will uphold the traditions of the righteous Jewish women of all generations.

With blessings for success in your work, through which you also open channels for Divine blessings for yourselves and all your loved ones, in both material and spiritual matters.

## 1505

B"H, 10 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, involved in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Chaim Hillel, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from this past Erev Shabbos Kodesh, with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed therein on behalf of the bochur... may he live: When I am at the holy *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will read the *pidyon nefesh*, and he will surely arouse Divine mercy for him. It is appropriate to ascertain from his mother, may she live—naturally, in a way that does not cause her unnecessary distress—whether he was born in purity. In any case, you should instruct her to ensure that there are *kosher* *mezuzos* in her home, and likewise, if possible, that he should wear *tzitzis katan* if he is of the age for this. I am certain you will inform me when there is good news regarding a change for the better in his aforementioned health condition.

I was pleased to read in your letter that you are making preparations to utilize the upcoming vacation days to recruit a number of students for the *yeshiva*. You should invest much energy and strength into this, to **increase** the number of such students. For, aside from what is stated in *Tanya*, end of Chapter 25, that this unification above is eternal forever and ever—and consequently, even the performance of a *mitzvah* just once with these students is eternal above forever and ever—there is also an additional point, and perhaps it is not an addition but the essence: when these students hear a word of Torah, a statement of *yiras shamayim*, or a matter of *mitzvah*, you are planting within them an infinite and eternal power. Consequently, it will eventually produce its effect below as well. May Hashem grant you success, and those who assist you in your holy work, with success in this holy labor that is above nature, and may you draw it down afterward into nature, such that your personal matters will also be successful in a revealed manner.

With blessing.

#### 1505

**Rabbi Chaim Hillel:** Azimov. Additional letters to him: above, Vol. 5, 1151, and in the references noted there. Below, 1794.

## 1550

1550

B.H., 10 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, etc., engaged in communal affairs with faith,
R' Michael, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Following up on my previous letter, I am writing regarding the following matters:

1) Has the exemption for students from attending school on Shabbos been established in Gercif? It is understood that one must exert effort in this, as weakness in one place is liable to weaken the matter in other places as well.

2) Regarding the library: The suggestion that it be located in the city’s community center—while there is an advantage to this, in that people might be drawn there—it is nonetheless more necessary that it be in a location affiliated with Ohalei Yosef Yitzchok, so that this, too, becomes part of the activities of Ohalei Yosef Yitzchok and the dissemination of our work. Consequently, it is to be hoped that through this, baalei batim will be drawn closer and more students will be attracted, etc. In general, the goal must be that the Yeshiva in particular, and Ohalei Yosef Yitzchok in general, should not be merely educational institutions and nothing more, but also places from which strength is spread regarding all matters of Yiddishkeit in their locale and its surroundings. It is understood that all this must be done diplomatically.

3) I am interested to know if you have already received the books in English about which you wrote some time ago, and also if there is room for these books to be in the library as well, or if this is liable to cause some laxity and an inclination toward studies that are not within our sphere...

5) Regarding your question about the letterhead: One should add there also about schools for girls. Regarding your question as to whether to also print the address here: Because of the change in the climate in your country regarding the attitude toward other countries and the differences of opinion on this, I am somewhat concerned about whether this should be printed permanently until the situation becomes clear. However, you can make a stamp or even print slips stating that this is my address, etc., and attach this slip to the letters which, in your opinion, need to have it attached.

6) Regarding your question about the expenses for the mikveh, etc.—there was no approval for this from the Lishkah. Because of the order that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, worked so hard to establish, any matter that is not in the work plan requires the deliberation of several people, not a single judge. Consequently, even regarding the matter of assistance—whether for building or repairing a mikveh—which does not enter directly into our work, but only indirectly (as mentioned above, that if a Lubavitch institution is located in a place, their activity in all matters of yiras shamayim must be evident), ultimately, the expenditure is worthwhile. However, to prevent confusion of the order, it was necessary to inform the Lishkah or me beforehand and then decide on it. But since it is done, it is done, and surely you have already included this amount in the expenses approved by the Lishkah.

7) In one of your letters, you mention copying the sichos into French. If the matter is possible—and especially as you wrote in one of your letters that it is not tied to expenses, or only very small expenses—then it is worth looking into. Provided that there is a responsible person to check the copy, and also if it is possible to send the proofs here for review after the typesetting is arranged and before it is printed—meaning that there would still be the possibility to correct it if errors are found. It is understood that if the matter comes to fruition, it must be done in booklets of sichos from previous years, so that the booklet appears in the appropriate month—meaning that they should take a booklet from previous years from two months before its time, and then surely the booklet will appear in its proper time.

8) Regarding your question if it is worthwhile to establish a school for girls in Meknes: It is certainly the right thing to do, and not only in Meknes but also in other places. And specifically **and precisely** that they should not be **together** with the boys—meaning not only that they should not study in the same room, but also that they should not study in a way that the entry and exit to the building is through one gate and one entrance. And how good it would be if it were possible that they be in separate buildings and streets, for in matters such as these, the more caution, the more praiseworthy it is...

With a blessing for success in your work.

## 1557

1557

B”H, 10 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...I was greatly alarmed when I received your telegram informing me that the *ramim* intend to strike and not teach, and the potential consequences of this are clear.

Without entering into the arguments and claims from the other side, I sent a telegram regarding the impression this idea makes on me. Thank G-d, I received a telegram from the *ramim* that they have resumed their studies. When I asked the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing man, involved in communal needs, etc., our teacher R’... who is here, and as also appears from the letter of the *ramim*, it is clear that they have grievances and demands. As is usual in all such matters, each side is partially right and partially at fault; it is merely a matter of clarifying which part is greater—whether that in which they are right or that in which they are at fault. However, the one thing for which I cannot find any justification at present is the claim of the *ramim* that they had long ago informed [the administration] of their demands and had requested to hold a meeting to discuss this, yet not only did they not receive a response to their demands, but a meeting was not even held, nor was there any discussion with them. I do not understand this approach at all, as the consequences are clear enough, and such a state of affairs could, in time, G-d forbid, lead to a situation where "that which is crooked cannot be made straight"...

The approach of "what do we have to do with this trouble"—firstly, it is not a "trouble," and secondly, they are already sworn to this from Mount Sinai, and from that time on, and after they accepted the appointment from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, as members of the Yeshiva administration... until someone is found who has the power to exempt them from this, the matter rests upon them one hundred percent, whether they participate in the meetings or not, and even if one officially notifies [the administration] in advance that he does not wish to participate in the meetings.

4) The conclusion from all of the above is that although it is the duty of every Chabad Chossid to assist them in their work in the administration of this Yeshiva, the responsibility rests specifically upon their shoulders... May the Almighty grant them success and help me so that, at the very least, from here on out, I will not have to write letters of rebuke, but rather only matters of expressing thanks and wishing success.

Awaiting good news, and thanking you in advance for the earliest possible response regarding this.

## 1559

10 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chossid, G-d-fearing, and involved in communal needs, etc., R’ Dovid, may he live;
To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and involved in communal needs, etc., R’ Meir, may he live;
And to the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and involved in communal needs, etc., R’ Zusya, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter informing me that you have been chosen by Agudas Chabad, Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, and the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok network to advocate for the expansion of institutions within the "non-affiliated" (bilti zrami) stream (and I am somewhat surprised that no official minutes from this meeting were received, as has been the custom until now), I have two points to make:

a) Since, for the time being, the matter concerns only Lubavitch institutions, it should seemingly not be treated as a new question or a new issue, but rather as an extension of what has already been authorized. That is to say, your approach should be—and perhaps not even as a formal request, but simply as an announcement—that since Lubavitch institutions have existed within the non-affiliated stream for some years now, specifically in Lod and Sefaria, then just like any living thing that grows and develops, the circle of Lubavitch institutions has also grown. Consequently, we are establishing additional educational institutions in such-and-such a place. It is understood that these possess all the same rights as the institutions established two years ago, since their founders are the same group and the reasons are identical in both cases. When you present the matter in this way, there is a double benefit: 1) It leaves no room for debate regarding whether to grant the license; 2) It does not touch at all upon the general situation and the current dispute regarding education—behind the scenes—between the Ministry of Education and the Charedi ministers, since you are not innovating anything, but merely adding another institution as a continuation of those already in existence.

b) If you meet with Mr. Shazar, may he live, you should certainly include at least one of those who have already spoken with him on this matter and who promised to assist you in this. It is understood that it is better to meet with Mr. Shazar before speaking about the matter officially with the body that holds the formal decision-making power in this regard.

According to reports, Mr. Shazar will be leaving the Holy Land (may it be rebuilt and established) in the coming weeks, and therefore it is worthwhile to hasten the matter, in addition to the reason that registration begins in three weeks, etc.

With blessings for success in your holy work.

Your letter of the 6th of Iyar has just been received, and I have sent a telegram in accordance with the above. It reads: "In response to your letter, in my opinion, you should propose the establishment of the new educational institutions as a continuation of the existing Lubavitch educational institutions that are already approved as non-affiliated. With blessing."

... c) In accordance with this, it is my hope that you will not encounter difficulties and will be able to register to open educational institutions in several more places. Surely, the Baal Shem Tov’s precision will be fulfilled in this as well: "Though your beginning was small, yet your end will greatly increase."

d) Enclosed is a check for 50 shekels as my participation in the expenses involved in the above...

With blessings for success,

**M. Schneerson**

Your letter has now been received, containing answers to some of my questions, and surely more will follow.
