## 1560

1560

B”H, 10 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rav, the G-d-fearing man, who occupies himself with communal needs, etc., Moreinu Harav Eliezer, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

...Regarding what you wrote in your letter concerning that which is stated in Likutei Torah, Parshas Shemini, in the maamar beginning "Leviathan Zeh," that you wish to understand the simple meaning of why shechitah with a blemished knife is invalid due to the interruption (hefsek), and consequently, you find this difficult, since the invalidity of a blemished knife is because it tears (nakiv), as is stated in Chullin 17b (and cited also in Teshuvos Tzemach Tzedek, Yoreh Deah, Siman 16; Shaar HaMiluim, Siman 63. See there).

Behold, this is the language of the Likutei Torah: "Such shechitah is completely blemished due to the interruption, etc." To my mind, this interpretation aligns with the literal sense of the phrasing. Even though there are several distinctions regarding the nature of a blemish as brought in the Gemara there—[whether it is] jagged, notched, or uneven, etc.—the Likutei Torah is stating that the shechitah on its fins is **completely blemished** due to the interruption (that exists between the parts of the fins). It is not discussing the reason for the invalidity of a blemish, but rather the quality of the blemish.

**A side note:** The statement of our Sages regarding the practice of hunting (kinegiya) is also explained in Torah Or, Parshas Toldos, in the maamar beginning "Veyiten Lecha," and it is in a different manner than what is written in Likutei Torah. This maamar is also cited—in a concise explanation—in the sefer Shnei HaMeoros, page 10 (on the title page of which it is written that it is from the Mitteler Rebbe—and so it was recorded by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the "Chain of Chassidus" printed at the beginning of the Hayom Yom calendar—but apparently, based on the style of the maamarim, these are short maamarim of the Alter Rebbe **which the Mitteler Rebbe recorded**).

#### 1560

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 12, p. 177, and completed according to a photocopy of the letter.

**Moreinu Harav Eliezer:** Kresik. Additional letters to him—see above, 1531, and the references in the notes there.

**Written on the title page:** See Y. Mondshine, Kovetz Yagdil Torah (N.Y.), Issue 28, Siman 39.

1561

By the Grace of Hashem, 10 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, who toils in the study of Chassidus, etc.,
Rabbi Efraim Eliezer, may he live.

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter from the evening following Shabbos Tiferes Sheb’Tiferes — the birthday of the Rebbe Maharash — regarding your question on the *maamar* in *Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Tazria*, s.v. *Kamiplegi B’Mesivta D’Rakia*, end of Chapter 1, which states: "The Keter is drawn from the Malchus of Ein Sof, which is only light and radiance from the Emanator Himself."

1) You are in doubt regarding the word **"שהוא"** (which is/he is): Does it refer to the Keter? If so, it is difficult to understand, for the Malchus of Ein Sof is also only light and radiance. Or does it refer to the Malchus of Ein Sof? If so, it is difficult, as it should have been written **"שהיא"** (which is/she is) in the feminine form.

**Response:**

To clarify this doubt: This statement is also found in the *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek, and in the version of the Tzemach Tzedek (p. 93a) it states: "The Keter is drawn only from the Malchus of Ein Sof, and the aspect of **Malchus** is called by the name 'light and radiance' from the Essence." Regarding your difficulty that it should also be "היא" (she) in *Likutei Torah*, it is well known that, in general, in the *maamarim* of *Toras HaChassidus*, one does not overly scrutinize such matters—unlike the *Tanya*, Part I, and similar texts, where the precision of masculine/feminine, singular/plural, etc., is strictly maintained. One may note the debate regarding this very issue between the Maharshal and the Rema, as printed in the *Responsa of the Rema*, Siman 4; see there at length. One may also note what the Rashbetz writes in Part I, Siman 43, cited in *Sdei Chemed*, *Klalei HaPoskim*, Siman 16, subsection 55: "It is no blemish for a sage if he does not know the nuances of grammar and words; there are many grammatical errors in the *piyutim* of Rabbi Elazar HaKalir, who was one of the greatest sages." It is also possible that the lack of grammatical precision in the *maamarim* of *Toras HaChassidus* is, as the Rema writes in the aforementioned *responsa*, due to the copyists.

Regarding the specific case in the aforementioned *Likutei Torah*, it can also be explained in another way, based on what is explained in *Toras HaChassidus* regarding the language of prayer: "Emunah kol zos" (Faith is all this) is feminine, while "V'kayam aleinu" (And it is established upon us) is masculine (*Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Eikev*, 16d, end of page). This is because when the Sefirah of Malchus stands at the end of the higher world, it is a receiver, and when it becomes the head of this world, it is a giver. Thus, initially it is "Emunah kol zos," and afterwards "V'kayam aleinu." Similarly, in the *Likutei Torah* here, which explains how the Keter is drawn from the Malchus of Ein Sof—meaning that it is in the aspect of a giver and draws down to the Keter—it therefore uses the masculine "הוא" (he), because it is drawing down to what is above it. The Tzemach Tzedek wrote "היא" (she) in the feminine, because he repeated the phrase, "and the aspect of Malchus—as mentioned above—'The Keter is drawn only from the Malchus of Ein Sof, and the aspect of Malchus is called...'"—speaking of the aspect of Malchus not merely as the light that draws down the Keter, but in its entirety and essence; therefore, he wrote "היא."

2) What is the reason for the double terminology, "light and radiance" (*ohr* and *ziv*), and why is "radiance" (*ziv*) alone not sufficient?

As mentioned above, it is a significant matter to resolve such double terminologies, even in *Tanya*, Part I. See *Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah*, Chapter 3, regarding the precisions there, where "light" alone is mentioned, "radiance" alone, and both together; sometimes "light" precedes "radiance," and sometimes "radiance" precedes "light," and similarly in many places.

In general, based on the usage of these terms in various contexts, the difference between "light" and "radiance" is understood, both regarding the giver and the receiver. Regarding the giver, the "light" is more essential than the "radiance," which is an external and secondary matter in relation to the light. Therefore, the terminology in every place is: "Light is like the source of the light," "the light is attached to the source of the light," etc.—and not "radiance." Regarding the receiver, the "light"—by virtue of being a matter more sublime than the source of the light—is received in a *makif* (encompassing) manner. This is not the case with "radiance," which, because it is secondary and external, is within the capacity of the receiver to receive it also internally. Hence the precision in the language of our Sages: "Their crowns on their heads" (a crown is a *makif*) "and they derive pleasure from the **radiance** of the Shechinah"—pleasure is received internally (*Rashi, Berachos 17a*).

In Malchus and Keter, both of these aspects exist, and therefore it says "light and radiance." See also *Likutei Torah* of this week, 20a-b.

3) In *Likutei Torah* there, end of Chapter 2, it mentions that there are several "garments" of thought. When one's thought is on a matter of wisdom in the wisdom of Torah, this is an "internal garment." When one thinks of wisdom necessary for the wisdom of Torah, such as astronomy, this is an "intermediate garment." You are in doubt as to whether thinking about the greatness of creation in order to contemplate the greatness of the Creator is an internal or intermediate garment.

In my opinion, there are two ways to look at this: If one contemplates the greatness of creation simply, as the Rambam writes in *Hilchos Yesodei HaTorah*, beginning of Chapter 2: "And what is the way to His love and fear..."—this is a preparation for the mitzvah, the mitzvah of the love of Hashem and the fear of Hashem. However, if one thinks about the knowledge of the *Seder Hishtalshelus*—meaning the chain-like descent of the Sefiros one from another, etc.—this itself is a lofty and exalted mitzvah, and on the contrary, it surpasses all others, as it is written: "And you shall know this day..." "Know the G-d of your father..." (See *Kuntrus Acharon* to *Tanya*, s.v. *Lehavin Mah Shekatuv* in *Pri Etz Chaim*, 156b).

Note: In our printed editions it is written *mitzvah* **rabbah** (great) (and this requires study from *Bava Basra 8b*, and *Tosafos* s.v. *Lo*, *Gittin 41b*) *v'nisah* (and exalted). However, in the list of corrections by the late Rabbi Rav Asher, who was involved in the printing of the *Tanya*, it states that it should be *mitzvah* **ramah** (lofty) *v'nisah*, and the Rebbe Rayatz approved his list of corrections.

4) There, Chapters 3 and 4, you are in doubt whether the *Kelipas Nogah* of Atzilus also draws from the Tiferes of Atzilus, or only from Chochma and Gevurah, etc.

Based on the presentation of the matter there, it is understood that if only the light of Abba is withdrawn, then it is possible for there to be a "sucking" (nurture for the kelipah). But that the "sucking" is from Tiferes, or at the very least from Netzach or Malchus—this is not so, and Heaven forbid to say such a thing. The meaning is that when the light of Abba is withdrawn, even though the other Sefiros are in their place, there is room for "sucking." But the "sucking" itself is not from the Sefiros themselves, Heaven forbid. That is why it is said in the verse, "When a person has in the **skin** of his flesh" (see *Likutei Torah* there, s.v. *Zeh*). And it is also stated in the *drush* of *B'Yah Askinan* that the "sucking" is from the letters, etc., but not from the Sefiros themselves, Heaven forbid.

5) Regarding your note on the logic found in several places* that a verse informs us of the certain and not the doubtful, and you connect this with the dispute as to whether the *baheres* (bright spot) precedes the white hair, etc.: See that very *drush*, end of Chapter 4, which explains the matter of doubt and knowledge, distinguishing between *nega'im* (plagues) and a *mamzer* (illegitimate child) in relation to other matters.

6) One should note the general theme of the *drush*, in terms of *mussar*, from the *sicha* of the Rebbe Rayatz of 18 Elul, 5703, page 15.

7) I have just received your letter from Sunday. Many thanks for the excellent points regarding what was written about "You shall be holy." Among the Chassidim of Chabad, it is told regarding this in the name of the Rashbetz, R' Sheftel (a *mashpia* in the Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim in Lubavitch), who would say at a *farbrengen* and emphasize: "You can be like me"—in a calm tone—"that there is the ability to be like me. For I am holy—holiness from above comes from your holiness."

With blessing.

Regarding the statement of our Sages, "They differ in the Heavenly Academy," there is a brilliant *drush* in the commentary of the Malbim to *Sefer HaMitzvos* (beginning of *Parshas Chukas*). And yet, the comparison highlights most clearly what Chassidus is: the springs and the flow of new light that were revealed through it.

## 1562

1562

B"H, 10 Iyar, 5712

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, engaged in communal needs,
Rabbi Meir Liber, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

It has been some time since I have heard what is happening with you and your family, may they live. I would like to clarify that all is well with you and your entire family, and that your livelihood is also good. Nevertheless, according to the ruling of our holy Torah that where there is an opportunity to clarify, one does not rely on the presumption of the status quo (Yoreh Deah, at the beginning), surely you will inform me of this explicitly.

Regarding what you noted previously concerning what is written in Tanya, page 30, line 7, "and they denied Hashem" — this is from the language of the verse in Yirmiyahu 5:12. See also in the sefer Derech Mitzvotecha, Mitzvas Achdus Hashem, at the end (page 62b).

With blessings for success in all of the above, and likewise in your involvement in the shiurim taught in public, to increase and magnify them so that it will be, in the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, a healthy and happy summer.

With blessings, and awaiting good news.

## 1563

11 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Avreichim who sit and engage in Torah and Avodah at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in the city of Paris, may it be rebuilt and established,
May they live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to hear from the esteemed Rabbi, a man of stature and accomplishment, who engages in communal affairs, the Mashpia and administrator, Rabbi Nissan, may he live, regarding the order of your learning and Avodah, and the progress you are making in this with the help of Hashem. However, on the other hand, it caused me pain and distress to learn that, apparently due to thoughts regarding the question of emigration, there is a lack of the necessary and required focus and depth in the study of Torah in general, and in the study of Chassidus and engagement in the Avodah of Tefillah in particular. Although time does not permit me to elaborate on this, given the great importance of the matter, I am writing these few lines:

You are surely familiar with the Sicha of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in which he explained the journeys of the Bnei Yisrael in the desert. From one journey to the next, they would dismantle the Mishkan and then set it up in a new location. Regarding this, the verse states that the duration of their stay at each stop was not uniform. In the words of the verse: "And there were times when the cloud remained from evening until morning, and the cloud lifted in the morning, and they journeyed... or two days, or a month, or a year." Yet, the common denominator in all these journeys was that "by the mouth of Hashem they would encamp, and by the mouth of Hashem they would journey." Furthermore, the common denominator was that "they kept the charge of Hashem, by the mouth of Hashem, by the hand of Moshe." This means that there was no change or difference in the setting up of the Mishkan or in all matters of the "charge of Hashem," whether they stayed in a place for a year or several years, or whether they stayed for only a day and a night, or even just from evening until morning.

It is also understood through human intellect—and even through the intellect of the Nefesh HaBahamis—that since they encamped by the mouth of Hashem and journeyed by the mouth of Hashem, which is above time and above space, and since the purpose of creation in general, and the journeys in particular, is to make for Him, may He be blessed, a dwelling place in physical time and space, we have nothing to do but fulfill the will of our Creator. Through this, we connect and cleave to the Atzmus and Mahus of the Ein Sof, may He be blessed, who does as He wills, whether it be in this place for many years or only from evening until morning. Since one's involvement in this is to bring the "above time" and "above space" into the world, the difference in the duration of time does not affect him at all.

Based on this, one can also explain what is stated in the Tanya, at the end of Chapter 25, that this unification above is eternal, forever and ever, etc., and likewise, the revelation of His will in His speech, which is the Torah, is eternal. Furthermore, this provides an additional explanation for what is brought in many places in the revealed Torah regarding matters that require a specific measurement: that if it is a matter of a Mitzvah, "the Mitzvah makes it important," and it is as if it possesses a physical measurement.

My hope is strong that these few words of mine will suffice, and I will be happy to receive good news soon that you are increasing in Torah and Avodah, both within yourselves and in your influence upon others. Surely the promise of our Sages and the Halachic ruling will be fulfilled in you: that a person who sanctifies himself a little below, they sanctify him (a promise) much from above.

With blessings for success in Torah study and Yiras Shamayim.

## 1564

11 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and involved in communal affairs, etc.,
Rabbi Nissan, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

As you requested, and for the sake of order, I am hereby confirming once again the receipt of all your letters from after the holidays of the month of Tishrei. They are: 28 Tishrei; 8, 13, and 17 Kislev; 2 and 29 Teves; 5, 16, and 19 Shevat; 20 and 27 Adar; and 7 Iyar, along with the lists and the *panim* attached to them, which were read at an *eis ratzon* at the holy resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

2) I derived special satisfaction from receiving the names of *anash* in Russia. This points to two main points: a) The concept of *ahavas Yisrael* and the unbroken connection between them and our brethren who are in Russia; b) It is highly probable that by maintaining a connection with them—at least in thought—this strengthens the concept that "all of Israel are responsible for one another." Consequently, just as the *he'elem* and *hester* (concealments and hiddenness) in that country have no dominion over those who are outside of it, the connection with those who are still within that country grants them strength to stand firm and fortify their standing and situation, and diminishes the control that the "oppressor" can exert over them. This is analogous to a body: when a part of the body is in a place of fresh, pure air, it brings additional vitality to the part of the body that is in a cellar in a place of stale air. But for this to work, it must be "as one body." This is the power of thought, and specifically the power of *tziyur* (visualization), as explained in many places in the *sichos* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that time and place do not limit this. See also the *sicha* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (Shemini Atzeres night in the *sukkah*, 5693). Even though it speaks there about a *Nasi* in Israel, something similar exists for all those who are connected to him, especially when it is a *tzibbur* (congregation), for "G-d is mighty and does not despise." Surely they will continue in such a connection in the future as well, and G-d willing, there will be great benefit in this for those who are there and also for those who are here. As the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, goes: "The *Ribono shel Olam* does not remain a debtor," etc.

4) Regarding what you wrote in your letter that the students' mood is not at the necessary level of tranquility to study as they should, due to the confusion surrounding the matter of travel, a short letter to them is enclosed herewith, and surely you will explain it in the appropriate manner.

6) I was pleased with your report regarding the order of studies, and especially that even those who are studying for *hora'ah* (rabbinic ordination)—namely *Yoreh De'ah*—you have now instituted that they should study *Gemara, Poshut, Tosafos* for at least a few hours a day. Regarding the studies of *Chassidus* and the fact that you are also training them in reviewing *Chassidus* by heart, one must take into account the capacity for comprehension and memory of each individual. Those for whom this is most difficult, and who consequently require the most time, should not be exempt from the matter, but one should not burden them to review as frequently as those who grasp it easily. It is for the *mashpia* on the spot to decide how much can be placed upon each individual, but as mentioned, everyone belongs to this, at least to some extent.

7) Another point to note regarding the review of *Chassidus* by heart: in those *maamarim* that are reviewed in public, some should be easy to understand, even for *baalei batim* or *avreichim* who are not so familiar with the teachings of Chabad *Chassidus*. These *maamarim* should not be tied to a specific *Yom Tov* or *Shabbos*, but rather be topics that are relevant all year round. Consequently, these *maamarim* can be reviewed when the need arises to review *Chassidus* outside of *Tomchei Temimim* and the circles of *anash*.

8) Since the vacation days from the government schools in France are approaching, appropriate preparation must be made so that it is possible to absorb, for the duration of the vacation, a certain number of youth who, for the time being, are not connected to our circles. By their being under your influence for several weeks, there is hope to change them and bring them closer to the Torah of Hashem and His *mitzvos*, and perhaps also to influence them to study even after the vacation in a proper *Talmud Torah*, to hear public *shiurim*, or even in the *Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim*.

10) Regarding your request for my opinion on whether it is worthwhile for you to move from France and come here, I have refrained from writing about this, relying on you to understand on your own that this itself is an answer. To those who asked me orally in your name about this—among them the esteemed Chossid...—I expressed my opinion more openly. However, since you ask about this in every single one of your letters, and also in your latest letters, I will address it, at least partially and briefly.

In general, regarding any such question of moving from here to there, one must weigh the matter in both places—both regarding the "here" and the "there." Regarding a general person, even the appointment of a minor official is decreed from Heaven; how much more so, and how much more so, for one whose influence is upon people of Torah, and who speaks the inner dimensions of the Torah—this concerns, first and foremost, the situation of those he influences. When you evaluate your situation in Paris and France, the Almighty has privileged you to stand at the head of an institution of our Rebbeim, the *Nesi'im*—*Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim*—which means the study of Torah with *yiras shamayim*, detachment from the physical and material *olam hazeh*, and a connection to the most elevated and refined matters. You see clearly, throughout the years of your being there, that there was a possibility to increase the number of students in the institution many times over, even in the higher grades and classes, and certainly in the lower grades and in the *Talmud Torah* associated with this institution. Likewise, among those who go from house to house to spread the "candle of *mitzvah* and the light of Torah" in the homes of the children of Israel in France, who have not yet reached the realization that they should leave their homes for a place of Torah and *mitzvah*. If you saw this clearly even without having made any effort to expand and increase the number of students, then how much more so would it have been visible even to the physical eye had you made an effort in this! And although there are several people involved and managing the administration of the institution, the influence, etc., etc., as in most institutions of this kind, the vast majority depends on one person who will guard the point and strive to maintain the spirit of vitality in all parts of the institution. As they told me about the situation in Paris, the situation that existed before that in Pocking, and also the situation while they were still in Russia—you are that person. Through you came the strengthening and the spirit of vitality in all parts of the *Yeshiva* and the circles of *anash* surrounding the *Yeshiva*. And once again I must repeat: even now, although several of *anash* have moved from France (and in my opinion, even now, except for a few of them, they committed a "foolishness" in doing so), there is a vast and large field to increase the quantity of students in the *Yeshiva* and the *chedarim* associated with it, and to increase them in quality as well. The condition for this, as in all matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, is that you must strive for it in practice, and strive truly—that is, for the sake of the matter, and not just to fulfill an obligation. After contemplating all this, I do not see room for doubt: if you were to move from the administration of the *Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim* in France, which is the only one for the time being in all of Europe and in which the spirit of *Tomchei Temimim* is preserved more than in *yeshivos* in other places—I do not know if all the above requires proofs and evidence from other places. Therefore, I will bring only points: the saying of the Rebbe the *Tzemach Tzedek*, "We are workers of the day; we must make it bright." Consequently, this is also our reality and our essence. The promise of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe that through *tzedakah*—and it is obvious that this also includes spiritual *tzedakah*—one's mind and heart become a thousand times more refined. As is understood from the annotations to this *maamar* in *Likutei Torah* at the beginning of the *parshiyos*, this is **a thousand** times, and not by way of exaggeration. That is, according to the simple meaning, what one can achieve and succeed in the ordinary way through the work of a thousand hours, one can achieve through involvement in *tzedakah* in the span of one hour. When one calculates the success in time in this regard, it is truly wondrous and awesome. And the main point in all of the above is: why and for what reason must one "carry the pack alone"? And consequently, to stand in battle by oneself against the matters from without and against the matters from within, at the very time that through your connection to the institution founded and managed by our Rebbeim, you become a part of this institution—that is, a part of the *Nesi'im*—and consequently, the responsibility for them is upon you, and your work is only not to interfere with the continuation of the blessing in spirituality and in physicality, and to receive it with the good receptivity that they extend to all those who participate in their activities in general, and in particular in those of spreading the wellsprings outward and guarding the point within.

It goes without saying that I do not rule out the matter of travel entirely, because the time now, in the "heels of Mashiach," is prone to extreme changes, and consequently the aforementioned situation could also change. Likewise, I do not rule out the matter of traveling for a visit, but regarding a permanent move, as mentioned, I do not see any basis in logic or reason for you to leave your place and seek new matters, etc., and further elaboration is superfluous.

With a blessing for success in your holy work to influence a spirit of life, connection, and *dveikus* to the Living G-d in the students in particular and in your surroundings in general, which will also serve as a channel and vessel for your proper health and for all your household, may they live, in health of the soul and health of the body. — Waiting for good tidings.

## 1565

1565

B"H, 11 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the brilliant Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, and esteemed, the arranger and dialectician, the swift scribe, etc., Rabbi R. Sh. Y. [Zevin]—may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive the third volume of the *Talmudic Encyclopedia* via Mr. Bar-Lev—may he live—and I extend my heartfelt thanks to you for this precious gift.

Although time has not permitted me to study it with the necessary depth, even in leafing through it, it is evident from a first glance that it represents a monumental labor and extensive research into the entire Talmudic literature—the *Rishonim*, *Acharonim*, and the most recent authorities. One can clearly discern the "power of the actor in the acted-upon" [i.e., the author’s influence on the work] in its excellent organization and clarity of language.

There is no doubt that this valuable work will bring great benefit, especially in our current era, in which, due to our many sins, the treasures of Torah are sealed off to many of our people, and many do not have the time to delve into the sources, etc. A systematically organized book such as this fulfills an important role, as one can easily find in it the essence of what is sought, with the sources noted for anyone who wishes to delve into them further. Furthermore, it is a hidden treasure for those who study Torah and are engaged in it.

May his strength be fortified in Torah, and may he be blessed to complete the work.

With blessings for success in his work, to merit the many with the light of Torah and the "light" within it,

**M. Schneerson**

*1565*

**Rabbi R. Sh. Y.:** Zevin. Additional letters to him: above, Vol. 5, 1354, and in the references noted there. Below, 1566, 1768.

## 1566

11 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the brilliant Rabbi, the Chassid, the G-d-fearing man, the meticulous editor and sharp scholar, the swift writer, etc., etc., Rabbi S.Y. [Zevin]—may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

A few days ago, Mr. Bar-Lev visited me and presented the third volume of the *Entziklopedia Talmudit*, asking if I could assist in its distribution and sale.

After discussing the matter, I gave him a letter addressed to you, in response to your gift, a copy of which is enclosed. I hope it will be of the desired benefit.

It goes without saying that, in addition to this, I will endeavor to assist him as much as possible...

I hereby acknowledge, albeit with some delay, the receipt of your letters from the 17th of Shevat and the conclusion of Shabbos Vayikra. In the meantime, you have surely received the *kuntresim* and the letters enclosed with them, as well as the *Sdei Chemed*, and I trust you will acknowledge their receipt.

Regarding the books: after inquiring with Rabbi Ch. Lieberman, who was the librarian for my father-in-law, the Rebbe, there is no identifying mark on the books, other than the fact that some of them bear an inscription indicating they are from the library of Shmuel Wiener. I may be able to obtain a photograph of this inscription and send it to you, and I will follow up with letters as you suggested.

Many thanks to you for your efforts on behalf of the affairs of Chabad in Eretz Yisrael—may it be built and established. I was happy to receive a letter from Aguch and from the village, stating that it is highly probable that they will all be able to remain together as one group in their current location. I trust their borders will expand with additional settlers, as I wrote to the village administration that this is where the greatest effort must be directed now.

I have a request for you... perhaps you could clarify whether there is any *heter* or clarification regarding a *tikkun* that has been made concerning the government loan, in light of the prohibition of *ribis* involved. You have surely seen the scholarly discussions on this in the monthly *HaPardes*, but the *heterim* presented there are not satisfactory.

In order to provide an answer to those who ask, I wanted to know if any *tikkun* has been implemented, as there are people spreading rumors that in some office (it is impossible to verify its name or affiliation) a general *heter iska* has been established.

Thank you in advance for your trouble in clarifying this matter.

Many thanks for your visit to the Yeshiva in Lod, etc...

Mr. Shragai visited me, but since it was before the reading of the *Megillah* and there was a *tircha d'tzibura*, our conversation was interrupted. He was supposed to visit me again, but it did not come to pass, and I do not know the reason.

And last, but certainly not least: I read with joy in your letter that you are reprinting your books: *Sefer HaMoadim*, *Halacha*, *Ha'arachos al Ishim v'Sefarim*, and *Sippurei HaChassidim*. Although I have only seen the first of these, the author has already proven his worth, and I hope that your other books are equally suited to your talents and abilities, and that they fulfill the needs of the Jewish public in general, and the *Chareidi* public in particular. It is a pity that, according to your letter, you were unable to make additions because they were printed from matrices, as surely, from time to time, notes and insights have been added to these books. You are familiar with the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in the name of the Rebbe Maharash: "If it is good, is it not better if it is better?"

Naturally, I thank you in advance if I have the opportunity to receive your two latest books mentioned above.

With blessings for success in your work, for long days and good years, filled with good deeds—for there is no "good" other than Torah and the inner dimensions of Torah, which is the *ilana d'chayei* (tree of life) through which Israel will emerge from exile with mercy.

## 1567

1567

B"H, 20 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of Thursday, Parshas Emor, in which you explain the matter of the meeting on 13 Iyar and also that you have approached Agudas Chasidei Chabad regarding assistance with registration, etc. Surely, in the interim, you have already received my letter responding to your previous correspondence. Nevertheless, I will reiterate my intention and opinion:

It is not necessary to conquer all the crossings at once. Rather, what is essential is to establish a strong foundation of administration and network (approximately ten chadarim). As I conveyed orally through the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned man, who occupies himself with communal needs, etc., Rabbi Moshe Gurary, may he live: one must begin the foundation of Oholei Yosef Yitzchok in those places where there is already some foothold for Chabad—meaning, where Anash live in close proximity—and certainly if they are located near Lod or the village, etc., or in such places where there is good material, meaning, bochurim who have the potential to enter one of our yeshivos soon, or who can be developed into mashpi'im and leaders, etc. Consequently, this will serve as an indication regarding the places that should take precedence in the founding of Oholei Yosef Yitzchok.

It is understood that what I mentioned—the number ten—is not precise; it could be more or less. I only intended to indicate that, for the time being, the quantity is not as significant. As I have already written, it is not worthwhile to create a stir or increase the quantity, in order to facilitate the attainment of all the necessary means and requirements, such as licenses, etc., without encountering such legal opposition that might arise from seeing the expansion of Lubavitch to an excessive degree.

What must be emphasized is that in those places where you do establish [a cheder], the matter should be conducted in a manner that is suitable to serve as a model, and that will prepare minds for the expansion of the network—meaning, that the parents and students will be satisfied, etc.

It is understood that one cannot, for this reason, compromise on the fundamental point—namely, that among yourselves, in private, you must know that ultimately it is necessary to strive for the students to be Chassidim, and therefore the matter must be directed toward this. However, regarding the order, the quality of the education, the cleanliness, etc., it is sometimes worthwhile to forgo an increase in quantity, especially for the sake of an increase in quality.

It is difficult to explain and detail every particular, for this is a matter determined on the spot, and the decision must be appropriate to the conditions of the location. May Hashem grant you success, with extraordinary success beyond the natural order, to increase Torah and glorify it through the number of school children, and to elevate them to higher and higher levels in holiness.

With the blessing of receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 1568

1568

B"H, 20 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

... The esteemed [name], may he live, informed me that you and your wife, may they live, are not feeling well.

Both of you should be confident that you will begin to feel better, especially as we approach the Yom Tov of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah. The Midrash states that at the time of the giving of the Torah, all the Yidden became healthy. This is further proof of what is stated in the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov: that Hashem desires that we serve Him with the body as well, and not by afflicting the body; rather, one should serve Hashem with joy and good health, and be dedicated to the fulfillment of Torah and mitzvos. May Hashem help you to receive the Torah with joy and inwardness, in good health.

With blessings.

## 1751

B"H, 23 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
R' Moshe HaKohen, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

... It was with pleasure that I learned that you have acceded to the request of the congregants of the Shaarei Tefillah synagogue, the children of Reuven, to accept the appointment as their president. May it be the will of Hashem that you utilize this position and your influence so that the synagogue will be worthy of its name, "Shaarei Tefillah" (Gates of Prayer), and its "Nusach HaAriZal." As is known, the AriZal clarified the correct and appropriate version for all Bnei Yisrael, as explained in *Likutei Amarim* by the Maggid, which is also transcribed in the introduction to *Shaar HaKollel*, which states: "The AriZal, to whom the paths of heaven were illuminated, taught knowledge to the people—for one who does not know his tribe—and established a liturgy compiled from several versions, as is known to those who are expert, etc. However, in this time, when the tribes are not known (and it is better that even those who do know their tribe) should enter through the 'Shaar HaKollel' (the inclusive gate). The proof is that we have Kohanim and Leviim among us, and how could there be one version for everyone?"—this is the end of the language relevant to our matter.

May the prayers ascend through the "Shaarei Tefillah" to the highest heights, to bring about their effect below in actual practice: to heal the sick, to bless the years, etc. It is also known that the virtue of the Kohanim in this regard is that, in this time, their primary virtue is *Birchas Kohanim* (the Priestly Blessing). Its purpose is to draw down blessings with speed through the entire *Seder Hishtalshelus*, without giving any room for delay by the *mekatregim* (prosecuting angels), etc., as is explained well in *Likutei Torah*, at the end of *Parshas Korach*, that the sign of Aharon’s Kehunah is the almond rod—*shkidah* (diligence) for the good.

Regarding the matter of Reuven, I would point out the Gemara in *Sotah* 7b: "He confessed, etc."

With blessings for success in your presidency and for proper health for you and your wife, may they live, and that you may soon find a suitable dwelling for yourselves, both physically and spiritually.

***

**1751**

**R' Moshe:** Shaiovitch. Additional letters to him—see above, Vol. 5, 1539, and the references in the notes there.

## 1792

1792

B"H, 23 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you mention in your letter about the amount you set aside each week: you are surely aware of the enactment of Usha that one who distributes should not distribute more than [a fifth], etc. And even though it is explained in Iggeres HaKodesh regarding the matter of tzedakah that our current times are different—as is explained there at length—nevertheless, even in this there must be some limitation. It is difficult for me to write about this in more detail since I do not know the basis of your custom. In general, the matter of tzedakah is good, and there is nothing higher than it, and it also has a benefit in gashmius in the literal sense; however, you should still think it over (arientrachten) once more regarding the sums you send week after week...

I have already conveyed through R' M.A. shlita that the point of everything I speak to you about each time you are here is to bring about an expansion of your keilim. You should not view yourself as someone who is merely receiving or helping someone else, but rather as a representative and shaliach of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, in that place. Consequently, it is incumbent upon you to fulfill your shlichus, and you have been given the kochos for this. It is clear that the intention of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, was to transform [the city] into a city of Chassidus—naturally, little by little, as with all matters of kedushah, as it is written: "Little by little I will drive them out from before you." The conclusion to be drawn from this is that when you encounter an acquaintance—a bakantshaft—through someone or through an intermediary matter, you must view that person or intermediary matter as nothing more than a remedy to expand your circle of acquaintances. In this way, you will be able to use it to penetrate with your influence into yet another group of people, and thereby influence the conduct of more people in upholding Yiddishkeit, and ultimately, in spreading the teachings of Chassidus and its customs. Therefore, I was not entirely satisfied that after there was an opportunity for you to make an acquaintance with... and your influence had grown, you were still waiting for instructions on every little detail, etc. If one does not utilize the opportunity that presents itself to a person, one eventually loses it, as our Sages have said: "The Holy One, blessed be He, did not create anything in His world in vain." There is no need to elaborate further on this, as you have been told many times that the strength and ability have been given to you, and a vast field for avodah exists. Nothing is missing but the ratzon—er zol zich ainshparen—that you must carry out the ratzon of my father-in-law, the Rebbe... and not look at or take into account all the he'lem and hester, the vast majority of which are nothing but imagination; for ninety-nine percent of the power of the opponents is merely that they know people are afraid of them.

With blessings for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness, from a place of true expansion.

## 1753

B"H, 23 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Through the intermediary of the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and upright, who engages in communal needs with faith, etc., R' Yehuda Zvi Fogelman, I received the news that you have begun building houses in Worcester in order to sell them later, and you request a blessing for success, as well as to derive nachas from your daughters, may they live and be well.

When I visit the Ohel of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will read your Pidyon Nefesh for the fulfillment of your requests.

However, you surely understand on your own—and it is superfluous to point out—that in order to receive the blessings of Hashem, one must create the appropriate vessels for them, which are the vessels of Torah and mitzvos. If possible, these vessels should be of the same nature as the requests for which one is in need. Thus, in this matter as well: in order for the building and selling of the houses to be successful, you must draw success into your own home. This means that your home should be permeated with the spirit of yiras shamayim, literally—that you should have fixed shiurim in Torah, and that your home should be conducted in the path of mitzvos and yiras shamayim. Just as you increase the appropriate effort in the success of your home—that is, in spirituality—so too will your success increase in the houses you are building, and the material profit from their subsequent sale will grow.

In addition to this, it is appropriate that you take upon yourself **now**—naturally, without a neder—that when you sell the aforementioned houses at a profit, you will set aside a certain percentage for tzedakah, provided that the tzedakah is connected to matters of yiras shamayim. May Hashem help you and bless you to derive nachas from your daughters—Yiddishe nachas, and from yourselves as well.

With blessings,

## 1574

B”H, 24 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed avreich, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc.,
R’ Shalom Dov, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter of 17 Iyar, in which you write regarding your participation in the work of organizing the *bilti zerami* (non-affiliated) stream: My letter in response to the committee’s letter regarding my perspective on the direction of their work and the organization of this network has surely reached you by now, and their efforts are undoubtedly in this direction.

I was particularly pleased by your participation in the aforementioned. My hope is strong that not only will this not detract from your *talmud torah*, but that the promise of our Rabbeinu HaZaken (in the beginning of *Torah Or*) will be fulfilled in you: that through involvement in *tzedakah* (in material terms, and all the more so in spiritual terms), one’s mind and heart become a thousand times more refined. According to what is explained in the *hagahos* to this *drush* (printed in *Likutei Torah* for the three *parshiyos*), "a thousand times" is not an exaggeration, but literally a thousand times over. This means that in one hour, one succeeds in his learning (mind) as he would have succeeded in the usual course of a thousand hours; and likewise, in the *avodah* of *tefillah* and in *ahavas yisrael* (heart), one becomes a thousand times more refined, as mentioned above.

In these days, the eve of the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah, as related in the *Midrash Rabbah*, the guarantors for the receiving of the Torah—due to whom Hashem decided to give the Torah to His people Israel—were specifically the children. Therefore, it is obvious that involvement in the education of *tishbar* (schoolchildren) is what assists in receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness (this was the language of the blessing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, on the eves of the festival of Shavuos).

With blessings for a happy holiday and *talmud torah* with *yiras shamayim*.

***

**R’ Shalom Dov, may he live:** Lifshitz. Another letter to him — above, 198.

**My letter:** Above, 1559.

## 1,575

B"H, 24 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, engaged in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Yitzchak, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings,

Thank you for your letter from this past Erev Shabbos—which has just been received—and primarily for your involvement in the matters of Taharah and the Levayah, as you wrote in your letter and as the Shadar, Rabbi Bentzion Shemtov, may he live, also wrote to me regarding this. May it be the will of Hashem that you utilize one another for joyous matters.

One may explain, by way of a clever insight, the teaching of our Sages that one interrupts Torah study for the funeral of the dead and for the wedding of a bride (Kesuvos 17a). It is well known that the ultimate purpose of wisdom is Teshuvah and good deeds. At the receiving of the Torah, the preface was "we will do" before "we will hear." This is the meaning of interrupting Torah study for the sake of the Mitzvos, the totality of which is the "funeral of the dead"—that is, the influence of the primordial serpent that brought death into the world, even upon the elite of the human race, including those who had no sin at all—and for the "wedding of a bride," which is the drawing down of holiness, the ultimate purpose of which is the nullification and inclusion within the Essence of the Blessed One.

With this, we can also explain the precision in why, even though one moves the funeral procession aside for the bride, the order is stated: one interrupts Torah study for the wedding of a bride (and afterwards) for the funeral of the dead. Yet, the funeral is mentioned first, because that is the **order** of Avodah—"turn away from evil" and only afterwards "do good." This is unlike the **priority** when they arrive simultaneously, where the positive commandment overrides the negative commandment.

I will conclude as I began, with thanks for your efforts, as well as the efforts of the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, etc., Rabbi Yehuda Zev Segal, may he live, in all of the above. May it be the will of Hashem that we all merit to be attached to the Living G-d through the Torah of Life, which we are all preparing to receive at the time of the Giving of the Torah, may it come upon us for good, and in the phrasing of the blessing of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, may his merit protect us: with joy and with inwardness.

With the blessing of the Chag.

#### ***1,575***

Printed in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 23, p. 326, and completed based on the secretariat's copy.

**Rabbi Yitzchak:** Dubov. Additional letters to him appear above in Vol. 5, 1,510, and in the notes indicated there.

**Taharah and Levayah:** See above, note to letter 1,566.

## 1796

B"H, 24 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 16 Iyar, in which you write that the doctor told your wife, tichyeh, regarding the matter of conception, that her organism is not developed as it should be:

One should not be afraid of this, for there are hundreds and thousands of cases where doctors calculate that the organism is not developed, and yet they have children who are alive and well. In accordance with this, if the doctors provide remedies such as pills and the like—but not sharp ones—you should follow their instructions. However, do not undergo any operations or similar drastic measures. May Hashem help that at the appropriate time, which I hope is not far off, you and your wife, shichyu, will be blessed with a child who is alive and well.

It is well known—and it is already in print—the letter of Rabbeinu HaZaken in which he writes that a segulah for having children is to engage in the study that brings one to Ahavas Hashem and Yiras Hashem, which is the study of Chassidus. Therefore, you should establish a shiur in the study of Chassidus with one of your neighbors, at least three times a week (meaning that three days should not pass without studying a shiur in Chassidus). Naturally, one of these three days should be Shabbos Kodesh, and the other two days as is most convenient.

Certainly, your wife, tichyeh, should observe the good custom of Jewish daughters to give to Tzedakas Rabbi Meir Baal HaNes every time before lighting candles on Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov. And you should instruct her to be strict in observing the custom of covering her head. I hope that as both of you fulfill the above, you will be able to inform me soon of good news that your wife has conceived, so that I may convey this at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, ztzel, nbgm, zy"a.

With blessings to him and his wife, shichyu, for a happy Shavuos and to hear good tidings.

## 1757

B"H, 24 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...I was distressed to learn that in his influence regarding Chassidus at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, he makes distinctions between the students, and there are those whom he drives away from hearing the shiur, or with whom he does not take an interest, etc., etc. I am extremely surprised at him. How did he arrive at such a path? Who among us has the authority to drive a bochur or avreich away from hearing a shiur in Tanya or Chassidus? On the contrary, it is incumbent upon each and every one of us to strive with all our might to attach everyone who is even slightly capable of this, even if it requires "feeding them like an ox." As is brought in several of the Rebbe’s sichos, beginning with the Baal Shem Tov, one would go to the recipient, unlike the way of the world, etc. It is understood that this "going" is not merely a physical journey, but also a descent from one’s own level in order to draw close and clothe the concepts in terms appropriate for the recipient, who for the time being is still on a lower level than oneself.

It is difficult for me to elaborate on this matter... but the situation is painful, and my hope is that they will rectify it as much as possible. That is to say, even if there is a mere doubt—perhaps hearing the shiurim in Chassidus, Tanya, etc., might benefit a certain student—they should include him in the shiurim and take an interest in his well-being and his situation. In accordance with this, when studying maamarim and kuntresim, one should choose those that the students will be able to grasp with their human, as-yet-undeveloped intellect.

With holiday blessings.

## 1758

1758

B"H, 24 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of the 13th, in which you ask, on behalf of your son, for advice regarding the shidduch being proposed to him, as he is uncertain whether the girl’s parents will be able to assist him with significant sums of money.

My opinion on this is that since you write that she possesses virtues that are suitable for your son, this is the essential factor in a shidduch. Regarding parnassah, Hashem will help, and in all likelihood, the parents of both sides will assist, at least for the initial period—especially since you write that the girl’s parents own a factory.

You write that you are concerned about a grievance held against you by Rabbi [Name], whose daughter was proposed for your son, shlita. It is difficult for me to answer this without knowing the details—specifically, how far the shidduch had progressed. If your son did not meet with her and you did not make any promises, there is nothing to worry about. However, if your son did make any promises to her, then you must ask for her forgiveness. I am certain you will write to me with more details regarding this.

When I visit the Ohel of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, ztzk"l, nbg"m, zy"a, I will mention you, your wife, and your son, may they live, for whatever each of you is in need of.

With wishes for a joyous Yom Tov of Shavuos.

P.S. I am sure you are careful to recite Tehillim every day and also to keep up with the daily shiur of Chumash, and that your wife gives tzedakah to Rabbi Meir Baal HaNes each time before lighting candles on Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov, as I have already written to you in previous letters.

## 1579

B"H, 24 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Through the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and diligent communal worker, Rabbi Shalom Pozner, I was pleased to hear that his health has improved and that he has already returned home. With blessings for a happy holiday.

## 1880

1880

B”H, 24 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write that you do not see a sign of blessing in your learning:

Our Sages have already ruled: “If one says, ‘I have labored and found,’ believe him; [if one says] ‘I have not labored and found,’ do not believe him.” Since this is the case, it is clear that if you only learn with the appropriate *yegiah* (labor), you will certainly see a sign of blessing in your learning. This is provided that your manner of learning conforms to the administrative procedures of the *yeshiva*, so that you may hasten the arrival of blessing in this regard. May the *Ribono shel Olam* bless you in *talmud Torah* and in *yiras shamayim* with success.

With blessing.

## 1581

B"H, 24 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter of 21 Iyar, in which you write about the distress you feel regarding the older members of your shul, and it seems this is causing both you and your wife to feel discouraged. I am surprised by this, as this is a common occurrence in any matter of rabbinate or communal leadership in a living community. That is to say, among those involved in communal affairs, there are always different perspectives, and it is possible that some are not satisfied with the conduct of those managing communal matters. One should not be affected by this; to the extent possible, one should appease their minds—naturally, without compromising on essential matters or on anything that contributes to the development of the community. I am certain that you yourself will find the appropriate path to achieve the maximum benefit with the minimum amount of distress and dissatisfaction.

Regarding your question about looking into obtaining an apartment: it is appropriate to show interest in this, although it is not advisable to move to a new apartment at the beginning of the summer, but rather toward its end. May Hashem grant you success in finding the one that is suitable for you, both for the sake of your leadership of the shul and the Talmud Torah, and for the matter of the apartment itself.

Regarding what you wrote—that you intend to travel here in about a month’s time by car—you will surely travel with the appropriate caution and take rest as needed. Perhaps it would be worthwhile to stop in one or two cities along your journey and make an effort in matters of Yiddishkeit where necessary. We do not know the ways of Divine Providence, and the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, is well known: that an effort in *ta'amulah* (outreach) never returns empty-handed. Especially when this is accompanied by actual action, such planting will surely yield growth, whether immediately or after some time.

You do not mention anything regarding your health or the health of your wife, and this is surely a good sign.

I do not know if it is necessary to remind Mr. and Mrs. [Name] that their promise regarding conduct in *taharas hamishpachah* applies not only before and after the birth, but also now and for all the days of their lives. I believe this was understood simply from the tone of our conversation, but nevertheless, regarding an essential matter such as this, perhaps it is not worth leaving the matter in doubt; it should be emphasized in a diplomatic yet clear manner.

With blessings for a joyous Shavuos and for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 1,584

B”H, 25 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

With blessings for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness, for you and for all the members of the administration, may they live.

## 1585

1585

B"H, 25 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter informing me that you have begun your studies at Yeshivas Toras Emes, and requesting a blessing for success in your learning:

It is well known that our Sages ruled, "If one says, 'I have labored and I have found,' believe him." The matter is in his own hands, especially during these auspicious days of preparation for receiving the Torah. You should engrave upon your heart and mind the manner of preparation for receiving the Torah, which is *na'aseh* (we will do) and *nishma* (we will hear). Both of these aspects are present within the study of Torah itself; that is, first and foremost, one must engage in the study of Torah through *kabbalas ol* (accepting the yoke), even if one does not yet understand the necessity of the exertion of soul and body required for this. Only afterwards will one merit the *nishma*. In this manner, one receives the Torah and merits to study it with success, with *yiras shamayim*, and to arrive at the truth—as all of this is brought in many places in the teachings of Chassidus, which is the Torah of the words of the living G-d.

With blessings for success in your Torah study with *yiras shamayim*.

## 1787

1787

B"H, 26 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn

To the brilliant Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, etc.,
Rabbi Moshe Aryeh Leib, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter—albeit with some delay—and regarding what you asked of me:

1) At the beginning of Sefer HaTanya, where it explains the teaching of our Sages, "They adjure him, 'Be a tzaddik...'," the interpretation in Chassidic discourse is well-known: "adjure" (*mashbi'in*) refers to "satiety" (*sova*) (see *Kitzurim VeHe'arot LeTanya*, p. 57ff and references there. In truth, this is also the essence of the matter of "swearing" to fulfill the mitzvos, even though one is already adjured and standing from Mount Sinai). You raise the point that if this is the case, the need for the oath is not understood in light of the conclusion of that same teaching: "Even if the whole world tells you that you are a tzaddik, consider yourself a rasha."

This observation is not entirely relevant to the interpretation explained in Chassidic discourse that *mashbi'in* refers to *sova*, because even according to the literal meaning—that they adjure him with an oath—the immense significance of the instruction "consider yourself a rasha, even if the whole world tells you that you are a tzaddik" still requires explanation. Regarding the substance of your observation: there are details within the matter of what they adjure him, as the Sages state: "And know that the Holy One, Blessed be He, is pure, etc." The content of all these **secondary** matters is that they are relevant to one's *avodah*, so that he may fulfill the **essential** oath: "Be a tzaddik and do not be a rasha." Consequently, it is of the utmost importance that he does not err in the manner of his *avodah*. The *avodah* of a tzaddik and a rasha are diametrically opposed. Specifically, as explained in Tanya, the level of a tzaddik is one "whose heart is hollow within him" and who has no evil at all; thus, he has no *machshavos* of his own. Evil is repulsive to him; therefore, all his affairs are not merely a matter of "In all your ways know Him," but are matters of holiness. Consequently, the tzaddik can hold onto them and elevate them, rather than needing to push them away, etc. This is not the case for a *beinoni*, for whom the instruction "consider yourself a rasha" means that he must scrutinize all his affairs to see whether they come from the "wise heart" on his right or the "foolish heart" on his left. If there is a doubt—and this is a *safek d'oraisa* (a doubt regarding a Torah law)—it must be treated stringently. It is understood how relevant this is to almost every single action.

One should also note what is written in *Kuntres HaAvodah*, Chapter 7, regarding *avodah* that is "above one's level" and the deficiency inherent in that. Based on this, one could also resolve the question if we were to interpret the Sages' statement "even if the whole world... tells you that you are a tzaddik" literally—meaning a tzaddik in the borrowed sense, one whose merits outweigh his sins.

2) In *Iggeres HaKodesh*, Epistle 15, regarding the difference in value between the *middah* of *ahavas Hashem* of our forefather Avraham and the level of *ahavah* that is above in the supernal *Sefiros*, it is written there: "One might think... only that it is infinitely greater and more wondrous than the *middah* of our forefather Avraham, etc., but that they are nevertheless of the same type and category as the supernal *middos*." To this, it says, "And I am but dust and ashes," which is only a value and a comparison of the essence of the dust that has become ash to the essence of the wood that it was initially. You find this difficult, for the disparity in value between the *belimah* (infinite) and the *gevul* (finite) is surely greater than the wonder between the comparison of the essence of dust and the essence of a "desirable tree." If so, what is added by this?

However, the matter is clear from the precision of our Rebbe’s language. When he brings the analogy of the dust and ashes and the desirable tree, he is careful to use the term "essence" (*mahut*) in every instance. This also resolves what you noted, for the difference between *gevul* and *belimah* can be a difference in quantity, but not in quality, and certainly not in their essence. By way of example: if we speak of a drop of water versus the ocean, or an individual person versus all the generations that exist **in potential**—which is more accurate regarding the matter of *gevul* and *belimah*—or in the statement regarding the value of one angel versus its countless legions: even though this is *gevul* and *belimah*, their essence and quality are exactly the same. In this, the matter of "dust and ashes" versus the "desirable tree" is precise—for both the essence and the quality are entirely different, as he states that they have no comparison or value. This is known only from the analogy of the ashes, and not from the matter of *gevul* and *belimah*.

With blessings for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 1,588

B”H, 26 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, involved in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Mordechai Hakohen, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 17 Iyar, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed. When I am, G-d willing, at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will read it. He will surely arouse Divine mercy for all those mentioned therein, for whatever they may need, and may Hashem grant you the merit to share good news regarding this.

2) I was pleased to read in your letter about the practice of reviewing *Mishnayos* by heart. It is well known how much our Rebbes, of blessed memory, praised this, as is brought in many places in the *sichos* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. You have surely also seen what I wrote regarding my opinion on the importance of this, even according to the revealed Torah, which was published at the time in *Kovetz Lubavitch*.

3) Regarding your request for my opinion on your plan to begin studying and reviewing *Shas* by heart: I do not understand what you mean by the acronym *Shas*. If you mean the same as mentioned above regarding *Mishnayos*, then it is a very proper thing, as stated. Or, are you referring to the study of *Gemara*? It would be appropriate to review chapters of *Tanya* by heart from time to time, especially the first twelve chapters along with the introduction, as my father-in-law, the Rebbe, spoke about this in his holy *sicha* on Simchas Torah 5731 in Riga.

4) Regarding what you wrote about the *mikveh*: I am interested to know if it is maintained according to the wishes of the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory. If not, and if it is an easy matter to rectify, you should surely fix it so that it conforms to those wishes.

5) I was very distressed by what you wrote, that regarding education, nothing has been done as of yet because all the youth attend the public school. I find this surprising, for in many countries this is the law, yet they still organize additional classes—or more precisely, primary classes—where they teach the essential subjects for Jewish boys and girls, such as *dinim*, *brachos*, *Chumash* with *Rashi*, etc. As for what one of the teachers told you—that the parents do not want this—one should not use the power of "belief" in such matters. Especially since the ruling of the *Rambam* is known, cited in many places in *Chassidus*, that in the inner recesses of his heart, every Jew desires to fulfill the will of the Creator, etc. See also *Tanya*, Chapter 41 (54a), which states: "But the unification of his soul and its inclusion in the light of Hashem, to be as one, this is desired by every Jew in truth, with all his heart and all his soul, out of the natural love hidden in the heart of every Jew to cleave to Hashem, etc." *Tefillah* and *taharah* (effort) do not return empty, especially when they see that your intention is for the sake of the matter itself, without ulterior motives. I hope and await good news that you have begun this activity, at which point you will surely succeed.

6) Regarding what you write—that when you repeat *maamarim* of *Chassidus* in their original language, the listeners do not understand, and consequently there is a concern that they will not come to hear the *maamar* at all—and you ask if you should add content from *sefarim* of *drush*: Seemingly, it would be appropriate not to mix chaff with wheat. If it is necessary to expand the explanation, you can surely find suitable explanations in the *sichos* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, or in letters, stories, and the like. If even that is not enough, it is better to draw from what is spoken during *farbrengens* of Chassidim, where the "garment" (the language) will have some proportion to the "thing being clothed" (the *maamar*). This is not the case with *sefarim* of *drush*, etc., and a word to the wise is sufficient.

With blessing for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 1,189

B"H, 26 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 9 Iyar, in which you write that you are distressed by the fact that you have not received a response from me to your letters. I have already written to several of anash—may they live—that I endeavor to fulfill their requests to the best of my ability, and likewise to read their pidyon nefesh at the tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, as soon as possible. However, regarding notifying them of this, it does not depend so much on me, due to the great pressure, the distress, and the multitude of letters received. May it be the will of Hashem that I succeed in time and in my avodah to fulfill the wishes of each and every one in this regard as well. In any case, if you feel distress, there is no basis for it, for the shortcoming is not in you, but rather in the fact that I do not have enough time, etc.

2) Regarding what you wrote—that the shidduch proposals for your daughter, may she live, have ceased—and you ask for my opinion, since she will soon turn fifteen, whether to think about a shidduch for her now or to wait:

In my opinion, it is not worthwhile to hold to either of the two extremes. Rather, one should be interested in the matter, but it should be done with composure and not with haste. Surely, at the appropriate time, Hashem will show the way regarding this matter.

Likewise, regarding your question as to whether you should specifically endeavor to find a Tmim, this insistence does not seem correct to me. It is enough that the candidate be of such a nature that it is possible to make him a Tmim—meaning, that he is inclined toward setting fixed times for Torah study in both the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus, and conducting himself according to the ways and customs of Chassidim. In that case, one can hope that through the appropriate influence from your daughter and the influence of anash—may they live—he will become a Tmim.

... As you know, I have already alerted anash—may they live—in your camp that they should utilize and take advantage of the newspapers published in their country to publicize, from time to time—and especially before the holidays and festivals—matters from the teachings of Chassidus and stories of the Chassidim that are appropriate for this direction. After all, the time has finally come to push away the darkness in all corners of the world and in all its reaches, for this is the preparation and the prelude to that hoped-for day, when "the night shall shine as the day."

With blessings for an ample livelihood and success in your holy work in public affairs, and for much Yiddishe nachas and Chassidishe nachas from all your children, together with your wife—may they live—and a blessing for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 1590

1590

By the Grace of Hashem, 26 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to hear from Anash in our Holy Land that you have arrived there for a visit. I hope that you will utilize your visit to our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, in the best possible way—one hundred percent.

In my opinion, it is highly necessary that you look around and pay attention regarding a *shidduch*. You surely have friends there, and according to the expression of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that all Chassidim are like one family, there is no doubt in my mind that Anash there will assist you in this, as well as in other matters, as much as they are able. If you act in this with the proper energy, Hashem Yisbarach will help that it should be successful.

I think it is superfluous to draw your attention to the name of Eretz Yisrael, which is not only what Jews call it, but even in the entire non-Jewish world it is called the Holy Land. As it is written in the holy Torah, it is a land upon which "the eyes of Hashem your G-d are always upon it, from the beginning of the year to the end of the year." This means that no matter how close one may be to the Holy One, Blessed be He, while being outside of Eretz Yisrael, one must possess the feeling of a far greater measure of closeness to Hashem Yisbarach while being in Eretz Yisrael.

Just as someone who finds themselves in a brightly lit place closes their eyes and refuses under any circumstances to open them to convince themselves that it is indeed bright, and insists that it is dark—it is self-evident that this does not change the fact that the place is brightly lit. So too regarding Eretz Yisrael: even if the eyes of the *neshamah* are not fully open due to various reasons, this does not change the truth that it is a land upon which "the eyes of Hashem your G-d are always upon it."

Consequently, when one has the *zechus* to be even closer to the Holy One, Blessed be He, it is certain that one receives an additional strength in the *neshamah* to be able to fulfill and bring all good resolutions into actual practice in daily life. All those things that seem impossible to fulfill—when one is in Eretz Yisrael, one has the opportunity to convince oneself that it is much easier than one had previously thought. Not only does it not cause any harm, *chas v'shalom*, but on the contrary, it actually helps in all the matters one is in need of.

Self-evidently, I do not intend to deliver sermons, but rather to speak of practical matters: each of us is not perfectly complete in everything; consequently, one also lacks in certain matters of Torah and *mitzvos*. Usually, one has an *amtala*—a justification—for this, claiming that it is difficult to implement in life due to *parnassah*, neighbors, or because of one’s own body. But when one thinks into it, even for a short while, it is clear that since He, blessed be He, is the Creator of the world and also the Creator of man, and He demands this of man, He will certainly not demand things for which He—blessed be He—has not given the strength to perform. Therefore, it is clear that it depends only on the person themselves.

It is also understandable that G-d, blessed be He, who is the *tachlis hatov* (the ultimate good), will not demand of a person to do things that would cause them harm. On the contrary, when G-d, blessed be He, demands this, it is not that one is doing a favor for the *Hakadosh Baruch Hu*, for He, blessed be He, lacks nothing and does not need any favors from people. Rather, it is entirely a favor for the person themselves, so that they—the person—should reach their true happiness in both material and spiritual matters. When one conducts oneself in the manner that the *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* requires, one can truly be happy. As mentioned earlier, even when it seems difficult, it is nothing more than a *nisayon*, and with the proper approach, one overcomes it, and one is even satisfied with that *nisayon*, for after it, one's actions are much more pleasant and agreeable.

In these days, when we all, within the entirety of *Klal Yisrael*, are going to celebrate the *Yom Tov* of Shavuos, the *zman matan toraseinu*, we must all deeply engrave in our memory the cry of *Klal Yisrael* at the giving of the Torah: **"Na'aseh V'nishma."** May everyone be able to take upon themselves "Na'aseh V'nishma" today as well, which is the correct path for each one of us to arrive at a happy, good life, both materially and spiritually.

With a wish that you be successful in your affairs, and that you report good tidings regarding this.

## 1,591

1,591

B"H, 26 Iyar, 5712

## 1,192

1,192

B"H, 26 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote to me, that they are complaining that lately their businesses are struggling: it is possible that last year they reduced somewhat their giving of tzedakah for matters of Torah and yiras shamayim. Therefore, it is appropriate that from now on they increase this, and in an amount that seems to them to be beyond what is expected of them. The promise of the Ribono shel Olam is well known: "Tithe so that you may become wealthy," and regarding the mitzvah of tzedakah in particular, the Ribono shel Olam says, "And test Me, please, with this."

With holiday blessings.

## 1,593

B”H, 26 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from the 4th of Iyar in due time, and as you requested, I mentioned you and your wife—may they live—when I was at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, for whatever you are in need of.

Regarding your complaint about your spiritual state, and your feeling that any movement toward the good is only momentary, etc.: It is a well-known saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that one must not speak lashon hara about another Jew, and one must not speak it about oneself, either. It is also well-known what is explained in the maamarim of Chassidus regarding the verse "We were like dreamers" (see Torah Or, beginning of Parshas Vayeshev, and elsewhere), that even if, after a movement toward the good, one finds oneself in the opposite state, G-d forbid, it is still possible that the movement was genuine. It is like a dream, where it is possible for two opposites to be joined.

In any event, even if things are as you describe, complaining is not the solution. The solution is action—specifically, beginning with the most "simple" things, such as keeping the three daily study portions established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for every person—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya (which I am sure you are familiar with). Conclude this with the dissemination of the wellsprings—that is, influencing your surroundings so that they become a Chassidishe environment as they should be.

These are all tried and tested methods to ensure that your prayer, which stems from the depths of your heart, will be accepted: that Hashem should help you become "a completely different person." When one walks on this paved path and engages in this with personal intent—which is accessible to everyone, and furthermore, is very close, as explained in Tanya—Hashem grants success so that, in the end, one changes and is transformed, even from one essence to another.

May Hashem grant you success to share good news, that you will succeed in making your surroundings Chassidishe, and in the natural course of events, this will also be proof that you yourself are ascending to higher levels of goodness.

With blessings to receive the Torah with joy and inwardness.
