## 1,195

1,195

By the Grace of Hashem, 26 Iyar, 5712

Brooklyn.

Blessing and Peace!

I received your letter in due time, in which you write that you have become the kallah of the avreich, the G-d-fearing and esteemed [name]..., and you request a blessing that it should be in a good and auspicious hour. You also write that you are not from a Chassidic family and do not know much about the things you ought to know, but that you will attempt to learn this as soon as possible through your new relatives, may they live:

It gave me pleasure to read everything you wrote in your letter. I bless you and your chassan, may you both live, that you should set the wedding for a good time, and that it should be in a good and fortunate hour, and that you should build a home in Yisrael upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, as explained in Toras HaChassidus, according to the ways of Chassidus and the customs of Chassidus.

Regarding what you write—that you are not from a Chassidic family—you need not be afraid of this. For according to the statement of Rabbeinu HaZaken, the Baal HaTanya, Chassidus is a matter for all of Klal Yisrael. It was written and transmitted in such a way that every Jew, man and woman, can attain it and conduct their daily life according to the guidance of Toras HaChassidus. One only needs to have the desire, and then Hashem shows the paths and also provides the ability to realize this in life.

Surely you know that at the time of the Giving of the Torah, which we will be celebrating in the coming days, the Midrash relates that Hashem told Moshe Rabbeinu that he should first speak to the women about it. This is a lesson for many matters among Jews, and in particular—that when one is going to build a home, whether an individual one or a communal one, a primary responsibility lies upon the women, for they are the *akeres habayis*, the essence of the home. As one sees clearly in practice, the management of the home, the education of the sons and daughters, and even the conduct of the husband, depends upon the woman. Consequently, the woman must know the responsibility that lies upon her, and she can also be certain that since Hashem demands this, He, blessed be He, also provides the ability and the strengths to bring this into daily life.

May Hashem Yisbarach help you to establish your home and lead it as mentioned above, and may you have a joyous Yom Tov of Shavuos, and subsequently throughout the entire year, in a life of Torah and mitzvos.

In the name of the Rebbe, shlita,

The Secretary

## 1596

1596

B"H, 28 Iyar, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and diligent in communal affairs, etc.,
Moreinu HaRav Mordechai Dov, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I am writing to you in connection with the upcoming Yom Tov of Shavuos, and the days preceding and following it, regarding the need for a special awakening concerning the dissemination of Torah among *baalei batim*, and in particular among the younger generation. As is explained in the *Midrash Rabbah*, it was the children who served as the guarantors, through which Hashem decided to grant the Torah to the Jewish people. There is certainly still time to make the necessary preparations for this.

My intention here is not directed toward you alone, for you surely have influence and acquaintances in other *batei knesios* as well, especially those in the vicinity of your residence. Therefore, please see to it that they, too, utilize the days of the upcoming Shavuos for this purpose.

I thank you in advance for the good news you will report regarding this.

## 1597

1597

B"H, 1 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Oholei Yosef Yitzchak - Lubavitch
in Australia,
May they live.

Peace and blessing!

I have received with pleasure your detailed report regarding the meeting in which you propose to appoint Rabbi Shalom HaCohen Gutnick (may he live) as Rosh Yeshivah, and you ask for my opinion on the matter.

In my view, this is the correct course of action. Surely, the aforementioned will not refuse to accept this appointment, for although on one hand our Sages have said that leadership is not a position of authority but of servitude, nevertheless, since even the appointment of a manager of an irrigation ditch is decreed from Above, how much more so is this true for a Rosh Yeshivah, whose role is to influence the students with the Torah of Hashem and, primarily, to exert effort to increase their borders with good students. Since a number of Yidden have chosen him, surely they will provide him with the strength to fulfill this role as required. May the Ribono shel Olam grant him success, and grant you success, so that the number of students will increase significantly and the quality of the students will also grow.

One should not be discouraged by the fact that, as is customary in the beginning and in a new country, the number of students is currently small. As is well known, the Baal Shem Tov’s precision—as transmitted by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—regarding the verse, "Though your beginning was small, **and through this**, your end will flourish greatly." This is especially true in these days before the festival of Shavuos, the time of the giving of our Torah. As related by our Sages, the schoolchildren are the guarantors who determined the will of Hashem to give the Torah to the Jewish people. These are auspicious days to awaken these matters even now, so that one may say, "Our children are our guarantors"—the children being the students—in great numbers, both in quantity and quality.

With blessings for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness, and for success in your holy work to increase Torah and fear of Heaven.

#### ***1597***

**The Baal Shem Tov’s precision:** See above, 1559, and the references in the notes there.

## 1,599

B"H, 1 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It was with joy that I received your letter of 21 Iyar. I had already been thinking about the fact that I had not heard for a long time regarding your health and the health of your wife, *shichyu*. Thank G-d that you are already going out into the street and also to shul. As I see from your letter, the health of your wife, *tichye*, is also much better than before. Since one can see with physical eyes that Hashem has granted you health and that your wife’s health is also improving, you must be strong in your *bitachon* in Hashem, that things will continue to get better and better, until you yourself are also satisfied.

It is distressing and painful to read in your letter those "unnecessary" expressions. Why are you doing this? Especially for a believing Jew who is also capable of influencing others—when one is weak in *bitachon* in Hashem, firstly, it causes harm in *ruchniyus* and in health, and secondly, it drains the will and desire to influence others and make them more lively and courageous.

I hope that by the time you receive my letter, your mood will have changed for the better, and you will see to follow the instruction of our holy Torah: "Serve Hashem with joy." As is brought in the holy *sefarim*, one must and can serve Hashem not only through *tefillah* and Torah, but also while eating and drinking and the like, by living with joy. And then, even on a simple level, one sees oneself as healthier and more courageous, and one accomplishes much more for oneself and also for others.

I conclude with a wish that the *middah* of *bitachon* should strengthen within you as soon as possible, and that you should have a peaceful and joyous Yom Tov Shavuos, and continue this throughout the entire year.

With holiday blessings.

## 1,303

1,303

B"H, 1 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from Sunday, Parshas Bamidbar... regarding the fact that the number of students is small and you are currently seeking advice and strategies to increase their numbers:

## 1404

B"H, 2 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I have received your letters (which were delayed in the mail longer than usual) dated 4/9 and 5/2. It was with joy that I read that your wife’s delivery went well and that she has given birth to a son, whom you have named [name]—may he live and be well.

May Hashem Yisbarach help you and your wife to raise him, together with your older son—may they live and be well—for Torah, for the chuppah, and for maasim tovim, and with expanded parnassah.

In your letter, you mention your concern regarding parnassah. You should remember what is written in the holy seforim: that when a son is born, it is a sign of blessing in the home, including in the area of parnassah. In order to hasten this, one must be strong in bitachon in Hashem Yisbarach, for He, blessed be He, is the One who sustains and provides for all, and He desires to give from His full hand. Another thing to remember is that one must create vessels to receive the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach; in general, this is through the matters of Torah and mitzvos, and in particular, through giving tzedakah. If you feel a tightness in parnassah, you should give more tzedakah than before, in order to demonstrate to Hashem Yisbarach through this that you have greater needs for tzedakah; consequently, He will provide more parnassah than before. May Hashem Yisbarach help you and your wife—may you live and be well—that you both be strong in bitachon, and may you soon see the blessing of Hashem Yisbarach fulfilled with expanded parnassah.

With blessings for good health for you, your wife, and your children—may they live and be well—and a joyous Yom Tov of Shavuos.

P.S. You did not write what the money you sent was for, so I have passed it on to Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch as a good beginning for the Torah education of your newborn son, for long, good days and years.

## 1707

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Agudas Chabad, may they live,

Peace and blessing!

Enclosed is a copy of my letter to the distinguished Chossid, Rabbi... It would be good if you could provide me with your opinion on this matter. If the aforementioned individual and his wife, may they live, are suitable for managing a kindergarten, then it would be appropriate to assist them in this with a loan and other suitable support. In time, there will surely be great benefit in the existence of a kindergarten founded and conducted in accordance with the spirit of Chabad.

I am writing now regarding the primary matter—to thank you with all my heart for the arrangement of the funeral of my brother, of blessed memory, as was fitting. May it be the will of Hashem that from now on, we should only need one another for happy and healthy occasions.

With blessing—in the phrasing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness, and for success in your holy work,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1512

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter of 21 Iyar, following the long silence that caused me distress, as I did not know the clear reason for it. Thank G-d, as you write, that you and your entire household, may they live, are well. Surely, despite what you write regarding the difficulties and various obstacles you are facing, as is explained in the teachings of Chassidus, these are nothing but concealments and hiddenness intended to be overcome, to perform *iskafya* of the *sitra achra*. Through this, the glory of the *Ribono shel Olam* is revealed in all worlds. Consequently, there is no reason to be so distressed by this; on the contrary, there is room for joy, as is explained in *Tanya*, chapters 27 and 30, please refer there.

In these days of preparation for the receiving of the Torah, I conclude my letter with a blessing—in the phrasing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—that you may receive the Torah with joy and inwardness. May it be the will of Hashem that you, may you live, also illuminate your surroundings in this manner, to light them up with the "candle of a mitzvah and the light of Torah," and the "light of the Torah"—which is the teachings of Chassidus.

With holiday blessings.

## 1511

1511

B”H, 3 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chassid, G-d-fearing, and meticulous in his communal work, etc.,
R’ Nissan, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

... 2) As R’ Chaim Avraham, may he live, Chadakov, conveyed to me regarding the contents of your letter to him, it seems that until now you have not received confirmation that I received the precious gift you sent me. It is a handwritten note from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, small in quantity but immense in quality, on the maamar beginning *El Elokim Hashem*. I hereby confirm receipt of it here, with an added thank you, thank you, for your precious gift. My hope is that in time, it may be possible to publish at least some excerpts from it with a brief explanation for the benefit of the many, and the merit of the many depends on you.

3) Regarding what you wrote about the time for *pas shacharis* (the morning meal), please see the *Piskei Dinim* of the Tzemach Tzedek to *Orach Chaim*, siman 89, where his conclusion is that *pas shacharis* is after davening. However, if physicians advise that one must eat specifically early in the morning, one must certainly heed their instruction, but this is not the *pas shacharis* mentioned in the Shas. In these matters, it depends specifically on the manner of one’s avodah in davening—whether it is at length, etc. The saying of the Tzemach Tzedek is well known: "It is better to eat for the sake of davening than to daven for the sake of eating." Simply understood, it is better that he eat before davening if, through this, his davening will be more orderly, rather than eating specifically after davening and then being distracted during the avodah of davening, etc., and a word to the wise is sufficient.

4) Regarding the list of maamarim found in the notebook belonging to your relative, it would be worthwhile to endeavor to have them lend me the notebook for a period of time. They may rest assured that if it were for the purpose of returning it, I will return it. If, in any case, you cannot arrange this, perhaps you could check the maamarim and compare them—as explained in the list of maamarim you attached to your letter, and I have added to your list a maamar from the printed books—to clarify whether it is indeed the same maamar and subject matter, or if only the beginning is the same. Thank you for your efforts in this.

With blessings for proper health for you and all your household, may they live, and for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

1,712

## 1513

1513

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter in due time, in which you write regarding your state of mind and the reasoning you had concerning your plans for the future. However, you ultimately decided for the best—to remain in the yeshivah and continue your studies—and you ask for my opinion on this.

It is clear that your decision is very good and correct. It is correct not only regarding spiritual matters, but also in physical ones. We have seen this tangibly, especially in recent years, how true are the words of our Sages that a person does not know in what he will succeed. The calculations that people make—specifically the details of how to prepare oneself for one’s path in life—in the vast majority of cases do not succeed. Regarding you in particular, my opinion is clear: your success and well-being, both physically and spiritually, lie in your continuing your studies at the Tomchei Temimim yeshivah in Lod. You should absorb into your soul the spirit of Chassidus and the strength of mind—a true strength (without stubbornness, Heaven forbid)—that is so necessary for a Jewish person at all times in general, and especially in these days. The merit of your father and your grandfather is great, and may they hasten the matter in such a way that you will recognize and see your benefit in this tangibly, even with physical eyes. May Hashem grant you the merit of Torah study with fear of Heaven and with success in the simple sense: to learn a lot, to understand well, and to grasp it thoroughly and internally. This will also be the channel and the vessel for drawing down everything you need, both spiritually and physically.

With blessings for Torah study with fear of Heaven and for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

P.S. You do not mention your mother, may she live, in your letter; surely all is well with her. Please convey to her my blessing for a happy Shavuos, and that she should receive much nachas—Yiddishe nachas, Chassidishe nachas—from you, with peace of mind and peace of body together.

## 1414

B.H., 3 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter from the Shabbos of Beha'alotcha, in which you write that through... you have become acquainted with Chassidus Chabad and have begun to study Toras HaChassidus, and you request to be counted among the community of Chassidim of Chabad.

I was pleased by all that was stated above. Regarding this, it is written in the Seforim HaKedoshim that when a Yid desires to conduct himself on a good path in truth, Hashem helps him. This is especially true regarding a matter connected to Torah, concerning which it is said: "If one says, 'I have labored and found,' believe him." This applies even more so to Toras HaChassidus, for in our current times of this double and redoubled galus, matters that lead to Ahavas Hashem, Yiras Hashem, and to "serve Hashem with joy"—all of which are the foundations of Toras HaChassidus—are very necessary.

I hope that in accordance with the instruction of our Sages, who said that "we elevate in matters of holiness... and whoever adds, they add to him," you will also increase your shiurim in Torah in general and in Toras HaChassidus in particular. You should also see to it that you participate in Chassidishe gatherings—both gatherings for study and a farbrengen of Chassidim—which should strengthen Ahavas Yisrael, Ahavas HaTorah, and Ahavas Hashem. All of this will give you an added vitality in Torah, avodah, and gemilus chasadim.

Surely you know about the three daily shiurim that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, instituted for all Yidden—the daily shiurim of Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—and you should maintain them.

With blessings to receive the Torah with joy and in an internalized manner.

## 1,515

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received a *pidyon nefesh* on your behalf, in which you write that you are not feeling well in health, suffering from headaches and the like.

When I am at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zi"e*, I will mention you for good health. Since this usually stems from overthinking and nerves, you must strengthen yourself in your *bitachon* in the Creator, *baruch Hu*, who created and directs the world—that He, *baruch Hu*, also directs your affairs. Consequently, you need not overthink, for He will certainly lead you to the good and grant you an improvement in your health as well. The more you strengthen yourself in your *bitachon* in *Hashem Yisbarach*, the faster this will come about.

It goes without saying that you must maintain your conduct in the ways of *Torah* and *mitzvos*, and increase in this—meaning, increase the amounts of *tzedakah* you have been giving until now, recite a *kapitel Tehillim* every day, and before going to sleep, recite the *parsha* of *Krias Shema*. It would also be good for you to have the *mezuzos* in your home checked to see if they are all *kosher*.

Awaiting good news that you are feeling better and that things are progressing even further, and I wish you a joyous *Yom Tov* of *Shavuos*.

On behalf of the Rebbe, *shlita*,

The Secretary

## 1517

B.H., 3 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned man, who occupies himself with communal needs, etc.,
R' Michael, may he live, Shaliach.

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter from 3 Sivan:

1) As is apparent from your letter, you are harboring an unfounded fear that there is someone who wishes to close, or at least weaken, the Yeshiva in Meknes. This concern has no basis. While for several reasons—including the reason you mention in your letter—it is necessary to have an institution under the auspices of Lubavitch in Casablanca (a place where tourists and representatives of various institutions from the USA, Eretz Yisrael, and Europe arrive, etc.), the highest-level institution—meaning the primary Yeshiva—must remain in Meknes due to the conditions of the location. This will be the role of the institution in Meknes. May it be G-d’s will that it be strengthened in yiras shamayim; for that which is good, there is no limit, and consequently, according to one’s yiras shamayim, one nullifies the fear of flesh and blood.

2) Regarding what you wrote that there are places where the efforts to exempt [children] from public schools on Shabbos have ceased: you are a friend who does not provide further details on this, and surely the information will reach me regarding this—as you write in your letter—from R' Shlomo, may he live.

3) Regarding your question as to whether, during the vacation period when they establish "Beis Rivkah," they should also institute secular studies: in my opinion, since there is the specific argument that this is a vacation period and a new institution, and consequently one should not increase expenses, they should begin with kodesh studies only. In the course of time, etc., and during the summer months, they will be able to clarify the matter properly—whether secular studies are necessary or not. But in any case, do not begin with it, because in matters such as these, it will be difficult to cancel it later, even if they should want to...

6) I am interested in knowing more specifically regarding the mikvaos of the Sephardim, whether they follow any specific leniencies that are not accepted by us (regarding the construction of the mikveh and its method)...

7) Regarding your question as to whether to provide the sum of 14,000 to repair the mikveh in the village: in general, it is not advisable to establish a precedent where we take upon ourselves **all** the expenses for any matter that arises in a city or village. In every single matter, the local residents must also participate in the expenses. Rather, in every place, according to its circumstances, one should determine the percentage (procenten) that we take upon ourselves, and the portion that the local residents must provide...

9) I hope that by these days, the Shluchim of the young scholar, the esteemed Rabbi, G-d-fearing and learned man, R' Shalom Haskind, may he live, have arrived in your country. In accordance with my previous letter, they should utilize his stay in Morocco in the most active way to elevate the spirit of the students in the Yeshiva and to strengthen their hiskashrus to Toras HaChassidus, the ways of Chassidus, and the customs of Chassidus.

10) Surely you will continue to write in detail regarding all matters in the future, and our Sages have already said that one should not be brief where it is required to be lengthy.

With the blessing for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness, and for success in your holy work.

***

**R' Michael:** Lipsker. Additional letters to him—see above 1447, and the references in the notes there.

**R' Shlomo:** R' Shlomo Matosov, may he live.

**My letter:** Cited above 1446.

## 1519

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your two letters in due time, in which you also write regarding the state of your health. It appears from them that your state of mind is not as it should be. It is proper that your heart be confident in Hashem, the Healer of all flesh who performs wonders, that He will send His word and heal you. And although, in addition to this, one must create vessels through natural means—namely, to follow the instructions of the doctors—there is a distinction to be made between the two: In matters of medicine, you should engage only your faculty of action. This is not the case with your faculty of thought and contemplation; since you are not a doctor, and you have a portion in the study of Torah, you must utilize these faculties only for matters of Torah and mitzvos. The *shakla v'tarya* and *pilpul* regarding medical matters do not pertain to you. Consequently, it is a waste of the time you dedicate to this. Since you are expending the power of your intellect in the field of medical science, surely you were given that power to use in another field (which, in my opinion, is the study of Torah, etc.). Thus, there is a deficiency there, and the loss is twofold: a deficiency in one place and a waste in the other. Through contemplation, even for a brief moment, on all of this, your heart will surely rejoice that Hashem has privileged you to be able to engage in Torah. You will add strength in this, and you will illuminate your "four cubits," in the manner of the ruling of our Sages that the entire city is like his four cubits. You will illuminate them with the "candle of mitzvah" and "Torah is light," and the light of Torah—this is the study of Chassidus.

With blessings for proper health for you, for your wife and your household—may they live—and for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 1,021

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 22 Iyar, I was pleased to read that you are striving to influence your surroundings in the army regarding matters of yiras shamayim. You will surely strengthen yourself and add courage in this for the days to come. The measure of good is greater than the measure of retribution; for if our Sages of blessed memory said that in the footsteps of Moshiach there is no day whose curse is not greater than the one before it, then certainly, all the more so, one must increase more and more in drawing down blessing each and every day—not only to nullify the curse, Heaven forbid, but to add light and vitality and to hasten the end of our exile, each person according to their ability.

Regarding what you write—that you feel that your words do not come from the heart, etc.—know that: 1) It is a well-known saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that it is forbidden to speak lashon hara about any of the Bnei Yisrael, and consequently, this applies to oneself as well. 2) Even if your claim were true, your surroundings and those you influence are not obligated to suffer and be deprived because of this. The damage you cause yourself through this [self-criticism] is enough, without adding to it the loss of others. Therefore, Heaven forbid that you should stop your efforts and the words of hisorerus that you speak. On the contrary, you should add further explanation in this, as mentioned above. However, at the same time, you must exert yourself in ways appropriate to your nefesh habehamis and your physical body. A person knows their own situation and standing, at least to some extent, and consequently, you will be able to find active means to achieve the necessary goal. Relying on the ruling of our Sages, "I have labored and found, believe it," you will surely succeed in this, especially since the merit of the many whom you awaken to Torah and mitzvos will assist you.

Let this be your comfort in your situation, relying on the explanation of the Rambam brought in many places in Chassidus: that in essence, every Jewish person desires to fulfill the will of Hashem, but their yetzer hara fights them and sometimes forces them not to behave as they should. See also Tanya, Chapter 41 (58a), which states: "But the unification of his soul and its inclusion in the light of Hashem, to be as one—in this, every person of Israel desires in absolute truth, with all their heart and all their soul, out of the natural love hidden in the heart of every Jew to cleave to Hashem." This is what pertains to our matter. I await good news that you are continuing your avodah to bring the hearts of the Jewish people to their Father in Heaven, and that you are also gradually feeling an improvement in your own situation.

In accordance with all the above, the answer to your question regarding whether to continue your position in the rabbinate is also understood: you should certainly continue in this, and strive with greater vigor in good deeds, and with the appropriate effort, you will surely succeed...

With blessings for receiving the Torah with joy and inwardness.

## 1,222

B"H, 3 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Kolel Chabad,
May they live,

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter of 17 Iyar, in which you inform me of the expansion and development of the "Gemach Keren Nachum Dov Denberg" project under the auspices of Kolel Chabad, and that you have selected an expanded board of directors: May it be the will of Hashem that your work from this point forward continue with success—success both for the project itself and for the borrowers. As our Sages of blessed memory said, Gemach is greater than Tzedakah, for Gemach is also for the wealthy. Surely you are paying special attention to assisting in cases where you can help the borrower establish a permanent source of livelihood; in such instances, it is worthwhile to waive some of the project’s requirements from the borrower, provided that the assistance enables the person to become self-supporting.

The great value of Gemach is also understood from the fact that of the three Patriarchs—where Avraham is the line of Gemach, Yitzchak is the line of Avodah, and Yaakov is "dwelling in tents," representing the Written Torah and the Oral Torah—the first among them is the matter of Gemach, Avraham, the greatest of the giants. May it be the will of Hashem that by clinging to His ways—"Just as He is compassionate, so too shall you be compassionate"—we will merit to receive the Torah, the Torah of kindness, with joy and inwardness.

With blessings for success in your holy work.

## 1,223

[3 Sivan 5712]

**Page 2b.** Regarding the age of eighteen for marriage, if they are complete, and similar to the age of five for Scripture, which the Rambam explains as age six — see Hilchos Talmud Torah by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, Chapter 1, Kuntres Acharon, subsection 1, at the end.

**Page 4a.** Regarding the permissibility of delaying, and if there is a set time, he discusses this at length in the aforementioned Hilchos Talmud Torah, beginning of Chapter 3 in the Kuntres Acharon; see there.

**Page 7a.** Regarding one who has children, whether he may sell a Sefer Torah to marry a woman who has children: in the Piskei Din of the Tzemach Tzedek, Chiddushim to Yevamos (61b), the primary conclusion appears to be that he must sell.

**Page 133b.** Regarding the law of one who was impregnated by a spirit (*ruach*): the Tzemach Tzedek, in his Piskei Din to Yevamos 59, is of the opinion that even in a case of willful transgression, she is permitted to her husband in such an instance.

**Page 104b.** Regarding the matter of *petzu'a daka* (crushed) spelled with an *alef*. In addition to what is written in Otzar HaPoskim there, and in the notes on page 168, end of column 2, transcribed below is what is found in the library of manuscripts of Mr. Sassoon in London:

a) The Tanach of the Rashba, by a scribe who wrote the Tanach for the grandson of the Rashba, namely Astruc ben Yitzchak ben HaRashba. In this manuscript, **daka** is written with an *alef*.

b) In a Tanach manuscript written in the actual handwriting of the student of the Rashba, R. Shem Tov ben Gaon, author of the book *Migdal Oz* on the Rambam, it was written **dakeh** with a *heh*, and subsequently R. Shem Tov himself erased it and corrected it in his own hand to **daka** with an *alef*.

c) In a very, very ancient Tanach, the Damascus Chumash, which was written eleven hundred years ago, described in *Ohel David*, pages 22–23, it is written there **daka** with an *alef*.

d) In a Chumash manuscript written five hundred years ago (number 516), see *Ohel David*, page 21, it is written **daka** with an *alef*.

e) In a Tanach manuscript (number 9) written five hundred years ago, see *Ohel David*, page 15, it is written **daka** with an *alef*.

f) In a Yemenite Chumash manuscript, written five hundred years ago (number 942), see *Ohel David*, page 607, it is written **daka** with an *alef*.

g) In the Plantin and Bomberg printings of the year 5326, **daka** with an *alef*.

#### 1,223

Published in *Otzar HaPoskim*, Even HaEzer, Vol. 1 (Jerusalem 5722), p. 340 (Notes to the aforementioned book).

*Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 24, p. 454.

**Regarding *petzu'a daka*:** See below, Letter 1,268. See also above, Vol. 4, Letter 1,093.

## 1125

1125

B"H, 10 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter dated Tuesday, the first day of Hagbalah. I had already been concerned by the long gap in receiving your letters, but thank G-d, all is well, and it seems there was no particular reason for the delay.

2) I read with sorrow in your letter that there is little hope for increasing support for our institutions. May Hashem help that there be an expansion in resources, for thank G-d, we are seeing extraordinary success—where with every dollar we obtain, we are achieving much more than until now. (This matter is understood based on what is written in Iggeres HaKodesh, Epistle 27, and its explanation, that a *tzaddik* who has departed is found **more** [in this world] etc., and consequently, the success must also be **more**. There is an additional reason for this based on the teaching of our Sages that Hashem prepares the remedy before the ailment; since the needs are constantly growing while the active forces have diminished, it is necessary to compensate for this with success.) May Hashem provide from His abundance, far beyond the **essential**, for the future as well. This is in accordance with the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe: One should be *zoche* to be among those to whom Hashem gives the expenses for the entire week on the first day of the week, and not, G-d forbid, among those to whom they give the expenses for the previous week on Erev Shabbos.

7) Thank you for your expression of condolences. You are correct in writing that I acted according to the ruling of the later authorities who hold that one should begin the mourning period from the moment the news is received (so as not to be prohibited from wearing *tefillin*, etc., for several days). Although my heart hesitated regarding this—since the opinion of the Alter Rebbe is not so, as written in Shulchan Aruch Orach Chayim, beginning of section 72—I was lenient in this regard by relying on a forced interpretation, as the language of the Alter Rebbe is "and the custom is," rather than the language of a definitive *psak*. Since the matter was placed upon my shoulders in place of the departed, I relied on the *Sefer Kol Bo* by Rabbi Grunwald, who cites this ruling in the name of Rabbi Refael Shapiro and the *Maharsham*, Vol. 2, beginning of section 2, and not like the *Netziv* in his book *Meshiv Davar*. This is also brought in *Sdei Chemed*, p. 73456*. I later saw in the notes to the aforementioned *Kol Bo*, Chapter 4, paragraph 26, that he cites from the *Responsa Teshuvah Shleimah* from the *Chidushei Torah* of Rabbi Epstein (of St. Louis), who innovates there that this matter depends on the dispute as to whether one counts "distant news" from the day of death or from the day of burial (when it occurred several days after the death). Since we heard an explicit instruction from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, to count from the day of death, this is also support for the aforementioned practice of observing mourning upon receiving the news.

Incidentally, I am in doubt regarding the practice of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, during the *shivah* after his mother, the Rabbanit, *a"h*, as he was called to the Torah even on weekdays and at Mincha on Shabbos—meaning, even those *aliyos* that he would not have been accustomed to take were it not for the mourning. I did not find a reason for this, and consequently, my heart did not allow me to act in such a manner, and I did not go up to the Torah except on Shabbos, as is the known *psak* of Rabbeinu Tam in this regard.

8) Enclosed is a copy of the *Reshimah* from 19 Iyar, which may interest you. May Hashem grant each of us the merit to bear only good tidings. With blessings and respect.

#### ***1125***

**Condolences:** See the note to letter 1166 above.

**In *Sefer Kol Bo*:** P. 118 and p. 269.

*) A different opinion of the *Shevet Sofer*, section 6, is that one is neither an *onen* nor a mourner at all. As of now, I have not found anyone who shares this view.

## 1,206

1,206

B"H, 10 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Rosh Chodesh Sivan, in which you share the good news that you have entered the second month of your pregnancy: As I surely spoke about with your father, shlita, when he was here, it is best not to publicize this, as per the expression of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, until you enter the fifth month. My suggestions are:

a) You should certainly follow the instructions of the doctors—those whom you have visited and who know your history—regarding eating and drinking, avoiding excessive exertion, etc.

b) You should have all the mezuzos in your home checked, and replace any that are not kosher with ones that are.

c) You should maintain the good custom of the daughters of Israel to set aside tzedakah for the charity of Rabbi Meir Baal HaNes—Rambae"n—before lighting candles on Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov.

d) Your husband, the Rav, shlita, should strengthen himself to keep up the daily Tehillim shiur (as divided by the days of the month) at least until after the birth, in a good and auspicious hour. Furthermore, when saying the Krias Shema al Hamitah, before the blessing of Hamapil, he should recite the chapter of Tehillim: "Lamnatzeach Yaancha..." and after finishing it, he should recite the verse "Yaancha..." once more, and contemplate that all the kavanos that are required during this act should be considered by Hashem as if he had intended them. May Hashem grant that your pregnancy be easy and be completed in its proper time, and may you give birth to a healthy child in the proper manner, in its time and with ease.

With blessings.

## 1,528

1,528

B"H, 11 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I have been informed by your wife, may she live, regarding your stay in the hospital and the state of your health.

I was distressed to hear that you are feeling downhearted. It is a great wonder to me, for it is surely superfluous to explain to someone like yourself the quality of *bitachon*, especially since you are among those who have seen the miracles of Hashem openly and with physical eyes, and who know that the *Ribono shel Olam* is the healer of all flesh and performs wonders. Thus, this is a wonder upon a wonder.

If you would consider my words, you will cease to dwell on matters of your medical condition. Your heart should be steadfast and trusting in Hashem that He will send you a speedy recovery, and you should firmly resolve that there is no basis whatsoever to feel "down on yourself" (*arapgefallen ba zich*), *chas v'shalom*.

While it is necessary to create vessels through the natural order—meaning, to follow the instructions of the doctors—one must distinguish between these two things: regarding medical matters, you should engage only your faculty of action. However, your faculty of thought and contemplation should not be involved, for you are not a doctor. Since you have a share in the study of Torah, you must utilize these powers only for matters of Torah and *mitzvos*. The *shakla v'tarya* and *pilpul* regarding medical matters do not pertain to you; consequently, it is a waste of time to invest effort in them. Since your intellectual power is superfluous in the profession of medicine, it has surely been granted to you to be used in another field (which, in my opinion, is the study of Torah, etc.), and thus, it is lacking there. The result is a double loss: a deficiency in one place and a superfluity in the other.

By contemplating all of this even for a short while, your heart will rejoice that Hashem has privileged you to be able to engage in Torah. You will add strength in this, and you will illuminate your "four cubits"—in accordance with the ruling of our Sages that the entire city is considered one’s "four cubits"—and you will illuminate them with the candle of *mitzvah* and the light of Torah, and the "light" within Torah, which is the study of Chassidus.

I hope that these words of mine will be accepted by you, and that you will engrave upon your heart the command of the Baal Shem Tov on the verse, "Serve Hashem **with joy**."

With blessings for true health, and awaiting good news.

#### ***1,528***

**Regarding medical matters:** See also above, Letter 1,519.

**Command... with joy:** See above, Vol. 5, Letters 1,362, 1,380. Below, 1,555.

## 1,129

B"H, 12 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, engaged in communal needs, etc.,
Moreinu Harav Shlomo Chaim, may he live, Shaliach.

Peace and blessing!

Following my letter which you have surely already received, please be so kind as to inform me of the details also...

2) Regarding what has been decided concerning the study of *poskim* and, in general, study for *hora'ah* (rabbinic ordination) or for the craft of *shechitah*: Seemingly, as it appears from the list, the oldest in their class is twenty-one years old, and most are twenty. If so, what is the rush to study for *hora'ah* before they have studied *Gemara, Pshat, and Tosafos* for a few years? Perhaps, given the conditions in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, this is necessary. You will surely provide further information on this.

3) In response to your question as to whether studying in the *zal* (study hall) for a year and a half is sufficient for transitioning to independent study (*far zich*): Generally, this is a sufficient amount of time. It is understood that there are exceptions based on one’s talents—at both extremes: those for whom even a year is sufficient, and those who require more than a year and a half. But in general, it is as stated above: the students must know that the standard time is a year and a half, and only through extra effort can the time be shortened. Anyone who remains longer is an indication that he is not utilizing his talents as he should.

4) I have already stated to several of the Yeshiva administrators that just as those tasked with the responsibility of providing for financial matters do not wait to be urged to search for and increase resources, this is all the more necessary regarding the "increase of persons"—that is, the students—both in quantity (the number of students) and in quality. The main thing is the quantity of students, as is known from our Sages, of blessed memory, that in order for one hundred to emerge for *Mishnah*, etc., one thousand must enter for *Mikra*. Aside from the fact that this is more necessary than searching for funds—for a Yeshiva’s ultimate purpose is spirituality, and spirituality precedes physicality—there is an additional point: increasing the number of students draws down from Above an increase in the resources allocated for this Yeshiva and educational institution. Then, when one searches below through natural means for ways to increase resources, there is something to draw down. This is not the case if nothing is being added from Above; what good will the effort to increase resources do, since there is nothing to draw down? This is similar to what is explained in many places in *Chassidus* regarding *parnassah*: that vessels larger than the measure do not help, and consequently, they only cause confusion, etc.

For the class that studies *Chassidus* only on Shabbos—it is worthwhile to add this study on weekdays as well, at least once.

With blessings for success in your holy work.

## 1,331

1,331

B”H, 12 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Through the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, who is involved in communal needs, R’ Yosef Weinberg, I have received your question regarding your desire to build an apartment house on the vacant lot you own. Your question is whether you should sell half the lot and use the funds to build the house, or take on a partner, or wait until the general economic situation improves, at which point it will be easier for you to obtain financing for the construction.

My opinion on this is that if the prices of vacant lots have not fallen at this time, it would be worthwhile to sell half of the vacant lot and use that money to build on the other half. In any case, do not enter into a partnership.

In general, the idea of building a house is a sound one. However, in order for it to be successful both materially and spiritually, my opinion is that simultaneously with beginning the construction of the apartment house, you should also contribute funds toward building rooms or a portion of a house in Kfar Chabad or Lod, in our Holy Land, where there are Chassidim who have been saved from Poland and Russia and lack the means to build the dwellings they need in order to live, learn, and daven. May Hashem help you so that the construction of this apartment house, as well as the rooms and houses for the refugees in Kfar Chabad or Lod in our Holy Land, should both take place at a good and auspicious time, in all details, for you.

Rabbi Weinberg does not mention your health, and therefore I hope that it is satisfactory. May Hashem help you to be able to continue your good deeds for Torah and mitzvos, and to an even greater extent than until now.

With blessings for success.

## 1332

1332

This shows that to ensure the eternity of the Torah, Jewish women must fulfill their duty with heart and soul.

This is especially important in the matter of Taharas HaMishpacha, which is one of the main pillars of the existence of the entire Jewish people, and one of the conditions for the *Hashraas HaShechinah* in Israel, which requires *kedushah* and *taharah* ("and it shall be a holy camp").

Although your endeavor is local, it is, as mentioned above, a matter that concerns the entire *Klal Yisrael*. Therefore, I wish to participate with a symbolic contribution, and enclosed is a check for this holy purpose.

With blessings for success.

## 1,733

B”H, 12 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn

Blessings and peace!

I was distressed to hear of the panic and the running to doctors throughout the entire day for something that has no basis. It is also surprising that her husband, the Rav, may he live, allows this—why and for what reason are they utilizing the trait of *zerizus* (diligence) where it is not needed? While *zerizus* is generally a virtue, apart from the fact that panic is a shortcoming in any case, *zerizus* is not appropriate in every situation. They should be confident in Hashem, who brings into being, sustains, and gives life to the entire world and all that fills it, and especially to every single man and woman of Israel, His close ones, that He will send her true health. Together with her husband, the Rav, may he live, they will raise their son, may he live, to Torah, to the *chuppah*, and to good deeds.

Although for every matter one must also use a vessel in the natural way—that is, to ask the opinion of a doctor and follow his instructions—the obsession with this, the hair-splitting, the back-and-forth regarding the doctors' opinions, and the deep immersion in medical science and its details—this is not a matter for anyone except those whose livelihood depends on it, so that they may perform their work faithfully according to the Torah’s command, "and he shall surely heal." But as for others, they should use their intellect and their power of understanding and knowledge with which Hashem has gifted them, whether in matters of Torah and *mitzvos* or in mundane affairs that can be transformed into a matter of *mitzvah*.

However, worry and melancholy are nothing but things that damage health—both physical health and spiritual health—and they distract and confuse them from fulfilling their role and mission in this world. May Hashem grant her and her husband, the Rav, may he live, the traits of the "hasty people" (*am paziza*) regarding matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, and [the traits of] patience and composure in their other affairs. May it be for success in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings for true health.

## 1334

1334

B"H, 12 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Through the esteemed *chossid*, dedicated to communal needs, etc., Rabbi Menachem Zev *sheyichyeh* Halperin, I received your regards. He also writes to me that you are preparing to move into a new home in these days. May Hashem help you that in this new home, all members of your household may strengthen themselves with fresh energy in all matters of Torah, *mitzvos*, and *yiras shamayim*. And if the neighborhood is not as observant as your previous one, may your home be the center from which the *ner mitzvah v’Torah ohr*—and the light of the light of Torah, which is the *pnimiyus haTorah*—spreads throughout the area.

Rabbi Halperin *sheyichyeh* also writes to me that your son... *sheyichyeh* is becoming a Bar Mitzvah on 15 Tammuz, and that for a certain reason, you wish to hold the celebration next week. I would like to wish you that you should derive much *nachas* from him—*Yiddishe nachas*. Among Jews, one cannot exist without the other; if one desires *nachas*, it must be *Yiddishe nachas*, and then one has a complete son, both *b’gashmius* and *b’ruchnius*.

There are many parents who ask: from where will their children draw the strength to withstand all the *nisyonos* and difficulties that a Jew encounters in this world?

The answer to this is: a) There is no choice. Since every person—whether a son or a daughter—who is born a Jew possesses the *zechus* and the strengths that belong to a Jew, they cannot change this. The only choice is to conduct themselves as Jews ought to conduct themselves, and then they are happy, *b’gashmius* and *b’ruchnius*. b) *Maaseh avos siman labanim*. The first Bar Mitzvah mentioned in the Torah is that of the only son of a Jew, Yitzchak ben Avraham. The *Midrash* relates that since Avraham was a king in those days, the kings of that generation were present at the Bar Mitzvah celebration, among them Og, King of Bashan. The latter mocked the entire spectacle, saying: "What significance does an only son of an old father and mother have, whom I could crush with my finger, *chas v'shalom*?" We all know the end of the story: from Yitzchak emerged the *Am Yisrael*, and it was into the hands of his—Yitzchak’s—descendants that this very Og, King of Bashan, fell, and it was from them that he met his downfall.

The *Midrash* does not relate this story merely for the sake of history, for the *Midrash* is not a history book; rather, it is a part of Torah. And since Torah is the *mein*—the source, the *limud* (learning), and the *hora'ah* (a path in life)—this narrative teaches us that even when one is no more than an only Jewish son, and the surroundings are hostile kings, there is nevertheless **complete** assurance that when the son is raised in the *derech haTorah v’hamitzvos*—which is the source of strength and steadfastness for all Jews, without distinction—then there is no one who can hinder him on the path of health and happiness. For he is connected—through Torah and *mitzvos*—with *Hakadosh Baruch Hu*, who is the absolute *Baal HaBayis* of the entire world and everything the world possesses. May Hashem grant you and your wife *shichyu* the merit to educate your son, the Bar Mitzvah, in the spirit mentioned above, and then he will grow up to be a healthy, happy Jew.

With blessings.

## 1535

1535

B"H, 12 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...You ask in your letter whether it is possible to change the order in some of the classes, so that they first study secular subjects and afterwards study holy subjects:

Surely you are aware of the extent to which this is contrary to the entire system of the Tomchei Temimim Yeshivos, as established and directed by its founder, and contrary to the entire concept of secular studies within the Yeshiva. I am not familiar with the progression of events, nor in what manner this was agreed upon—whether there was a change where they bypassed the instruction, not by way of transition but by way of *hislabshus* (garbing), as is known the difference between transition and *hislabshus* (and even in this, in the second manner of the concept of *hislabshus*). However, in any case, this entire matter of such study is only due to necessity and duress. It is therefore understood that there is no need to make any change in the opposite direction, since even regarding the current situation one must remain in distress. Especially when the change comes to alter an established order that has already been practiced in such a manner for several years, and to change it to a worse state. Furthermore, it is certain that this change would become known in all the other branches, and it is impossible to estimate in advance all the consequences of this. From all the above, my opinion on your question is clear: if there is room for effort to change, they should instead be strengthening the matter even more than now, and not the opposite.

And in order that it be easier for you to *durchgein* (persevere) and to act, both within yourself and with the *baalei batim*: imagine for yourself, as all the Jewish people who are believers, that we too have the hope that every single day Moshiach Tzidkeinu will come and take us out of exile, both physically and, consequently, also from the exile in spirituality. Then, picture for yourself that if you had made the aforementioned change—and furthermore, consider that for about ten years you stood the test, despite all the difficulties, concealments, and hiddenness, and the expenses involved—*hat er durchgetragen* (he carried through) that holy studies came first and foremost. And at the very last moment, before the liberation from the concealments and hiddenness, the situation was, G-d forbid, turned upside down. And upon his emergence with those he influenced from the exile, his institution is recorded among those where they first study A-B-C, and only afterwards—*lehavdil*—Aleph, the *Alufo Shel Olam* (Master of the World); Yud above, Yud—each and every one of the sons and daughters of Israel below; and the line connecting them—is the line of *Seder Hishtalshelus*, the line of Torah and Mitzvos, through which Yisrael and Kudsha Brich Hu are all one.

With blessings for success in your holy work, and that the matter be accepted by you easily, and not only from the side of the *nefesh ha'elokis* but also from the *nefesh habehamis*.

#### ***1535***

**That they first study secular subjects:** See *Igros Kodesh* of the Rebbe Rayatz, Vol. 2, Letter 527, and the references in the notes there.

## 1336

1336

B"H, 12 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your special delivery letter in which you describe the visit with your daughter, shetichyeh, to the doctor, and that he suggested performing various tests in order to determine to which category she belongs, and you also describe those categories. As is evident from the tone of your writing, you have been caused much distress, and you ask my opinion regarding performing these tests:

In my opinion, I see no difference in the upbringing of your daughter regardless of what the tests might show. Since this brings no benefit, and even to the extent that the tests might be harmless, they are performed using electricity near the head and the like, so it is difficult to predict whether this might not cause harm, chas v’shalom. Such things should only be done when one is forced to do so, especially since all these tests are not yet a certain proof, as it is only a few years that they have been developed, and they are still largely groping in the dark. You should also take into account that you yourself have seen that the doctors were incorrect regarding your daughter, and there is an improvement in her greater than what was anticipated, and it is certain that this will continue further. Consequently, I do not know why you should lose money and exert yourselves regarding tests that are of no use and, in the best case, are nothing more than a potential harm.

Regarding the doctor’s suggestion to place your daughter in a chair, etc., my opinion is that in all these matters, when there is an agreement on this from two doctors, one may rely on it. May Hashem Yisbarach give the doctors the correct insight for the proper treatment for your daughter, shetichyeh, and may the doctors utilize the power that the Torah has given them to heal; regarding anything else, they are not the masters. When one hears a harsh word from a doctor, one should pay no attention to it, and one should accept it as nothing more than a test from Hashem, as He, blessed be He, wishes to test you and your husband, the Rav, sheyichyu, in your emunah and bitachon in the power of Hashem. The more you strengthen yourselves in your bitachon in Hashem, the sooner you will see with your physical eyes the improvement in your daughter’s health. May Hashem Yisbarach help you and your husband, the Rav, sheyichyu, that all of this should come about very soon.

I believe it is unnecessary to repeat what I have already written, that to the extent possible, you should take part in the preparations required for a Chassidishe farbrengen taking place in your city. This will also be a sign that you are certain of Hashem’s help, that He will surely gladden your hearts and the heart of your husband, the Rav, sheyichyu.

With blessings for much nachas from your daughter, together with her husband, the Rav, sheyichyu.

## 1,338

B"H, 16 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It was with great sorrow that I read your letter of 2 Sivan, in which you write to me regarding... [the departed], may he rest in peace. Surely, in the meantime, you have received my letter of consolation, and may Hashem help that from here on we may only be able to share good news with one another.

It is also distressing to read in your letter that there are those who blame certain individuals for the tragedy, may Hashem spare us. Naturally, this cannot help but affect the relationship between one person and another. Surely you know, and it is easy to understand even through human intellect, that such a matter has no basis whatsoever, for the entire world is guided by **Hashem**, and a Jew has free choice only over himself. He cannot influence matters that belong to another, even in small things, and certainly not in matters concerning life and death. See *Iggeres HaKodesh* by our Alter Rebbe, Epistle 25. I am confident that this was written only in a moment of grief, but afterward, no impression of it will remain—not only in action and speech, but even in thought.

Regarding what you write about the *tichel* that he tried to discuss, and that she did not want to wear it, with force and noise, G-d forbid—that is not the way. On the contrary, it should be done with gentleness, simply explaining that this is a matter that brings success to her, to her husband, and to their children, may they live, directly from Hashem. If so, what is the weight of the difficulty (even if there is difficulty) in wearing a *tichel* compared to what Hashem gives in return for it? If the matter is settled (*apgeleigt*) in the mind of the speaker with simplicity, then these become words that come from the heart. After all, the conversation is with children of Israel who have seen miracles with their own eyes, through *hashgacha pratis*. Therefore, there is no doubt that, in the end, it will be effective. Moreover, in time, they will be grateful to those who helped set them on the straight path. I hope that, first and foremost, he will influence himself, so that it will be simple for him; consequently, his speech will be warmer. May Hashem grant him the appropriate words, in peace and gentleness, and with *nachas* and love.

I am also distressed by the situation of the Yeshiva—not because the number of students is currently small, as you write in your letter, but because there is division among some of *anash* who are there. They should have been united with one another to fulfill their *shlichus* in the light of Torah; instead, there has arisen a matter of conflict and friction—*reibenish*—and so on. I have written about this to some of *anash*, and I hope that in the near future you will all unite and see that everything will be as it should be. Through this, success will be drawn down in all general matters, and in private matters as well.

With blessings.

## 1339

B"H, 16 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Refael Nachman, may he live, HaKohen

Peace and blessing!

I received with pleasure your previous letter from Erev Shavuos, in which you inform me that you have moved into your new apartment. May it be the will of Hashem that this change of place brings a change of fortune for the good, both in proper health and in all other matters you require. I hope to Hashem that you will be able to inform me of good news regarding this.

2) It is surprising that you do not mention anything about the arrangements made at the Yeshiva in Tel Aviv, as I am sure you have received an increase and that the studies are proceeding as they should. I have already said many times that when one increases the number of students below, one also increases from above the attainment of the physical means required. I await good news that Hashem has expanded their borders with good students who are successful in their Torah study and in yiras shamayim.

3) Regarding your question concerning secular studies in your Yeshiva: in general, this is not a matter in which one should be *mehader* (strive for excellence), and in this case, such *hiddur* is actually to be disparaged. It is difficult for me to provide details on this, as I do not know the current study schedule or the requirements involved. However, the time has already come that they should be broader in their approach. In truth, it would be appropriate for them to be the ones to initiate this expansion, for since Hashem is with us, the verse concludes, "do not fear them." Especially since we see tangibly how one succeeds in every matter that is done with truth and without ulterior motives—even in matters such as these, which those who consider themselves knowledgeable, and certainly those who have access "behind the curtain," initially said were impossible, yet in the end, they succeeded. How much more so, then, that this breadth should come from this side, especially in matters that the Rebbes, our Nasiim, considered fundamental. And to those who understand, a word is sufficient.

4) Thank you, thank you for the story of what the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, said to R' Shmuel Gronem, of blessed memory. Surely, if you recall any other such precious matters, please write them down. Enclosed is a *dvar Torah* for those who are mourning on the day of 19 Iyar. May Hashem grant each of us the merit to hear from one another only good news.

With a blessing for proper health.

1339

Rabbi Refael Nachman: HaKohen. Further letters to him: see above, Vol. 5, 1231.

I have already said: See also above, letter 1329.

1140

16 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from the conclusion of Shabbos, Parshas Beha’aloscha—albeit with a slight delay—as well as your previous letters. It is a pleasure for me to read about your involvement in spreading the wellsprings of Chassidus outward, its customs, and its guidance. Surely, in accordance with the ruling of our holy Torah, you will increase your strength in this, for we elevate in matters of holiness, and to he who adds, more is added.

2) Regarding what you wrote about your son, that you intend to enroll him in a cheder... even though he has not yet turned five years old: generally, such matters depend on the development of his body and his talents. The main thing is whether you can find a class there where the age difference between the other children and your son (may he live) is not too great. If so, may Hashem grant that it be successful.

3) Regarding your question about the path one should take to bring the youth in Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established) closer to the spirit of our ancestors: this question is not understood, as it is not explained in detail. You have been involved in such matters for several months now (even if the involvement is not yet with the vigor that the Rebbe, my father-in-law, would have demanded—and the change is not only in quantity but also in quality—nonetheless, you have found ways). Thank G-d, you are succeeding to a certain degree. If so, what is the meaning of your question, "in what way to bring the youth closer"? Perhaps your intention is related to the continuation of your letter, as understood in the following section:

4) You share the content of your speech at the Lag B’Omer celebration in Meron, where you ask if this is considered "touching" (interfering with) the other religious parties, and if so, whether it is worthwhile to do so in the future.

Generally, it is difficult to provide uniform rules for every person, as this changes from situation to situation and from place to place. The general point must be that the primary goal is the concept of "do good"—that is, to annex as many as possible to proper education and to Torah and mitzvos. One must make every effort toward this goal. Consequently, if touching upon the honor [of others] would cause damage to the aforementioned goal, then after all calculations, it is not our task to conduct propaganda against [them]. On the other hand, if it is necessary to explain the nature of the parties and the destruction that this opposition has brought and continues to bring—meaning negative propaganda and not only positive—in order to save the youth, then one must do so. However, where there is doubt, the rule is known: "sit and do nothing" is preferable. "A morsel that brings closer is great"—and "brings closer" means first in physical matters, and afterward in spiritual matters as well. It is self-understood that extreme caution is required here, in the words of the Rebbe, my father-in-law, in one of his holy sichos: "To lift the other person up to yourself, but not to lower yourself down to the other person."

5) I was alarmed to read the content of your speech in your letter, which states: "Now that we have reached, with the help of Hashem, the beginning of the redemption—I emphasize only the beginning, and the complete redemption will be at the time of the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu," etc. As mentioned, I was alarmed upon reading this. Not so much because of what you said—for a speaker in the heat of the moment is not entirely responsible for his words—but my astonishment is great that you transcribe this in your letter as a simple matter, without feeling or sensing the element of concealment of faith, G-d forbid, contained in that sentence. Consider that the Mishneh Torah of the Rambam begins with the words: "The foundation of foundations and the pillar of wisdom is to know that there is a First Being," and it concludes with the nature of the redemption. This is no coincidence, for their end is rooted in their beginning, and their beginning in their end. The Rambam rules specifically how the redemption will come about, and consequently, its beginning as well. His words are (Hilchos Melachim, Chapter 11, Halacha 4): "A king from the House of David will arise, who studies Torah and occupies himself with mitzvos like his father David, according to the Written and Oral Torah. He will compel all of Israel to walk in its ways and strengthen its breaches, and he will fight the wars of Hashem. He is in the presumptive status of Mashiach. If he succeeds, builds the Temple in its place, and gathers the dispersed of Israel, he is definitely Mashiach, and he will rectify the entire world to serve Hashem together," etc.

It is clear, then, what our Torah rules regarding the redemption and its beginning: it must be a person in the literal sense, with 248 limbs, who studies the Torah of Hashem and fights the war of Hashem, and he is the one who will begin the spreading of Torah and the raising of its prestige, and afterward he will gather the exiles, etc., etc. This is according to the revealed Torah. Regarding the Torah of Chassidus, you have surely seen in many, many discourses the concept of Mashiach and the lights and revelations connected to it. When one is in Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established) and sees the situation on the ground—where they call light darkness and darkness light, etc.—and then says that this is the "beginning of the redemption" and declares it in a loud voice, it is astonishment upon astonishment. I do not wish to elaborate on this: a) because the matter is simple after a moment of reflection, b) because, as mentioned, our task is positive propaganda and not negative, as we heard from the Rebbe, my father-in-law, the adage of the Tzemach Tzedek: "We are workers of the day; we must make things bright," c) because regarding Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established), it is forbidden to speak lashon hara. It is also known that according to the law, lashon hara applies even when speaking the truth (and this is the difference between lashon hara and motzi shem ra). It is understood that, as mentioned, one is not obligated to conduct propaganda all day and all night regarding the negative aspects of the situation, but it is clear that it will eventually cause a mistake and turn the concept of *Golah* (exile—spelled without an *Aleph*) into a concept of *Geulah* (redemption—spelled with an *Aleph*). A word to the wise is sufficient.

6) It would be appropriate that from now on, regarding such general matters as mentioned above, the question should come from the administration of the youth after they have conducted a proper deliberation and consultation among themselves, rather than each person writing individually. It is impossible to answer each one in detail, especially since it would be repetitive and entirely unnecessary.

With blessings for the spreading of the wellsprings outward, which will serve as a conduit and vessel for the drawing down and receiving of the blessings of Hashem for you and for all your household, may they live.

## 1,741

1,741

B"H, 16 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It is pleasant for me to hear from the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, etc., our teacher Rabbi Gavriel Zalkind, may he live, that he has set times for the study of Gemara, Poskim, and Tosafot, and surely he also participates in the appropriate study shiur that is taught in public. However, it goes without saying that this is not sufficient at all, as is discussed in the Gemara and ruled in the Shulchan Aruch, Hilchos Talmud Torah, and especially in the Shulchan Aruch of our Alter Rebbe, Hilchos Talmud Torah. The rule of "one chapter in the morning and one chapter in the evening" is a schedule intended only for those who, according to Torah law, are compelled to earn their livelihood in a manner that requires them to dedicate several hours a day to it. This is not the case for those who are not so compelled; the choice is in their hands—and very often, there is actually no choice at all, and they are obligated **to engage** in the study of Torah and to limit their involvement in worldly matters to only a few short hours.

For the most part, the determination of which category one belongs to must be made specifically by others, and not by oneself, since one is biased in the matter, and the *yetzer hara* finds many ways and enticements to divert a person from the path that leads to the House of G-d. Since I do not know him, nor do I know the specifics of his manner of study, the duration of his study, the nature of his business, or the amount of time he invests in it, he must consult with the elders of Anash in his camp who know him, regarding the division of his time between matters of Torah, fear of Heaven, and worldly affairs. He should act according to their instruction, and may the Almighty grant him success in finding the correct path before him and to ascend from level to level, in accordance with the ruling of our holy Torah: "We elevate in matters of holiness."

With blessings,

## 1,742

1,742

B"H, 17 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings,

In response to your letter of 2 Bamidbar, in which you complain about your spiritual state, and in particular about the fact that doubts in faith sometimes occur to you, etc.

It is a well-known saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, that one must not speak lashon hara about a fellow Jew, and one must not speak it about oneself either. Even if it is true that these thoughts sometimes occur to you (and even then, this is included in the category of lashon hara, as is known from the distinction explained in the poskim: that motzi shem ra is when one speaks a lie, whereas lashon hara applies even if it is true), it is certainly nothing more than a tactic of the yetzer to distract you from the avodah of Torah, tefillah, and mitzvos.

The segulah for this is to increase the recitation of the letters of Torah, and for them to be engraved in your mind—to know them by heart, meaning certain matters of Torah, and specifically Mishnayos and Tanya. See Likutei Torah at the end of Parshas Kedoshim, in the maamar entitled *Ve'hadarta Pnei Zaken*. This is also explained in accordance with the takanah of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, regarding Mishnayos by heart.

In general, you should divert your attention from this entire issue—that is, whether or not these doubts occur to you. If you dismiss these thoughts and study some topic of Chassidus, the pnimiyus haTorah—which, as is known, is in the world of Atzilus (for Kabbalah, which is the pnimiyus haTorah, is in the world of Atzilus; see Tanya, beginning of Chapter 5, regarding the unity from every side and corner)—then "no evil shall dwell with You."

May Hashem grant you success in your avodah of tefillah and in spreading the wellsprings outward, and may He remove from you all matters that cause confusion, etc.

With blessings,

## 1443

1443

B”H, 19 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc.,
Rabbi Yechiel Michel, may he live.

Shalom u’vracha!

It has been some time since I have heard from you. I trust that everything is as it should be with you. I am somewhat surprised that among the names of those involved in the various facets of the activities of Agudas Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, your name is not mentioned. Perhaps it is not just that your name is not mentioned, but that you are performing your work in its entirety; nonetheless, this is not the place for humility, and it would be appropriate for you to write explicitly regarding this. Especially since you are in Haifa, a place where Agudas Chabad is not yet evident, even though there are talmidim of the Tomchei Temimim there, and you and Rabbi Chen, may he live, are among them. I am certain you will endeavor to rectify this in the near future, for it is a pity to lose even a single day. As is known, the interpretation of the concept that "every single day must perform its own work," and "days are fashioned, and not one of them is [missing]," is explained in many places in Chassidus.

2) Regarding your inquiry from some time ago concerning what is written in the Siddur Tehillas Hashem, as well as in the Siddur Torah Or printed in the United States in the year 5701, and also copied in the Luach Tomchei Temimim, where the text for the lighting of the Shabbos candles is: *ner shel Shabbos **kodesh***—what is the source for adding the word ***kodesh***?

**Answer:** As of now, I have not found a source for this. It seems to me that it is not part of the essential text. My proof for this is that in places where there is a concern of *hefsek* (interruption), the word *kodesh* is omitted (see the text for the lighting of candles for Shabbos and Yom Tov). As for why the word *kodesh* is added (in places where there is no concern of *hefsek*), this is from the blessing of my mother-in-law, the Rabbanit, may she live, and it is a **tradition** from the generations before her. Surely, it was practiced this way, generation after generation, in the house of our Nasi. It is known what is written in the Responsa of the Rashba, cited in the Responsa *Hashiv Moshe* (Siman 13), that one should not reject a tradition held by the elderly women of our people on account of six hundred thousand miracles that appear to contradict it.

3) You also commented on the text of the blessing for lighting candles on Rosh Hashanah as printed in the *Siddur Shel Yom HaZikaron*. This was more difficult for me than the previous point, as it involves a new text for the blessing. I asked my father-in-law, the Rebbe, about this some years ago, and he told me that the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, had debated this with the esteemed Rabbi R. Y. Raplovitz of Kremenchug. Despite the questions raised by the aforementioned Rabbi, the Rebbe replied that it must be *shel Yom HaZikaron*. Perhaps the reason is that we equate it to the blessing of Kiddush, the Haftorah, etc. This is the custom of our Rebbe’s house, and *ma’aseh rav* (the practice of a great person is a binding precedent).

4) You further noted what is written in *Sefer HaMaamarim Yiddish* (page 80) on the verse, "And Hashem Elokim shall blow the shofar"—that *Elokim* is *din* (judgment) and *Havayah* is *rachamim* (mercy). You asked: is it not the case that the name *Havayah* here is pointed with the vowels of the name *Elokim*? Please see *Likkutei Torah*, *Derushei Rosh Hashanah*, in the *maamar* beginning "And it shall be on that day, he shall blow," which is the source of these words. See also there in the *maamar* beginning "For as the earth brings forth its growth" (51c).

5) You mention in your letter Rabbi Moshe Linschitz, may he live. I trust you have a set time to study together, including the study of Chassidus. Both of you should strengthen yourselves, at the very least, in the three daily study portions that are equal for every soul, as established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe—Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya—as is known.

With blessings for proper health.
