## 1,746

1,746

B"H, 19 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding your own situation, as you complain about your spiritual state, you have surely heard the adage that my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, would say in the name of his father: "One action is better than a thousand sighs." Simply put, enough sighing—do more. This is also understood through logic: a sigh is, first of all, detrimental to one's health, and the Rambam writes in *Hilchos Deios* (Chapter 4) that maintaining a healthy body is one of the ways of Hashem. Furthermore, there is an additional drawback: after sighing, one feels as though they have already done a favor for the Ribono shel Olam by "doing teshuvah," and consequently, one can now go and rest. The damage this causes to one's avodah is obvious.

This is not the case with a single action; no matter how small it may be, something is accomplished. From every action, even in spiritual matters for a Yid, health is added even in physical terms. Consequently, this is the opposite of the aforementioned results of sighs, which bring no benefit.

With blessings that you bring good news of positive actions and good tidings regarding your personal matters as well.

#### ***1,746***

**The adage:** See also above, Letter 1,735, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 1,497

B"H, 19 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

... 3) Regarding what you wrote concerning the uncovering of the head, I am very distressed by this... One should have sought [...] the appropriate methods to rectify the matter of head covering without entering **for the time being** into the differences of opinion that exist regarding this (the Maharam Alashkar, the Tzemach Tzedek, etc., etc. Beyond the responsum printed in *Shu"t Ahalei Shem*, end of Part 1, Siman 139, it is also found and printed in *Shaar HaMiluim*, Part 1, Siman 45; see also *Chiddushei HaTzemach Tzedek* on the *Shas*, *Berachos* 5a). Likewise, regarding the uncovering of the arm, one must also act according to what is explained in the *Shas* and *Poskim* regarding the laws of *Das Moshe v'Yehudis* in this regard. Once the above is rectified, one can hope that in time, it will be possible to make one correction after another.

4) Regarding what you wrote concerning your notes on the *Shulchan Aruch* of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, if you have any further notes, I would be pleased to receive them as well. When I have the time, it is my hope that I will finally be able to examine them properly.

5) As per your request, when I am at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, I will mention you for long days and good years—"good" with all its interpretations. That is to say, first and foremost, in a physical sense, with proper health, as per the ruling of the Rambam in *Hilchos Deios*, Chapter 4, Halacha 1: "For the body being healthy is one of the ways of Hashem" (this is how it appears in all the printings I have seen; seemingly, the word **avodah** was omitted, and it should read "one of the ways of the **avodah** of Hashem," and it is surprising that, for the time being, I have not found anyone who has noted this). And "good" also in its literal sense—that they be filled with the good teaching that has been given to us in the *hemshechim*, in a good that is visible and revealed.

With blessings for physical and spiritual good, and with the proper blessing included in this—as is understood.

## 1,448

1,448

B”H, 19 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter of 26 Nissan in due time, and I was happy to read that the Joint is behaving well regarding the *Moshav Zekanim* and has rectified the matters that required fixing, providing a dedicated space for the *beis haknesses* so that they will not be disturbed. Regarding what you write—that they are creating difficulties for you, etc.—I do not know if it is worth taking this seriously. Especially since this could be part of the *yetzer’s* counsel to intervene, so as not to allow room for these improvements that are within your hand and ability to rectify. Consequently, the *yetzer* tries from this angle, and it is not worth listening to him. One must examine well his methods of incitement, for sometimes he dresses himself in a *Chassidishe kapote*, as is known from the adage of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (Maharashab), *nif’toro alav*, regarding this.

...You also write in your letter that your son... studied first in Bruna and in Tel Aviv, and now has gone to another place. It is somewhat strange to me that you write about this with such coolness. Even though our Sages of blessed memory said, "Throw a stick into the air, it will land on its base," nevertheless, every day that he is not found in the *ohel* of Chassidus, Torah, and *yiras shamayim* is a great loss. This is especially true in these days, the *ikvesa d’meshicha* when the end of our exile is near, and the *Toras HaChassidus* is the preparation and vessel for the coming and revelation of Mashiach. If you find that you yourself are unable to influence him in this, you should find a suitable person from *anash* who will take an interest in this and see to it that the matter is rectified as soon as possible, and may Hashem help you to be able to share good tidings regarding this.

With blessings.

## 1449

19 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod,
May they live.

Peace and blessing!

My previous letter regarding the conversation with Dr. Shapiro has surely been received by now. I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters dated 26 Iyar, 3 Sivan, and 11 Sivan, along with their enclosures.

2) I noted in your letter that you were offered a loan from the Jewish Agency about two years ago, and you write that you did not utilize it. I am interested in learning the details of this matter.

3) As understood from my previous letter and your current one, regarding the loan of the four thousand liras, one must act quickly.

4) Regarding what you wrote concerning the two options for construction—whether to erect a shack, build on the roof, or connect the two existing buildings in the Shikun HaRakevet—the second option, on the face of it, has more merit than the first. In general, when one sets out with a broader vision, Hashem helps. Especially when one begins construction in practice but lacks the means to complete it, it becomes much easier to obtain additional assistance in the form of a loan, or even in a better way. Surely, with the sum you will receive now (and perhaps you will succeed in arranging for them to grant you the four-thousand-lira loan from before as well), it is possible to utilize this amount—at least a portion of it—even before the entire project is completed.

5) Regarding the location for the vocational school in the village, whether to place it at the beginning of the village or at the end: based on your description of the situation, it should be placed at the beginning of the village, as it will be more visible, among other advantages you mentioned in your letter. The most essential point is that it brings the matter closer to fruition—that is, that it should finally begin in practice to teach, etc.

6) In response to your question: I have already expressed my opinion previously that the aforementioned school must be in a trade from which one can expect a livelihood in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established. It seems to me that printing, carpentry, and the like are suitable for this.

I have already conveyed through Rabbi Moshe Gurary—when he was here—that one should rule out a school for electrical work, radio, and the like.

7) Regarding your question whether to combine the vocational school with the proposal for an agricultural school from Aliyat HaNoar: there is a great concern that one program will confuse the other and stir up questions among the institutions that need to support the endeavor as to who is in charge, **etc.** Therefore, for all these reasons, this idea should be ruled out in the current state of affairs. However, in the realm of thought (and not in the realm of speech to others, even), you may consider the pros and cons of this idea, so that when both of the aforementioned matters—or at least one of them—are already in practice, perhaps one could then discuss the matter of linking the two schools in a way where "a light for one is a light for a hundred." But I reiterate my opinion: if you propose and begin to discuss the matter of combining the two aforementioned schools, there is room for the concern that they will seize upon this idea as a pretext to defer both proposals indefinitely to the theoretical realm, which has no connection to practical reality.

8) Regarding a name for the institution: for the time being, it is not advisable to tie yourselves to a permanent name. You should leave room for flexibility, and it should be called only "The School for Printing or Carpentry, etc., under the auspices of Yeshivas Lod." Seemingly, it is not advisable to specify the name "Tomchei Temimim," because then there would be a conflict regarding the fundraising for this school and the fundraising for Tomchei Temimim. A word to the wise is sufficient.

9) I was very pleased with your detailed letter regarding the state of the yeshiva in both quality and quantity, and that, as you write, the quality of the yeshiva has been elevated compared to what it was until now. I was also pleased to read in your letter that you are sending students to take part in Chabad communal activities, especially in "spreading the wellsprings outward." Surely you will continue this in the future, naturally in a way that the students know that their primary role and mission is to study Torah—both the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus—but that due to the needs of the hour and a literal matter of saving lives (*pikuach nefashot*), they are compelled to dedicate some of their time to engage in saving souls, *un di hartz darf zein veitahn oif dem* (and the heart must ache over this). The *mashpiim* in particular must explain this to the student-activists: that we are demanding both extremes of them. We send them to engage and work in this with faith and the greatest possible effort, and at the same time, they must view this as work that is not their ultimate purpose, without the demands of the times of the "footsteps of Mashiach." Surely you will explain this to all the students more than what I have written here.

10) Enclosed are some scripts in connection with the communal activities in which the yeshiva students are engaged.

11) You conclude your letter by stating that until now you were not accustomed to reporting in detail, but now you found it necessary to do so. It is a pity you did not do this earlier, and consequently, there is no need to apologize for doing so now.

Surely you will give your shack to the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchak as a loan, since the times demand it.

I did not intend for you to take upon yourselves the part that is incumbent upon Agudas Chassidei Chabad to exert effort regarding your yeshiva, but only that you should urge them, etc.

With a blessing for success in your holy work, and may Hashem grant you the merit to bring good news in all matters frequently,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1550

1550

B"H, 19 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily,
May they live,

Peace and Blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the eve of Shavuos, along with the minutes of your meeting on 12 Iyar. It is somewhat surprising that the minutes were delayed for so long. I was very pleased to hear of your good activities on Lag B'Omer, though it is a pity—as you write—that upon your return trip, you were unable to spend much time in the places you passed through. It is well known that the custom of the Chassidim in the days of the Mitteler Rebbe, as related by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, was to make a point of stopping in every place they passed through on their way home from Lubavitch to repeat Chassidus...

4) Surely, in these coming days, the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, R' Shalom Haskind, may he live, will arrive in the Holy Land. He comes as one of the Tzeirei Agudas Chabad from here, and also as my shaliach, to convey regards, particularly to the youth, and to visit the camps and transit centers, etc.—both in those places where you have already plowed and sown, and in those where you have not yet plowed or sown, and where this must be done now. It is my hope that you will arrange this in the most appropriate manner, and it will surely be, as with all other matters of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, with exceptional success.

5) I am sorry that I do not find the young man... in your lists, and I do not understand the reason for this. I am confident that there is no need to bring him proof from our Sages' teaching, "Throw a stick into the air and it will land on its base," for surely he, too, will return to his base. Rather, he needs to have explained to him the promise of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe in the beginning of Torah Or, that one who performs tzedakah has his mind and heart refined a thousand times over. See also Eliyahu Rabbah, Chapter 13, which states: "Regarding Aharon the High Priest—he would tie an iron rope around his waist and go around to all the doors of Yisrael. Anyone who did not know how to recite Krias Shema, or anyone who did not know how to daven, he would teach him to recite Krias Shema and to daven. Similarly, anyone who did not know how to enter into the body of Torah, he would teach him. And not only Aharon, but any Torah scholar who teaches Torah in Yisrael for the sake of Heaven... the Holy One, Blessed be He, has mercy on him and grants him wisdom, understanding, knowledge, and intellect, and gives him a portion with the righteous: Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov." See also Eruvin 54b and Yoma 28b, that Aharon, Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov were heads of yeshivos and, in the simple sense, great scholars.

I await good news and bless you with exceptional success in your holy work.

Two copies of what you published were received. Thank you.

It is strange that the footnotes were omitted in the letter to the Chaf-Pey.

## 1553

1553

B"H, 23 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., R' Shalom, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of the 20th of Sivan, and at the time, the esteemed Chossid and G-d-fearing man, who occupies himself with communal needs, etc., R' Chaim Mordechai Aizik Hodakov, may he live, also conveyed to me the content of your letter to him. Regarding what you wrote—that this is "a young man, his portion alone from all his labor"—immediately following that, its refutation is at its side, as you write that you hope to come here with some of your students for the upcoming 12th of Tammuz.

Regarding your question about the missionaries: in my opinion, it is not worthwhile to engage in intellectual debates with them. Rather, one must seek appropriate ways to expose their disgrace publicly—namely, that they deceive people, that they do not reveal that they are inciters and seducers, and that they do this for the sake of receiving a reward, etc., etc. I believe that in the *Jewish Life* magazine from the month of Iyar-Sivan, an article was printed regarding their activities in the Bronx, which might be of use to you as well.

It has happened at times that when the aforementioned individuals deceived people, inquiries were made officially to the clergy, and they were forced to publicize their opinion to the community that they, the clergy, do not agree with the methods of falsehood and deceit that the missionaries have adopted. However, one must first clarify what the nature of their deception is, and almost always there is some detail in which they are lying, and the like...

With blessings.

Enclosed is a copy of a letter in connection with the festival of Shavuos, which might be of use to you in your influence upon your surroundings.

## 1554

1554

B”H, 23 Sivan, 5712

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your questions from some time ago regarding the beginning of the *maamar* in *Torah Ohr*, *d.h. HaShamayim Kisi*:

1) Regarding the fact that the Torah preceded the world by two thousand years and was subsequently drawn down into heaven and earth — is this the same concept as that mentioned in the *Zohar* in *Idra Rabba* regarding the "one path and the 613 paths of the Torah"?

In general, what is stated in the *Zohar* pertains to the *mitzvos*, whose root is in *Keter* (the *galgalta*), as explained in *Iggeret HaKodesh*, section 20. This is also the case in the *maamar d.h. Tiku* (5691), section 6, which you cite in your letter (unlike the Torah, which "emerges from *Chochmah*," see *Iggeret HaKodesh* there), for the 613 paths are also in the *galgalta*. Sometimes, however, the *Zohar*’s statement is also interpreted as referring to the Torah, but only as it is rooted in *Keter*. See *Likutei Torah*, *Bamidbar* 11d.

2) What is the connection between *Binah* and contemplation in the heart, and the "supernal mercies" and the creation of the Torah?

In *Likutei Torah* for the Three Weeks (1b), it explains this, stating: "See *Tanya*, chapter 45... and also, just as Yom Kippur—which is the revelation of *Binah*—is achieved by awakening mercy." See *Tanya* there, and the *Hagahos* of the *Tzemach Tzedek* on this, which are printed in *Kuntres Reshimot Eicha*, page 22.

3) Regarding what you wrote—that the *middos* are nullified and included in their source—if you mean the "hidden *Sefiros*," the intent is the source of the *middos*. That is, the one who gives birth to them: the *Zat* of *Imma*. See this at length in *Likutei Torah* for the Three Weeks (1c, 6c), and in the *hemshech* for Rosh Hashanah printed for this year.

4) The Torah was already given in the world at the time of the Giving of the Torah; why is an *is'arusa d'letata* (awakening from below) necessary?

This is understood based on what is explained regarding the difference between the Torah [studied] before *tefillah* and [the Torah studied] after *tefillah*. See *Likutei Torah*, *Berachah* (96b) and elsewhere.

5) You write that "He gathers his spirit and soul into the depths of a man and a deep heart," yet at the end of the *maamar* it says this is only in the category of *makif* and *sovev* (encompassing).

Indeed, it is written at the end of the *maamar* that a very small amount is grasped in the *penimiyus* (interior) of the heart. And *memalei kol almin* (filling all worlds) in relation to *sovev kol almin* (encompassing all worlds) is [also] a very small amount; see *Tanya*, chapter 45. See also the *Hosafot* to *Torah Ohr*, *d.h. Im Yasim*—that "gathering" refers to *oros* (lights) in *keilim* (vessels).

6) The drawing down of "And Hashem spoke to Moshe" is also accomplished through "And you shall love," etc., as explained in *Likutei Torah* for the Three Weeks (11c). See also *Amrei Binah*, *Shaar Krias Shema*, end of chapter 47.

7) "The earth is My footstool"—it is explained that the practical *mitzvos* elevate the "foot"—the *Knesses Yisrael* above and the person below—and this is the elevation and inclusion of the **three** (*Netzach, Hod, Yesod*—which are outside the body, the two legs, and the foot) into the *mochin* (intellect), by first being included in the *middos* (**Vav**) and the *middos* into the *mochin* (**Yud**). This is explained in detail in *Likutei Torah* for the Three Weeks (8a and onwards).

8) That the soul clothed in the body effects the *yichud* (unification) of the Torah and the Holy One, Blessed be He—there are two reasons for this: because it engages with the *nitzotzos* (sparks) of *Tohu* that preceded *Tikkun*. And the primary reason—that its service below causes, *b'v'a*, the service of its root in all the worlds, and even that which is above the worlds, for it is like a rope whose head is tied above. See *Iggeret HaTeshuvah*, chapter 5; *Kuntres Acharon* to *Tanya* at the beginning; the second *Hagah* in *Tanya*, chapter 40. See also the *maamar* for *Shabbos Mevarchim Sivan* 5712.

9) What is written in the explanation of the *maamar d.h. Ki Ka'asher HaShamayim* (end of section 4) regarding the three *Vavs* of *Vayisa*, etc.—this is as a proof to explain from where one draws down, which is from the *Yuds*, etc. See *Torah Ohr*, *Vayetzei*, the explanation of *V'shavti B'shalom*.

10) The power of growth of a specific plant, of a specific vegetation, is also found in the **earth**, not in the seed; rather, the seed awakens it—meaning, that this herb should grow and not another. See *Iggeret HaKodesh*, end of section 20; *d.h. Yavi’u Levush* (section 1), chapter 25; *Kachah HaGadol*, chapter 44, and elsewhere.

With blessings for strengthening in the commitment to Torah and the refinement of character,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1557

B"H, 23 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

...As I told you before your departure, it is appropriate that your visit be conducted with "a broadness" (*mit a breitkeit*). This does not mean, Heaven forbid, to belittle others, but rather that the order of the day should be *va’eshalcha varchavah* (and I will walk in a broad place) — to speak about *nigleh*, *Chassidus*, public affairs, and to inspire the spirit of the students, as well as the teachers, and so on. For you are not speaking on your own behalf; the intention is to elevate the spirit of the students, the teachers, and so on, as much as possible for the benefit of these matters. Consequently, you can accompany this "broadness" with the holiness of these matters and their great value. After all, it is simple that in matters concerning our *Nasi*, the Rebbe *shlita*, there should be no lack of "broadness." However, as mentioned, it must be done with *nachas*, and not by breaking the other person, Heaven forbid, or by nullifying them...

With blessings for success,

## 1558

1558

B"H, 23 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 17 Sivan with pleasure, although its content is not of the sort that brings joy, as you complain about the state of your health. However, the very receipt of the letter after your silence is pleasant to me, and I hope that soon the content of your letter will also be joyful regarding your physical health and also regarding your spiritual health. As is well known, the saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, is that one should not speak lashon hara about a Jew, and this includes even speaking about oneself. It is also known how the poskim explain the difference between lashon hara and motzi shem ra: motzi shem ra is specifically when one tells a lie, whereas lashon hara involves telling the truth, yet it is still harmful, as the Sages state in Tractate Arachin. This is similar to what we find regarding prophecy, where the prophet would perform some physical act so that the matter of the prophecy would be realized, as it had already been drawn down into actual deed. It is also a known custom of the great figures of Israel that when a new insight in Torah occurred to them, they would express it verbally, and they explained the reason for this is to draw it down into the lower world. This is also the damage caused by lashon hara, even if the matter is true: by drawing it out into the open and into the world of speech, it gains more influence, whereas if it had remained hidden, the consequences would not have materialized so easily.

I hope that by the time you receive this letter, you will have had the opportunity during this time to accomplish something with your neighbors in the hospital, and that you will report good news regarding this as well.

With blessings for a speedy recovery and proper health.

Received your letter of 22 of this month. Many thanks for the good news regarding your health. And whoever adds [to his efforts, may he be blessed].

***

**1558**

**The saying... lashon hara:** See also above, Letter 1593, and the references in the notes there.

**The custom... verbally:** See Maamarei Admur HaZaken HaKetzarim, p. 404. Below, Letter 1792.

## 1660

1660

B"H, 25 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive regards from you through the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, involved in communal needs, etc., R' Eli Simpson, may he live. However, I am not satisfied to hear that you still experience dizziness from time to time.

You should have—if you are not doing so already—eaten *mezonos* before *davening*, in addition to what you drink. The saying of the Tzemach Tzedek is well-known, where he said that it is better to eat in order to *daven* (meaning, so that one can *daven* with composure) than to *daven* in order to eat (which, naturally, leaves the nerves and head weakened, the *tefillah* is not with composure, and the *yetzer hara* and the body are craving for when they will finally be able to grab a bite). Many of *anash* received an instruction from the Rebbe, my father-in-law, that for the sake of their health, they should eat before *davening* and not fulfill their obligation with drinking alone. If you conduct yourself in this manner, it will bring benefit both for your good health and for your work.

With blessings for proper health for you and your household, may they live.

#### ***1660***

Printed in *Likutei Sichos*, Vol. 14, p. 235.

**Saying:** See also above, Letter 1611.

## 1661

B"H, 25 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter from Parshas Beha'aloscha, in which you describe your situation at home. This is your second marriage (you were divorced from your first wife), and the *shalom bayis* is not as it should be.

You do not write the details of whether the *get* from your first wife was given willingly or if she was coerced. If it was the latter, and you do not know where she is now to ask for her forgiveness, you should gather a *minyan* of people and ask for her forgiveness in their presence, even though she is not present.

Furthermore, regarding *shalom bayis*: you should have the *mezuzos* in your home checked. You must also, as much as possible, be willing to overlook your own feelings (*leha'avir al midosav*). Our Sages have already said that women have a "light mind," that their tears are readily available, and that they save us from sin. This is especially true since she is raising your children. As you write that your son is learning in a Lubavitcher yeshiva, surely your wife, *tichyeh*, has a share in this. You also write that she has helped you all this time, and that a second marriage is according to one’s deeds. If you conduct yourself in this manner, there is reason to hope that your situation regarding *shalom bayis* will improve, and you will be able to share good news in this regard.

You should make it a practice to recite *Tehillim* (at least the portion divided for the days of the month) every day after *Shacharis*. Anyone who adds to this is praiseworthy. You should also study a portion of the *Chumash* with the commentary of *Rashi* from the weekly *sedra* every day. Find friends who can influence your wife and children to draw hearts closer together. Even if—as you write—you have several grievances against your wife, *tichyeh*, you must remember that this *galus* came about because of *sinas chinam* (baseless hatred). Consequently, the rectification for this is **ahavas chinam** (baseless love)—meaning love, even in a situation where there is no basis for it, even according to *Torah*. Nevertheless, one must demand of himself love, as a remedy for the *sinas chinam* through which we were exiled from our land and distanced from our soil. When each person conducts himself [this way] within his own "four cubits," he will naturally exert an influence in his portion of the world. And when the entirety of *Am Yisrael* conducts itself this way, it will naturally bring about the refinement of the world, which will draw down the revelation of *Mashiach* immediately, as explained in *Tanya*, Chapter 37; see there.

You should certainly give *tzedakah* at least on Mondays and Thursdays, and it is proper to do so every day before *Shacharis* (excluding, of course, *Shabbos* and *Yom Tov*).

With blessings to hear good news soon regarding the above.

## 1662

25 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 13 Sivan, in which you outline the chapters of your life and your current situation, noting that you are in Milan and have met there with the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, a man of stature and reputation, R. Mordechai Perlow, and with the esteemed Chassid, a man of stature and reputation, R. Yaakov Gansburg.

Since you mention only your parents in your letter, it appears you are still single. It would be appropriate, since you earn enough to support yourself and a family, to search for your soulmate with the necessary vigor. It is a well-known teaching of our Sages that this search must be like one searching for a lost object—one does not sit with folded arms waiting for the lost item to be brought to the one who lost it, but rather, one makes an effort to go out and search for the lost object.

I was pleased to read in your letter that you studied Chassidus in a group of Anash while you were in Eretz Yisrael, and that you still maintain a regular study schedule. I am interested to know what your study routine is now, both on Shabbos and on weekdays. Even on weekdays, study is essential—and in one sense, even more so than on Shabbos, since on weekdays the body and the animal soul (and consequently the divine soul clothed within them) are immersed in the mundane, in matters of *kelipas nogah*, which serves as the intermediary between the side of holiness and the three completely impure *kelipos*.

It is a well-known maxim of the Baal Shem Tov, which we heard from the Rebbe, that everything a Jewish person sees and hears certainly contains a lesson for him in his path of *avodah*, whether in matters between man and Hashem specifically, or in matters between man and his fellow (for even matters between man and his fellow are matters between man and Hashem, as is known from the explanation brought in *Chassidus*, that the fulfillment of the *mishpatim*—social laws—must be with the same acceptance of the yoke as the fulfillment of the *chukim*—statutes—and not because the intellect dictates them. In our days, we have seen this clearly: the very nation that prided itself on its intellect and a social order based on a supposedly scientific system, etc., is the very one that committed the most horrific evil acts, justifying them with arguments of "intellect and science"). The Baal Shem Tov’s explanation is also understood through human logic: since Hashem is the Master of the entire world, there is certainly not a single thing or event in the world that is in vain. Since a person—according to the ruling of our Sages in the Mishnah at the end of *Kiddushin*—was created **only** to serve his Creator, if he sees or hears something, it is not in vain. For his *avodah*, he must use it to draw closer to his purpose—namely, to serve his Creator, which is the *avodah* of Hashem. This can be through a "do" action, or through a "do not" action of negation and rejection.

I see from your letter that you are an engineer, though it is not entirely clear what your specific field is—whether it is in building construction or matters of measurement, surveying land, and the like. In any case, at the foundation of all the above lies the science of engineering—geometry. What is one of the things to be learned from this science as a whole?

The science of engineering has the character of both an exact science (mathematics) and an applied science, and therefore it is not entirely precise. To distinguish with an infinite number of distinctions, this is the nature of our holy Torah. Although it is the wisdom of Hashem—the ultimate truth and precision, whose value no human can know, and which is hidden from the eyes of all the living, etc.—its ultimate purpose is, as its name implies, *Torah* (instruction), providing guidance in daily life in this physical and material world. Therefore, in the difference between the two aforementioned matters, one can find the fundamental and infinite difference between our holy Torah—of which it is said, "It is your wisdom and understanding in the eyes of all the nations"—and the wisdom and understanding of the nations, or even the intellect of the animal soul of a Jewish person. And it is this:

Human intellect, even that of the sciences called "exact sciences," is based on foundations that the science itself cannot prove. For science, and especially exact science, does not accept a conclusion unless there is proof for it, yet the foundations of all the sciences—and the science of mathematics and engineering in general—have no proof for them. Consequently, it is within the human’s discretion to accept or reject them. This is particularly evident in the science of engineering, where, as is known, there are three main systems, each based on a number of assumptions (axioms), and the axioms in one system contradict those in another. In other words: science cannot give a person a definitive instruction; it can only provide conditional matters. That is, if you accept as true a number of these assumptions and the method of dialectic (*shakla v'tarya*) used with them, then several results will emerge, and these are they. Consequently, there are two points here: a) It is left to the person’s will whether to accept the foundations or not; b) Even if he accepts them, there is nothing to **compel** him to perform an action corresponding to the results, because the science only tells him, "If your actions are in this direction, the result will be such-and-such." If the person does not care about the damage involved, nothing compels him not to act in that direction. In other words: science does not provide life guidance; it only provides a narrative and a form of fortune-telling, stating that based on past experience and the foundations we now choose to accept as true, the course of events will follow a certain order.

Our holy Torah is entirely different in this regard. Being the wisdom of the Truth of Existence—Hashem—it is an absolute matter, meaning truth in its ultimate sense. Both the foundations and the principles of the Torah, and the manner in which one must conduct the *shakla v'tarya* regarding these foundations, are the wisdom and will of the Creator of the entire world and of man. Therefore, it is understood that all the conclusions **compel** the person to act and behave precisely in accordance with this conclusion, and not in any other way at all.

This is one of the points that, as an engineer, it is appropriate for you to have engraved in your mind: it is impossible to raise any difficulty from science against Torah. Since Torah is absolute truth, and science itself testifies that it is not absolute but dependent on the assumption of human will—and it is within human discretion to establish contradictory systems, all of which may have the right to exist based on human will, just like the three systems in geometry: Euclid, Lobachevsky, and Riemann—there is no comparison.

I hope that what is written above is understood. If you have any comments on this, I would be happy if you would inform me in detail. It is known from our Sages that they rejoiced when others challenged their words, as it is a sign that they are interested in what was said, and primarily, it serves to clarify and refine the matters and topics proposed during the *shakla v'tarya*.

I trust you are strengthening yourself in the observance of the three daily study sessions established for every person by the Rebbe: the *Tehillim* (as divided by the days of the month) after every morning *davening*; the study of one *parsha* of *Chumash* (from the weekly *sedra*) with *Rashi* every day; and the study of *Tanya* as divided for the days of the year.

I am also interested to know your regular study times in *nigleh* (revealed Torah) and *Chassidus*, as well as your good deeds in influencing your environment in general, and your family and relatives in particular, to draw their hearts to our Father in Heaven, and thereby bring eternal happiness in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings for the proper arrangement of your affairs in a manner suitable for you, both materially and spiritually.

## 1663

1663

B"H, 25 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from the 4th of Iyar, in which you describe the state of your business affairs, noting that you are under great pressure, etc., etc. You write that you have the opportunity to sell some plots of land you own, but you cannot decide for yourself what to do. Most importantly, as is evident from your letter, your spirits have fallen, and consequently, your level of *bitachon* has also weakened. I am writing to you regarding this most important point, because according to what is brought in holy books in general, and in the books of Chassidus in particular, everything depends on this. The level of *bitachon* is the yardstick for the connection and *dveikus* of a person’s material affairs with the Creator, B"H. If this *dveikus* is complete, then it is certainly impossible for there to be any lack, since Above, such a concept does not exist at all.

Since you ask for my advice—after the preface that, as you requested, when I was at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nevgam, zya*, I mentioned you for what you need—it seems to me that you must work on yourself, *arueven oyf zich*, to strengthen your *bitachon* in Hashem to the greatest possible degree. The truth of the level of *bitachon* is that even when one sees no natural path, it is beyond any doubt that everything will certainly be good—and in a good that is visible and revealed to physical eyes, meaning with expanded livelihood, health, etc. Regarding Above, the matters of nature do not touch upon Him at all. Since a person below establishes himself and elevates himself, at least to some degree, above the earth—meaning, when he acts upon himself so that, because he is a believing Jew, he is absolutely certain that there is no "boss" over him other than Hashem—he has the ability to draw down here below that even here, all the matters of nature will be unable to touch him in a way that is not for the good, *chas v'shalom*. My hope in Hashem is strong that if you only strengthen your *bitachon* to the ultimate degree, you will immediately see a change in how your business affairs are conducted, and your situation will begin to go from good to better, *un fun gut tzu noch besser*.

In addition to this, you should immediately begin giving *tzedakah* according to your custom, and increase it at least slightly beyond what you have been doing until now. I will await good news from you regarding all of the above.

With blessings for success in material matters, and may the saying of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, be fulfilled in you: that Hashem gives Jews materiality, and they make spirituality out of that materiality.

***

**Note:** See also above, Letter 1637, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 1664

1664

B"H, 25 Sivan, 5712

...As is evident from your letter, there is now a channel to influence your brother, may he live, regarding matters of Yiddishkeit in general. And in general, it is known from our Sages, of blessed memory, that this world is like a wedding feast: **seize** and eat, **seize** and drink...

## 1,165

B"H, 25 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the venerable Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, etc., Moreinu HaRav L. [Spitzer]
May he be well.

Peace and blessing!

In response to your notification that in your work of making tzitzis, you are careful that everything required is done for the sake of the mitzvah of tzitzis and by human hand:

For your good deed in bringing merit to the many, I say *yashar chilo* (may your strength be firm), and may Hashem be your help, and bless you and grant you success in all that you need.

With blessing,

P.S.
In a separate package, I have returned to you the volume of the Alter Rebbe’s Shulchan Aruch, parts 3-4. Regarding what you noted and marked in the margins:

1) In Hilchos Pesach, siman 433, seif 17, regarding what is written "one should be concerned" (*yesh lachush*): There is no printing error here. Rather, the words "but small holes, etc., do not require checking" are a parenthetical statement, and "one should be concerned" refers to what precedes it. In the *Kuntres HaShulchan* by Rabbi Naeh, he writes that in the Kapust printing of the Shulchan Aruch, these words are in parentheses.

2) There, siman 442, seif 27: This seif has omissions and additions in the Kehot printing, which was printed from the Vilna edition. The text in the Zhitomir 5616 printing is: "Therefore, the kneading trough does not combine them into a *kezayis*, whether they are stuck to it firmly or whether they are resting in it loosely." This is how it should be, as is understood.

3) Siman 447, seif 45: In the Zhitomir printing—as you noted in the margin—it is *niklash* (weakened) instead of *nikrash* (congealed).

4) Siman 453, seif 8: In the Zhitomir printing, it is correctly written: *af al pi chein ein tzarich levarer lehasir* (nevertheless, there is no need to sort to remove).

5) Siman 456, seif 8: In the Zhitomir printing, it is correctly written, as you noted, *liknos* with a *samech* and not with a *tav*.

6) There, 463, end of seif 3: In the Zhitomir printing, it is correctly written: *yitpartzu* (they will break out) and not *yitpazru* (they will scatter).

7) Siman 467, end of seif 38: It should be as you noted: *litlot bezeh kemo bezeh* (to attribute to this as to that). This was also corrected in the aforementioned *Kuntres HaShulchan*.

8) There, siman 483, seif 1: It says *Yaknehaz*. This is also how it appears in the Zhitomir printing. One should check earlier printings, because obviously, it should not be the blessing on wine here, but rather the blessing of *HaMotzi*.

## 1676

1676

B"H, 25 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you enclosed a *pidyon nefesh* for yourself and your wife, *shichyu*, to be blessed with children in a healthy and kosher manner.

I was shaken to read in your letter the words, "despair is gnawing at our hearts," etc.—words that are the opposite of our holy Torah.

You do not mention in your letter whether you have consulted with specialists in this field. My suggestion is that both you and your wife, *shichyu*, visit such doctors and follow their instructions. You should strengthen your trust and conviction in Hashem, who is the Healer of all flesh and performs wonders, and for Whom nothing is impossible. Consequently, you should contemplate the prospect of having children in a healthy and kosher manner.

You must immediately begin to create *keilim* (vessels) for the drawing down and reception of Hashem’s blessings. These *keilim* are the establishment of fixed study sessions in both the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus, in addition to the three daily study sessions ordained for every soul by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zya*: the recitation of the daily portion of Tehillim (as divided by the days of the month) every day after Shacharis; the study of the weekly parsha of Chumash with Rashi’s commentary every day; and a daily *shiur* in Tanya, as divided by the days of the year.

As you requested, I mentioned you and your wife, *shichyu*, when I was at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nbg"m, zya*, and I look forward to hearing good news from you.

With blessings.

## 1657

1657

B"H, 28 Sivan, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of the Yeshiva and Talmud Torah
in Sifria, Kfar Chabad
May Hashem preserve them and grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

It was with pleasure that I received the 26 newsletters, along with the photographs of the administration of the Yeshiva and Talmud Torah, and the students—may they live—whose faces bear witness that they are the seed blessed by Hashem.

I noticed in the newsletters that under the question regarding their talents in Nigleh and Chassidus, nothing was recorded. It seems this is because you think that at their age, it is still too early to study Chassidus.

However, in light of the fact that: a) a significant portion of the students are Sephardic, whose custom until now has been to leave the walls of the Yeshiva at an early age; b) the talents of Sephardic children mature earlier than those of Ashkenazic children; and c) in accordance with the winds blowing in the world today, one must introduce the habit of studying Chassidus as early as possible—

It is my opinion that it would be appropriate to begin the study of Chassidus with all those who have reached the age of twelve. Furthermore, even at an age younger than that, one should accustom them to the ways of Chassidus and its conduct, and make it pleasant for them through stories from the lives of our Nesi'im, our holy Rebbes—may the merit of the righteous protect us—and through farbrengens.

It is understood that a farbrengen for boys of this age does not need to involve drinking mashke; one should suffice with soda or cake, and the like.

I am interested to know if you organize Shabbos gatherings for your students, and if there are already some among the students who inspire their peers regarding the necessity of studying our holy Torah, observing its mitzvos, and walking in its ways.

With a blessing for success in your holy work.

## 1069

B"H, 1 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter from Friday, Parshas Shelach, in which you write that after reconsidering the question of the education of your children, may they live, you and your husband, may he live, have come to the decision to send them to the Lubavitcher yeshiva. You add that you struggled with this thought, as the children are very dear to you.

I wish to reiterate what I told you orally: you need not struggle with yourself regarding this at all. On the contrary, because the children are dear to you, it is certain that you want the maximum you can provide for them, especially in the matter of chinuch, which establishes and influences their entire lives. By placing them in one of the best yeshivos in the world, it is certain that this will do them good in their lives, even in ways that, for the time being, one cannot imagine. I am also certain that in a short time, you yourselves will see the wisdom and goodness of the decision you have made.

Regarding your question as to whether you should take up an occupation in order to diminish the longing for your children, may they live: the first condition for this is that you must know to what extent your health allows you to do so. If you think it will not cause harm, Heaven forbid, to your health, it is perhaps advisable that you be occupied or work a few hours a day, not full-time.

... I wish for you that your home should be a true Yiddishe, Chassidishe home, and that you and your husband, may he live, should have Yiddishe nachas from your children, may they live.

With blessings.

P.S. Your donation has been handed over to the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, which works in this field to improve the chinuch of Yiddishe children, and this will draw down blessings upon the chinuch of your own children, may they live.

Enclosed is a copy of a letter of mine in connection with vacation time, which I think you will be able to utilize to influence your acquaintances for the good.

## 1,079

1,079

B"H, 1 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Enclosed is a copy of my letters: 1) for the holiday of Shavuos, and 2) in connection with the vacation period, which will surely bring you benefit in your surroundings and among those you influence.

With blessings.

## 1771

B"H, 1 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

In response to your letter of the 23rd of Sivan, in which you ask for a *tikkun* for *ch"n* (a private matter), I have already stated long ago that first and foremost, one must divert one's mind from this and increase the study of the letters of Torah and *tefillah*—naturally, without disrupting the *sedarim* of the *yeshivah*. ## 1571

B.H., 1 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Blessings and Peace!

I received your letter of the 26th of Sivan, in which you briefly describe your background and your life, particularly in recent times, and you also write regarding your weakness and that you must visit a specialist doctor in the coming days who wishes to perform an analysis, etc.

My opinion is that you must be strong in your bitachon in Hashem Yisbarach, Who conducts the entire world and desires that there be good in the world. He—Baruch Hu—will help you so that the analysis and whatever the doctors advise to do afterwards will all be for the good, and in the near future you will return to your full health and will be able to manage your home so that it is a Yiddishe home in all respects.

Regarding what you write concerning your husband and the shalom bayis, you should overlook various things that you consider to be shortcomings. For even if it is so, at these years and at this age it is difficult to change him; pointing it out to him several times, when he is unable to control himself, only upsets him more and brings no benefit. When he sees that you overlook it and that it does not affect your attitude toward him, it is certain that in the course of a short time, the shalom bayis will improve.

You mention your older daughter, who is in a delicate condition, and you ask for a blessing for her. When I am at the tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, zatzuklalah, nbgm, zi'e, I will mention her, her husband, and all of you whom you mention in your letter, for whatever each of you requires, and I hope that you will be able to report good news to me.

In order to receive the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach, one must have the appropriate vessels, and as many as possible; these are the matters of Torah and mitzvos. Therefore, I would suggest to you: 1) That in your home and in the homes of your children, there should be **kosher** mezuzos on the doors. 2) That you and your married daughter should give tzedakah before lighting candles for matters connected to the Torah education of Yiddishe children. 3) That your married daughter, and you as well, should have a strictly kosher Yiddishe kitchen. 4) That your husband and your sons should put on tefillin every day (naturally, except for Shabbos and Yom Tov).

I wish to reiterate my wish that you have a healthy summer with your entire family, and in the near future you will be able to report good news to me that your health has improved, that the shalom bayis has become better, and also regarding your daughter, tichyeh.

With blessings.

## 1773

1773

B"H, 1 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 22 Sivan, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed therein, which I will read at an auspicious time at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulah"h, nbg"m, zy"a*.

Regarding what you wrote in your letter concerning what you told your wife, *tichyeh*, and that she also agreed not to go to the *mikveh* for several years because she does not have the strength to give birth, etc.:

I was startled by what I read in your letter. Aside from the fact that according to many *poskim* it is well-known even according to *nigleh* that a waiver in this matter is ineffective (see *Shulchan Aruch, Even HaEzer*, siman 76 and the beginning of siman 1), and consequently this is an obligation—furthermore, as for the order of self-affliction and practicing *sigufim* at someone else’s expense, I have never heard of such a thing. If it is as you wrote, that the doctors’ opinion is that it would be a danger to her health to conceive, then the ruling of the *Tzemach Tzedek* is well-known—*Responsa Even HaEzer*, Part 1, siman 89—that this is one of the three categories of women who may use a *moch*. Please refer to it there. I do not wish to elaborate on this, as the matter is explained, and surely this little bit will suffice.

Regarding what you wrote about whether it is worthwhile to afflict yourself—for example, by sleeping on a bench with only a pillow under your head—you do not state the reason for these *sigufim*. In general, in these generations of ours, anyone who wishes to choose *sigufim* must choose those that do not, *chas v'shalom*, harm the health of the body. As is known, the *Rambam* rules in *Hilchos Deios*, Chapter 4, that maintaining a healthy body is one of the ways of Hashem. This is especially true when we see tangibly that a weakening of physical health hinders one’s *avodah* in Torah and *tefillah* before anything else. The matter of *sigufim* should be conducted according to what is explained in the book *Toldos Moharash*, page 72, at the end, which notes an additional advantage in this: a) it does not harm the health of the body; b) it does not lead to an increase in *yeshus* (self-importance) or showing off before others, since others do not see great and wondrous things in it, and only the person himself knows how difficult it is to endure; c) in several details, this is even harder than *sigufim* and fasts, because since it is something that is entirely permissible, one does not see it as a tangible *avodah* (that he is accomplishing great things); d) through such *avodah*, it is possible that, little by little, one may be transformed from one essence to another, and consequently, one stands against the *yetzer hara* with full force, and "according to the effort is the reward."

Regarding your birthday—which you mention at the end of your letter—for long days and good years: may it be the will of Hashem that your days and years be "good" in all interpretations—that is, simply in a physical sense, and filled with Torah and *mitzvos* and the "light of Torah," which is the true good. May Hashem grant you success in illuminating your students and those you influence with this light.

With blessings.

## Letter 1524

B"H, 1 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, etc.,
Rabbi Eliyahu Chaim, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter of the 24th of Sivan, in which you write regarding the progress — the *shtaygen* — of the young students under your influence in their studies. Surely this is also the case regarding their *yiras shamayim* and *mitzvos maasiyos*. May it be the will of Hashem that the ruling of our Sages be fulfilled in this: "We elevate in matters of holiness..."

Regarding your question as to whether one of the *chareidim* should teach religious subjects at the aforementioned school, or whether there is a concern that this would attract students who otherwise would not attend such a school: As I mentioned, since you do not explain what the deficiency in this school is, nor what the curriculum, its goals, and so on are, my response can only be speculative. Seemingly, one should follow the middle path: a G-d-fearing and *chareidi* individual should teach religious subjects there, but not one of such stature that his teaching could serve as a *hechsher* for the entire institution. I look forward to further details regarding all of the above.

Regarding what you wrote—that in a limited amount of time it is impossible to influence many students: If, by not teaching for a limited time, they would instead study for a long time, then there would be no need to arrange a limited session. However, as I understand from your letter, if they do not study for a short time, the students will not know anything at all about religious matters and *mitzvos maasiyos*. In that case, even in a limited time—provided there is a suitable teacher—one can accomplish **much** with the students. Especially since, in speaking with them, one must emphasize frequently and repeatedly that one should not be satisfied at all with studying for only a short time, but that one must enroll in a *cheder* or the like, a place where they study holy subjects for several hours. The second point to emphasize in your discussions with them is the necessity of conducting oneself with *mitzvos maasiyos* in their daily lives. **Tangibly**, we have seen that through this, it is possible to acquire many children and "bring forth the precious from the vile."

With blessings for success in communal matters and in your personal affairs.

#### ***Letter 1524***

**Rabbi Eliyahu Chaim, may he live:** Roitblatt, Pocking. Another letter to him—see above, Vol. 5, 1330.

## 1175

1 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings,

I received your letter of 10 Sivan with pleasure. In it, you write about your commitment to studying Chassidus, and that you are not entirely satisfied because you have no one to ask when you encounter a difficulty, and—most importantly—no one with whom to study.

I find this surprising. Surely you are acquainted with several of the young men of Agudas Chabad and our yeshivos; with some effort, you could certainly arrange to set aside times for study with them, in addition to what you study on your own. Most importantly, it is necessary that you **participate** (not merely be present) during the farbrengens of Anash, such as those on the upcoming Chag HaGeulah of 12-13 Tammuz and 18 Elul. It would be best if you did not settle for what you imagine to be "enough," but rather continue to maintain a connection with them and participate in their farbrengens until you come to the realization that not only have you not "absorbed enough," but that what you have is merely a tiny fraction. As our Sages have stated, "I have labored and found—believe it."

2) You write that you saw my letter for Pesach, and that it was the first you had seen addressed to young people. It is surprising that you did not also see my letter from Erev Rosh Hashanah 5711 to the yeshiva students. You can surely find it now among Anash. However, the ruling of our Sages is well known: it is not the study that is the main thing, but the action. You should fulfill the suggestions in the aforementioned letter, and "whoever is early is praiseworthy." For every single moment that passes without being filled with appropriate content is a loss that cannot be recovered. To elaborate on such a simple and self-evident matter is unnecessary.

3) You ask about the intent of my letter for Pesach regarding the words, "even if through this one is forced to change one’s nature and habit." It requires study as to what you found difficult, for my meaning is simple: Yeshiva students are accustomed to the concept of *gadol ha-talmud* (the greatness of Torah study). Consequently, it seems novel to them to dedicate a portion of their time—which they could use to excel in Torah—to instead use it to draw their surroundings closer through simple matters, such as keeping Shabbos, teaching the Aleph-Beis, Hebrew, and so on. Many yeshiva students justify this to themselves as being out of *yiras shamayim*, arguing that since our Sages ruled that a mitzvah which can be performed by others should not cause one to interrupt their Torah study—and that even the education of children should not be interrupted for the building of the Beis HaMikdash—they should not, Heaven forbid, separate themselves from Torah even for a moment. They argue that the Ribono shel Olam must ensure the proper education of the sons and daughters of Yisrael who are in danger of assimilation and heresy, Heaven help us. But in truth, this is not out of *yiras shamayim*, for the mitzvah is passing and there are not enough others doing it; rather, this is a suggestion of the *yetzer hara*.

(As is known, the interpretation of our Sages' statement, "Such is the craft of the *yetzer hara*: today he says to him, 'Do this,' etc." Seemingly, the word "such" (*kach*) is difficult; it should have said, "Do *this* (*zos*)." But the way of the *yetzer hara* is that initially, when he comes to a G-d-fearing person, his statement is "such" (*kach*)—meaning that he, the *yetzer hara*, also agrees with this. However, he mixes in a reason that gives him a foothold. Consequently, after some time, when it is convenient for him to expand further, this provides the possibility for him to eventually say, "Go and worship idols.")

In this matter, one must be particularly wary of the incitements of the *yetzer hara*, because for yeshiva students, this is their **nature**—

(As is known, those who toil in Torah in their youth, before they understand through their intellect the immense value of Torah, are diligent by nature and are not so obsessed with matters of play and levity)—

—and their **habit**. Even those who entered the yeshiva not by their own desire but due to the insistence of parents and teachers—even if this was contrary to their nature—once they have become accustomed to the life and order of the yeshiva, it is difficult for them to depart from it. As the wise man said, "Habit becomes second nature."

4) In your letter, you ask about the statement of our Sages in Rashi on Bereishis (1:11-12) regarding the sin of the earth and its subsequent curse. You ask: what is the sin and punishment in the case of vegetation? You should examine *Maseches Avodah Zarah*, Tosafos s.v. *ad*, page 17a, and Tosafos s.v. *amar*, *Chullin* 7a. It is similar in the *Chiddushei Aggados* of the Maharsha, *Chullin* 60a, on the verse "The grasses carried a *kal v'chomer* themselves"—that their prince and constellation said so. See there also regarding the matter of the *kal v'chomer*.

With blessings for success in Torah with *yiras shamayim*, and for connection to the "Light in the Torah" and the "line of truth" in Torah, which is the inner dimension of Torah.

## 1,176

1,176

B"H, 2 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received the news that your daughter, Mrs. ..., has entered the fifth month of her pregnancy. May it be the will of Hashem that she complete the days of her pregnancy properly and with ease. Surely she is following the instructions of the doctor who examines her from time to time, as is the custom of the land. May the birth be at its proper time and with ease, and may you, may you live and be well, derive from her and from your other children, may they live and be well, much nachas—Yiddishe nachas and Chassidishe nachas.

It is surely unnecessary to point out and emphasize the necessity of maintaining a correspondence with your son-in-law, the husband of your aforementioned daughter, Rabbi ..., to explain to him in detail the magnitude of the privilege and the responsibility that rests upon him to bring the hearts of Yidden closer to their Father in Heaven. We do not know what may come of it; sometimes, by bringing one Yid closer, one establishes generations of sons and daughters who are G-d-fearing and observant. Consequently, every effort, toil, and labor—both the toil of the soul and the toil of the flesh—is worthwhile, even for the sake of a single Yiddishe soul. For a soul is not only a whole world in itself, but also, quite simply, in terms of their offspring and their offspring's offspring until the end of all the world (and the explanation in Chassidus is well known: "the end of all the world" means *az zei machen a sof tzum helem v'hester*—that they bring an end to the concealment and hiddenness). May Hashem grant us the merit to see this with our physical eyes, which comes through bitachon that transcends the limitations of intellect and reason. As is also well known, this is one of the interpretations of the word *tzitz* and *tzitzis*. *Tzitz* is from the expression, "Behold, He stands behind our wall... **peering** (*metzitz*) through the lattices" (see Likutei Torah, Sefer Devarim 91c), which refers to the time of the galus. The place of the *tzitz* was on the forehead, representing the concept of bitachon and hiskashrus that transcends intellect and reason; see Likutei Torah regarding the forehead (Shir HaShirim 23c, from the Zohar, etc.).

The second interpretation is that *tzitz* comes from the expression of illumination and radiance, as in "the pomegranates have blossomed (*hinitzu*)" and "his crown shall blossom (*yatzitz*)." See Torah Or and Torah Chayim, Parshas Tetzaveh, the maamar entitled *Ve'asisa Tzitz*, where all three verses are cited, and they relate to the days of Moshiach. See also there regarding the connection to *tzitzis* and the forehead.

With blessings for success in both general and personal matters,

**Postscript:** This is also discussed in Sefer 5627.

## 1777

1777

B"H, 2 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

It has been a long time since I have heard from you. I trust the reason is not that you were dissatisfied with my last response, as I hope you do not take offense at it; I am compelled to state my opinion as it is, without having one thing in writing and another in my heart.

2) I am pained that after I wrote regarding... all vision on this matter has been blocked. I fear this is because they have become disheartened due to the events and tragedies, etc. One must view this as a matter of concealment and hiddenness (*he'elem v'hester*). Furthermore, we have not yet merited that the fulfillment of our mission should be easy; rather, it is through concealments and hiddenness. It is well known that the purpose of concealment and hiddenness is to awaken higher powers. Consequently, if the concealment and hiddenness have produced the exact opposite effect—meaning that not only have they failed to awaken higher powers, but even the revealed powers have disappeared—this is the exact opposite of the Divine intent. As is well known, one of the interpretations in *Etz Chaim* regarding "we have sinned before You with the *yetzer hara*" is that the purpose of its creation was in order to overcome it. Even the *yetzer hara* itself desires this, as is known from the *Zohar* and as is also brought in *Tanya*, end of Chapter 29.

See also there, in Chapter 27, in continuation of the above. Further elaboration on this is unnecessary, as it is well known and explained in many places. I have come only to call attention to it...

Awaiting good news, and signing with blessings.

## 1778

1778

B"H, 3 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...I was pleased to read in your letter that you foresee a bright future for the activities of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, even though they certainly still require guidance. In truth, this is a positive sign; for in general, every one of us is in need of guidance. The only exception is one who does not wish to receive it, or, even more significantly, one who has already reached the end of his growth and prosperity, and consequently has turned from a traveler into one who stands still. This is not the case when one requires guidance and accepts it; that is clear proof that the source of the hidden powers within them is alive and flowing, and that from time to time they add to their activities and ascend from strength to strength.

As for the fact that there is a cause and a catalyst from the side of the one providing the guidance, this is for the most part as explained in several maamarim of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: the analogy of digging an artesian well. The person’s effort in this is merely the removal of the dirt, stones, and so forth, which conceal and obstruct the revelation of the spring. Once the things that prevent it—which are located **outside** the water—are removed, the spring **of its own accord** flows and spreads with great force and to a great height.

The same applies in our case: in the vast majority of cases, great powers exist within every son and daughter of Yisrael, especially those from the lineage of anash, whose ancestors' merit assists them. The purpose of the guidance is to remove the concealment and obstruction caused by external matters and external things—namely, the bad habits that come from the environment, idleness, and the like. Then, the source of living waters, the point of Yiddishkeit, performs its function in actual deed.

May the Ribono shel Olam enable each of us to fulfill his mission in the aforementioned avodah—namely, to make a breach in the wall and the partition that separates Yisrael from their Father in Heaven; a breach additional to the breach made by the Sages and Nesi'im of Yisrael, generation after generation. For then, the light will naturally spread from both sides: the light of the Ohr Ein Sof, B"H, from one side, and the light of the neshamah within Yisrael from the other.

With the blessing of Chag HaGeulah, that it may be a near beginning to the redemption of our souls through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily and in reality.

#### ***1778***

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 23, p. 428.

## 1719

1719

My time is not at all my own, due to the multitude of burdens and the distress of the heart, as each and every day brings its own tasks. Nevertheless, my hope remains that Hashem will grant success, so that there will be a time when even a little time will contain a great deal, and there will be room to also attend to the aforementioned...

With blessings for the *Chag HaGeulah*.

## 1,880

1,880

B"H, 3 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, etc., R' Nissan, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

It is surely unnecessary to elaborate on the well-known and famous significance of the Chag HaGeulah of 12 and 13 Tammuz, on which my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, was—at the time—liberated. This was not a private victory, but a victory for Torah, yiras shamayim, and Yiddishkeit. These days are days of *segulah* to strive with added courage in the awakening of spreading Torah and strengthening Yiddishkeit, each person in their own place of residence, according to the conditions of the time and place. This means that even in a place that is already strong in matters of Torah and mitzvos, one must still add in many areas, for "its measure is longer than the earth" (Iyov 11:9). And even in a place most distant from Torah and mitzvos, as long as there is even one Jew there, there is no doubt that it is within his power to accomplish things there in matters of Torah and Yiddishkeit. Especially since you reside in a city where many who are G-d-fearing and observant of His word dwell (fitting the first category), and where there are also many simple folk (fitting the second category mentioned above). Consequently, you will accomplish there in both ways. It is a well-known saying of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, that propaganda (ta'amulah) is strong and does not return empty. May Hashem grant you success in your private matters and also grant you success in the general matters.

With blessings.

#### ***1,880***

**R' Nissan:** Altschuler, Cleveland.

## 1,181

1,181

Especially a shamash in a shul can accomplish a great deal today, in his shul—and often more effectively in an inconspicuous manner than through overt, stormy efforts. Hashem does not remain a debtor and rewards with an abundance beyond the primary measure, with Yiddishe and Chassidishe nachas, from one's children and from oneself as well.

With blessings for proper health in both material and spiritual matters.

## 1882

B”H, 3 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive regards from you through the esteemed Chossid, the G-d-fearing man who engages in communal needs with faithfulness, Rabbi Menachem Shmuel Dovid Reitzes, the shaliach. He also delivered your *pidyon nefesh* to me, and in accordance with your request, I mentioned you at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, during a time of favor.

Rabbi Reitzes also informed me that you were previously involved in *shechitah* and are now a businessman.

Surely you have heard the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov, which we were privileged to hear many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe—that every thing a Yid hears and sees, he must derive from it a lesson in his *avodas Hashem*.

Regarding the matter of *shechitah*, it is stated in *Tanna D’bei R’ Yishmael*: "‘And he shall slaughter’ (*v’shachat*)—it means nothing other than drawing (*moshach*)" (*Chullin* 30b). According to the path of Chassidus and *mussar*, this means that the act of *shechitah* is what renders the meat of the animal fit for human consumption. When a person eats this meat, it becomes "blood and flesh of his flesh." Consequently, he *moshach*—he draws up—the animal, which is merely a *chai* (living creature), to a higher level, that of *medaber* (a speaking being)—a human.

So too it is in the *avodah* of the soul, for every Yid possesses a *nefesh habehamis* and a *nefesh elokis*. The mission of the *nefesh elokis*, which is hewn from beneath the Throne of Glory and has descended into a most profound descent to clothe itself in a body and a *nefesh habehamis*, is that the purpose of this descent is to perform *avodah* with its *nefesh habehamis* in particular, and with its portion in the world in general. This is analogous to the concept of *shechitah*: that the very vitality and passion (*koch*) that the *nefesh habehamis* has for worldly, *olam hazeh* matters, is to be transformed—*v’shachat* means *moshach*—into matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, into matters of *Elokus*.

And since *kol Yisrael areivim zeh bazeh* (all Jews are responsible for one another), one must not be content with working only for oneself and one’s household. Rather, one must also influence one’s environment, so that instead of physicality, materialism, and animalistic tendencies, there should be matters of Torah and *mitzvos* illuminated by *Ohr Eloki*, as is explained at length in the teachings of Chassidus.

With blessings that you should succeed in the aforementioned *avodah*, which will serve as a channel and vessel to draw down and receive the blessings of Hashem for everything you and your family need.

## 1883

B"H, 3 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I am sorry to hear that, according to the reports I have received, his physical appearance is not particularly good. It seems that he has once again taken up the path of self-affliction and asceticism, and is neglecting his physical health. This is despite the fact that he is aware of the ruling of the Rambam in Hilchos De’os, beginning of Chapter 4, that maintaining a healthy and sound body is one of the ways of Hashem. It is also well known that the ruling brought in the Shulchan Aruch of our Alter Rebbe, Hilchos Nizkei Guf V’Nefesh, section 4, states: "A person has no authority over his own body at all to strike it, to shame it, or to cause it any pain, even regarding matters of food or drink, unless he is doing so as a path of teshuvah, in which case it is for his benefit." Since our Alter Rebbe has already written in Iggeres HaTeshuvah that in our generations the path of teshuvah is different and not through fasts, then clearly, what remains is as stated above in the language of our Rebbe in his pure Shulchan Aruch. And how much of a limit is there to not listening and insisting on doing exactly as one sees fit? Surely he has also seen the letter of the Baal Shem Tov to his student, the author of the Toldos, which is printed in *HaTamim*, etc., etc. I await good news regarding this.

*1883*

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 14, p. 200.

## 1,784

B”H, 3 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, who engages in communal needs, etc.,
R’ Naftali, may he live, Hakohen

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter dated 1 Beha’alotcha in due time. May Hashem grant that from now on you will be able to share good news in all matters, and I trust you will keep me informed of the situation from time to time.

In connection with the upcoming Chag HaGeulah, 12-13 Tammuz, a Kuntres and Reshima have been published, which I am enclosing. I am certain that you will use them not only for yourself, but also to illuminate your surroundings with the light of Torah and the "light of Torah"—which is the teachings of Chassidus, its paths, and its practices.

One should not be surprised that we demand of each one of us avodah at both extremes: both to influence the most basic matters—such as the observance of Shabbos, eating kosher, intermarriage, etc.—and simultaneously to address the most lofty matters, such as the dissemination of the teachings of Chassidus. For in this time, the *ikvesa d’meshicha* (the footsteps of Moshiach), we know the analogy brought in the teachings of Chassidus: that among the methods of medicine, there are times when, in order to heal the head, one draws blood from the foot. The analogy is understood. This is especially true when we see, even with physical eyes, an awakening in our time—even among the youth, including those who until now were completely distant from Yiddishkeit. They are searching, searching again and again for the truth, because they have been disappointed by the other "ideals," etc., that they were told about until now. Consequently, one must utilize—*ausnutzen*—this awakening. This will be beneficial in two ways: both in "turning away from evil" and in "doing good." As is known from our Sages (Shabbos 156a), "He who is born under Mars will be a man who sheds blood." R’ Ashi says: "Either a surgeon, a thief, a slaughterer, or a mohel." Thus, when one assists such a person to be drawn toward the profession of a mohel, one saves him from the other possibilities, etc. The same applies in our current situation.

With blessings.

#### ***1,784***

**R’ Naftali:** Hakohen, Greensboro. Another letter to him—above, 1,473.

## 1,285

The significance of this celebration has already been explained by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, in his letter regarding the **first** celebration of 12-13 Tammuz in the year 5688 (1928):

To establish it as a day of gathering and inspiration for the strengthening of Torah and Yiddishkeit in every place, according to its specific needs.

He concludes with the blessing: "To all our brothers, lovers of Torah, those who study it, and those who teach it publicly—may Hashem be upon them and may they live—that Hashem may open His good treasury and bestow upon them, and upon all our brothers the Children of Israel, may they live, an abundance of life and blessing without measure. May He strengthen their hearts to increase their courage in the dissemination of Torah and the upholding of Yiddishkeit, and may we all merit to see children and grandchildren occupied with Torah and mitzvos in comfort and with ample livelihood."

May the Ribono shel Olam fulfill the blessings of the Tzaddik, the Nasi of our generation, in their entirety.

**Menachem Schneerson**

3 Tammuz, 5712, Brooklyn, N.Y.

1886
