## 1887

1887

B"H, 7 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Sivan, in which you write that you hope the wedding will take place, *b'sha'ah tovah umutzlachas*, in Menachem Av or before, and that you have set it for Elul in the *tenaim*:

Seemingly, if you do not hold the wedding on 13 Tammuz or before, it is worthwhile to hold it in the month of Elul, the month of mercy, especially since, as you write, you have already set it as such in the *tenaim*...

3) Regarding what you wrote concerning your apprehension that people likely consider you a *lamdan*, while you know your own situation to be otherwise: It is a known ruling of our Sages, "If one says, 'I have labored and found,' believe him." If so, it is in your hands to achieve success in this as is required. Especially since, thanks to your involvement in *chinuch*—performing *tzedakah* in both spiritual and material matters with the sons and daughters of Yisrael—you are aware of the promise of our Rebbe HaZaken (*Torah Or*, at the beginning) that through this, one’s mind and heart become refined a thousand times over. From this, two things are understood: First, that even though one is performing *tzedakah*, one must also engage in Torah study, for it only says that one’s mind and heart become refined. Second, that when one does engage in Torah study, there will be extraordinary success in it—simply put, that in one hour, one will succeed as much as one would have succeeded in a thousand hours without your *tzedakah* work. As explained in *Likutei Torah* for the three *parshiyos*, in the *hagahos* to the aforementioned *drush*, "a thousand times" means literally a thousand times.

4) Regarding your question as to whether it is worthwhile to travel a long distance to *daven* within the walls of the *yeshivah*: Generally, it is impossible to give a blanket answer, as it depends on how long the journey is and whether it affects your health, etc. However, on the other hand, it is worthwhile to make an effort to maintain your connection with the *yeshivah* and its students, etc., for the future as well. Especially since you are marrying into a family that, by your account, is not from Chassidic circles; consequently, even if the travel takes extra time, it is a worthwhile endeavor, and the reward for the walking and the action is in your hands.

5) The same applies to your second question regarding whether you should take upon yourself the work of registering those coming to study *Chassidus* in the *yeshivah*. You should consult regarding this with those who are on-site and are able to assess the importance of this work, etc.

6) Regarding your question: whether the outer garment worn at the *chuppah* should be worn on the first Yom Kippur: This only concerns the *kittel*. There is no requirement that it be the exact same *kittel* worn at the *chuppah*; rather, since one has already worn a *kittel* at the *chuppah*, one should not wear a *kittel* (even a different one) on the Yom Kippur that falls within that year.

7) Regarding your question if it is permitted to taste a little or drink before sleeping: I have never heard of a prohibition regarding this, and perhaps there is some clarification missing from your letter.

8) Regarding what you wrote concerning the books being published by Kehot: I requested some time ago that a library be organized, both in *Yeshivas Toras Emes* and through the *Kollel*, and they promised me months ago that it would be arranged. It is surprising that, according to your letter, the matter is not yet organized. Please be kind enough to inform me of the details, as there is surely a way to rectify this.

With blessings for success in communal matters and in your personal affairs.

#### ***1887***

**worn at the chuppah:** See *Sefer HaMinhagim Chabad*, p. 76.

**to taste... before sleeping:** See below, letter 1916.

May He send you a complete recovery and perform wonders to transform your situation from one extreme to the other. ## 1,190

B"H, 7 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Great peace to the great man, the brilliant Rabbi and pious Chassid, G-d-fearing, sitting in judgment and leading his congregation with integrity, a man of vitality and many accomplishments, etc., etc., his honor, the brilliant Rabbi Raphael Baruch, shlita.

To endless peace and boundless blessing.

Many thanks to your honor for receiving the brilliant Rabbi and pious Chassid, G-d-fearing, engaged in communal needs, etc., Rabbi Shalom Haskind, may he live, with a pleasant countenance. I was pleased to receive a letter from the aforementioned shaliach, in which he engaged in a pilpul with your honor regarding words of Torah.

May Hashem grant each and every one of us our portion in His Torah, to magnify Torah and glorify it, with peace of mind and peace of body, in true abundance.

I ask for your honor’s forgiveness for not having replied to your letter of 26 Iyar and the one preceding it. I have anchored myself in the reliable place of our Sages’ teaching: "One does not respond to a failure." For, given the situation here, to our great pain and sorrow, there is little hope of convening assemblies and protests against the injustice being done to children of religious parents by those who wish to separate them, G-d forbid, from our holy Torah. This situation is well known here, and for several reasons, it has not been possible until now to sway public opinion to come out in an appropriate protest, even though we have made efforts in this regard.

For the time being, there is seemingly no other way but to influence the parents on the spot, so that they might respond with a sharp protest against those who rise up against the souls of their sons and daughters to separate them—may it never be—from the source of living waters, the living G-d, and the Torah of life. May Hashem protect His people Israel wherever they may be, and illuminate the darkness of the galus until the arrival of our Mashiach, the righteous redeemer, speedily in our days.

With abundant blessing to you, your Torah, and those who gather in your shadow.

Rabbi Shalom Haskind, may he live, wrote to me with the names of the associations and organizations here that he handed to your honor in connection with the above. Perhaps, if you were to approach them directly, there might at least be some small measure of salvation, since the matter is coming from "new faces"—from a Rabbi and leader of his congregation in a great city, whose name goes forth, etc., etc.

**1,190**

## 1,191

B"H, 7 Tammuz, 5712

To my dear friend, the distinguished and G-d-fearing man, engaged in communal needs, a man of energy and many accomplishments, etc., R' Yitzchak, may he live.

Shalom and blessings!

I received your letter of May 23rd along with the enclosures, albeit with a slight delay.

I recall what the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, said regarding the center you established and the benefit that can be expected from it; he even participated with his own personal donation for this purpose. Consequently, there is no need for my approval. Nevertheless, I follow in the footsteps of the King and express my encouragement for what you have done in this regard. Through our office, you will also receive my contribution to the center’s activities in the amount of fifteen thousand francs.

Regarding what you write in your letter concerning the erection of a memorial monument for the "grave of the unknown Jewish martyr" in the city of Paris: after asking for your forgiveness that my opinion does not align with yours, I imagine those holy ones who were killed for the sanctification of Hashem’s name, and their reaction to the idea of erecting a monument to their memory in the middle of the city of Paris, and by an organization headed by Chassidim—though Chassidim of the nations of the world—what would they say to such a notion?

Especially since there are now hundreds, thousands, and tens of thousands of living, known martyrs who are in need of a crust of bread in a physical sense, and an even greater number in need of a crust of bread in a spiritual sense.

The primary reason their hunger is not being satisfied is a lack of resources. Consequently, if it is possible to obtain any sum of money, the question immediately arises: should this sum be used to erect a stone monument in a large square in the city of Paris, so that passersby might know or remember that several million Jews were killed for the sanctification of Hashem’s name, or should it be used to revive the souls of those who are hungry and thirsty in the literal sense, or those who are hungry and thirsty for the word of Hashem, the Life of all life? It seems to me that the resolution to this question is not in doubt.

It is true that there is a sort of pretext for the aforementioned idea: that reviving the soul of the hungry and thirsty has already become a routine matter and a daily occurrence, and not everyone will set aside their money for this. Whereas, to erect a large monument in a large city, so that many great figures of Israel and many great figures among the Chassidim of the nations of the world will know of it—in this, they will participate willingly and eagerly.

But after all is said and done, it is difficult to decide and agree to invest thousands of dollars in stone and earth in a corner of Paris, when thousands and tens of thousands of Jews in the Holy Land—may it be built and established—and also outside the land, are crying out for urgent help.

I reiterate my request for your forgiveness for what I wrote above, which is contrary to your opinion, and my hope is strong that you will not take offense at this.

With blessings and respect to you, your wife, and all your household, may they live, your friend.

## 1,994

B"H, 9 Tammuz, 5712

I am sorry that you do not mention anything in your letter regarding *shidduchim*. You have long known my opinion on this, for our Sages of blessed memory have said that it is the way of a man to search, and the parable is of one who has lost an object. We see tangibly that the owner of the lost object does not wait in his place and in his home until someone or other comes and says to him, "I found an object, perhaps it is yours." Rather, he leaves his place, and as our Sages of blessed memory even said, a *chosson* descends a step [in status] and searches for his lost object. May Hashem grant you success.

#### ***1,994***

Published in the *Yagdil Torah* collection, Yerushalayim - *Teshuvos U'Biurim*, p. 317.

## 1,295

B"H, 9 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter of 29 Sivan, and I was pleased to read that you visited Kfar Chabad and attended a Chassidic farbrengen, and that you were inspired by the sincerity and the genuine Yiddishe Chassidishe warmth that you witnessed there.

You surely know the statement of our Sages, "It is not the study that is the essential thing, but the deed"—meaning, the essential thing is not theory, but practical action. This applies to people in general, and especially to the youth.

Everything a person experiences is by Hashgacha Pratis, which should be viewed as a horah mil'ma'alah—a Divine instruction and lesson for oneself personally in life.

You, who still have your whole life ahead of you, must understand that the warmth and Yiddishe Chassidishe spirit that was shown to you is not merely something to be appreciated as a good thing in others, but an instruction to take a deeper look at life and work, and to integrate these good things into your own life.

It goes without saying that a good thing should be shared so that it reaches others as well. I hope that you will see to it to influence your environment to bring in this spirit, this outlook, and this aspiration.

I hope that you will not be satisfied with one visit to Anash, and that you will see to it to be with them from time to time, and also visit the "Beis Rivkah" there, etc.

May Hashem help that your visit to Eretz Yisrael should be successful, and I will be pleased to hear good news from you.

With blessings.

## 1,797

1,797

B"H, 10 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding what you wrote concerning yourself and your wife, may they live: that your wife, may she live, was examined by a specialist physician who found that everything is in order with her, and he is requesting that you also allow yourself to be examined, but you are reluctant to do so because of the *din*, etc.

We have heard regarding this from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, that for these matters one must engage in *mesiras nefesh*, and therefore you should permit yourself to be examined. However, since there are two methods—namely, that they take the *zera* after the *bi'ah* from the woman, which is more lenient according to *din*—you should first proceed in this manner. Only if the specialist physician states clearly that this method is insufficient for the examination, then you should proceed with the second method.

## 1898

1898

B"H, 10 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod,
May they live.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters dated 17, 24, 27 Sivan, and 3 Tammuz, along with the 21 student reports attached, as well as the telegram regarding the handing over of the barracks to the Reshet administration.

2) Regarding what you wrote about the vocational school: I believe I have already written to you that they spoke here once again with Dr. Shapiro, and he promises to do everything in his power—namely, that the Joint will take upon itself all expenses, excluding the building. (Perhaps it is not yet worthwhile to publicize this in a place where it is not relevant, so that they do not cause complications, etc., especially since, judging by your letter, the Vaad HaYeshivos is not satisfied with this.)

I have also already written regarding the building, that you must exert every effort to at least begin it. Perhaps there is hope that even if the Joint cannot assist with the construction, they are permitted to assist with the improvement and refinement of the building. The extent of this improvement and refinement depends on the discretion of the judges and one's acquaintance with them. According to Dr. Shapiro’s assessment, his attitude toward this will be favorable.

3) As for whether to use your barracks for the vocational school: seemingly, it is not worthwhile, as it is too small and cannot be expanded. As mentioned above, it is better to begin the building, which has no such impediment to its expansion.

4) Regarding the budget of four thousand from the Agency, as well as the loan of that amount offered to you some two years ago: I have also already written that you must exert the utmost effort to obtain these as soon as possible, as is understood.

5) Regarding what you wrote about taking the building in the village for the vocational school: since you yourselves add in your letter that it was built and refined for the Yeshiva, I do not understand for what reason they would take it from you. Especially since the Yeshiva already exists, and the vocational school still needs to be founded, etc. It seems from your letter that it is also your opinion not to take it. It is obvious that this will also be the opinion of the Yeshiva administration in the village.

6) I was pleased to read in your letter that you have expanded your borders with more students, but it is understood that you should not grasp at the other extreme and try to take on too much. In any case, one must take into account, to some degree, the size of the income. This is all the more so given the conduct of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, who, although he was accustomed to saying, "I have always been a *baal chov* (debtor)" (referring to the expenses of communal work), nevertheless, even for him, there was a limit to how much the expenses should exceed the income. And it goes without saying that you **must not** take in young children and turn the Yeshiva into a Talmud Torah!

7) Regarding what you wrote concerning the Central British Fund: a letter and memorandum from the office in Paris have been with you for some time, and you must maintain contact with our office in Paris so that your letters and those of the Paris office do not conflict with one another.

8) The *kuntres* that was published for the upcoming Chag HaGeulah surely arrived on time. May you utilize the upcoming days of 12 and 13 Tammuz in an appropriate manner. I look forward to hearing good news regarding this.

Enclosed are seven letters for your students, may they live.

With blessings for Chag HaGeulah to the entire group, may they live,

**M. Schneerson**

1,899

I will conclude my letter with respect, with regards, and with wishes for true health for you and your household, may they live.

Your friend.

P.S. You mention in your letter the adage, "Every delay is for the good." For some time now, I have been searching for the source of this adage in Jewish literature, and I have yet to find it.

## 1772

1772

B"H, 13 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Great peace to the great man, the Torah scholar and Chassid, G-d-fearing, who sits in judgment, etc., etc., Rabbi Eliyahu, may he live, known as Mercado, son of Malka.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter in due time, and I was pleased to hear of your positive interest in the **Ohalei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch** institutions.

Great is the holy merit of the great founder whose name these institutions bear—my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the tzaddik who is the foundation of the world—to bring blessing and success to all who participate in the holy work of these sacred institutions. For **Yosef** is the one who provides sustenance to the entire land, and **Yitzchok** went out to pray in the field toward **evening**—a time when the kelipos and the sitra achra gain strength, G-d forbid, and seek to darken the light of the sun and shield of Hashem Elokim. And our Sages of blessed memory have said: "To pray" (*lasuach*)—*siach* means nothing other than prayer (*tefillah*), *tefillah* being related to the word *tofeil* (to join), as one who repairs and connects earthenware vessels—earth from the ground—to their Creator, their Father in heaven.

It is my prayer and my hope that his merit will stand eternally for all who assist in these holy activities.

And my confidence is strong that your honor, shlita, and all who gather in his shadow, as in the past so now, and especially in the days to come, will extend a helping hand with the lofty strengths with which Hashem, may He be blessed and exalted, has graced every leader among his congregation and community.

And the King—the kings are the Sages—has said: "Uproot the mountain"—the mountain that stands between Yisrael and their Father in heaven due to our sins in this time of double and redoubled darkness of the galus, the "northern" darkness that appears to the tzaddikim as a mountain. And with Heavenly assistance, may it be His will that in our very near future, the prophecy will be fulfilled: "The earth shall be full of the knowledge of Hashem as the waters cover the sea," and they shall see eye to eye when Hashem returns to Tzion through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days, amen.

With blessing and honor.

## 1753

1753

B”H, 13 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and noble philanthropist, a man of distinction, an energetic activist and man of great deeds in supporting Oholei Yosef Yitzchok, crowned with lofty character traits, etc., R’ Yitzchok Almalich, may he live and be well.

For **Yosef** is the provider for all the land, and **Yitzchok** went out to meditate in the field toward **evening**—at a time when the kelipos and the sitra achra gain strength, Heaven forbid, and seek to darken the light of the sun and the shield of Hashem Elokim. Our Sages of blessed memory say that "meditate" (lasuach) refers only to prayer (tefillah). Tefillah is related to the word "to join" (tofeil), as one who repairs and connects earthen vessels—dust from the ground—to their Creator, their Father in Heaven. And prayer, in its literal sense, is that he carries song and prayer on behalf of all those who assist and participate in the support and expansion of the institutions he founded to disseminate Torah and yiras shamayim among the masses, especially during these days of redemption and auspiciousness, the birthday of our Rebbe and his day of redemption.

My confidence is strong that you, as in the past so now, and especially in the days to come, will extend a helping hand in our work with the lofty strengths with which Hashem, may He be blessed and exalted, has graced you.

With wishes for much nachas from your son, may he live and be well.

With blessings for success in all your endeavors, in general and in particular, in both material and spiritual matters alike, I look forward to hearing good news.

## 1,404

1,404

B"H, 13 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

...Regarding your articles, I have read them with interest. In my opinion—and please forgive me for saying this—they do not fulfill the great need of the hour. That need is not to prove to religious people that they must dedicate time to secular studies, for in that area, thank G-d, there are many factors and many people working, and that is not where you should be focusing your efforts. The primary task should be to utilize your knowledge to demonstrate that science cannot contradict religion, and that secular studies without holy studies are untenable. Although I found all of this to a certain extent in your articles, it lacks the strong emphasis required. The assumption that because not everything in science is understood, it is therefore acceptable if there is also a lack of understanding in religion, will not satisfy even the average person who desires and strives to understand and seeks an explanation, etc.

In my opinion, you should utilize your strengths to show that science is merely a product of the human intellect, and the vast majority of it is built upon hypotheses. Even scientists themselves admit this. Consequently, any possibility of using science in general to challenge religion, or to bring contradictions from fields of science such as geology or biology against the knowledge of Torah, is refuted from the outset; for these questions and contradictions have no basis even according to science itself, etc.

Enclosed is the Kuntres that we published in connection with the days of redemption, 12-13 Tammuz—the redemption of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, from his imprisonment by the Soviets. I am certain you will find it of interest for yourself and for those around you.

With blessings.

## 1755

B"H, 13 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter of 22/7, in which you describe your standing in Yiddishkeit and add that you do not wish to commit to a firm decision, as you do not know how the future will turn out.

I wish to emphasize to you here, as I pointed out in my letter of 3 Tammuz, that it is known to all that to a certain extent, a person’s future depends on the person themselves. Specifically regarding you, as I wrote to you, the very fact that you will make a firm, genuine decision to lead a Jewish home—observing Taharas HaMishpacha, keeping a kosher kitchen, and observing Shabbos—with the conviction that it cannot be otherwise, will itself bring your destined zivug to you sooner. Furthermore, it will ensure that the zivug is such that he himself will uphold all of these things, or that you will be able to influence him to do so. A lack of a firm decision in this matter weakens the aforementioned points, both regarding the shidduch itself and the suitability of the shidduch to these standards.

Your request for forgiveness for not making the decision is groundless, for this is a matter that concerns you more than anyone else in the world. It is simply a pity and a source of pain to see that you have the possibility to influence your future in a positive direction, yet you do not grasp it with both hands.

I also understand that through intellect alone, one cannot grasp how your decision can influence the two aforementioned points. However, when one reflects deeply, one sees clearly that through intellect one only understands a small part of this world, and for the majority—the greater part—of the things one does, one must rely on the Ribono shel Olam.

I hope that Hashem Yisbarach will grant you the good thought to make the aforementioned decision, which is good for you both materially and spiritually.

With blessings.

## 1,456

B"H, 14 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 6 Tammuz, in which you write regarding your young daughter... may she live, who has suddenly begun to stutter:

Surely you have sought the advice of a specialist in this field. Even so, there is generally no reason to be overly concerned. It is worth investigating, as it is quite likely that she experienced some sudden fright. Once the cause of the fear is identified and it is explained to her that it has no basis, the stuttering will pass little by little. It might also be worthwhile to change the room in which she sleeps, and likewise to have the mezuzos in your entire home checked to ensure they are kosher. May Hashem grant you success, so that you may bring good news that your daughter has returned to her healthy state.

I hope that you are familiar with the three daily study sessions established for every person by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory: the daily Tehillim, as divided for the days of the month, to be recited each day after Shacharis; the daily study of the Chumash with Rashi from the weekly parsha; and the daily Tanya, as divided for the days of the year. I trust you are maintaining them, as they are a channel and vessel for drawing down and receiving the blessings of Hashem in whatever each person requires.

With blessings.

## 1708

1708

B"H, 14 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Efraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter of 10 Tammuz and the one preceding it with pleasure. As you requested, while I was at the Ohel of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, on the festival of redemption and special virtue, 13 Tammuz, I mentioned you and your household, may they live, as noted at the bottom of your letter.

Regarding what you noted in your letter of 22 Sivan, that the matter of Zerubavel mentioned in *Likutei Torah*, *Beha'aloscha*, in the *maamar* beginning "Beha'aloscha" and in the *maamar* "Zeh Ma'aseh HaMenorah" was not clear to you: You did not explain in your letter what contradiction you found in this. In both discourses, it is explained that Zerubavel is named for the verse, "And I will sow the house of Israel with the seed of man and the seed of beast" (*Yirmiyahu 31:26*), which is the concept of *Bavel* (Babylon), for there He confused (*balal*) the languages, and it is by way of sowing—this is the name Zerubavel. This is applied both to the entire generation—that the Jews of that generation are called Zerubavel—and to the Nasi, the head, in whom all the limbs are included.

Your observation is correct that the *maamar* "Zeh Ma'aseh HaMenorah" is one of the shorter *maamarim* in *Likutei Torah*, as it is one of the *maamarim* from before Petersburg, as explained in the *sicha* of 19 Kislev printed in *Toras Shalom*, page 33.

With blessings for a healthy summer for you and your entire household, may they live, and with respect.

#### ***1708***

Rabbi Efraim Eliezer, may he live: Yalles. Additional letters to him—above 1529, and in the references noted there.

Page 33: In the new editions, p. 26.

## 1509

1509

B"H, 15 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and accomplished man of many virtues, a great activist, scion of a noble lineage, etc., etc., R' Shazar, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings,

As you have informed me that you are preparing, G-d willing, to depart tomorrow on a successful journey, I hereby wish to convey my blessing for a safe trip, that you may reach your destination in peace and good health, and for many years to come, continue to utilize your influence to assist in the affairs of the Chabad movement in all areas within your reach.

I look forward to receiving good news of your successful arrival, and I thank you in advance.

On this occasion, I wish to express my gratitude for your visit and for the opportunity to become personally acquainted with you.

I have once again witnessed the truth of the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, that the tradition of the forefathers and the lineage of Anash live on, exist, and remain active in their descendants until the end of all generations.

This was confirmed for me in our conversation, for although, as you noted, it has been about forty years since you left Russia, the vitality of Chassidus—the heritage of your fathers—is still alive within you and finds expression in actual deeds. It is my hope that, just as with any living thing, where the sign of life is growth and development, so too will your participation in the good works of Chabad, the root from which you were hewn, grow and expand.

Following up on our conversation, I hope that the matter we discussed at length has found a proper echo in your heart and that you are attending to it with special care. This is the necessity of providing the opportunity for those individuals connected to our movement who have immigrated to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, to gain a foothold in the land and arrange productive lives there, without being forced to expend their energies defending their views and way of life. One of the primary conditions for this is that the vast majority of them be concentrated in one location, which would then enable them to continue their way of life more easily. Regarding the economic aspect, since they lack means—having left their countries destitute and empty-handed—they require extraordinary assistance, both for settling into the field of agriculture and in the fields of industry and manual labor. First and foremost, according to my information and also based on your own words, this requires suitable buildings, both for vocational training and for developing their sources of livelihood.

As I mentioned to you in person, the straightforward way to bring the matter of the buildings to fruition is for the appropriate offices in Eretz Yisrael to provide the materials and means required for the construction. Then, it would be possible to proceed immediately to organize these matters. When I have to resolve the question of settling many of Anash, may they live, who are currently abroad—in about a few months’ time—I will be able to do so with a confident heart, knowing that by then the buildings will have been completed, or at the very least, will be nearing completion.

Furthermore, since under the influence of Anash there is also youth entering the age of Youth Aliyah, the question of a suitable building for the absorption of these youths is also on the agenda, just as you pointed out to me during your visit.

If, after all efforts in this regard, the appropriate offices are unwilling to erect the buildings at their own expense under any circumstances, I reiterate the proposal I made to you in person: that it be done on a fifty-fifty basis, meaning that over the course of several years, I will reimburse half of the expenses incurred for the buildings.

I hope that through your great influence, you will succeed in ensuring that at least my second proposal is accepted, in order to put the plan into action as soon as possible.

I will conclude as I began, with hope and confidence in your keen sensitivity to all matters close to us, which will find their proper expression in actual deeds—especially since you yourself began by questioning why more of Anash are not settling in the land. This proves that you will do whatever is within your power to assist in this with a willing heart and dedication.

I look forward to hearing good news from you, and I wish you good health and a safe journey.

## 1510

1510

B"H, 15 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R' Aharon Hakohen, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

Through your brother, the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R' Yaakov Hakohen, may he live, I received your request for a blessing and the enclosed check for tzedakah to be distributed at my discretion: $100.

Since we are still in the week of 12-13 Tammuz, which is the birthday of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and the anniversary of his liberation from imprisonment (for his work in establishing yeshivos, Talmud Torahs, and strengthening Yiddishkeit in that country), and you surely know that since his passing, a network of yeshivos and Talmud Torahs has been established which bear his name, "Ohalei Yosef Yitzchak," in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, in Africa, Australia, and so on—I have therefore deposited your contribution into the fund that supports the aforementioned institutions. The merit of this tzedakah is great enough to draw down blessing and success for you in your needs. Because these institutions are connected to the name of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and, most importantly, to his spirit in their conduct, helping these institutions especially strengthens the connection with him, which is an additional channel to draw down and sustain the blessings of Hashem.

Your brother, may he live, also asked on your behalf whether you should send your children to study at the Talmud Torah in Miami Beach, where they study for only an hour and a half.

My opinion on this is that you should do so. There are many reasons for this: 1) The children will maintain a connection with Torah every day, and not, G-d forbid, the opposite, for regarding Torah it is written: "If you forsake Me for one day, I will forsake you for two days"—meaning that if one leaves the Torah for one day, it leaves him for two. 2) Associating with children from a frum Talmud Torah brings the children much benefit, which is not so easy to find in your surroundings. There are also other reasons, and because of all this, you should send your children to the Talmud Torah in Miami Beach.

With a blessing for parnassah.

## 1511

1511

B”H, 15 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Through the intermediary of the G-d-fearing, honorable, and faithful businessman, our friend Rabbi Yaakov HaKohen Katz, I have received your request for a blessing, specifically regarding the fact that you and your kallah—may they live—have set the date of your wedding for the Sunday following Shabbos Nachamu.

I wish you that your wedding take place in a good and auspicious hour, *b’mazal tov*, and that you build a Jewish home upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos.

It is, of course, unnecessary to emphasize that the deeper meaning of a wedding is that you are going to build a life together—a happy life, a structure for many good years. It is self-evident that the most important thing is that the foundation upon which this structure is built must be of strong material, capable of withstanding various changes in temperature, humidity, earthquakes, and the like. So too, when one goes to build a life together, it must be established upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos. These are the strongest materials in existence, which have stood the test of various difficulties throughout the approximately 3,300 years since Torah and mitzvos were given to us by Hashem Yisbarach. These are the vessels for receiving the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach, so that it may be a truly happy life. May Hashem Yisbarach help you, as stated, *b’mazal tov*, and may you build an eternal structure upon the foundations of Torah and mitzvos.

With blessing,

## 1952

## 1753

1753

B"H, 18 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter informing me that you have received your kabbalah as a shochet. May it be the will of Hashem that you succeed in your work, which is a *meleches shamayim* (heavenly craft). You are surely aware of the ruling of our Nasi, our holy Rebbes—and specifically our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, and the Tzemach Tzedek—in their Shulchan Aruch and responsa, that a shochet must be exceptionally *yirei shamayim*. Since everything occurs via *hashgacha pratis*, you have certainly been granted the strength for this; the matter depends only on you. With the appropriate *yigias nefesh* (exertion of soul) and *yigias basar* (exertion of body), you will succeed in this as well.

This corresponds to what is written in *Tanna D'bei Rabbi Yishmael*: "‘And he shall slaughter’ (*veshachat*) implies only ‘and he shall draw’ (*umashach*)." Just as it is the role of the shochet in the physical sense to draw the flesh of the animal or bird from the level of a living creature so that it may become blood and flesh like the flesh of a human (*medaber*), so too may you succeed in drawing your own *nefesh habehamis*, as well as that of others, so that it becomes *batel* and is integrated into the *nefesh elokis*, which is called *Adam*—*adamah l'elyon* (I will resemble the Most High).

With blessings for success.

***1753***

Published in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 12, p. 141.

## 1514

1514

B”H, 18 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter asking for my opinion on whether you should look into moving:

I have long since stated to all of anash—may they live—who are in Paris and its surroundings, that I see no reason for panic and I see no reason for moving. This is especially true since you are surely aware of the difficulties and burdens involved in the proper resettlement of those who moved to Canada, Australia, and so on. To my regret, these difficulties concern not only their material situation, but also their spiritual state, which has not improved. Since the Ribono shel Olam has granted you the merit of working in the tent of Torah at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, why would you leave a position where you find your livelihood in peace and tranquility, only to place yourself in trials? May the Ribono shel Olam grant you success in finding satisfaction and being happy with your lot; and there is certainly much to be satisfied with.

With blessings,

P.S. Please be kind enough to show this letter of mine to the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and refined, involved in communal needs, etc., Rabbi Nissan, may he live, Nemesov, and ask him to publicize this opinion of mine to all of anash—may they live—with the appropriate explanation, so that I will not need to answer each person individually.

Enclosed is the reshimah published for the days of redemption and special significance, 12 and 13 Tammuz; I am sure you will share this merit with the many.

## 1515

1515

B”H, 20 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the honorable Rabbi and Chassid, a man of stature and wisdom, etc.,
Rabbi Avraham Yaakov, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

It has been some time since I received your letter, and due to the press of many duties, I did not have the time to answer it as I should have. Although even now time does not permit me to write at length, I will at least respond briefly:

You note in your letter what the Beis Yosef writes in *Siman* 262, *d.h. Garsinan*, in the name of the Ritva, in the name of his teacher (the Ra’ah), that on a cloudy day, one who does not wish to rely on the principle that "Hashem protects the simple" (*shomer pesaim Hashem*) has the authority to postpone a *bris milah* past its proper time, and he acts correctly. You raise a difficulty: why did the Beis Yosef not rule according to this opinion in his *Shulchan Aruch*, especially since it is a matter of *pikuach nefesh*? You remain with this question.

To my mind, the difficulty you raise is not well-founded. One cannot question why he did not rule or cite a lone opinion in his *Shulchan Aruch*, given that all the *Rishonim* hold contrary to the Ritva (as they did not include the matter of a cloudy day or a windy day in their works). Among them are the Rif, the Rambam, and the Rosh, who are the pillars of the Beis Yosef’s rulings. Furthermore, it is evident that Rabbeinu Yeruchem and the R’ Manoach, who are cited there in the Beis Yosef, disagree with the Ritva. And if you were to say that it is still difficult why those aforementioned *Rishonim* did not rule that it is forbidden to perform a *bris* on a cloudy day, one can say simply that they followed the conclusion of the Gemara that "Hashem protects the simple." One can also bring proof from *Yevamos* (71b), where Rav Papa should have answered that we are dealing with a case where it was a cloudy day at the time of the procedure, and afterwards the clouds dispersed (though this is difficult for the R’ Yeruchem as well, as is understood). The reason of the author of the *sugya* itself can be explained by the fact that it is a remote concern that a cloudy day would harm the infant, who is in bed at home—similar to what the Tzemach Tzedek wrote in *Piskei Dinim* for *Yoreh Deah*, *Siman* 263. Even one who is aware of the concern regarding a cloudy day still falls under the permit, because since the masses have practiced it, "Hashem protects the simple," as is the implication of the simple reading of the *sugya* in *Yevamos* 12b and our own *sugya*. Moreover, even according to the Ritva, it is only **the authority** of the individual to postpone, etc., which itself implies that he also has the authority to rely on "Hashem protects the simple," etc. Aside from the above, see regarding this in *Responsa Chaim Sha’al*, Vol. 1, *Siman* 50; *Tzemach Tzedek Responsa*, *Even HaEzer*, end of *Siman* 11; and *Sdei Chemed*, *Asifat Dinim*, *Ma’arechet Milah*, *Siman* 2, subsection 13. See there also that the dispute of the Ritva, etc., follows their position regarding the dispute of the "three women who use a *moch*," which the aforementioned *poskim* omitted.

I saw in the introduction to your book that you mention your grandfather, of blessed memory. I will transcribe here what I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which will surely interest you. Here is the holy content:

R’ Zalman Neimark was a Rav in Starodub. When they wanted to fabricate the blood libel against the grandfather (the Rebbe Maharash, regarding the blood libel), he took it upon himself, saying: "It is his hour!" And he sat in prison for several years. When he heard the *maamar* "All who derive pleasure" from the Rebbe Rashab, he said: "I do not desire Your people; I do not need *Moshiachim*—right now I am being included in the *Atzmus*. And when we left the *tish* and went to the *mikveh*, the father (the Rebbe Rashab) went in alone, and we all remained waiting outside. R’ Zalman said, using the language of the Rambam: '...and the *mikveh* does not purify, rather it is a decree, etc.'—as if I am a Jew who needs the *mikveh*, not the *mikveh* needing me—'but I have issued a decree, I have enacted a statute, etc.'"

Enclosed is the *kuntres* that was published for the *Chag HaGeulah* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—the days of redemption and special spiritual influence, 12 and 13 Tammuz, which have passed—which will surely interest you. Please accept my apologies for the delay in my response until now.

With blessings.

## 1,516

B"H, 21 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you inform me that you have reached the age of twelve:

Surely you know that at this age you become obligated in the performance of mitzvos. As our Sages of blessed memory have said, "extra understanding" was granted to women, which is why the "bas mitzvah" of the daughters of Israel occurs one year before the "bar mitzvah" of the sons of Israel. May Hashem grant that you grow ever higher in knowledge and upright conduct, and may your parents—may they live—derive from you, and from their other children—may they live—Yiddishe nachas and Chassidishe nachas.

Surely you are also making an effort to influence your surroundings, to instill within them the warmth of yiras shamayim and Chassidus, for this is also an additional channel and vessel for receiving the blessings of Hashem.

With blessings.

## 1757

1757

B”H, 21 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To our dear Anash and G-d-fearing individuals, all who cherish Torah and mitzvos,
Residing in the city of Chicago,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life,

Shalom Rav and Bracha!

The holy institutions of Lubavitch — the **Tomchei Temimim** Yeshiva network and the institutions under its administration; the **Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch** and the institutions under its administration — are in a very precarious financial state, which, G-d forbid, places their very existence in jeopardy.

Divine success has hovered over these institutions since the day of their founding, and we are witnesses to a Divine spectacle: the flourishing and expansion of these institutions, which bear fruit and the fruit of fruit—lights that illuminate our brethren, the Children of Israel, in all their places of residence. Yet, at the same time, the institutions are currently facing a severe financial crisis that touches upon their very existence.

This situation necessitates seeking extraordinary financial resources, and it has been decided to organize a **United Emergency Campaign** in Chicago for the aforementioned Lubavitch institutions.

Knowing the attitude of our brethren, the Children of Israel, in Chicago in general, and Anash of Chicago in particular, toward the monumental enterprises of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and their inner desire to come to the aid of the institutions he founded, it is my hope that now, too, they will extend a helping hand and a generous hand to fill their dire need.

Upon each and every one of Anash in Chicago rests the duty and the privilege to exert effort in this assistance, both through their own participation with an extraordinary sum, and through their influence upon all their acquaintances and friends to do the same, thereby assisting in the success of the campaign and enabling the continued existence and future development of the institutions, to increase Torah with yiras shamayim and to make it glorious.

And all who assist and volunteer are already assured that this great mitzvah of tzedakah will draw down upon them and upon all their households, may they live, the blessings of Hashem in all that they require: children, life, and abundant sustenance.

With regards and blessing them with an abundance of goodness, both material and spiritual,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1518

B.H., 21 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter from the eve of Shabbos Parshas Shelach, in which you describe your current life, how you have become drawn close to Anash, and the remnants that still remain of the "opposite of good," etc., etc., and that you cannot control yourself, etc., etc.:

Since you see that Hashem has taken you out of that place of darkness and placed you in the source of light—namely, Torah, mitzvos, and specifically the study of Chassidus—it follows that you are moving from left to right. Therefore, the despair and the conclusion you have reached that your teshuvah is not genuine come from the counsel of the Yetzer Hara, who seeks to overcome a Yid in whatever way he can.

You must observe the three well-known shiurim established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, zatzuklalleh, nvg"m, zy"a: a shiur in Tehillim—as the Tehillim is divided according to the days of the month—every day after davening in the morning; studying every day a parsha of Chumash with the commentary of Rashi, from the weekly sedra; and a shiur in Tanya—as the Tanya is divided according to the days of the year. Furthermore, give a prutah to tzedakah every day—naturally, excluding Shabbos and Yom Tov—before davening. All of this will provide the Yetzer Hatov with the strength to overcome the Yetzer Hara.

Regarding your wife, one must always remember that the entire Knesses Yisrael, and every Yid in particular, is called the spouse of the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He. When we ask Hashem that He—blessed be He—should conduct Himself with Knesses Yisrael, whom He calls "My beloved," by fulfilling their heart's desires for the good, it is well known that an *is'arusa d'leila* (arousal from above) comes through an *is'arusa d'lata* (arousal from below). Therefore, one must conduct himself in the same way with his own wife. As the Gemara says, one should honor her more than himself. Especially when one reflects on the fact that we are standing at the end of the galus and the complete Geulah is near, may it come immediately, at which time "the female shall encompass the male," this in itself brings a feeling of respect and caution regarding one's wife. View her as a daughter of Avraham, Yitzchak, and Yaakov. Even if she has a shortcoming, many times that shortcoming is actually the result of the husband's conduct, which makes her an "eshes listim" (a wife of a robber); however, it is also possible for her to be an "eshes chaver k'chaver" (a wife of a scholar who is like a scholar).

You must have the mezuzos in your home checked to ensure they are all kosher. Also, have your tefillin checked. Surely you check the tzitzis of your tallis gadol every day, as well as those of your tallis katan, as is the law and custom. You should also sleep in a tallis katan. All these things, together with what was mentioned above, lead to yiras shamayim and shalom bayis. I look forward to hearing good news from you regarding all of the above.

Enclosed is the reshimah that was published for the days of redemption and segulah, 12 and 13 Tammuz. Surely you will use this to be *mezakeh es harabim* (merit the public) and also share the content of this reshimah with your wife, tichyeh.

With blessings,

## 1519

B"H, 21 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

...I was pleased to read in your letter that you are occupied with the construction of a new mikveh that will be of the highest standard of *hiddur*, although you do not write the specific details of the mikveh’s construction. I am certain that you, too, will endeavor to do so in your mikveh. Great is the merit of this mitzvah, for "the mikveh of Yisrael is Hashem," to bless all those who occupy themselves with this with children, life, and sustenance, and to bring closer the general salvation of *Klal Yisrael*, as explained in *Tosafos Yom Tov* at the end of *Maseches Yoma*.

With blessing.

## 1760

1760

May Hashem grant you success in establishing times for Torah and for public study sessions, and in particular to teach the practical conduct that they should follow in their daily lives. The most suitable material for this is the study of halachos, whether from the Siddur in Shaar HaKollel, the Kitzur Shulchan Aruch, or similar works, and "action is the essential thing."

Enclosed is the reshimah that was published for the days of redemption and spiritual elevation, 12 and 13 Tammuz, to be used to bring merit to the public.

With blessing,

## 1761

1761

B.H., 21 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok-Lubavitch
in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established,
May they live.

Peace and Blessing!

I received in due time your letter of 27 Sivan and 3 Tammuz, along with the enclosures. Enclosed herewith is the return of the letter from the Ministry of Education and Culture dated 11 Sivan that you sent to me, as you may need it during the course of your work. In general, the proper procedure is for the original to remain at the institution to which it was addressed, and for you to send me a photocopy of such letters.

Regarding the opposition from the municipality of Lod, you should try to approach Mr. Ephraim Krasner, may he live, and remind him that he visited me some time ago together with Dr. Yaakov Griffel, may he live. In the course of our conversation, when we spoke about religious coercion in the Holy Land, he promised me that if I were aware of such a case and informed him, he would arrange matters to align with justice and fairness. (Although directly this does not fall under his purview, as I believe he is in the Settlement Department of the Jewish Agency, he is nevertheless a man of influence.) Since this is the first time I am approaching him in accordance with his promise, it is my hope that he will intervene and succeed. You may also approach Mr. Shazar, may he live, and tell him as well that, in accordance with our conversation, he will surely utilize his influence to rectify the injustice.

I hope that you are arranging matters in such a way that you do not invest funds in shacks and buildings, especially since the administration of Yeshivas Lod promised me they would provide one shack. Surely there are places where you can work to have the local municipality provide a suitable building, and in other places, with the appropriate pressure, you will certainly receive support from the activists. This is all the more true given what they provide to political parties; how much more so should they provide for non-partisan, Charedi institutions.

5) A rumor reached me that for the summer months you have taken some bochurim from Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod to serve as teachers. Surely you considered beforehand that they would be suitable and successful in matters of education and guidance. As I have written many times, the institutions of the Reshet must serve as a model and symbol for the activities of Chabad institutions. This opinion was further strengthened in me after my conversation with Mr. Shazar. It is also understood that for the avreichim, it is not appropriate to leave the walls of the yeshivah to become teachers. This is certainly only a temporary measure, until you are assured of the approval of the Reshet institutions and their budget, at which point you will hire professional teachers, and the avreichim will return to their studies with diligence, persistence, and added success.

11) Regarding the proposal that the students of the Reshet study at Yeshivas Lod and be brought to the yeshivah daily: one should not mix one matter with another. Just as Yeshivas Lod must be careful to maintain its character as a **yeshivah**, so too must you maintain your own character, which is that the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok is for everyone, and not specifically for Temimim or the children of Temimim. You must be extremely careful at the initial stage of this endeavor, as there are surely those who are watching with a critical eye, looking for faults.

12) Regarding what you wrote about whether to demand from the Minister of Education that there be a supervisor specifically for your institutions: one should not do this without first investigating the prospects for fulfilling this request. It is possible that it is still too early for this, especially since there is a rationale to say that after the institutions are approved, your demand will be more justified, and one should not put the approval of the institutions at risk by doing it after the fact, which is not the case now. There is also a rationale to the contrary, but since it is a responsible step, it should not be taken without prior investigation and inquiry.

13) Thank you for sending the transcript of your conversation with Mr. Shazar. Surely you will do the same in the future, in due time, so that the transcript arrives here in good time, the day before he comes here.

14) I learned that Rabbi Abuchatzeira, may he live, published his letter regarding you. It is strange that you did not inform me of this beforehand. Please send a copy of his letter.

15) The Reshet is named after my father-in-law, the Rebbe. It is explained in Chassidus in many places that a name indicates the source, the channel of vitality, etc. Consequently, it is understood and simple that this is not a place for personal agendas, ulterior motives, etc. It is also understood how great the merit, the responsibility, and the potential for success (and from the positive we can infer the negative) are in this.

With a blessing for success in your holy work, awaiting the good news that peace and success dwell upon you and among you.

## 1,722

B"H, 22 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, who engages in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Dovid Nosson, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter from the past day of redemption and unique spiritual potential, 13 Tammuz. Regarding what you wrote—asking for my opinion on whether you should publicize the view of those who prohibit machine-made tzitzis: while it is true that several of the great Acharonim are stringent in this matter, as is known from the Responsa Divrei Chaim, Maharsham, and Machazeh Avraham, it is also known, on the other hand, that several Acharonim were lenient and permitted it; see Responsa Chesed L'Avraham and Tiferes Yosef. Most importantly, there is the practical halachic ruling of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, from his father, the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory.

Therefore, in my opinion, it is not advisable to decide in favor of either side. This is especially true since the ruling of the Rebbe (Rashab) was regarding the practical application. Furthermore, there is a risk that people will say that your declaration, may you live, is merely a stringency, and consequently, the other details you write regarding this matter will also be viewed as nothing more than stringencies and refinements for those who wish to be extra meticulous (*mehadrin min hamehadrin*).

Enclosed is the *reshima* that I published for the days of redemption and unique spiritual potential, 12 and 13 Tammuz. Surely you also have the *kuntres* that I published for these days, and may you merit to share them with the public...

With blessings for a healthy summer, both physically and spiritually.

#### ***1,722***

**Practical halachic ruling:** See above, Vol. 3, letter 417; below, 1,800.

## 1724

1724

If a little light pushes away much darkness, then certainly a great deal of light does so all the more, and there is nothing that can stand before the will. ## 1,725

B"H, 22 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter—which lacks the date of writing—containing the good news;

Surely you will contemplate the goodness of Hashem, how "closeness to Elokus is good for me," and may the Ribono shel Olam grant that, little by little, you will also come to contemplate the goodness of Elokus and the goodness of Hashem as they are from their own perspective. As is explained in many places in Chassidus, there is a distinction here. Simply put, this means that in matters of holiness, one should not think only of what is necessary or what is good for oneself, but rather of the essence of the matter itself. This will naturally lead to action for the benefit of others as well, which is the purpose of the creation of man—that he strives for the good of his fellow no less than for his own good. This is especially possible for one to whom the Ribono shel Olam shows a good matter through Hashgacha Pratis, for then the Yetzer Hara becomes smaller. May the Ribono shel Olam help you that, through your avodah, you will diminish it even further.

With blessings.

## 1756

B"H, 22 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from the day of redemption and unique spiritual potency, 13 Tammuz, in which you announce that the *tana'im* (engagement contract) were written in a good and auspicious hour, I reiterate my blessing that it should be in a good and auspicious hour and result in an everlasting edifice.

Regarding your complaint about your standing and situation, specifically the lack of tangible and visible results in the outreach activities you are conducting: enclosed is a copy of what I said to the students traveling on a *shlichus* for the *Malach* (Merkaz L'Inyanei Chinuch). In truth, these words apply to all those who wander from their place, and perhaps even to all *Bnei Yisrael* in general. For every single *neshamah* has wandered from its place—having been hewn from beneath the Throne of Glory, with its source even higher than that—and has traveled and descended, etc., from a high roof to a deep pit, to fulfill its *shlichus* in this world. It is known what is explained in *Tanya*, and it is also evident in practice, that matters performed out of sadness are not as they ought to be, whereas *simcha* brings benefit to all matters of *avodah*.

Regarding your question about the timing of the wedding—whether it should be in Kislev or specifically after your release from the army, in Nissan: why must you decide this now? Since this concerns the coming year, after the upcoming *Rosh Hashanah*—when we will be inscribed and sealed among all of *Klal Yisrael* for a good and sweet year—you can decide this matter then as well.

With blessings for success in your activities among your surroundings and in all your affairs.

## 1726*

[Late Tammuz, 5712]

...Although my words on Wednesday, the 16th of Tammuz, were addressed to the students traveling on behalf of the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch to the various regions of the United States to strive to uphold Yiddishkeit, in truth, they apply to every single Jewish man and woman. Just as with these matters, so it is with every Jewish man and woman: for the neshamah is hewn from beneath the Kisei HaKavod, and even higher than that. As our Sages of blessed memory stated, the thought of Yisrael preceded everything, even the Torah, which preceded the world by two thousand years. And although a human’s thought is merely a part of the person thinking and not the thing itself, regarding the Ribono shel Olam—of Whom it is written, "For My thoughts are not your thoughts"—it is through His thought that the thing came into being, albeit in a loftier manner and on a higher level. As is explained in several places, there exist higher worlds called the worlds of thought, through which the neshamos came into being, even though they were on a much higher level than when they descended below (see Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah by our Alter Rebbe, Chapter 11). From there, the neshamah traveled and descended, level by level, through the Seder Hishtalshelus, from the highest roof to the deepest pit, to this physical and material world, where the concealments, the hesterim, and the obstacles to the avodah of Hashem are many, preventing one from beholding the pleasantness of Hashem. This is the reason, as our Sages of blessed memory stated, that "against your will you live." Yet, the demand of the Torah remains: "Serve Hashem with joy."

All of a person’s life must be an uninterrupted continuation of the avodah of Hashem, so that all his days are complete, filled with actions that fulfill his shlichus in this world, and they must be with joy. And even if he knows in his soul the magnitude of the descent his neshamah has undergone, this does not prevent the great joy of having merited to be a shaliach of the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He, to illuminate the world and all that is in it with the "candle of a mitzvah and the light of Torah." And even if he does not understand this with his intellect, knowing his standing and his situation—as the saying goes, "Would that your departure from the world be like your entry into the world"—it has nevertheless arisen in His will, may He be blessed, even if it is not understood by human intellect, that there should be a descent from the highest roof to the deepest pit for the sake of an even higher ascent. And every man and woman who approaches the fulfillment of this shlichus with joy and a glad heart is promised by our Sages of blessed memory that they are assisted from Above; and even if one sanctifies himself only a little from below, they sanctify him greatly from Above...

## 1,727

1,727

B"H, 22 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 4 Tammuz, in which you inform me of your current situation, and that there is now an opportunity to enter into a partnership with your brother-in-law, which would then lead him to also become a Shomer Shabbos, and you request a blessing to find a good buyer for the house you wish to sell so that you can enter into this partnership:

I was startled to read such a thing in the letter of a Jew, for all Jews are believers, the children of believers. If you will listen to my opinion and advice, you should immediately become a Shomer Shabbos, without waiting for the partnership to be finalized. This very act—not placing conditions upon Hashem (that first you will sell your house and only then keep Shabbos)—will itself draw down additional blessing and success, enabling you to find your livelihood in abundance.

Reflect within yourself: what effect does this matter (the lack of Shabbos observance) have on your children, may they live? Even if they are not speaking about it at the moment, it surely remains in their memory, etc., etc.

When I am at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention you for the fulfillment of your request—that you be able to arrange your livelihood as soon as possible so that you are not placed in a test regarding Shabbos observance—and for the fulfillment of my request: that you become a Jew who keeps Shabbos, Torah, and mitzvos immediately. It is well known that for a Jewish person, the physical and the spiritual are bound and united, as it is written: "If you walk in My statutes... then I will give your rains in their season," etc.

You do not mention in your letter the manner of education for your daughter and son, may they live. It is superfluous to point out the necessity that they receive a Jewish education in the fullest sense of the term.

It would be appropriate to have all the mezuzos in your home checked to ensure they are all kosher, and to arrange to recite some chapters of Tehillim every day. It is best if it follows the division of Tehillim for the days of the month or the days of the week.

The donation you sent has been delivered to the Bikur Cholim fund. May Hashem grant you a healing of the soul, so that you may be healthy and whole in the 248 positive mitzvos and 365 negative mitzvos, for this draws down complete health in the 248 limbs and 365 sinews. I look forward to hearing good news regarding all of the above.

With blessings,

P.S. Enclosed is the Kuntres published in connection with the days of redemption and spiritual elevation, 12 and 13 Tammuz, which just passed. Surely you will share its merit with the public.

## 1729

B"H, 22 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the G-d-fearing, honorable, and diligent worker in the holy task,
R' Moshe שי' Lachiani

Peace and Blessing!

Your letter of 18 Tammuz has been received.

For some time now, I have heard of your good work in the field of education, drawing the hearts of the sons and daughters of Yisrael closer to their Father in Heaven. It is a well-known ruling of our Sages (at the end of Taanis) that "whoever adds, they add to him." One of the interpretations of this is that whoever adds to their efforts in Torah and mitzvos, they add to him from Above—both in the capacity to expand his activities in Torah and mitzvos, and in the growth of his desire to do so, as he goes from strength to strength.

Especially in your current work, where you oversee the villages where our brothers and sisters reside, a holy duty and privilege has been placed upon your shoulders by Divine Providence: to bring, awaken, and illuminate the settlements of the children of Yisrael with the "lamp of a mitzvah and the light of Torah," and the "light of the Torah"—which is the teachings of Chassidus. Through this, one also draws down blessing and success in one's material affairs. As it is written in the Torah: "If you walk in My statutes"—which refers to the study of Torah, as stated in the Sifra and cited in the commentary of Rashi—"and keep My mitzvos"—which refers to the negative commandments, for as our Sages said, wherever the terms "guard," "lest," or "do not" are used, it refers to a negative commandment—"and perform them"—this refers to the positive commandments. The verse then promises: "I will give your rains"—and furthermore, I will give them "in their time," etc.

Happy is his portion, for he is one of the shluchim of the Ribono shel Olam to fulfill this task in His world. May it be the will of Hashem that very soon, blessing and success will also be extended to your personal matters. That is to say, in accordance with the promise of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe (in the beginning of Torah Or), may your mind and heart become a thousand times more refined, so that you may increase your fixed times for the study of the revealed Torah and the teachings of Chassidus, and ascend from strength to strength. And may it be arranged for you very soon, in a manner that is fitting, regarding the matter of shidduchim, both materially and spiritually alike.

With blessings for success.

B"H, 22 Tammuz, 5712

This is especially true in these days of exile, a double and redoubled darkness, where an additional light is required to shine with the "sun and shield" of Hashem Elokim, until the end of our exile arrives, and the prophecy is fulfilled: "Even the night shall shine like the day."

## 1731

B"H, 23 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the honorable Rabbi, the Chassid, the G-d-fearing man, who sits in judgment, a man of vitality, a man of many accomplishments, etc., etc., Rabbi Shaul Danan, shlita,
Av Beis Din of the holy community of Rabat, may it be preserved.

Peace and blessing!

I received your esteemed letter, and I was pleased to receive regards regarding the good work of the **Ohalei Yosef Yitzchak Lubavitch** institutions, which carry the name of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, the tzaddik who is the foundation of the world. **Yosef** is the provider for all the land, and **Yitzchak** went out to pray in the field toward **evening**—at a time when the kelipos and the sitra achra gain strength, G-d forbid—seeking to darken the light of the sun and shield of Hashem Elokim. Our Sages of blessed memory said, "There is no 'siach' (prayer) other than the language of tefillah," tefillah being related to the word *tofeil* (joining), as one who joins earthenware vessels, repairing and connecting the earthenware—the dust of the earth—to their Creator, their Father in heaven.

It is my prayer and hope that his merit will stand forever for all those who assist and participate in these holy activities. I am firmly confident that your honor, shlita, and all those who gather in your shadow, will—as in the past, so now, and especially in the days to come—extend a helping hand with the lofty strengths with which Hashem, may He be blessed and exalted, has graced every leader of his congregation and community.

And the King said—"Who are the kings? The Rabbis"—that they uproot the mountain, the mountain that stands between Yisrael and their Father in heaven due to our sins during this time of double and redoubled darkness of galus, the "northern" darkness that appears to the tzaddikim as a mountain. With the help of Heaven, may it be His will that in our very near future, the prophecy will be fulfilled: "The earth shall be full of the knowledge of Hashem as the waters cover the sea," and they will see eye to eye when Hashem returns to Tzion through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days, Amen.

Regarding your inquiry as to whether it is possible to find in the United States copies of the *Beis Yosef* and the *Rambam*, and their prices in local currency: the *Tur Beis Yosef* is difficult to obtain. However, the *Shulchan Aruch* (the volumes of *Even HaEzer*, *Choshen Mishpat*, and *Orach Chaim*) can be obtained for a price of 44 dollars, and the *Yoreh Deah* for approximately 30 dollars. The *Rambam* is priced at 56 dollars; all of this is available through the booksellers here. Since your honor, shlita, wrote that you require four copies, if it is a burden for you to pay for all of them, I will instruct the office of **Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch** to send one of the four copies free of charge as a gift, provided I receive your confirmation regarding this.

With blessing and appropriate honor.

## 1733

1733

B”H, 24 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

Through the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and diligent communal worker, [Name], I have received a *pidyon nefesh* on your behalf, in which he writes that your health is not as it should be due to your gallbladder, and that doctors are advising you to undergo surgery.

You should certainly be able to obtain the opinion of two specialist doctors in this field, and may Hashem Yisbarach help that they should have the correct insight and serve as the proper *shluchim* through whom you will receive your recovery.

It is surely unnecessary to remind you that in order to draw down and maintain the blessings of Hashem, one must have appropriate *keilim* for them. These *keilim* are the matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, which every person—according to their own standing and situation, as they know themselves without self-deception—knows where to begin to strengthen and improve their state of Torah and *mitzvos*. When one becomes healthier in *ruchniyus*, this draws down an added blessing and health in *gashmiyus* as well. I thank you in advance for bringing me the *besurah tovah* of your improved health in both areas, both *gashmiyus* and *ruchniyus*. In truth, for a Yid, these two things are one, as our Sages of blessed memory state that the 248 *mitzvos asei* are connected to the 248 limbs, and the 365 *mitzvos lo saasei* are connected to the 365 sinews. The wholeness and observance of *mitzvos asei* and *lo saasei* protect and make whole the physical 248 limbs and 365 sinews as well.

With blessings that you should soon report good news regarding all of the above.

## 1735

B"H, 24 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received with pleasure your letter dated Monday, 20 Tammuz, along with the *pidyon nefesh* for you and your entire family. I was very pleased to read that Hashem has provided a suitable *shidduch* for your daughter, *tichyeh*. May it be Hashem’s will that it take place at a favorable and auspicious time, and may they build an edifice that endures forever, based on the foundations of Torah and *mitzvos*.

Once again, I wish to reiterate what I told you in person: it is beyond any doubt that the saying of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukulleh"h, nishmaso b'eden*, in the name of his father, is correct—that there is a *chazakah* (presumption) that *ta'amulah* (outreach/propaganda) does not return empty. This is especially true when it comes from people who have no blood relation, and certainly when it comes from parents to their sons and daughters. Consequently, it is a holy duty upon you and your wife, *shichyu*, to utilize all your influence on your daughter, *tichyeh*, so that she herself decides to conduct her home in accordance with Torah and *mitzvos*—first and foremost in the matters that depend on her, namely *taharas hamishpachah*. I am well aware of the common argument made by parents in America, and in the United States in particular: "Who knows if we will succeed?" or "We don't know how to begin the conversation," etc. But surely, for you, *shichyeh*, it is unnecessary to explain that these arguments hold no weight whatsoever when compared to the magnitude of the matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, and especially *taharas hamishpachah*, upon which the entire House of Israel rests. With appropriate effort and the necessary exertion, you can find the ways—whether by yourselves or through other suitable people—to influence your daughter in this direction. Relying on the words of our Sages, "Fortunate is the generation in which the elders listen to the younger ones," my hope is strong that you will heed my words to influence your daughter in the aforementioned matter. My hope is also strong that you will see, even with your physical eyes, that it proceeds successfully—especially when you explain to her the matter of her *shidduch*, which came about after it was mentioned several times at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, etc. I rely on your own understanding, especially since the fact that the matter concerns you personally will itself provide you with the appropriate words.

With blessings for proper health for you and your entire family, *shichyu*, in both spiritual and material matters alike.

P.S. Enclosed is the *reshimah* that was published for the days of *geulah* and *segulah*, the 12th and 13th of Tammuz that have just passed. Surely you will share the merit with the public, for the entire year is a time to learn a lesson in *avodas Hashem*: not to be affected by the *he'elem* (concealment) and *hester* (hiddenness). For that very thing transforms the *he'elem* and *hester* into an increase of light within one's own four cubits.

## 1736

1736

B”H, 24 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter, which included a kvittel requesting a blessing for yourself and your family, and specifically regarding a shidduch for your daughter, tichyeh.
