It is known from our Sages that whoever adds, they add to him; this includes two things: they add to his reward and what he requires, and they add to his desire to increase in Torah and mitzvos, as our Sages have ruled that one mitzvah leads to another.

Enclosed is the reshimah published for the days of redemption and segulah, the 12th and 13th of Tammuz that have just passed. I am certain you will study it, for in truth, the entire year is a time to learn a lesson in the avodah of Hashem: not to be affected by the concealments and hesterim, and to increase light within one’s own four cubits.

With blessings,

## 1737

B"H, 24 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 3rd of the current month, in which you write regarding the state of your health and ask for my opinion, as there is a doctor who suggests that you should undergo surgery.

Generally, in cases of ulcers, healing is achieved for the most part through maintaining a diet and ensuring rest for both the mind and the body, which is obviously a more correct path than surgery, etc. However, since you write in your letter that there have been several instances of bleeding, *l'havdil*, etc., and it appears that this is already a chronic condition for you, and the necessary adherence to dietary restrictions, etc., is difficult for you, you should therefore, in my opinion, consult with two specialists in this particular field and act according to their instructions. As for traveling to Rochester for this purpose, I do not know if it is necessary, since there are specialists in this field in Chicago; why subject yourself to the burden of travel, additional expenses, etc.?

May the Ribono shel Olam grant the doctors whom you consult the ability to provide the correct opinion, through which the ruling of the Torah—which grants the doctor permission (which also implies the power) to heal—will be brought from potential into actualization. See *Tikkunei Zohar*, *Tikkun* 19, page 40b, regarding the precise wording of "from potential into actualization." May the Ribono shel Olam grant you the merit to bring good news regarding the improvement of your health, and that you may add strength and vigor to influence your congregation and your surroundings, to draw their hearts closer to our Father in Heaven through strengthening the three pillars of Torah, Avodah, and Gemilus Chasadim, illuminated by the light of Torah—which is the Torah of Chassidus.

Enclosed is the *kuntres* and the *reshima* that were published in connection with the days of redemption and *segulah*, 12 and 13 Tammuz, which have passed—though in truth, their time is all year round. It would be appropriate for you to use your stay in the hospital to share them with your neighbors there as well. We do not know what may come of it, and perhaps this is the purpose and the primary intent of why you were brought to the hospital. Once you complete this mission successfully, then, as a matter of course, the secondary matter will follow the primary one, etc.

With blessings for a speedy recovery.

## 1748

B.H., 27 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I recently received regards from you through the esteemed R. Mordechai Dov, may he live, who is involved in communal affairs, as well as through your relatives who visited me. I am writing to you now regarding your son, the esteemed R. [Name], may he live. You are certainly aware that he spent some time in Mexico, where he was involved in matters of chinuch and, thank G-d, was successful. Later, due to various reasons, he left that post.

According to the information I have now received from there, the situation regarding chinuch is critical. There are—bli ayin hara—many children who want to learn as they should, but there is no suitable person who can lead the effort so that things can improve as necessary.

When I spoke with your son during his visit to me, one of the reasons he gave for his hesitation was that he did not know how his parents, may they live, would view this, as in their opinion, he still needs to spend a certain amount of time studying for his own personal growth.

It is surely unnecessary to elaborate on the necessity of Torah study for every Jew in general, and for young men in particular. However, when it concerns hundreds of children who must be saved so that they remain Jewish, everyone must have mesiras nefesh to set aside their personal goals of advancing in Torah and other aspirations. At the very least, one must dedicate a certain amount of time to saving Jewish sons and daughters from the danger of forgetting Yiddishkeit entirely, chas v'shalom. Now is precisely the time when your son, may he live, can accomplish this, and it can be done with success. We have the promise of our Sages that when Hashem sees that one performs tzedakah with His children and helps them become Jews as they should be, Hashem helps to refine the heart and mind of that person a thousand times over, so that in a short time he achieves what would otherwise have required a great deal of time, were it not for the merit of the tzedakah he is performing.

I believe it is unnecessary to elaborate further. What has been said should be sufficient for you to reconsider your approach to this matter. I hope and am certain that you will use your influence on your son, may he live, so that he will dedicate his time to this. Even if it seems to him that this is a mesiras nefesh, for the sake of ensuring that Jewish children remain Jewish, it is worthwhile. May Hashem reward him and you a thousand times over in all the matters that each of you requires.

Enclosed is the transcript of the remarks I made to the students who are now traveling across the country on behalf of the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch, which is truly relevant to your son's situation as well.

With blessings for success in his affairs, and awaiting good news.

## 1739

1739

By the Grace of G-d
27 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished R. Mordechai, may he be well.

Shalom u’Bracha!

I have received your letter of the 20th of Tammuz. Your request for me to send you mezuzos, tefillin straps, and tzitzis has been passed on to the administration of Merkos L’Inyonei Chinuch, and they will send them to you as soon as it is possible for them to do so.

Regarding what you write about the ongoing difficulties with your Canadian visa: this itself should serve as proof that you still have work to accomplish in your current location, in strengthening Yiddishkeit, Torah, and mitzvos. It is well known what my father-in-law, the Rebbe, related in the name of his grandfather, the Rebbe Maharash: he explained to someone at length that Hashem can provide physical parnassah to every Jew in an environment of Jews, among Jews who are shomrei Torah u’mitzvos, in a large Jewish community, and so on. If a Jew finds his parnassah in a remote location, it is proof that he certainly has something to rectify there—to bring more Yiddishkeit, the *ner mitzvah v’Torah ohr*, among the Jews who are found there. Consequently, this is connected with physical parnassah, so that the body and the *nefesh habehamis* will also be willing to go there, and once there, he will have the opportunity to carry out his spiritual shlichus.

Enclosed is the list of points that I spoke about to the yeshiva students who are traveling for several weeks through the cities of America to inspire people regarding Yiddishkeit, Torah, and mitzvos. In truth, these words are relevant to every Jew who is in a remote location where one does not find all these spiritual necessities. Even more so, in a general sense, this applies to all Jews, for every neshamah that is hewn from beneath the Kisei HaKavod has descended into a body, occupies itself with physical matters, and goes through various trials and difficulties—all of which are *tzorech aliyah* (for the sake of an ascent).

With the wish that you should be successful and carry out your spiritual shlichus, which itself will draw down success for you in your physical matters.

P.S. Your contribution has been turned over to the fund that supports the Talmud Torahs and yeshivos founded in the name of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, "Oholei Yosef Yitzchak," in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt, in Africa, and so on.

## 1740

1740

B"H, 28 Tammuz, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Organization of N'shei U'Bnos Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily,
May they live,

Blessings and peace!

It is well known how highly our Sages of blessed memory spoke of the virtue and merit of the women of Israel, who brought redemption and salvation to individuals and to the entirety of Israel in times of distress, Heaven forbid. Our holy forefathers and Rebbes, the leaders of Chabad, and in particular my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, emphasized the great role of the women of Israel in general, and the women of Chabad in particular, in these days of ours. My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, has already written that one of the primary intentions behind the publication of his sichos is to provide benefit and supply material suitable for the women and girls of Chabad in their education and their avodah, both for themselves and regarding others. To elaborate further on this is unnecessary.

In accordance with the above, and as a continuation of the Organization of N'shei U'Bnos Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily, I hereby propose the following general outline for a program of work:

A. Avodah regarding themselves:

(1) To gather at regular intervals for study (the weekly parsha, matters pertaining to the upcoming Yom Tov, halachos, and the like).

(2) To study appropriate maamarim, sichos, etc., that speak of the foundations of the teachings of Chassidus, its customs, the guidance of Chassidus, etc., and through this, to strengthen the spirit of Chassidus and the light of Chassidus in their homes.

B. Avodah regarding others:

(1) To strive with added courage, first and foremost, for the benefit of those closest to them—namely, in the education of their sons and daughters, and the education of the sons and daughters of Israel in their surroundings.

(2) To conduct outreach to strengthen matters of Yiddishkeit in general, and taharas hamishpacha, kashrus, and proper education in particular.

(3) To strive to strengthen institutions of proper education in general, and in particular to take an active part in all Chabad educational institutions in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily, especially regarding the arrangements for food and lodging, supervision of cleanliness, dress, and the like.

May the pleasantness of Hashem be upon them, and may the work of their hands bring forth fruit and the fruit of fruit for the glory of the elder Israel and the splendor of Chabad.

With blessings for what is needed for each and every one, and for their households, both materially and spiritually.

## 1742

1742

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 2 Tammuz, in which you raise a point regarding the *beraisa* in the *Yerushalmi*, beginning of *Horayos*: "Perhaps if they tell you about right that it is left, etc. The verse states: 'to go right and left'—that they tell you about right that it is right, etc." You wish to explain:

1) That the intention is to the verse in *Devarim* 28:14: "And you shall not turn aside from all the words which I command you this day, to the right or to the left, to go after other gods to serve them." You suggest that the *Yerushalmi* inverted the order of the verse based on the principle of *Tosfos* (s.v. *v'nasan*, *Shabbos* 128a) that it is the way of the *Shas* to be brief and use different phrasing.

In my humble opinion, it is difficult to say this, because: (a) In that verse, the text negates the matter mentioned in the word "to go," and the meaning of the verse is: "And you shall not turn aside..."—whereas the *Yerushalmi* is precise about the word "to go" as an obligation. (b) That verse speaks of the commandment of Hashem, not the instruction of a *Beis Din*. (c) That verse and the entire passage are a promise to Israel and a narrative, not a commandment.

It appears straightforward (and this is also the view of the *Mar'eh Panim* on the *Yerushalmi*, in *Torah Temimah*, and elsewhere) that the *Yerushalmi* also intends—like the *Sifri*—to refer to the verse in *Devarim* 17:11: "According to the Torah... you shall do; you shall not turn aside from the word which they tell you, right or left." And this is according to the aforementioned rule of *Tosfos* that it is the way of the *Shas* to use different phrasing.

The *Yerushalmi* is precise in adding the word **"to go"** (*laleches*), because the entire lesson depends on it. For the words **"right"** and **"left"** in this verse can be interpreted in three ways: 1) "You shall not turn aside right or left from the word which they tell you." This is similar to what is written in many places (*Devarim* 5:26, 17:20; see *Torah Temimah*). 2) Like the *Sifri*—"they tell you" (this is) right and left (because your own opinion is not so). 3) "According to the Torah... you shall do" (you shall not turn aside from the word which they tell you) (to go) right and left (specifically).

The words "not... you" are a parenthetical phrase, as if the word "to go" were written in the verse.

It may be said that the reason the *Yerushalmi* is not satisfied with interpreting the verse according to the first way—for if so, it should have placed the words "right and left" next to the word "turn aside," as is the case in most verses, although it is found otherwise as well, such as in *Devarim* 28:14 (but in that verse there is no room for error, unlike in the case at hand)—is because it also does not fit the second way (which is the foundation of the *Sifri's* teaching that even if they tell you about right that it is left, etc.)—for if so, it should have remained silent and left it general: "You shall not turn aside from the word which they tell you," and from where would the limitation of the commandment arise? This requires further study.

2) That the *Yerushalmi* and the *Sifri* do not disagree. The opinion of the *Yerushalmi* is only that one is not obligated to accept the opinion of the *Beis Din* without questioning them. On the contrary. But if, after the discussion, his colleagues outvoted him, he is included in "you shall not turn aside," etc., even if they say about left that it is right. See on this *Sefer HaChinuch*, end of *Mitzvah* 436; *Ramban* in his *Hasagos* to *Sefer HaMitzvos*, *Shoresh* 1; *Tosfos HaRosh*, *Be'er Sheva*, *Rashash*, *Maharatz Chayes*, and *Yafeh Einayim* to *Horayos* (2b); the commentators on *Rashi* to *Devarim* (17:11), and others.

This interpretation is very forced, because if so, the main point is missing from the *Yerushalmi* (also, according to the above, it is a great novelty here—to learn two opposite matters from one verse).

3) In *Sdei Chemed*, *Kelalim* 30, it is brought from the book *Pesach Einayim* of the *Chida* (*Rosh Hashanah* 25a) that if one knows without a doubt that the *Beis Din* has erred, he should not act according to their words. This is also stated in *Torah Temimah* as the subject of the *Yerushalmi*, unlike the *Sifri*, whose language is "even if they **appear to your eyes**."

This is also very forced, for who can guarantee this, as is understood. See *Ramban* on *Shoftim* there. And furthermore—follow the reason: so that disputes do not multiply in Israel; if so, what is the difference?

(And one could forcedly answer that a dispute from one extreme to the other is not common at all. And it is similar to the concept of "opposing opinions" in *Tosfos* s.v. *mevarech berachos* (39b). And we do not fear that it will happen again.)

In my humble opinion, it is clearer according to the simple language of the *Sifri* and the *Yerushalmi* that they do disagree, as mentioned above. And this is also what is written in *Mar'eh Panim* on the *Yerushalmi* there.

## 1743

1743

B”H, 1 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned,
R’ Shalom, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 21 Tammuz...

I am writing with a personal request, and I am certain you will inform those who are relevant to this matter. It is as follows: I am looking to fill my library with books by various authors, as well as Seforim on Kabbalah, both from Sephardic and Ashkenazic sources. Naturally, I am extremely limited in the means to purchase these books. Since in Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established) there are many authors and many books of this type—some of which are sitting in the homes of private individuals or even in shuls, with no one turning their pages or making use of them—I would be very grateful if you could make an effort to collect these books and send them to me gradually. In those places where it is not possible to obtain them as a donation to my library, one may propose exchanging them for books published by Kehot. I would point out that many books of this nature were brought to Eretz Yisrael by Sephardic immigrants from North Africa, Yemen, Persia, etc., and they are also found among the books that were saved and brought from Germany, Poland, etc. I therefore authorize you to inform all those relevant to this matter of my request as stated above. My thanks are given to you in advance for the notification, and primarily for bringing this matter from potential into actuality. Regarding the method of sending these books, they can be sent gradually; surely, in any case, you will not obtain all the books at once. Regarding those to whom letters of thanks need to be written for this, please let me know, and G-d willing, it will be done.

With blessings for success in fulfilling your shlichus, and I am certain you will acknowledge receipt of this letter at your earliest convenience.

***

R’ Shalom Haskind.

To fill my library: See above, Letter 1550, and the references in the notes there.

1744

1744

B"H, 1 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad,
May they live.

Peace and Blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from 26 Tammuz after the long hiatus. Surely, for the future, you will arrange for correspondence to be more frequent, without waiting for a written reply from me, as I am extremely occupied. Even if time does not permit a written response, I endeavor to do what is possible regarding the content of your letters as soon as possible, even if the notification regarding this is sometimes delayed.

2) Surely the esteemed Chossid, a man of noble character, etc., R. M. Ashkenazi, may he live, has delivered a copy of the *Reshimah* to the students traveling now on the *shlichus* of the *Meluch* (the summer activities), just as the Rebbe, my father-in-law, used to arrange annually during the summer months. I told him that it is worthwhile to publicize it in an appropriate manner, and I am adding here a segment taken from my letters that can serve as an addition to the aforementioned *sicha*—an addition that emphasizes and explains how this is a matter relevant to every soul.

3) In response to your notification regarding your reasoning for holding the *farbrengen* of 12 Tammuz in the Great Synagogue in Tel Aviv, and that you subsequently retracted this thought: since the deed is done, one does not cry over the past. However, I am surprised that you retracted it. The concern that there might be speakers who will not speak according to the intent is generally mitigated by the very fact that they are invited to a Chabad gathering, which restricts the speaker to a great degree. Furthermore, one is not obligated to publish a stenographic report of the *farbrengen*; it is within your authority, as is customary in such matters, to emphasize and highlight the points appropriate to the holiday and its spirit. As for the fact that during the *farbrengen* itself some *zaitike* (extraneous/side-issue) remarks are sometimes heard, the advice for this is to always invite a reliable speaker and stipulate with him that he should correct anything that needs correcting. The main thing is that the final speaker should be as he ought to be, since, after all, this is the impression that remains and is taken home by the participants when they leave. But as mentioned, one does not cry over the past. Surely, if it is not "this too is for the good," then at the very least the principle "everything the Merciful One does, He does for the good" will be fulfilled. As is known, the distinction is that "this too is for the good" means the matter itself is good—like the story of Nachum Ish Gam Zu, where the dust itself became a source of miracles—whereas "everything the Merciful One does..." means that the results of the matter are good, even if the matter itself was not, as in the story of Rabbi Akiva, where the death of the donkey, the rooster, and the lamp were not good, but the result was the saving of his life.

4) If you have a transcript of the conferences of 12 and 13 Tammuz, surely you will send a copy here.

5) I am surprised that you do not mention, as results of the *farbrengen*, good resolutions regarding setting fixed times for Torah study in both the revealed and hidden aspects, strengthening the *takanos* of the Baal HaSimcha, and participating in his institutions in a manner appropriate for each individual. Perhaps this was omitted from your letter, even though it occurred in practice; if so, it should be included in the next letter.

6) I am interested to know if anything was printed in the press regarding the 12 Tammuz *farbrengen*, how it went, the content of the speeches, etc.

8) Regarding your proposal to publish a monthly journal, and you conclude that you do not yet have an editor, etc.: before you find a suitable person, surely you cannot estimate the expenses involved in the matter, and therefore it is difficult for me to express an opinion. In any case, at the beginning, the appearance of the bulletin should be such that you are not forced to publish it on a specific day—that is, if you have material on hand, you publish it. This means the time of its appearance should not be frequent, and only when enough material has been gathered for the bulletin. Therefore, as a first step, if it is true as you write in your letter that publishing the names of activists will cause "wisdom to increase" (even though, on the other hand, it could give rise to various matters of resentment and perceived slights to honor, etc.), then it is worthwhile to publish a bulletin from time to time with the most essential news, without specifying the time when the next bulletin will appear. One must also take into account what is more worthwhile: whether to publish this news in a newspaper whose subscribers reach several thousands—among whom are those who would not read a separately printed bulletin—or if it is better to publish a bulletin, in which case there is a risk that some newspapers will not want to print news that has already appeared in your bulletin.

9) I was pleased with what you wrote about the radio broadcast regarding 12 Tammuz. It would be worthwhile for one of the administrators of the general Agudas Chabad to also join the committee that organizes and reviews the broadcasts, for several reasons.

10) I was pleased to see in your letter that two people signed it, as I have requested for some time now to one of the institutions in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, that in general matters I ask that at least two people sign, in order to avoid questions and contradictions thereby.

With a blessing for success in your work.

## 1,745

B"H, 1 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I have received your *pidyon nefesh* on behalf of yourself and your family members, may they live, in which you request a *shemirah* (protection) for your wife and son, may they live. I am writing this in Yiddish so that you may read the text as it is to your wife, may she live.

Your husband, may he live, writes to me that you are not feeling well in your health and are feeling nervous, and also that you had a dream that you should ask me for a *shemirah*.

The *shemirah* is as follows: You should have the *mezuzos* of your home checked to ensure they are all *kosher*. Also, every *Erev Shabbos Kodesh* and *Erev Yom Tov*, before lighting the candles, you should give 18 cents to *tzedakah* for *Rabbi Meir Baal HaNes*. Furthermore, your husband, may he live, should recite a *yom* (day’s portion) of *Tehillim* every morning after *davening*—according to the monthly division of *Tehillim*—and your husband and son, may they live, should wear a *tallis katan*. It is surely unnecessary to point out that the home must be strictly *kosher* and conducted in every way as a Jewish home should be conducted. The main thing is to be strong in *bitachon* (trust) in *Hashem Yisbarach*, who—blessed is He—is the Creator of the world and directs it, and likewise, He—blessed is He—directs the life of every individual person. He—blessed is He—will watch over you, your husband, and your son, may they live. You have nothing to worry about in this regard, and the more you strengthen your *bitachon*, the more clearly you will see that *Hashem Yisbarach* is helping you, especially regarding your health, which will improve, as well as the health of your son, Avraham Ozer, may he live. I hope that you and your husband, may you live, will be able to share good news with me regarding this.

Your donation has been given to the fund that supports the *chadarym*, *yeshivos*, and *Talmud Torahs* "Ohalei Yosef Yitzchak," named after my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May this serve as a *tzinor* (conduit) and vessel to draw down an increase in blessing and success for you all in whatever you are in need of.

Awaiting good news.

## 1,746

1,746

B"H, 1 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter of the 23rd of Tammuz, as well as the one preceding it, and I was pleased to read that you are engaged in the field of proper chinuch... May it be Hashem’s will that it be successful.

Regarding what you wrote—that you know it can and should be much better than it is now—it is well known that our Sages have ruled: "I have labored and found, believe it." It is also a well-known adage of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that "one action is better than a thousand sighs." This applies to your situation as well. It is understood that every person must strive to improve themselves as much as possible; yet, on the other hand, one must not halt all avodah for the sake of achieving the ultimate perfection possible for him. Rather, one must hold onto both: continue the work while striving for improvement. This is especially true regarding the avodah of chinuch, where every single day you touch the souls of scores of Jewish boys and girls; this work must not be interrupted. It is known what our Alter Rebbe ruled—in the beginning of Torah Or—that through the avodah of tzedakah (whether material or spiritual), one's mind and heart become a thousand times more refined.

With blessings for success in your holy work, and may this also draw down an increase of blessing in your personal affairs.

## 1747

1747

B”H, 2 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter (which did not indicate the date of writing) with pleasure. In it, you write that until now you have not succeeded in receiving the *hashpaah* to be able to study Chassidus and cultivate good *midos*. Now, however, you have been inspired by seeing the esteemed Chossid, the G-d-fearing man, who occupies himself with *tzarchei tzibbur*, etc., Rabbi Menachem Shmuel Dovid Reitzes, *sheyichyeh*. Observing his conduct has increased your desire and yearning to connect to the *ilana d’chayei*—the inner dimension of Torah and the teachings of Chassidus—and you are requesting a blessing in this regard.

My words have already been stated in the teachings of Chazal: “I have labored and I have found—believe it.” Since you possess the desire, the yearning, and the will for the aforementioned, you will surely find what you are seeking. However, you must not be discouraged (*opshreken zich*) if you do not attain the entire matter all at once. For this is the path of holiness; just as the *Ribono shel Olam* said regarding the physical conquest of Eretz Yisrael, “Little by little I will drive them out from before you,” so too is the matter regarding the conquest of the spiritual Eretz Yisrael. That is to say, when a Jewish person wants to sanctify the order of his life—just as Eretz Yisrael is holier than all other lands, so too should his life be holier than that of the other people in his surroundings—the order of this is “little by little I will drive them out.” He goes from strength to strength and from level to level, but it is “little by little.” Nevertheless, since he is guaranteed that he will ultimately reach his goal, even the beginning of his *avodah* must be with true joy, for this is merely a matter that requires labor and time, and in the end, he will become a *Chossid* and a *yirei Shamayim*.

The paths and vessels for this are explained and detailed in many *seforim*, *kuntresim*, and *maamarim*. First and foremost, you should hold fast to the three daily *shiurim* established for every soul by my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzuklalleh, nishmaso b’Eden, zya*:

a) Reciting the *shiur* of Tehillim—as divided for the days of the month—every day after *davening* Shacharis.
b) Studying the *parsha* of Chumash with the commentary of Rashi from the weekly *sedra*.
c) A *shiur* in Tanya, as divided for the days of the year.

Furthermore, set fixed times every day for the study of *nigleh* and also for the study of Chassidus, each person according to his standing, situation, understanding, and grasp. It is also good to give a cent or two to *tzedakah* every morning before *davening* (this, of course, without a *neder*).

My hope is strong that by doing the above, the light of the *ilana d’chayei* will begin to shine in your *nefesh*, *ruach*, and *neshamah*, and you will go from strength to strength. I would be pleased if you would inform me of good tidings in this regard.

With blessings,

## 1749

1749

B"H, 2 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, engaged in communal needs, etc.,
R' Hillel, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

For some time now, I have been intending to fulfill my promise—which I made to you some time ago—to respond properly to your letters. These included the maamar of the holy and learned Rabbi, etc., my grandfather, the Rebbe Rashab, entitled *Olas Tamid*, the summary of the maamar *Naftali Ailah Shlucha* from the year 5627, and the indices for the notebooks (bichlech) 20, beginning with "V'zeh Asher Ta'aseh," the receipt of which I already confirmed some time ago. However, due to the pressure of many preoccupations, I have not been able to do so until now, and I will therefore be brief.

2) Regarding these notebooks: It is possible that they are among those that belonged to my father-in-law, the Rebbe. Among them were notebooks that were purchased from Chassidim or given as a gift by Chassidim. Consequently, it is possible that it is noted in some notebook that it belongs to so-and-so, and it was later handed over to my father-in-law, the Rebbe, or even to his father, the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory.

3) As it appears from the summary of the maamar *Naftali Ailah Shlucha*, it is based on the maamar entitled *Zeh* that is printed in the sefer *Orot HaTorah* on Bereishis by the Tzemach Tzedek. However, it seems it is only *based* on it; from the content you sent me, the maamar is more extensive than the printed version. Nevertheless, if the sefer *Orot HaTorah* is available in your camp (it was among the books of my brother-in-law, R' Shneur Zalman, may he live, Shneerson), it is worthwhile to compare it with the printed version, and you will surely inform me of this. If it is seen that it is not the one printed in *Orot HaTorah*, then it is worth copying it in its entirety, and perhaps it can be printed as a supplement to the sefer of 5627 that was printed last year, as this maamar is missing from it.

4) If the work of compiling the indices continues, please be so kind as to inform me of the page numbers and the beginning of each notebook—that is, the *d"h* (opening phrase) of the first and second maamar in each—and also if there is any writing number or the like on the spine or the cover. Please convey in my name many thanks and appreciation to your brother-in-law, the esteemed R' Shalom, may he live, who, according to your letter, assisted you in copying the maamar, compiling the indices, etc. Surely he will also assist you in the aforementioned in the future, and I express my appreciation for his help and assistance for the future as well.

6) As a token of thanks, I have enclosed the supplements to the *Reshimot* on Eichah—the content of what I said to the students traveling on shlichus for the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch to strengthen the spirit of Yiddishkeit in the cities of the United States. In truth, however, the content of these words touches every single Jew, for the soul's place is under the Kisei HaKavod, from where it was hewn and descended through hidden levels until this physical and material world. Therefore, it does not desire to descend, and as our Sages of blessed memory said, "Against your will you live." Yet, precisely through this descent from the "high roof," a much greater ascent is possible, as is explained in many places in Chassidus. Even though the matter is not understood by intellect—and especially regarding the individual avodah given to every soul—it is said regarding this, "But by lot shall the land be divided," as is explained in the enclosed *Reshimah*.

With blessings,

## 1750

1750

B"H, 2 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the gathering
for the benefit of the
United Emergency Campaign in Chicago for the
educational institutions
of Lubavitch, convened in the home of
Mr. and Mrs. Yechezkel Lyssner,
may they live and be well.

Peace and abundant blessing!

Regarding your gathering, G-d willing, on Monday, 6 Menachem Av, to continue and expand with success the United Emergency Campaign in Chicago and its surroundings, I wish you that the gathering should bring the desired results in actuality and with success.

It is known to all the statement of our Sages, that where ten are gathered, the Shechinah rests; meaning that when ten Jews gather, the Shechinah rests there. Although His glory fills the entire world, where there are ten from Israel, the resting of the Shechinah is more revealed. This is especially true if these Jews gather for a matter of Torah and mitzvos, and in particular, when they gather for a matter of kosher chinuch, which unites Torah and mitzvos together. Then the Divine revelation rests in a greater measure, which expresses itself in various ways. One of these is that it instills the correct thoughts on how to establish the work and the influence upon others, as well as the correct approach regarding one's own participation in this work: through a generous contribution with one's money, through tireless participation with one's body, and through warm participation with one's soul.

I hope and am certain that the leader of all these institutions, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, will awaken abundant mercy so that the aforementioned work should proceed with great success, and will also bestow blessing and success upon all those participating in this gathering in particular, and all those participating in the campaign in general, in whatever each one needs, he and his household, may they live.

With blessings for success and regards to each and every one.

## 1551

1551

B"H, 2 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and noble benefactor, a man of stature, G-d-fearing, an energetic activist and man of many accomplishments, crowned with lofty character traits, etc., R' Yitzchak Almalich, may he live and be well.

Peace and blessing!

I received your esteemed letter of 21 Tammuz with pleasure, and I was very gratified by the joyous news contained within it: that you have appointed a religious, G-d-fearing director for Otzar HaTorah, and that you have uprooted and broken the propaganda of the free-thinkers—those who steal and rob the souls of the sons and daughters of Yisrael, inciting and leading them away from their Father in Heaven. I hope that you will proceed with this strength of yours and not allow them to rise again.

Regarding your heart’s hesitation, fearing that G-d forbid they might harm you because of your battle against the aforementioned inciters: do not be concerned about this at all. On the contrary, did our Sages not say that one who sustains a single soul in Yisrael is as if he sustained an entire world? How much more so, then, when one exerts effort in saving many souls in Yisrael, as you, may you live, are dedicated to doing. The magnitude of the merit and the magnitude of the reward for this are beyond measure; these are among the things whose principal remains for the World to Come, while a person enjoys their fruits in this world as well, drawing down blessing and success for you, your wife, and your son, may he live, in all that they require.

Relying on our Sages' teaching that one mitzvah leads to another and that we must always ascend in matters of holiness, I am confident that you, may you live, will add strength and courage to your holy work, through which you will add further blessing and success, both in general matters and in your own personal affairs.

Enclosed is a list in connection with the Chag HaGeulah, 12-13 Tammuz, of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which I am sure will interest you. The deeds of the Nesi'im and the Patriarchs are a sign for their children and students; just as their mesiras nefesh in spreading and raising the banner of Torah and Yisrael Saba brought success and days of celebration and spiritual elevation to Yisrael, so too will the mesiras nefesh of each one of us—even if it does not reach the level of their mesiras nefesh—add an increase of Divine light within Yisrael, in one's home, in one's surroundings, in one's community, and in one's country.

With blessing.

## 1552

1552

B"H, 2 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, refined, engaged in communal needs, etc.,
R' Shmuel, may he live, Shochet u'Bodek

Greetings and blessings!

I have just received your letter of 27 Tammuz, and I am hastening to reply to it, even though several letters from some time ago have still not been answered. This is because you write in your letter that it has caused great anxiety, etc. Regarding what you write—that it has been about two months since the leaders of the shul [Kehal Chassidim] wrote here—it seems from your letter that they wrote directly to me and did not receive a response. It is possible, and indeed likely, that their letter was lost in the mail. If you still have a copy and the matter is still relevant, perhaps you could send me a copy of their letter.

2) Regarding the substance of the matter—you ask for my opinion concerning the suggestion that you make a trip here around the coming month of Kislev. The question regarding this is that, unfortunately, you have been suffering for some time from a heart condition. Since then, you are limited and must be careful with eating and drinking, and in general, you must be careful with walking. Expert doctors have told you that everything depends on whether you can guarantee that you will not become agitated, etc., and also that the strain of travel is a concern, etc.

In my opinion, it is not worth entering into all these doubts and debates. Since Divine Providence has brought you to your current location—and especially in recent times, one can see tangibly a vast field for great activities regarding the actual dissemination of the teachings of Chassidus, its ways, and its customs in your camp, and especially among the students of the Yeshiva—which, in contrast to other yeshivos in years past, the Yeshiva in your camp not only does not oppose, but on the contrary, asks that you disseminate the spirit of Chassidus among the students—it is therefore worthwhile, appropriate, correct, and good to utilize every day and every opportunity in this direction. If our Sages said of every single Jew that he is an entire world, then all the more so regarding students of a yeshiva, most of whom, if not all, will eventually be mashpi'im in their surroundings. Thus, through every improvement and refinement that you introduce into one of the students, you will naturally cause improvement and correction for that environment where, after several years, this student will be the mashpia. The magnitude of this matter cannot be estimated in advance at all, as is known from the parable that a small repair—or G-d forbid, the opposite—to a large tree is only a small repair. This is not the case with a small repair to a seed that is planted; it is possible that the entire existence of the tree that grows from it after a duration of several years depends on this. And even if the matter takes a long time, it is explained in Chassidus regarding the difference between sowing and planting, that the length of time itself indicates the magnitude of the change and the growth for the good. Further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

3) I am enclosing a copy of the talk I gave to the students from the Yeshiva who travel every year during the summer days on a mission for the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch to strengthen the spirit of Yiddishkeit in the cities of the United States. But in truth, the content of these words pertains to every single Jew. For the soul, its place is under the Throne of Glory, from where it was hewn, and even higher than that, for it "arose in [His] thought." It descended through the hidden levels until this physical and material world (and therefore it does not want to descend, as our Sages say, "Against your will you live"). And yet, it is precisely through this descent from the high peak that the greatest ascent is possible, as is explained in many places in Chassidus. And even though the matter is not understood by the intellect, and especially in the personal avodah given to every soul, it is regarding this that it is said, "But by lot shall the land be divided," as is explained in the enclosed notes.

With blessings for proper health and all good.

## 1,753

B"H, 2 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was distressed to learn that I caused you pain by not sending a response to your letter, and that you are interpreting this with explanations and intentions that are not at all accurate. I have already written several times to various members of anash that due to the multitude of pressures, etc., when I receive a letter containing a question or request, I endeavor to fulfill it to the best of my ability and strength, even if there is not always free time to notify the sender of this in writing or even orally. This is also the case regarding your situation: the pidyon nefesh, etc., that you sent, I read at a time of favor at the tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and I mention you for the fulfillment of your heart’s desires for the good—even if notification of this in writing does not arrive or is delayed. It is absolutely certain that there is no intention of distancing, chas v’shalom, for my entire purpose is only to bring closer, and matters of the "left line"—even where they are necessary, chas v’shalom—can be fulfilled by others. If only I had the strength to fulfill the matters of the "right line."

In order to clear your mind—even though there was no basis for this (and surely this too is from the counsel of the yetzer hara, which seeks out paths suitable for each individual, whether to lower him in his own eyes or to elevate him in his own eyes, as long as it prevents him from the proper persistence in the avodah of Hashem)—I am enclosing a copy of what I said to the students traveling on a shlichus for the Merkos L'Inyonei Chinuch. In truth, the content of these words pertains to every Jew, for the soul’s place is under the Kisei HaKavod from where it was hewn, and it descended through the hidden levels until this physical and material world. Therefore, it does not desire to descend, and as our Sages of blessed memory said, "Against your will you live." Yet, precisely through this descent from a high roof, a much greater ascent is possible, as is explained in many places in Chassidus. Even though the matter is not understood through intellect—especially regarding the specific avodah given to each soul—regarding this it is said, "Only by lot shall the land be divided," as is explained in the enclosed notes.

With blessings for the avodah of Hashem with joy and expansiveness.

## 1755

1755

B"H, 6 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to hear that you have already been back home for several months, and I hope to receive a letter from you detailing your state of health.

You are certainly aware of the ruling of the poskim, and it is also printed in *HaTamim* among the letters that the Maggid of Mezeritch wrote to his son, that a small hole in the body creates a small hole in the neshamah. This helps us understand the importance of a person in general, and a Yid in particular, guarding the health of their body. This is one of the paths of avodas Hashem Yisbarach, as the Rambam writes in *Hilchos Deios*, Chapter 4: "Maintaining a healthy and sound body is one of the ways of Hashem." It is also well known that the Baal Shem Tov established the order in avodah that one must "serve Hashem with joy." We have heard many times from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Baal Shem Tov’s interpretation of the verse, "When you see the donkey... you shall surely release it with him" (and this is also printed in *Hayom Yom*). The essence of this teaching is that serving Hashem is **not** through afflicting the body, but rather through the body itself. The fact that this was told to us and demanded of us is a sign that this is our avodah and that this is the path of the Chassidim.

It goes without saying that I am not giving a sermon, but rather speaking regarding [...] *al hapo'al mamash*. Now that you are at home and no longer under the supervision of doctors, *chas v'shalom*, you should not overexert your body. On the contrary, follow the instructions of the doctors and ensure that you have a healthy body in *gashmius*; then you will be healthy in *ruchnius*. May Hashem help that you, together with your wife, should raise your children, *shichyu*, to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, with much Yiddishe nachas, with peace of mind and physical well-being. I hope to hear good news from you regarding this.

With blessings, and awaiting good tidings.

## 1556

1556

B"H, 6 Menachem Av, 5712

I received your letter from Wednesday, Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av. Perhaps, at the very least, it will be of benefit for the future: one should either not ask, but if one does ask, it is proper to listen to the instruction.
