## 1757

1757

B”H, 6 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 10 Tammuz—which was received with a delay—in which you write about your state of mind in general, and especially of late, concluding that you feel you are currently experiencing a decline in spirituality:

In general, you must know that such imaginings, especially when they cause sadness as you write in your letter, come from the *yetzer hara* and the *sitra achra*. This is explained in *Tanya* regarding sadness and the necessity of distancing oneself from it. Especially when Hashem has merited to place you in a "corner of light"—the candle of a *mitzvah* and the light of *Torah*, and the "light of the Torah," which is the inner dimension of *Torah*—you should be in a state of the greatest joy regarding this good fortune.

As for the fact that you feel your shortcomings in various matters: as mentioned above, firstly, it is possible that this is nothing more than an imagination. Secondly, even if there is a basis for your perspective, what is this similar to? It is like a person who was not healthy and did not know it, and consequently did not guard against harmful things, nor did he take measures that would bring him healing, because he imagined that he was perfectly healthy. The "Cause of all causes" and "Mover of all movers" has finally brought it about that he knows of his deficiency. Consequently, there is now hope that he will begin to engage in healing practices and distance himself further from harmful things. Clearly, the fact that his condition has been revealed to him is not only no reason to be sad, but on the contrary, it is a preface and preparation for a state of true health.

Surely, as is the case with the vast majority of people, both of the above aspects are present in you: namely, that there is some basis for your thought regarding the deficiency, while in other parts it is exaggerated by the *sitra achra*. Or, what is more likely, it is showing you the deficiency not where it actually exists, but in a different place (and its intent in this is twofold: that when he exerts himself in an area where it is not needed, the excessive exertion in that area will cause harm, and the correction of the necessary and essential matter will be lacking, as is explained in several places in *Chassidus* and also in *mussar* books).

In general, it is known what is written: "Serve Hashem with joy," for then the *avodah* is performed more, with greater energy, and with greater success. And even if one knows one's standing and situation, the standing and situation of one's *nefesh habehamis* should not disturb the joy of one's *nefesh elokis*, as is explained in *Tanya*.

Regarding your birthday, which you write about in your letter: may it be the will of Hashem that you be a *yirei shamayim*, a *lamdan*, and a *chossid* as is fitting. Great is the merit of your involvement in the field of proper *chinuch* to bring the hearts of Yisrael closer to our Father in Heaven, and may our Father in Heaven reward you with an addition that is greater than the essence, with whatever you need in both *gashmius* and *ruchnius*.

With blessings for success in *Torah* study with *yiras shamayim* and for whatever you need in your affairs.

## 1558

1558

B"H, 7 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Matos-Masei, informing me that you are already home and have also brought your daughter back with you. However, you do not state the reason why your daughter traveled back as well—whether it is because she has already finished what she intended to do, or if there is another reason for this. After all, the environment in London, where she was until now, is certainly strictly religious. Even though she longed for her parents and the parents for her, one must utilize the young years that are relevant to chinuch to provide the maximum chinuch that can possibly be given. But since the matter is already a fait accompli, we must hope that it will be for the good. I trust that you and she will not be content with her studying alone with Mrs. ..., but will also see to creating an environment where she can find the same spirit as in London. Perhaps it would be appropriate for her to be a mashpi'ah for a group of Jewish girls; this in itself would lead her to delve more deeply into these matters.

I was pleased to read in your letter that the business in the islands has been settled, and I hope that this will prove to be a good channel for parnassah.

Regarding the business affairs in your country, you surely remember what I spoke to you about: that you need to find out whether you have wronged anyone through your business dealings, and if so, to rectify it. Hopefully, you have done this or are doing so now. I hope that you will be able to report good news to me, that you see Hashgacha Pratis even with your physical eyes. You need not overthink regarding your former partners—that they might do you harm—for the Ribono shel Olam is the Creator of the world, He sustains it and directs it, and He, blessed be He, is the true Baal HaBayis in all details and minute details. May it be the will of Hashem that He grant you parnassah with abundance, and may you act as the Alter Rebbe, author of the Shulchan Aruch and Tanya, said: that Hashem Yisbarach gives Jews gashmius, and the Jews transform that gashmius into ruchnius.

With blessings, awaiting good news.

P.S. It is certainly unnecessary to ask you again and to thank you for the help that you have given and continue to give to anash, may they live, in your country. I hope that, like every living thing, it grows—especially a davar sheb'kedushah—and that you will fulfill the teaching of our Sages, "We ascend in matters of holiness."

## 1,559

B"H, 7 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of the 25th of Tammuz, accompanied by the *pidyon nefesh*, I will read it at an auspicious time at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

Regarding what you wrote in your letter concerning the reasons why your *avodah* in spreading *Chassidus* is weak: even if we assume that these reasons are valid, this only pertains to the matter of reward and punishment. However, the objective that is meant to be achieved through this *avodah* is not fulfilled by offering justifications. Every day that passes—and who can say what happens when a week, a month, a year, or even a week of years passes—is a loss that cannot be recovered. These days are "lacking days," not "complete days." Any further elaboration on this is superfluous, for either way: if you act, these lines will have been effective, and if this is not effective, what good would it do for me to write another page? The matter depends solely on your *ratzon*, for the ability is in your hands, and may Hashem grant you the merit to bring the matter into action as soon as possible. Very soon, you will feel the sense of lack—what you are missing because of this. As the well-known saying goes, when one feels that something is not right and needs to be fixed, that very feeling itself is the beginning of the *tikkun*.

You mention in your letter that you encouraged one of the *temimim* to participate with you in this activity. The aforementioned individual also complains in his letter to me about his isolation and other reasons for his lack of activity. You may tell him in my name that I have written to you regarding him, and my hope is that if he is at all able to join in the spreading of *Chassidus*, this mention will surely be enough to draw him into it.

You do not mention anything in your letter regarding the health of your family, may they live. I trust that all is well, and may Hashem grant you the merit to act in the aforementioned direction, and very soon.

With blessings, awaiting good news.

## 1760

1760

B”H, 7 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 24 Tammuz, in which you announce the birth of your daughter, mazal tov—may it be the will of Hashem that you and your wife, may they live, raise her to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds, with peace of mind and physical well-being.

It is known from my father-in-law, the Rebbe (the Rashab), of blessed memory, that our custom is to say "to Torah, to the chuppah, and to good deeds" even upon the birth of a daughter, based on the words of our Sages (Berachos 17a): "How do women merit? By sending their children to learn... by waiting for their husbands..."

Regarding what you write in your letter concerning the reasons why you are not maintaining a connection with anash, may they live: even if we were to say that these reasons are valid, this only pertains to the realm of reward and punishment. However, all that is gained through the bond of friends and being among Chassidim cannot be replaced by justifications. Every day that passes—and who can say what happens when a week, a month, a year, or even a week of years passes—is a loss that cannot be recovered. These days are "lacking days" rather than "complete days." Elaborating on this is superfluous, for in any event, if you are going to take action, these lines will suffice; and if this is of no avail, what good would it do if I were to write another page? The matter depends solely on your will, for the ability is in your hands. May Hashem grant you the merit to bring this about as soon as possible, and may you very soon feel the void of what you are missing because of this. As the saying goes: when one feels that something is not right and needs to be fixed, that feeling itself is the beginning of the rectification.

With blessings that you bring good news regarding all of the above.

## 1751

1751

B"H, 7 Menachem Av, 5712

Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...I am not at ease with matters of *machlokes* in any form whatsoever... It is understood that one cannot compromise on fundamental issues regarding *chinuch*, but in matters involving only money, one must be wary of *machlokes*. It can easily lead to a descent—getting dragged into a dynamic of *nitzachon* (victory). As is explained in *Chassidus*, when it comes to the *middah* of *nitzachon*, there are no restraints. This is not only true on the side of *kedushah*; on the contrary, *le'umas zeh* (in the opposing realm), when one enters into *nitzachon*, he will stop at nothing. Therefore, it is worthwhile to make the greatest effort and seek out many different strategies to obtain everything necessary for the *avodah* without becoming involved in *machlokes*, and without touching or provoking others—especially to the point where one would go with *mesiras nefesh* just to win, whatever the cost may be. I look forward to hearing good news from you regarding all of the above...

## 1762

1762

B"H, 7 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and learned, engaged in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Efraim Eliezer HaKohen, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter in due time, dated Rosh Chodesh Menachem Av, in which you write regarding the Yahrtzeit on the 10th of Menachem Av. Regarding your mention that this is perhaps the difference between Shaul and Dovid—that Shaul did not have a connection with all the various types of people in his generation—this is explained in the words of our Sages as to why the kingdom of Shaul did not endure: because there was no blemish in him, etc., and we do not appoint a communal leader unless he has a "basket of reptiles" hanging behind him (Yoma 22b). Even though it is necessary that they be only **behind him**, nevertheless, the matter must exist. This applies not only in a general sense, but also in a personal sense. As is known from the story of the Mitteler Rebbe, one should not answer a question asked during Yechidus regarding spiritual rectifications until one finds that same thing within oneself, in the most subtle of subtleties. In simple logic, this can be explained based on the exposition of our Sages (on the verse in Shemos 23:21): "Do not rebel against him, for he will not forgive your transgression," for he is from the category of those who do not sin. See also the matter of Shaul and Dovid in Sefer HaLikutim by the Arizal, Shaar Alef, Chapter 19.

Enclosed is the addition to the Reshimah on Eichah that was published recently, and it will surely reach you before the aforementioned Yahrtzeit.

With blessings that these days be transformed into gladness and joy, very soon.

***

**Rabbi Efraim Eliezer, may he live and be well:** Yalles. Additional letters to him appear above, 1729, and in the references noted there.

**The story of the Mitteler Rebbe:** See Igros Kodesh of the Rebbe Rayatz, Vol. 3, Letter 718.

## 1763

B"H, 7 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Having written responses to your questions, I will take the liberty of addressing a general point: "Days are fashioned, and not one of them is [extra]" (Tehillim 139:16). It is explained in several places in Chassidus that a person’s days are given in a measured amount in order to fulfill their mission in this world, and there is not a single day or even a single moment beyond what is required for their avodah. It is also understood that any amount of time, even the smallest, spent on trivial matters, naturally results in a deficiency in the fulfillment of that mission.

Consequently, regarding the content of your letter, it is a pity to spend time raising questions about others—why they act in one way and not another—because that is the business of others. What is most necessary and essential for each of us—except for those who bear responsibility for the many and the like—is to dedicate one's time, energy, and strength to fulfilling one's own mission. When the Yetzer Hara sees that questions about others do not prevent you from your own avodah, it will naturally cease to bring upon you the concealment and obfuscation that causes you to see faults in others, since there will be no benefit in it for the Yetzer Hara.

The same applies to the matters you discuss at length in your letter regarding whether or not you can influence your surroundings; this is a waste of time. The ruling for each and every one of you has already been stated by the founders and directors of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim: every single one of the Temimim must be a lamp **to illuminate**. This is explained in the reshimah from the fifth candle of the past Chanukah, which you have surely seen. Since you know the halachic ruling that you are a lamp and that you must illuminate your surroundings, you must proceed immediately to the work. Any further debate is superfluous and, consequently, only harmful...

## 1764

B"H, 7 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 11 Tammuz, in which you write briefly about the events of your life until now, and that you are currently occupied with your work in the field of proper chinuch as a teacher in a moshav at a Talmud Torah, bringing the hearts of the children of Yisrael closer to our Father in Heaven, and you ask for my opinion as to whether you are permitted to remain in your position, due to several reasons, etc.

Regarding the situation you describe in your letter, that there are about one hundred children in the Talmud Torah—may they increase—and that you influence them and teach them in a spirit of yiras shamayim, not only are you permitted to remain in your position, but you are obligated to do so. As for the arguments you write in your letter against this, you must seek counsel and strategies on how to remove them, and surely Hashem will provide you with ways for all these obstacles to be removed.

Regarding your question as to how you can attain a great measure of yiras shamayim, ahavas Hashem, ahavas haTorah, etc., in our days the path to this is the study of Toras HaChassidus, which deals with and brings one to yiras Hashem, ahavas Hashem, ahavas haTorah, and ahavas Yisrael. Everyone sees this tangibly, and "what is well-known requires no proof." Surely you can find acquaintances who can advise you on how to begin this study and guide you in a manner appropriate to your sensibilities and talents. May Hashem fulfill the requests of your heart in a profound way, that you may be a true yirei shamayim and merit to bring the hearts of those you influence and your students closer to our Father in Heaven.

With blessings, awaiting good news.

## 1765

1765

B"H, 10 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I have received your letter on behalf of the woman requesting prayer and a blessing for her son, may he live and be well, who is not in proper health. When I visit the Ohel of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention him for a speedy recovery.

You must clarify with his mother whether he was born in purity. If, Heaven forbid, he was not, inform me immediately. Also, tell her to ensure that in the home where the bochur lives, all the mezuzos are kosher. Furthermore, she should wrap a kosher mezuzah in three layers of paper or envelopes—one of which should be waterproof—and the bochur should carry it on his person (naturally, when entering a restroom or a bathroom, he should remove it; likewise, he should not carry it on Shabbos or Yom Kippur). Additionally, she should have all the mezuzos in her home checked to ensure they are kosher according to the law, and he should wear a tallis katan and carry it. I do not know the age of the bochur, but if he is of an age to pray, he should daven every day; if he does not know Hebrew, he should at least do so in English. The bochur’s mother should give one penny to the charity of Rabbi Meir Baal HaNes before lighting candles every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov.

Beyond what is stated above, you must consult a specialist physician for this condition, as in recent years they have found treatments that help those suffering from epilepsy, may Hashem protect us—either curing it entirely or alleviating it. Surely in Johannesburg there are doctors who are knowledgeable about this. I hope to hear good news regarding all of the above.

With blessings, and awaiting good news.

## 1756

1756

B"H, 10 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Directorate of Agudas Chassidei Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily,
To those upon whom they shall live,

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from the 24th of Sivan, the 8th of Tammuz, two letters from the 17th of Tammuz, and the minutes of the meetings from the 10th and 13th of Tammuz. It is surprising that there are no minutes from the other meetings scheduled according to the plan; after all, there is supposed to be a meeting every week. Perhaps this schedule has been interrupted due to the summer...

In general, the work of Chabad in the Holy Land is currently at a crossroads. That is to say, there is a choice: either the work will continue from here on as it has in recent years—meaning, in a way of "how could it be otherwise," where if it goes well, it goes well, and if it earns a profit, it is good, and if not, it does not matter, and perhaps it is even better that way—

Or, they will establish the work on a proper foundation, with appropriate development and expansion, both internally and externally.

It goes without saying that when one chooses the first approach, it does not preclude the possibility that after some time, they might adopt the second approach. Furthermore, in that case, one does not take any responsibility upon oneself: he promised nothing, took nothing upon himself, and on the contrary, for every action, even the smallest of the small, he receives thanks both in this world and in the World to Come.

This is not the case when one chooses the second path; then, one takes upon himself a very great responsibility, both internally and externally. And then, one also rules out the possibility of adopting the first approach later. But it is also understood that it is impossible to know in advance whether, after some time, the same ability and possibility to develop Chabad work in the Holy Land will exist as they do now—and even now, they are less than they were last year.

Therefore, I have requested that R. M. G. [Rabbi Moshe Gourarie] arrange a meeting, and **not** to conduct propaganda, but rather to convey my aforementioned perspective regarding the manner of Chabad’s work in the Holy Land. He should propose to each and every one that they inform me of their opinion—that is, whether they hold by the first approach (in which case, it goes without saying that either they will inform me of this, or even those who do not inform me and do not answer at all, I must necessarily count them and include them in the camp of those who hold by the first approach, or those who do not wish to participate in the work of Chabad in the Holy Land at all),

And those who are truly connected to the activities of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and consequently desire their development and are prepared to dedicate to this a specific portion of everything that belongs to them—their money, their body, and even their soul—should inform me as well. Then I will know if I have the ability to proceed with an expanded work plan in the Holy Land, or if we have not yet merited this.

Once again, I wish to emphasize that each person should answer individually and in a separate envelope, so that there should be no element of coercion, embarrassment, or shame, etc., since this matter is extremely serious, and as mentioned, one must invest (ein-shtellen) not only money and body, but also soul. By writing in this manner, there will be no room later for self-justification (even before oneself), as there was in other matters where they signed in public and consequently justified themselves afterward (whether between themselves, or between them and their Creator, or between them and their friend): "What could he have done? It would not have been appropriate not to sign, but he does not truly stand behind it..."

May it be the will [of Hashem] that each one of us merits to fulfill his shlichus with joy, expansiveness, and tranquility of soul and body.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

***

**R. M. G.:** Rabbi Moshe Gourarie.

## 1757

10 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Kfar Chabad,
May they live,

Peace and Blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters from Tuesday, Wednesday, and Thursday, 24 Tammuz, and from the eve of Shabbos Parshas Pinchas, as well as from Thursday, 5 Menachem Av, with its attachment.

2) It causes me very great distress to see the lack of discipline and the resulting disorder prevailing in the Kfar.

I do not know the clear solution for this, and seemingly, no advice is needed beyond recognition. As has been explained, recognition also entails internal understanding and the feeling that the village bears the name Kfar Chabad. When it was founded, it received the blessing of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and it is known what he said here while he was still alive in this world: **"He himself directs the matter."** Consequently, you must view all matters of the Kfar as touching upon the desire, will, and name of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. This is not merely a private matter. The practical difference in this is twofold: On the right side—since this is his concern and he is the Nasi of the generation, meaning that through him all the influences relevant to our generation are drawn down, not only spiritual influences but also material ones (and as is known, this is the concept of the Nasi, that all the influences of the generation—without exception—are drawn through him; this is why it was necessary that even physical meat for the generation of the desert be influenced through the medium of Moshe Rabbeinu, even though he said, "Whence should I have meat?"—and as explained in Chassidus, the interpretation of this is that he said, "Whence should *I* have meat?"), therefore, you receive his influence (provided the channels are aligned with his desire and will) with success (which means above the natural order), and you use it for healthy, joyful things. And also on the other side—meaning that when things are not done as they should be, you thereby increase the power of the *sitra achra*, not only within your own four cubits, but also within the four cubits of the Nasi of the generation. Consequently, this affects the collective to a much greater degree than the aspect of the mutual responsibility that all of Israel is responsible for one another. Elaboration on this is superfluous, as the matter is quite simple, especially for those who have studied Chassidus and possess the sense for the matter of *hiskashrus*, etc.

4) I have written some time ago regarding the great necessity to conduct a campaign to increase the number of residents in the Kfar. Even if space is tight for the time being, you wrote to me long ago that you are preparing to add houses, and therefore, the campaign should be started in good time.

5) During Mr. Shazar’s visit with me, he told me, as a simple matter, that everyone had already agreed that they would remain in their place now, and that they would assist them in every respect. Therefore, I do not understand why you write in your letter as if there is still doubt about the matter.

6) I have written some time ago to the administration of Agudas Chabad regarding the greater necessity of building: 1) A vocational school, 2) For the agricultural youth aliyah. Although the vocational school belongs primarily to the plan of the Lod Yeshiva, since for several reasons the location of the aforementioned vocational school will be in the Kfar, the matter pertains to you to a great extent as well. Especially since one can hope for a source of livelihood through this, as well as from the agricultural school, for many families. Consequently, it is a wonder and requires investigation why the negotiations regarding all this are being conducted with negligence. May it be the will of Hashem that you do not miss the hour, and that you utilize it to its fullest.

7) Regarding what I wrote about the aid you received for the *Shemittah* year, my astonishment was not so much about the matter itself (as the sum is very small), but rather that I received such information from the side and by chance (which, as is known, is by *Hashgacha Pratis*), at a time when I have been urging for some time that for the benefit of these matters, information must be received here promptly, because often, the practical difference is felt here on the spot. This is not, Heaven forbid, a matter of giving me honor. I am astonished why this detail has not been arranged until now.

8) I am distressed that both in the Kfar and in our institutions in the Holy Land (may it be rebuilt) in general, each institution conducts itself as an independent unit. The manager of one institution views the other institutions as competitors and opponents. Even though the position is correct that the manager of every institution must first and foremost be interested in the welfare of his institution—as that is his primary duty—at the same time, they must know that the growth of any Chabad institution in the Holy Land, whatever it may be, will almost certainly also assist in the development of the institution that he heads. Furthermore, there are times when one institution must "bend" its own current benefit for the sake of the benefit of a fellow institution, and this is not a loss for him, but only for a short time, for surely in a short while, good will sprout from this very loss for the one who seemingly lost out.

I do not mean this regarding matters and conduct that are above human intellect, but simply as a matter of human logic.

(The proof is that even among non-Jews, they conduct themselves in this order.) It is possible—and sometimes it is likely—that since the institution for which they are arguing is involved, its management is suspected of distorting the judgment. But surely it is possible each and every time to find several of *Anash* who are neutral in the matters being discussed, and to present the arguments from all sides before them. Then, it will be according to the saying of the Mitteler Rebbe, that when one tells his own situation to another, "the two *nefesh* become one *nefesh*." My hope is that, at least in the future, you will correct this detail as well, both in the Kfar and in the other institutions.

The specific matter that brought me to write about this is:

9) I have written some time ago regarding the lack of development of the girls' school in the Kfar.

Although I understand the cold attitude toward all this from *Anash* (may they live), as they are not accustomed to paying special attention to the education of girls during the time when their character is being formed, we have only the instruction of our Nasi, my father-in-law, the Rebbe. Even while he was in Riga, he began to take a great interest in the education of girls, and especially from the year 5700, he set his holy heart to this more and more, and invested his energy and his lofty powers in this matter even more than was known publicly. This is an instruction for us regarding the demand of this hour, especially in the Holy Land (may it be rebuilt), and in the most recent times, when the education of girls has become more and more of a necessity. Consequently, it is also necessary that each of us change, or at least suppress, his opinion and habit, and decide for himself: "Does this matter sit well with me? No, since my father-in-law, the Rebbe, commanded it, it is surely a necessity in Chabad." And regarding the practical action: since I hear that the greatest obstacle to the development of the girls' school in the Kfar is the lack of a suitable place, I propose and request, doubly and triply, that as soon as possible (so that the matter can be publicized some time before the start of the school term), you choose a more suitable place for the girls' studies, and it would be even better for an expanded kindergarten for boys and girls as well...

With a blessing for success in all matters for each and every one.

## 1758

1758

By the grace of Hashem, 10 Menachem Av, 5712

Brooklyn.

To the brilliant Rabbi, the G-d-fearing Chossid, who toils in communal affairs,
Rabbi R. Sh. Y. (may he live and be well),

Greetings and blessings!

With pleasure, I acknowledge receipt of your letters from the evening following Shabbos, Parshas Matos-Masei. I also confirm that I have received, in these past few days, the first two volumes of the *Talmudic Encyclopedia* from the "Sifrei Yisrael" publishing house, by order of Mr. Bar-Lev. Many thanks for this. Although I have not yet had the time to even leaf through them, I would like to offer two general observations, and I ask your forgiveness—though I fear this may not be within your direct control—namely:

a) Since an encyclopedia in general, and a Talmudic one in particular, is intended to be a reference work—and especially a Talmudic one, which is used by yeshiva bochurim and those toiling in Torah, who are not always careful about preserving the pages of a book—it is essential that the paper upon which the encyclopedia is printed be extremely durable and resistant to staining, which is not the case with this encyclopedia.

b) If the encyclopedia were to include illustrations, diagrams, and maps, it would bring clarity to many subjects. Furthermore, it would not be painful, in the spirit of what is said in *Lecha Dodi*: that the books of the "other side" are built upon a furrow, while the holy books, etc.

The tenth volume of the *Sdei Chemed* has not yet appeared, due to my lack of time to review—at least cursorily—the manner in which the indices and so on are arranged. For in addition to the approbations and various *kuntresim* (which were already printed in the *Sdei Chemed* of the past), the tenth volume contains: a general index in alphabetical order of the entries (in which the entries appearing in *Ma'areches HaKlallim* and those in *Asifas Dinim* will be integrated, as I doubt the author himself had a specific, consistent system for their division), as well as an index of authors and books. It is understood that when it is published, it will be sent to you.

I trust you received my letter, along with a copy of my letter to Mr. Shazar (may he live and be well). I look forward to a detailed response regarding it.

It was pleasant for me to read of your participation in the *farbrengen* of 12-13 Tammuz, and surely it will be so in the future as well.

May Hashem grant you success in inspiring your listeners and the readers of your books toward Torah and *yirah*.

Regarding what I asked about government loan bonds: my intent was, of course, toward those bonds in the United States.

Regarding the registration: according to the information I have received from *anash*, it appears that they have torn up and nullified—under various *amta'los* (and the explanation of *amta'la* is known: *emes-lo*, "it is not true")—many of the registration forms (apparently, the majority). This does not correspond at all to what Mr. Shazar (may he live and be well) told me when he was here.

Enclosed is a *kuntres* of supplements to the *Reshimos* on *Megillas Eichah*, which was published in these days.

With respect and with blessings for success in communal and personal matters, and for good health,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1759

12 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

...In general, your reasoning is correct in my opinion. However, one should not rush the aliyah. It is out of the question for it to take place during the Shemitah year, in 5712. The main point is that one must arrange for a livelihood in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, since, to my knowledge, the Joint Distribution Committee does not provide support there, nor do other institutions—which is not the case in France.

Furthermore, it is generally appropriate, with the help of Hashem, to be of benefit in one’s current location. At a time when you have a professional position in Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in France, I do not know if you would find a similar opening in Eretz Yisrael.

Surely you are aware that many of the activists located there do not have a profession in communal work. Moreover, even for those who are activists, the work there is currently bound up with friction and politics to a much greater degree than abroad.

And although this matter is explained in Chassidus regarding the nature of machlokes and the like that is found more in Eretz Yisrael, the explanation does not make the situation any easier—on the contrary. Consequently, one must take this change into account.

May Hashem grant you the correct perspective to make a decision that is good for you and your wife, may they live, in both material and spiritual matters alike.

Regarding your question as to whether it is permitted to interrupt davening by expressing additional words in Yiddish: In truth, there is no distinction between Lashon HaKodesh and Yiddish, for the concern is regarding the interruption itself, not the language used.

Although I have not heard a specific ruling on this, and there are many stories known about the early Chassidim who would add certain words during davening, in general, I am not comfortable with it. The point is that if it helps the kavanah of the davening and its effect, perhaps one could find a justification for it. But it is difficult to discern and know with certainty whether this comes from an expansion of the nefesh habahamis—which also has a foothold and an expansion during the intensification of davening, as explained regarding the "Philistines of holiness" and their counterpart (see Torah Or and Torah Chayim, beginning of Parshas Beshalach, and in Kuntres HaTefillah and Kuntres HaAvodah at the end, regarding hisbonenus in general)—or whether it comes as a spontaneous expression from the nefesh ha'elokis. Consequently, the question remains: why enter into doubt?

The justification according to the revealed Torah is explained in Shu"t Imrei Yosher (by the Rav of Tarnów), Vol. 2, section 9 (post facto), and in Nimukei Orach Chayim (by the author of Minchas Elazar), section 1 (even initially).

I am enclosing a Kuntres Miluim to the Reshimos on Megillas Eichah, which was published last week. May Hashem grant each of us the merit to be a suitable vessel for the Torah of our Nasi, our Rebbeim, may their merit protect us, and to fulfill its ultimate purpose as well, through the greatness of Talmud that leads to action.

With blessings for long life and good years, with all that implies, for you and your wife, may they live,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1170

1170

B"H, 12 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and learned R' Ben Zion, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to hear from the avreichim, R' Yisroel Gordon and R' Moshe Levertov, may they live, regarding the hachnasas orchim they received from you and the assistance you provided for their work. They also wrote to me regarding...

In general, all Yidden believe what is stated in the pasuk: "From Hashem are the steps of a man established." Taking into account that the Ribono shel Olam is *etzem hatov* and *mitva hatov l'heitiv*—an expression used regarding the Holy One, Blessed be He—the meaning of "From Hashem are the steps of a man established" is that when the Aibishter brings a Yid to a remote city and a foreign environment to which he is unaccustomed, and as a result he struggles—spiritually, materially, or both—it must be accepted with certainty that the Aibishter did not do this to cause him suffering. Rather, he has a specific shlichus to fulfill in that place. To ensure that even the body and the *nefesh habehamis* agree to this, it is connected with material matters, such as parnassah, and so on.

Often, it is not so easy to discover what that shlichus is, but in most cases, with a little reflection, one can discern what the shlichus is (provided the *yetzer hara* does not interfere). Especially in your case, as I hear that in your location there are not many *Yidden chareidim* and *yirei shamayim* in general, and *Chassidim* in particular, it is clear that your shlichus is to bring about a revival of *Yiddishkeit* in your city and environment in general, and specifically regarding the *ruach hachassidus*. The essence of *Chassidus* consists of *ahavas Hashem*, *ahavas haTorah*, and *ahavas Yisrael*.

It should not surprise you that, on the face of it, a wealthy person who possesses influence and whose words are heeded would seem better suited for such a shlichus, rather than someone who barely has parnassah. This would be a valid argument only if one were acting on one's own strength. However, since this is a shlichus from the Ribono shel Olam, who is *kol yachol*, all obstacles and hindrances fall away. This is understandable even to human logic: when Yidden see that one has no ulterior motives or politics, they listen with trust, as the rule states: "Words that come from the heart enter the heart." And as we see even in a shlichus from a human being—*lehavdil havdalos ein ketz*—the shaliach receives a reward or a gift from the sender. Today, *al achas kamah v'kamah*, since the Sender is the Ribono shel Olam, and He sees that one accepts His shlichus willingly and with *simchah*, He provides great *siyua mil'ma'alah* so that one can fulfill the shlichus.

Another point is that since the primary reason for his arrival in that place is for the sake of the shlichus, once he fulfills that shlichus, the Aibishter will *mesabev sibos*—in a positive way—to bring him to an environment that is suitable for him personally, with good parnassah.

May the Aibishter help you fulfill your shlichus easily and as soon as possible, which will surely also hasten... and in general, everything you need.

With blessings.

## 1711

1711

By the Grace of G-d
12 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh, and it caused me much pain to read what you wrote regarding your daughter, may she live.

In my opinion, you should have immediately found acquaintances of your daughter and had them begin to influence her directly, so that she would stop seeing that non-Jew. This is only part of the matter; the main thing is that you should have immediately contacted a shadchanim bureau, told them of your daughter’s fine qualities, and had them find a suitable shidduch for her—naturally, one that would also be pleasing to your daughter. It goes without saying that your daughter should not know that you requested this of the shadchanim bureau, and they must not tell your daughter about you. You should not be afraid of the idea of a shidduch through such a bureau, as a large portion of the youth arrange a shidduch through such mediation; they simply do not talk about it, and even tell their parents that they met by chance.

Based on what you write in your letter, it is perhaps not advisable for you to argue intensely with your daughter about this. Since the relationship between you is strained, it may provoke her even more. Although, on the other hand, she must not see that you are letting this pass easily, and she must know your position on this clearly, but not by entering into conflicts.

You should have the mezuzos in your home checked in general, and specifically in your daughter’s room. Your wife should give tzedakah to Rabbi Meir Baal HaNes—Rambehan—each time before lighting candles on Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov. You should add two chapters to the daily Tehillim that you recite, until Hashem Yisbarach provides a suitable shidduch for your daughter, in a good and auspicious hour—naturally, all of this should be done *bli neder*.

I hope that you will be able to bring me good news regarding this. Please also write to me the Jewish name of your daughter and the Jewish name of her mother, so that I may mention her at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, as well as that of his son, may he live.

With blessings, and awaiting good tidings.

## 1772

1772

## 1763

B"H, 13 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pained to hear the report that you are still in a state of low spirits, and as I understand it, this mood prevails in your home as well. It is not my intention to dwell at length or to enter into arguments as to whether you are justified or not. It is understood that it does not require great contemplation to understand why you are in such a state, following the tragedy—may Hashem spare us—that occurred. However, despite all this, Bnei Yisrael in general, and Chassidim in particular, must cleave—*גלוי און האלטען עס ברייט אפען* (openly and hold it wide open)—to Hashem Elokeinu. As it is written, "And you who cleave to Hashem your G-d are alive, all of you, today." This implies true life in its entirety—not merely to "push through day after day" (*שטופען א טאג נאך א טאג*), but that life should be without any lack in all that is needed materially, and without any lack regarding yourself and your household, may they live, in spirituality. 

Since perhaps, G-d forbid, you are not earning this from the Ribono shel Olam, it is stated in the holy Zohar (Vol. II, 184b): "If he stands with a shining countenance from below, then he is shone upon from above... in this manner, 'Serve Hashem with joy.' The joy of a person draws down another, higher joy. So too, the lower world, in the manner that it adorns itself, so it draws down from above." 

In short: when one strengthens oneself in *bitachon* in Hashem that He will provide that which one can be happy, courageous, and upbeat about, and one is so strong in this *bitachon* that it influences one's daily life, then one draws this down from above. One then sees, even with physical eyes, that the *bitachon* was justified. May Hashem help that you, your wife, and all your household, may they live, should see this soon and in a tangible, concrete way.

Awaiting good news.

## 1774

13 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn

To the learned Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, R' DovBer, may he live:

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 4 Tammuz with pleasure, and subsequently the package of booklets. Many thanks for the shipment. I trust that you will also send the remaining booklets, as well as letters of the Rebbe (Rashab) that contain substantive content—not merely private matters, such as responses to personal requests for advice and the like.

2) Regarding the booklets you sent: as I mentioned, one booklet is the *Sefer HaMitzvos* of the Tzemach Tzedek. Among the individual *maamarim*, a large portion are those already printed in *Torah Or*. In the second booklet, a portion consists of *drushim* printed in *Likutei Torah*. This is what I observed upon a preliminary review; when time permits, it may be possible to clarify the status of the other *maamarim* as well.

3) Regarding the question you posed: concerning an individual whose hair has turned white and who is a bachelor, which makes it difficult for him to find a *shidduch*, and he is requesting permission to dye his hair:

The matter of "a man shall not wear..." and "there shall not be a man's article..." involves several categories. There is the category of women's attire or men's articles that are prohibited by Torah law—such as weapons (it is forbidden for a woman to go to war according to Torah law [since weapons are inherently unbecoming for her (*Shabbos 63a*), and this explains the simple reading of Rabbi Yehuda ben Beteira (*Nazir 59a*) and the *Targum Yonasan* in interpreting the verse regarding weapons; there is no dispute regarding this], because "all the glory of the king's daughter is within") or matters pertaining to modesty and the like. Then there is the category of things that are considered women's attire due to nature, such as matters pertaining to beauty—for "a woman is only for beauty." Finally, there are matters that depend on local custom.

It is a simple matter that for the last category, a change is possible; that is, if the custom changes, the laws of "a man shall not wear..." may change accordingly. It is also clear that a matter prohibited by Torah law remains forbidden even if the custom changes (as in the case of the royal attire of women, end of *Maseches Tamid*). Regarding the middle category, there is room for discussion, but it is more likely that since it is not a Torah prohibition, it depends on the prevailing custom of the world in a given country.

Consequently, regarding our own situation: since many women now dye their hair from black to white due to fashion, and the barrier has already been breached—in that all men, even those who are already engaged, wish to appear younger and therefore dye their hair—since this falls into the middle category, there is reason to say that the barrier has been breached. Even if it was breached by those who are lax, and primarily by non-Jews, it has nonetheless already become a form of men's attire. Only the beautification of women is forbidden* (*Shabbos 50b*).

It goes without saying that all of the above is only for the sake of *halachah* and *sh'eilah u'teshuvah*, not for practical application. Therefore, I have been brief and have not brought proofs from the *Gemara* and *Rishonim*, as it is not for practical implementation, and time does not permit elaboration.

Regarding the practical ruling: many of the *Acharonim* have already discussed this. You should examine *Responsa Shoel U'Meishiv*, First Edition, Vol. 1, Siman 210, and the sources cited there; *Sefer Maorei Ohr* (*Kitzur Shulchan Aruch Yoreh Deah*, Siman 182); *Responsa Mahar"i Ashkenazi* (Av Beis Din of Zaltshov), *Yoreh Deah*, Siman 19; *Responsa Divrei Chaim*, *Yoreh Deah*, Siman 62; *Responsa Mahar"am Schick*, *Yoreh Deah*, Siman 173; and *Responsa Minchas Eliezer*, Vol. 4, Siman 23. See also *Sdei Chemed*, *Klallim*, Klal 116, where the content of several of the aforementioned books is cited.

With blessings for proper health. May it be the will of Hashem that your son’s marriage takes place on the day agreed upon by both sides, in a good and auspicious hour.

## 1059

1059

B”H, 13 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the learned Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, Rabbi Moshe Aryeh Leib, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 13 Tammuz (it is surprising that you did not note in your letter the significance of the date, as it is the day of *segulah* and *geulah* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, especially since it was also a general *geulah*, as explained in the letter of my father-in-law, the Rebbe). It seems I did not explain my comments and your questions regarding Tanya sufficiently, so I will address them again briefly:

1) Regarding what you wrote concerning the statement, "They adjure him, 'Be a *tzaddik*... and even if the whole world tells you that you are a *tzaddik*, consider yourself a *rasha*...'"—you ask how the term "adjuration" (*shevuah*) applies to the part about "even if the whole world tells you." To this, I answered you with two points: a) The essence of the *shevuah* is to "be a *tzaddik* and do not be a *rasha*." Everything else is merely a means to fulfill this, just as it concludes, "And know that the Holy One, Blessed be He, is pure"—regarding which it is obvious that a *shevuah* does not apply. b) Even if you were to say that the *shevuah* also applies to the clause, "and even if... consider yourself a *rasha*," it is because, in the vast majority of cases, this is most relevant to one's *avodah*. Someone who has not yet reached the level of a *tzaddik* should not be misled by this (it is understood that the primary point is as in section 'a', that the *shevuah* does not apply to this, as it is only a means).

2) Regarding your comment as to what loss would result if a *tzaddik gamur* (it is slightly difficult that you specify *tzaddik gamur*, as the question applies also to a *tzaddik* who is not *gamur*) knew that he is a *tzaddik*—the answer is that there is no harm in this. The harm is only for someone who is not at the level of a *tzaddik*, lest he be misled by this, as mentioned in my previous letter and as explained in Tanya, Chapter 13. The main warning is not to rely on what the whole world tells him.

3) Regarding your question that many *tzaddikim* testified about themselves that they were *tzaddikim*—as mentioned above, there is no contradiction here. They knew they were *tzaddikim* not because of what the world said, but through other proofs, and they were *tzaddikim* in truth. Consequently, there is no harm in this; on the contrary, as explained in many places in *Chassidus*, just as one must know one's own shortcomings, one must also know one's own virtues.

4) Regarding your comment once again that the distinction between *bilti gevul* (infinite) and *gevul* (finite) is also qualitative, and your proof is that there is no value at all of the finite compared to the infinite, and therefore the infinite is not within the category of the comprehension of created beings—and you support this with what is explained in many places in *Chassidus* that the value of one compared to a thousand thousand and myriads of myriads is equal regarding the infinite—the empirical reality proves otherwise. Namely: every person has a concept of this physical and material world, even though the number of worlds is infinite, and they are all called by the name "world," meaning they have a common denominator. Another proof is from our Sages in *Chagigah*, cited in the discussion of *bilti gevul* and *gevul* in Tanya, Chapter 46, that "every battalion of a thousand thousand... and its battalions are without number." This means that the infinite is composed (*shtelt zich tsuzamen*) of things that have number and limit. There is no contradiction here from what is brought in many places that it is impossible for the infinite to be composed of finite things, because that is only from the perspective of the created beings. However, in a place where the power of the Creator is involved and relevant, the matter becomes possible from the perspective of the Creator. Therefore, this itself serves as proof of the power of the Creator within created beings*. Furthermore, the very terms *gevul* and *bilti gevul* relate to quantity, or in the language of the philosophers, to the category of "how much" (*kamah*), and not to the category of "what" (*eich*).

I hope that this is now explained sufficiently, and I will conclude with a blessing.

## 1796

1796

B"H, 13 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Tammuz, in which you write that on the part of B.G. (may she live and be well), the proposal to hold the wedding in the month of Elul is not being accepted (and furthermore, that they are afraid (?) of Elul, though you do not state the reasons for this), and you ask for my opinion on whether you should insist on this:

Certainly, you should not insist on this, nor should you even pursue it without insistence. For although our Sages of blessed memory have said that there is no *kesubah* that does not involve some friction, this is one of those matters that one should not be particular about; and even without being particular, one should not exert effort in this regard. Consequently, you should agree to their opinion, and may Hashem grant that whatever time they set, it should be in a good and auspicious hour. Surely you will inform me in advance of the time they have set.

It is correct that you interpreted my words in my letter regarding not eating and drinking before sleep as referring only to a large meal; it does not apply at all to a light snack, and it is certainly not a matter of prohibition at all. It is merely a piece of good advice, and even then, only regarding a large meal, as mentioned above.

Regarding what you wrote concerning the library at Yeshivas Toras Emes, that it should not be publicized because the quantity of books is very small: I do not understand this. Surely in this yeshiva—as in other yeshivos—there are books in addition to those sent from here, just as in every yeshiva where there is a sufficient number to provide for the needs of the *ramim* and the students in their study of the *Rishonim* and *Acharonim*. If so, together with what was sent from here, there should seemingly be a decent amount.

Regarding what you wrote concerning additional explanation on the concept of "I, Hashem, have not changed," you should study the *maamarim* marked in the margin *, and it is my hope that through studying them, you will quench the thirst of the student who is asking. If there are further questions on this, write to me in detail. It is a pity that you did not write the name of the student and his mother’s name, so that I could mention him at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. For after all contemplation and explanations, one needs *siyatta d'shmaya* so that the matter of Torah in general, and the inner dimension of Torah in particular, should be internalized and absorbed properly and in accordance with the truth, since these are not tangible things, and especially since the *sitra achra* opposes their understanding and revelation within the soul. See *Kuntres Limud HaChassidus*, chapter 13 and onwards, regarding this.

With blessings for a proper settlement soon and for the wedding to take place in a good and auspicious hour.

***

 *) The author of the calculation erred; they are 500 complete and [the rest is] appended to the 500.

## 1779

1779

B”H, 13 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Blessings and peace!

In response to your letter from Erev Tishah B’Av, I was pleased to read that you are already home and feeling well. May Hashem Yisbarach help that your state of health should go from good to even better, and may you be able to report good news regarding this.

Regarding what you ask for my opinion concerning your non-Jewish neighbors, who are causing you difficulties and you are taking it to heart:

You must be strong in emunah—faith—which all Yidden are, believers the children of believers, that Hashem Yisbarach, who created the world, also leads the world now. He is the only Baal HaBayis over the world, both in great matters and in small details. When one strengthens oneself to conduct oneself in the ways of Torah and mitzvos, then, as it is written in the pasuk, "I will fear no evil, for You are with me"—I have no fear of evil because You, Hashem Yisbarach, are with me—and no one can, chas v’shalom, do anything that is not good. You should not overthink this at all; you only need to strengthen your bitachon. Just as Hashem Yisbarach has improved your health and brought you back home, so too will He, Baruch Hu, grant you a good life so that you will no longer know of any agmas nefesh, together with your husband, shichyu.

I hope that you will take my words to heart, and also that you will—bli neder—read Krias Shema at night, and before reading it, give a few coins to tzedakah. This will strengthen your bitachon in Hashem Yisbarach and your health, and you will be able to always report good news.

With blessings.

## 1780

1780

B”H, 13 Menachem Av, 5712

Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 26 Tammuz, in which you describe the situation regarding your American visa—that you have been working on this for some years, and each time various delays arise due to different papers and documents—and you ask for my opinion on whether to renew the exit permit, etc.

The essential point is missing from your letter: what is the reason that compels you to leave Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, for America? Although you write that you have to work hard there, etc., our Sages have already said, “No person knows in what way he will earn his livelihood,” and consequently, even in another country, it is impossible to know in advance how one will settle. Since it appears that you are earning enough for your livelihood and that of your family, may they live, and you are living in an environment that has a spirit of Torah and a spirit of yiras shamayim, and your son is being educated in the Talmud Torah of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, and in addition to this, you see through Hashgacha Pratis how many delays there have been until now in obtaining the papers required for immigration—in my opinion, for the time being, you should put this whole matter out of your mind. It is understood that you should endeavor to improve your situation within Eretz Yisrael itself, and may Hashem grant that your settlement there be successful, both materially and spiritually.

I was pleased to read in your letter about the impression made upon you by the manner of conduct and guidance at Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod. Surely, as our Sages have said, “The study is not the main thing, but the action,” this impression will be engraved within you and will lead to an increase in goodness in your thoughts, speech, and actions in your daily life.

With blessings for whatever you and your family, may they live, require.

P.S. Surely you are aware of the three daily shiurim for every person established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which are in Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, and you are keeping them.

## 1783

B"H, 13 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding the situation in his shul and the dispute between the elders and the younger members: it is the duty of a Rav and Mara D'asra to be above party lines. This means that his conduct must be such that he stands above them, and consequently, his role is to mediate between them and bring about peace. The general approach in this matter—as the specifics depend on the nature of the individuals, their soul-traits, and so on—is that the elders should be given matters of honor and provided with their needs in terms of study and the like, while the younger members should utilize their strengths in matters requiring energy and practical action, and consequently, the positions related to these tasks belong to them. Certainly, there are times when one side must give to the other—that is, providing some matters of honor to the younger members as well, and matters of action to the elders—but this is only the minority. As for the methods of implementation, it is appropriate to multiply friends among the stubborn individuals on both sides, so that they may soften their stubbornness; consequently, it will be easier afterward to bring the matter to a good conclusion. May Hashem bless His people, and this congregation among them, with peace, and may peace be the vessel that holds blessing in all matters.

With blessings for success in the above.

## 1,784

B”H, 13 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 7 Menachem Av, in which you write regarding the state of your physical health, and primarily regarding the condition of your eye:

My mind is not at ease with the fact that you write that it has been about two years since you began to feel something in your eye, yet you have not gone to see doctors. However, there is no point in crying over the past. Now, in my opinion, you must seek the advice of two specialists in this particular field. You should urge them to exhaust all possible medical treatments before they suggest anything regarding the removal of the eye, ch”v. Be strong in your trust in Hashem that it will not come to that. It is surely superfluous to remind you to be careful with Kiddush and Havdalah, as our Sages, of blessed memory, have stated that this relates to the light of a person’s eyes. Likewise, strive to increase your efforts in the study of Pnimiyus HaTorah, in a manner appropriate to your standing and situation. I will await good news from you.

I will read your Pidyon Nefesh at the tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and he will surely arouse Divine mercy on your behalf.

With blessings for true health in all matters.

## 1757

1757

B”H, 23 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to see from the invitation that your Bar Mitzvah will be celebrated this Shabbos, G-d willing.

I wish you that from the age of thirteen for mitzvos, you should grow to the age of fifteen for Talmud, and ascend in Torah and mitzvos. As our Sages say, the Torah teaches that we must always ascend in holiness—meaning that in all matters connected to Yiddishkeit, one must constantly climb higher and higher.

You surely know that the Baal Shem Tov taught his students, and all who follow in his ways, that everything is by *Hashgacha Pratis*. This means that all events in life—in human life, and especially in the life of a Jew—are not mere accidents, for everything is by Divine *Hashgacha*.

Since your Bar Mitzvah is being celebrated on Shabbos Parshas Re’eh, one should also derive a lesson for daily life from it. In truth, one can learn a great deal from the *sedra*, for the Torah is without end or limit (longer than the earth and wider than the sea). I only wish to underscore one *horah*, one lesson, that we find right at the beginning of the *sedra*, where Moshe Rabbeinu says in the name of Hashem to all Jews—young and old, for all generations and in all places:

"See, I set before you today a blessing... the blessing, if you listen... and the curse, if you do not listen."

Every expression and word in the Torah is calculated and precise.

We see in the aforementioned verses that regarding the blessing, it states: "The blessing **that** (*asher*) you will listen"—without a condition. The simple meaning is: the blessing—[is] that you will listen. But regarding the opposite of the blessing, *chas v’shalom*, it states "**if** (*im*) you do not listen"—**if** you do not listen, with doubt and condition.

This teaches all Jews, and especially a Bar Mitzvah who is just beginning his path as a Jew obligated in Torah and mitzvos by the Torah, that Hashem gives all Jews a blessing in our holy Torah: that it is a certainty that, in the end, you will all "listen to the mitzvos of Hashem your G-d." This is because in every Jew there is a *nefesh Elokis*, a Divine soul, which will ultimately fulfill its purpose.

The second case, of "not listening," is stated with doubt, because there are those for whom this never happens at all, as their entire life is according to Torah and mitzvos. But even for those for whom this case occurs—as it says later, "and you turn away from the path," *chas v’shalom*—it is nothing more than a temporary matter, for there will eventually be the "that (*asher*) you will listen," as stated above.

I wish you that you should belong to the first category: that from your Bar Mitzvah onwards, you should walk straight on the path of "listening to the mitzvos of Hashem your G-d," through *hasmadah* in learning and care in mitzvos. Then, what is said in the verse will be fulfilled for you—"the blessing," Hashem’s blessing in everything you need—and your parents will have much *nachas* from you, Jewish *nachas* and also Chassidishe *nachas*.

With blessings,

## 1788

B"H, 23 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
R' Yechezkel
Lissner, and his esteemed wife, the important activist,
may she live, etc.

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to see the first fruits of the United Emergency Campaign in Chicago for the Lubavitcher mosdos, through the first contribution that has arrived.

In the name of all the mosdos, and in my own name, I take this opportunity to express appreciation and a yasher-koach to you and to all the participants and supporters of this campaign. It is my hope, in accordance with the statement of our Sages—"we increase in matters of holiness"—that you will continue to exert every effort to carry on the work for the benefit of the holy Lubavitcher mosdos, and in particular for this current emergency campaign.

It is very important to remember that every detail and every small matter in the chinuch of Jewish children affects the future of those children. This is comparable to a seed that must take root and blossom into a fruitful tree. A small blemish in the seed, which would have no effect on a full-grown tree, can have very significant consequences for the future of the seed and can even cripple the tree.

The Lubavitcher mosdos chinuch, where the emphasis is placed on Torah and yiras shamayim—a chinuch that is kosher and on the level of taharas hakodesh—occupy a completely unique and vital place in Jewish life in various parts of the world. They bring light, warmth, and chayos into Jewish life, and this is done with true mesiras nefesh, according to the path that was indicated to us all by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Consequently, the work to strengthen and expand these mosdos must also be done with mesiras nefesh. Thereby, one enlarges the channels through which the Ribono shel Olam sends His blessings, midah k'neged midah, and the measure of good is even greater, in all that is needed, both in gashmius and in ruchnius.

In the hope of hearing good news regarding the continued work in Chicago, and with a blessing for good health and all the best.

#### 1788

For the content, see above, letter 1750.
