## 1790

1790

B"H, 26 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily,
May they live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Finally, your letter of 12 Menachem Av has been received, in which you summarize the situation regarding the Oholei Yosef Yitzchok schools in the Holy Land, and ask for my opinion regarding the various locations where you have registered students and hope to establish schools.

In addition to what I wrote in my previous letter, it is difficult, from such a distance, to provide instructions regarding the particulars and the details of the details, especially since, as is evident from your letter, the situation is liable to undergo several changes. I will therefore provide only a general directive, in addition to what was stated in my previous letters:

1) **Do not** create a stir about the entire matter. It is like the teaching of our Sages that the final missions were carried out in secret, as I wrote from the very beginning. It is a pity that, as it seems, there was excessive publicity. Not long ago, I received a copy of an article printed in the Holy Land calling this a "fifth stream," and it seems the intent is to incite strife among Jews, and a word to the wise is sufficient. We cannot cry over the past, but in any case, you must rectify this for the future.

2) In general, you must strive to organize the Oholei Yosef Yitzchok schools in those locations where you are certain of legal support, since our own resources are limited.

3) It goes without saying that the Oholei Yosef Yitzchok schools that existed last year must be maintained by all possible means. As I have already written, the distinction between the old Oholei Yosef Yitzchok schools and those being founded this summer is of no consequence at all. Surely, from here on, they will all fall under one general administration—both the old and the new. Please inform me about this as soon as possible, as I am distressed that this question has been omitted from your responses until now.

4) Regarding the debts of the old Oholei Yosef Yitzchok schools: as I have written previously, the donations from Mr. Moshe Meirzon are given on the condition that you pay off at least a certain portion of the debts of the old Oholei Yosef Yitzchok schools, and that you include them in the Reshet budget moving forward.

5) It is surprising that you mention nothing about the assistance from the activists in providing a structure [tzrif]. It is unbelievable that at a time when they are providing structures to political parties, they would withhold their assistance from a non-partisan cause.

6) Regarding what I wrote about not investing funds in structures and buildings: as mentioned above, this is only a general directive. However, if you all decide together that a certain location is an exception, I will rely on your judgment, provided that you have the capacity to maintain the institution for as long as is necessary.

7) Regarding your visit with Mr. Mordechai Surkis, you conclude that he listened to my letter with respect. I do not know your intent—whether it is worthwhile for me to write to him specifically from here, in which case there is hope for practical benefit, or whether the aforementioned person is compelled (by his party or by those who already have schools) not to permit the opening of any more schools.

8) Regarding your question as to whether to print stationery with the new letterhead: in accordance with what was said above regarding avoiding a stir, it is not worthwhile to initiate such things now, as you yourselves write in your letter that at the initial stage this is not desirable.

I look forward to your detailed letter regarding all of the above, bringing good news in practice.

With blessings for success in your holy work.

## 1791

B.H., 27 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...It is surely unnecessary to elaborate to one such as you regarding the concept explained in many places in Chassidus, as well as in works of mussar, that an *is'arusa d'leila* (arousal from Above) requires a corresponding *is'arusa d'לתתא* (arousal from below) to serve as its vessel. It is simple, with the utmost simplicity, that there is no need to introduce any innovation that contradicts the very *is'arusa d'leila* for which one is requesting and praying. I was shocked to see him in the office of the *Melach* [Military Service], striving and forcing his *nefesh elokis* to remove, *chas v'shalom*, the *tzelem Elokim* from his face, and to shear and remove the thirteen *tikkunei dikna* (rectifications of the beard), which correspond to the thirteen *mechilin d'rachamei* (channels of mercy), and which are the very conduits of *parnassah*, as explained in the Zohar and in many places in Chassidus. Further elaboration is superfluous, especially for one who comes from a Sephardic lineage, who have held fast to the study of the Zohar throughout the ages, and among whom there was never any opposition to this (as was found in some places, and in earlier times, among the Ashkenazim).

It is difficult and heavy for me to write at length about this, and surely these lines will suffice. In seeking to judge him favorably, perhaps his intention in this was that, since he sees and contemplates the words of our Sages that a person’s sustenance is as difficult as the splitting of the Red Sea, it occurred to him that perhaps it would be worthwhile to "ease" the burden of the *Ribono shel Olam* in His work—He who provides for all, from the eggs of lice to the horns of the wild ox—by making his external appearance resemble that of the nations, thinking that then it would be easier for him to be granted a position as a rabbi or the like. But this opinion is not even "easily understood by the wise"; it is the opposite of simple faith to say that by making light of the fulfillment of the Torah’s *mitzvos*—that is, by distancing oneself, *chas v'shalom*, from the Source—one will thereby be influenced with abundant *shefa*. See what is explained at length regarding the concept of "in order to add the watered to the thirsty."

My hope is strong that the strength invested in him by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *ztzukl"h, nbg"m, zy"a*, as his student and Chassid, will assist him in emerging from the aforementioned erroneous line of thought. And if there is still someone in the middle inciting him, he should explain to that person as well that such conduct is contrary not only to Divine intellect but even to human intellect, since every believing Jew knows that it is specifically the *Ribono shel Olam* who is the Master of the house, even in this physical and material world, and He, and He alone, is the One who determines the sustenance of a person and his household. Consequently, the *is'arusa d'לתתא* must be in accordance with this.

Awaiting good tidings and blessing him
With success in spirituality and materiality,
In a manner where the man and the woman,
The Jewish couple, shall walk hand in hand.

Regarding the trimming of the beard, our Nasi, the Tzemach Tzedek, wrote at length in *Responsa Yoreh Deah* 93. See also *Chiddushei Maharitz Chayes*, Chapter 3.

*Piskei Din* to *Yoreh Deah* 181, 2. *Derech Mitzvotecha*, Part 2, 221.

In the book *Amudei Arazim* (by Rabbi Margalit, may his light shine), at the end, he collects the opinions of the *Acharonim*, etc., regarding the above.

## 1792

1792

B"H, 27 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which it appears that I have not yet succeeded in elevating your spirits: I believe I have already told you several times that according to what is explained in the sefarim—and not only in Chassidic texts—one should not invent reasons for melancholy, for this is a suglah that the thing will actually come to pass. And it is not only in speech that one should not invent such things—consistent with what is brought in Chassidic discourse (I believe it is printed at the end of the *Siddur Meah Shearim*) that when the Maggid would have a thought, he would express it in speech in order to draw it down into the world—but even in thought one should not invent such a premise. The reason is as stated above, and it is also understood from the sayings of our Rebbes, the Nesi’im, as the Rebbe, my father-in-law, related that they would say: "Think good and it will be good."

You surely feel that it is very difficult to exert control over the power of thought in the manner mentioned above. If so, you have no choice but to clothe the power of thought in thoughts of Torah, and from that good in spirituality, good will also be drawn down in physicality.

The conclusion from all of the above is that the more you strengthen your *bitachon* until you influence your mind and heart as well, the more this will be tangibly realized in expanded *parnassah*, both in physicality and in spirituality...

With blessings.

#### ***1792***

**Siddur Meah Shearim:** 28a. See also Letter 1558 above.

**From the sayings:** See Letter 872 above, and the references in the notes there.

## 1793

1793

B”H, 27 Menachem Av, 5712

Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

...The continuation of the Rebbe’s, my father-in-law, memoirs regarding his imprisonment has not yet been published; when it is printed, it will, G-d willing, be sent to you.

I was pleased to read in your letter that your daughter, may she live, has promised to conduct herself and manage her home according to the customs of Jewish homes. However, it is a known halachic ruling that in a situation where one can verify, one should not rely on a presumption (*Shulchan Aruch, Yoreh Deah*, section 1, paragraph 1, in the *Hagah*). This is especially true regarding a matter that affects generations and generations to come until the end of time. Therefore, I take the liberty of prompting you once again: regarding the laws of *taharas hamishpachah*, at the very least, one must know for certain whether she is familiar with the relevant details. There are now books printed in the local language containing all the laws and details, published by the Young Israel and similar organizations.

In years past, there were those who were embarrassed to speak about this. Yet, experience has already taught us that, in contrast, people speak about and print matters of obscenity, etc., and even receive awards—*preizen* in the local tongue (and, as a play on words, one could say it is close to the word *pritzus*—immodesty). Yet, when it comes to speaking about matters that touch upon the very soul of parents and their children, the *sitra achra*—the "clever one"—arrives and reminds us of the trait of the Jewish people, that they are bashful. Further elaboration on this is unnecessary.

I would point out the Gemara in *Nedarim* (20a)—see there in the *Chiddushei Aggados* of the Maharsha—and also *Yevamos* (79a) regarding the three traits (*Gevurah, Baishanus, Rachmanus*) for which the Jewish people are distinguished. Compassion and acts of kindness are innate, dating back to the days of our forefather Avraham. Bashfulness, however, was only acquired at the time of the Giving of the Torah (which explains the remarkable precision in *Tanya*, end of Chapter 1, where it mentions only *rachmanim* and *gomlei chasadim*, but not *baishanus*, and does not even conclude with the word "etc."—the reason being as stated above). The moral lesson for us all is that bashfulness must be consistent with what was sworn and established at Mount Sinai, for that is when it was given to the Jewish people. Without this, the Jewish people are, in fact, the "boldest of the nations" (*Beitzah* 25b).

I am sure you will forgive me for all the above, for my intention is only for the good. The main thing is that you clarify and endeavor to ensure the aforementioned, for as our Sages have ruled, words that come from the heart enter the heart.

With blessings for true health for you, your wife, and all your household, may they live, and regards to your son, may he live, who visited me with you. I am interested to know in what way he has drawn closer to Hashem, our G-d, during this time—as we surely draw closer, according to our Sages, "we elevate in holiness." Indeed, we are all drawing closer to the time of the coming of our Moshiach and the end of our exile.

With blessings.

## 1794

1794

B"H, 27 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, who engages in communal needs, etc.,
R' Chaim Hillel, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

...I was very pleased by what you wrote in your letter regarding the efforts to circumcise the children of your students who, for various reasons, have not yet been circumcised. Beyond the immense importance of bringing a Jewish person into the covenant of our forefather Avraham—and great is the mitzvah of milah, for which thirteen covenants were sealed, and milah is an **acronym** for "Who shall go up for us to heaven" (*Mi ya'aleh lanu hashamaymah*) and its **final letters** spell the Name Havayah—I was especially pleased that you do not settle for merely fulfilling your duties as teachers, but have grasped the essence and the inner purpose of education: to draw the hearts of the children of Israel to their Father in Heaven. May it be the will of Hashem that you have success in this avodah that transcends nature, and that you influence your students—and through them, their parents' homes as well—to illuminate them with the candle of mitzvah and the light of Torah...

With blessings for success in all your general and personal matters, and for your family, may they live.

## 1796

1796

B"H, 27 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

The esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned man, who occupies himself with communal needs, etc., R' Moshe Leib Radstein, may he live, conveyed your regards to me, as well as your request that I mention you regarding your livelihood, as you are not satisfied with how things have been going until now.

Without a vow, when I visit the resting place of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, on the eve of the upcoming Rosh Chodesh, I will mention you and your household, may they live, for what you require—specifically regarding your livelihood, as per your request—and I hope to hear good news from you in this regard.

I am not familiar with the conduct in your hotel, but it would be appropriate—and this is also a vessel for blessing and success in livelihood—that in the hotel lobby, or in the designated reading room or on the tables, there should be a number of Jewish books that would inspire fear of Heaven and knowledge of Torah for the readers, both in Yiddish and in English. I believe you will be able to find someone to help you compile a list of such books.

I conclude my letter with a blessing for an abundant livelihood, and may Hashem grant you material success, and may you transform that materiality into spirituality.

With blessings.

In response to your letter—which lacks an indication of when it was written—regarding your good intention to come here for the upcoming Yomim Noraim, and that your wife, may she live and be well, agrees to this, just as it was last year:

Likewise, it would be appropriate for you to gladden your wife, may she live and be well, in a suitable manner, since you will be traveling here for the aforementioned duration and she will remain there...

## 1888

1888

B"H, 28 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter, in which you write that you have been offered the opportunity to set up a tzitzis manufacturing operation by machine in the village, and the proposal comes from someone who has a license for this as well as the necessary machines, but neither he nor you have knowledge of the methods and ways required to arrange for them to be sold abroad—which is your primary intention, to supply tzitzis abroad.

In my opinion, since he is requesting that you participate in this with a significant sum, and most importantly, since it is not known to you in what manner you would be able to sell the large quantity abroad, I do not know—and it is highly doubtful—if this proposal is good even from a commercial perspective. In addition to this, there is the spiritual reason: although it is known that my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory, permitted—during the First World War, in the year 5675—the use of tzitzis made by machines operated by Yidden, surely this was a permission granted due to the exigencies of the time, as refugees were arriving in Russia from Poland and Lithuania. But, of course, there is no *hiddur* in this at all. Consequently, since a livelihood is not clearly visible from this, and rather, it creates a stir—at a time when there are enough tzitzis made by hand, to come to Lubavitch and publicly validate as *lechatchilah* tzitzis made by machine—for the sake of a very meager salary that this provides. Therefore, the matter is not worthwhile, neither in *gashmius* nor in *ruchnius*.

Conversely, I have heard that there is someone interested in organizing the manufacturing of *batim* for tefillin, as well as the writing of *parshiyos*. If it is possible to organize such an operation that would be *mehudar*, and the letters of the script would be in the form that the Alter Rebbe ruled, and surely one can find in Eretz Yisrael—may it be built and established—those who know this by tradition, scribe from scribe, then in my opinion, one should take an interest in such a proposal, provided, of course, that it is sound (*oisgehalten*) from a basic commercial perspective.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1882

B”H, 28 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Saadia, may he live, Shaliach

Greetings and blessings!

## 1803

1803

B"H, 28 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of the 10th of Menachem Av, in which you express your satisfaction with the matters I **touched upon** in my previous letter. I write "touched upon" precisely, for it is difficult to detail things in writing as much as is necessary, especially when I do not fully know your inclinations and sensibilities. As is stated in the introduction to the Tanya regarding the superiority of oral communication over written communication: the reader interprets the text according to his own path, mindset, and level of intellectual grasp, etc., for not all minds and opinions are the same, etc.

Regarding your question as to whether it is possible to interpret the time of the six days of Bereishis such that each "day" refers to a period of many years, which would consequently allow it to be reconciled with the claims of the scientists of geology, astronomy, etc.:

This interpretation cannot be accepted (even though some Jewish scholars, with all due respect, have erred in this). The entire concept of Shabbos depends on this, for one of the two reasons for observing Shabbos is: "For in six days Hashem made..., and on the seventh day He rested and was refreshed." This is the simple proof—in addition to many other proofs and evidence in both the revealed and hidden Torah—that these six days are literally as they are understood in their plain sense. This is also how we write on legal documents in this year: the year 5712 from the creation of the world. Do not let this cause you any confusion, for the scientists themselves contradict one another **from one extreme to the other**, etc., regarding these calculations.

I was very pleased to learn that the esteemed Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, engaged in communal needs, etc., Moreinu Harav Mordechai HaKohen Perlow, may he live, is assisting you with the construction of the mikveh so that it will be built with the proper hiddur (beautification) according to the opinion of our holy Torah. May it be the will of Hashem that his efforts to bring taharah into the world—which is one of the foundations for the endurance of the families of the Jewish people (according to what is explained in the Tosafos Yom Tov at the end of Maseches Yoma, this also hastens the end of the Geulah)—will bring him success and blessing in his affairs, and especially in finding his suitable match, both materially and spiritually, very soon.

Enclosed is a segment of what was discussed on Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Elul, which I am sure you will publicize in an appropriate manner among your acquaintances. I do not know your talent for translation, but if you could endeavor yourself, or through others, to translate such segments into Italian, I would be pleased if they were printed. It would be best if you could send me a copy (as I have some familiarity with that language) before printing.

With blessings for success in material and spiritual matters.

 **In my letter:** See above, letter 1762. See also below, letter 1824.
**The scientists themselves contradict:** See this at length in the booklet "Emunah U'Mada" (Kehot, 5737), p. 89 and onwards.

## 1505

B"H, 29 Menachem Av, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Blessings and peace!

...Regarding your inquiry as to our custom concerning leaving peyos on young boys:

The custom is that until the age of three, one does not cut the hair at all, not just the peyos. From three years old and onward, one cuts the hair while leaving the peyos at the proper length.

Enclosed is a receipt.

## 1555

B"H, 1st of Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter from Tuesday, Parshas Vaeschanan, and due to various reasons, the response has been delayed.

You write regarding your house on New York Avenue, that a colored family has purchased a house in the neighborhood, and consequently, your mother (may she live and be well) does not know what to do regarding your house.

As far as I recall, I have already answered a similar question in the past: it seems to me that you should sell the house to a buyer who will offer the best price and conditions, but at the same time, the money should be invested in a house in a suitable section.

Regarding the second question, that your mother is facing a lawsuit from someone who fell down the stairs and is demanding $20,000, and you are covered by insurance for only half of that amount, and you ask if it is worthwhile to hire a lawyer: it seems to me that this itself is something you should discuss with a lawyer, because in such a case, the court usually does not grant the entire amount of the claim. On the other hand, there are lawyers who take on a case not for a fixed fee, but for a percentage (on a contingency basis) of the amount they win for their client. You certainly have someone you can ask about this.

In any event, you should tell your mother that she has no reason to be in a panic because a colored family is moving into the neighborhood, for they are also people with whom one can live, and conversely, among white people, there can also sometimes be those who are not suitable. The reason I advise you to sell the house is: a) in case the price drops, and b) to calm her nerves.

I was very pleased to read that you have been reviewing a maamar from 12 Tammuz. I hope that you will generally utilize the time you are at the hotel, where various people from different cities gather, to convey to them at least the fundamentals of Toras HaChassidus regarding Ahavas Hashem, Ahavas HaTorah, and Ahavas Yisrael.

May Hashem grant you success in finding a good arrangement, and may your mother have much Yiddishe nachas from all her children (may they live).

## 1807

B"H, Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter in due time, in which you write regarding your situation concerning *shechita*, etc. I was especially pleased to see that you are seeking advice and strategies on how to organize a *shiur* for young people and *bochurim*. Regarding your doubt as to whether your knowledge of the local language is sufficient for this, experience has already shown that if one understands well what the other is saying, even a limited ability to speak the local language is more than enough—provided that you do not show any sign of discouragement due to a lack of complete fluency in the language. This is especially true since the purpose of your speech is of the highest order, and consequently, there will be *siyata d’shmaya*. I hope that by the time you receive this letter, this idea has already been realized in practice, or at the very least, has moved closer to fruition. It is surely unnecessary to remind you that the goal of this *shiur* must be to guide them in matters of *mitzvos maasiyos*. The starting point for this—since, as you write in your letter, some of them say *Kaddish*, etc.—is that they must put on *tefillin*. It is very easy to explain to them that it is a contradiction to say *Yisgadal v’yiskadash shmei raba* while at the same time refusing to accept upon oneself the yoke of the Kingdom of Heaven, etc., etc.

Enclosed is the *kuntres* for the *yeshiva* students traveling on the *shlichus* of the *Melach* [Merkaz L'inyonei Chinuch], which is truly relevant to every single Jew, especially those who find themselves in an environment to which they are unaccustomed. For the soul of every Jew ascended in [Hashem’s] thought—and as is explained in *Chassidus*, even in that thought they are at a lofty level—and descended from a high roof to a deep pit, to this world, the world of *kelipos* and *sitra achra*, where the wicked prevail, etc., as is written in *Etz Chaim* and cited in *Tanya*, end of Chapter 6.

Regarding the enclosure in your letter, you did not indicate to which fund it belongs; therefore, it has been given to the *kupat chashaim* [anonymous charity fund], which is among the most excellent levels of the *mitzvah* of *tzedakah*.

With blessings for *parnassah* in both body and soul, and *ksivah v’chasimah tovah*.

## 1808

1808

B"H, 1 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter from Tuesday, the day on which "it was good" was doubled, in which you write about yourself and your wife, ask for my opinion on the matter, and also request a blessing.

When I am at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention both of you so that Hashem may help you with good health and parnassah, and gladden your hearts soon with living and enduring children.

In order to receive the blessings of Hashem, one must have the appropriate vessels for them, which are the matters of Torah and mitzvos. I was pleased to hear from the esteemed Chossid, a man of action, involved in communal needs, etc., Rabbi Ben Zion Shemtov, that you are conducting yourselves as you should. I would only like to suggest that in the morning, before davening, you should give a few pennies to tzedakah, and that your wife, may she live, should give tzedakah each time before lighting candles on Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov.

You should also convey to your wife that she should strengthen herself in her bitachon in Hashem, who created and directs such a vast world, and who certainly oversees each one of you with hashgacha pratis to lead you in the best possible way. She should rely on the Torah and the Shulchan Aruch, not being more stringent than the Shulchan Aruch requires, but also, Heaven forbid, not making light of the Shulchan Aruch. When one conducts oneself as the Shulchan Aruch prescribes, these are good vessels to receive the blessings of Hashem for whatever one needs.

You should also ensure that the mezuzos in your home are kosher. Especially in this month of Elul, the month of mercy, each of you—or you together with your wife—should speak for at least a few minutes about bitachon in Hashem. I hope that soon you will be able to share good news with me, that you and your wife are feeling well, that you have strengthened yourselves in your bitachon in Hashem, and that you see hashgacha pratis, that He, blessed be He, is leading you toward the good, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*, and awaiting good tidings.

## 1,018

B"H, 1st of Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

The Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch
in Montreal,
May they live.

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your questions:

a) The curriculum for the upcoming term should, if possible, be one of the tractates that will also be studied at the Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in New York. This will be decided in the coming days, and I request that you be informed accordingly.

b) You will surely arrange that those students who are suited for such guidance will not study secular subjects. They should not remain idle during the time allotted for secular studies, but rather be occupied either with other Torah study or with reviewing their lessons. It is understood that the essential point here is the supervision to ensure they do not remain idle.

c) You surely already have a plan regarding the students who arrived from France as to how to arrange their Torah studies, and I would appreciate it if you would inform me of the details regarding this.

d) Consistent with what I have said in the past, I am interested in knowing about the efforts being made to determine how the students spend Shabbos and Yom Tov, particularly the days of the holidays and festivals of the upcoming month of Tishrei. It is understood that this can be arranged in several ways; if they live in one district of the city, it will be easier, but even if they are scattered throughout the city, one must endeavor that at least a few times they hear words of hisorerus, etc., and not be satisfied with what is told to them several days in advance regarding the holidays and festivals.

e) Even if you have never done such a thing until now, there is no need to be intimidated or afraid. On the contrary, since this is a new initiative, although it will add to the burden of the administration and the teachers, it will interest the students and those being educated more. Therefore, one should not establish rigid foundations that it must be done specifically in a certain place and at a certain time, but rather consider the benefit of the matter...

g) It is surely superfluous to remind you regarding the utilization of the days of study before Tishrei to teach the relevant students the laws of this month, and for all students, at the very least, words of hisorerus regarding the month (and also regarding the month of Elul, even though a portion of it has already passed).

With a blessing for success in your holy work and for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*, awaiting good news.

## 1111

B"H, 1 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, etc., R' Shalom, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I have received the *pidyon nefesh* that you sent on behalf of Mrs. ..., may she live, who is not feeling well in health and has already been in the hospital for several months, and who requests a blessing for a *refuah*.

When I am at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention her, so that the Rebbe may arouse great compassion for her for a speedy recovery.

However, you must explain to her that in order to receive and sustain the blessings of Hashem, she must prepare the appropriate *keilim* for this. These *keilim* are what Hashem has stated bring life, health, and *parnassah* for Jews—both women and men, both old and young. These are the *mitzvos* that the *Hakadosh Baruch Hu* gave us Jews at Mount Sinai, which must be fulfilled at all times and in all places. Especially for a woman, who can accomplish more in many matters than a man, it is very important that she acquire those *keilim*—*mitzvos*—that she does not yet have. And the *keilim*—*mitzvos*—that she already has, she should make even better and more beautiful. This means that regarding those *mitzvos* that she has not been careful with until today, she should see to it that from today onward she observes them; and the *mitzvos* that she does observe, she should perform with more vitality and more satisfaction. This will bring the blessings of Hashem to her and her family as soon as possible.

I hope that you will arrange for this to be explained to her as soon as possible, and may Hashem grant you the merit to be able to report and convey that her state of health has improved, and that she has taken upon herself to fulfill what was said regarding the observance of *mitzvos* and, in general, the matters of *Yiddishkeit* that a Jewish daughter must fulfill.

With blessing.

## 1812

1812

B.H., 1 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I received with satisfaction your letter from the middle of the month of Menachem Av, in which you write that both you and the doctor see that things are much better, and that the blood pressure was merely a **coincidental matter.** And it is not as the world calls "coincidental"—*mikreh*—for according to the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, everything is by *Hashgacha Pratis*, and there is no such thing as coincidence. Rather, within *Hashgacha Pratis* itself there are two types: those that even *sechel enoshi*—human intellect—recognizes as being by *Hashgacha Pratis*, and a second case, where *sechel enoshi* argues that it is merely a *mikreh*. But the *nefesh ha-elokis*, through its *sechel eloki* which **clothes itself** in the *sechel enoshi*, shows it the truth: that this, too, is by *Hashgacha Pratis*. Indeed, it is an even deeper form of *Hashgacha*. 

As the parable for this goes, based on what we see in *malchusa d'ara* (earthly kingdom)—for *malchusa d'rakia* (heavenly kingdom) is like *malchusa d'ara*—in the governance of a king, there are also these two types: there are the direct commands and decrees of the king, and there are matters where, for a certain reason, the king does not want it to be obvious that it comes from him. In such conduct that he demands and desires, as in the latter case, more wisdom is required so that there is a "thing and its opposite"—the matter is carried out, yet it is not known that it comes from him. And this is how one can understand it in the *nimshal* (the concept being illustrated), as it is written, "And G-d has done it, that they should fear before Him," similar to the matter of thunder. When the intent is fulfilled and it has aroused a matter of *yiras shamayim*, the phenomenon naturally ceases, and there is no longer a need for that "coincidence." The difference between a mortal king and the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He, is that with a mortal king, there can be things that happen without his knowledge or command, whereas in *malchusa d'rakia*, such a thing is *chas v'shalom* impossible.

I was pleased to read in your letter regarding the state of health of your family members, and I hope that in the future as well, you will be able to report good news to me.

Regarding your question about *davening* before the *amud*, it goes without saying that you must guard your health. But on the other hand, you must also ensure that the other person who will be the *shaliach tzibur* is a *shomer Torah u'mitzvos* and understands the meaning of the words. Therefore, it might perhaps be better to adopt a middle path: that you should *daven* the main *tefillos* of the day, and in order not to strain yourself too much, another person—for whom there are certain *ba'alim* (designated individuals)—should *daven* a portion of the *tefillos*. But as mentioned, he must be a *shomer Torah u'mitzvos*.

It pleased me to read in your letter regarding your influence on children in matters of *Torah u'mitzvos*. You should only do this on a larger scale, and also include in this not only children in physical years, but also "children" in Jewish years. As my father-in-law, the Rebbe, *zatzuklalleh"h nbg"m zi"e*, explained: among Jews, days, months, and years are counted as those in which one has conducted oneself according to *Torah u'mitzvos*. This is the meaning of "advanced in days" (*ba bayamim*). Consequently, one can be seventy years old, and in actual fact—according to the explanation given—one is still a small child.

With a wish for a *Kesiva V'chasima Tova* and to hear good news from you in both material and spiritual matters. And do not forget to write in your next letter about your *shiurim* in *Chassidus*, about which I have spoken several times: that in our time, *ikvesa d'meshicha*, learning *Chassidus* is a necessity for every Jew.

Enclosed is the *reshima* (transcript) of what I said to the students of the *yeshiva* who are traveling on a *shlichus* for the *Merkaz L'Inyonei Chinuch*. In truth, this is relevant to **every** Jew, for the Holy One, Blessed be He, has sent everyone into this world to illuminate their surroundings with the "candle of a *mitzvah* and the light of Torah," and the light within Torah is the *pnimiyus haTorah*.

With the blessing of *Kesiva V'chasima Tova*.

## 1816

## 1,517

1,517

## 1818

B"H, 1 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter of 26 Tammuz—which was somewhat delayed in transit—and regarding what you write about the state of your wife’s health, may she live: after the summer, she should consult with two specialists in the field of gynecology as to whether surgery is necessary, and she should act according to their instructions. May Hashem grant the doctors the correct insight to advise her on what is best for her.

You write in your letter that your eldest son is currently in the army. It is surely unnecessary to urge you to write to him so that he knows that every Jewish person, wherever he may be, is an emissary of the Ribono shel Olam to illuminate his surroundings with the "candle of a mitzvah and the light of Torah." This is especially and uniquely true when one is in the army, where the foundation and essence of the matter is the acceptance of the yoke of authority. He must be awakened and reminded at every moment that if he accepts upon himself to obey the commands of flesh and blood—as it is impossible otherwise—then how much more so does this apply regarding the King of Kings, the Holy One, blessed be He. It is understood that he cannot be satisfied with his own goodness; rather, he must have a "good eye" for the sake of others in this regard, as our Sages of blessed memory said, "‘Love your neighbor as yourself’—this is a great principle of the Torah." This is especially true according to what is explained in the teachings of Chassidus, that "Love your neighbor, etc." is a vessel for "Love Hashem your G-d," as explained at length in the sicha of 19 Kislev 5689 from my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

With the blessing that Hashem should merit you, together with your wife, may they live, to have Chassidishe nachas from all your children, may they live, with peace of mind and body, and with the blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*.

P.S. You are surely taking part in the activities of Agudas Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, and surely in your next letter you will write in detail regarding this.

***

1818
Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 17, p. 501, and completed according to the secretariat’s copy.

## 1519

1519

B”H, 1 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to finally receive your letter from Parshas Re’eh—the first letter since you departed—and I hope there was no other reason for the delay besides what you wrote in your letter.

I was pleased to read in your letter that you have spoken in several shuls. If time permits, you should seek an opportunity to speak specifically to the youth, especially those who do not understand Yiddish and would otherwise have the opportunity to hear a word of hisorerus regarding Torah and Yiddishkeit. Surely, when you have the opportunity, you will do so.

Regarding the bochurim whom it is possible to influence to go learn in the yeshiva, you should have consulted with Rabbi Alay, shlita, on how to continue speaking with them and the hishtadlus regarding this, even after your departure, b’sha’ah tovah u’mutzlach.

Regarding your question as to whether you should stop in Salisbury and Bulawayo, this depends on how much time you have at your disposal. It is worthwhile to be in those places for at least a day, or at least several hours, and tell them generally about Yiddishkeit, Torah, and Chassidus. Tell them where you are traveling, and that you will have the opportunity to submit their names at the Ohel of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, ztzk”l, nbg”m, zy”a, Nasi of our generation. It is a great zechus to be mentioned at the Ohel of a tzaddik in general, and of a Nasi HaDor in particular. Those who wish to have this zechus can provide their names along with their mother’s name—including women as well. At the same time, you should explain to them that in order to receive and sustain the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach, one must create appropriate keilim for them, each according to their standing and situation. You will know what to call to each person’s attention—whether it is putting on tefillin, a hidur mitzvah, keeping a shiur in Tehillim, learning a parsha of Chumash with Rashi’s commentary, or checking their mezuzos, etc., etc. With the women, one should speak about matters that are relevant to them, etc., etc.

Regarding your question about stopping in the places you are passing through: if this is not connected with any excessive expenses, it would be very appropriate, especially in places where you can utilize your knowledge of the English language. If you happen to be in London, England, you surely know that the esteemed chossid, who is involved in communal needs, Rabbi Ben Zion Shemtov, shlita, is located there. His address is 89 Cranwich Road, N16, London. May Hashem Yisbarach help you in your journey, that it should be proper in all its details.

Regarding your question about kissing your mother: it is self-understood that you may do so.

I am surprised that you do not mention your brother and sister, with whom you surely spent a considerable amount of time...

With blessings for a proper journey, for good health, and for a kesivah v’chasimah tovah—for you, your mother, and your brother and sisters, shlita.

## 1820

1820

B”H, 1 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished, engaged in communal affairs,
R’ Dovid, may he live and be well,

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter of 11 Tammuz in due time, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed therein. I read it at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and may he surely awaken great mercy for all the matters mentioned in the *pidyon*.

2) Thank you for what you wrote regarding the Beis Rivkah in the village and the kindergarten there. I was pleased to hear that they have developed and progressed over the past year, despite the various difficulties involved. Surely, for the upcoming school year, you will increase your efforts in this regard many times over, in accordance with the demands of the hour and the will of our Nasi, my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

3) I wrote some time ago to the village committee regarding the effort to secure a spacious location for the Beis Rivkah and the kindergarten. They will surely do **everything** possible in this regard. For as for the reasons you write regarding why this has not yet been accomplished—even if they are true and correct, that is only a matter concerning reward and punishment, as the Merciful One exempts one who is coerced (*oness*). However, the matter itself remains lacking. Especially according to the opinion that we do not say that one who is coerced is considered as having performed the act. And it is obvious, based on what is explained in *Toras HaChassidus* regarding the concept of *asiyah* (action) above, that the act must be performed in practice, through the refinement of physical and material matters and objects.

4) Regarding your personal situation and the health of your wife, may she live and be well, may the Ribono shel Olam surely fulfill the days of her pregnancy properly and with ease, and may she give birth to a healthy child. It is appropriate—if it has not been done yet—to have the *mezuzos* in your home checked. Your wife, may she live and be well, should give *tzedakah* before lighting candles on *Erev Shabbos* and *Erev Yom Tov*, and you should give a small sum to *tzedakah* (an amount that is not a burden to you) every weekday before *Shacharis*, until after the birth, in a good and auspicious hour. It goes without saying that all of this should be done *bli neder*.

5) I cannot clarify how much Kehot still owes to the person who handled the printing of the *Shulchan Aruch Piskei Dinim*, etc. Since you, too, were deeply involved in the matter at the time, please be kind enough to inform me of the final total owed by Kehot, and also where the person to whom the funds should be transferred is located.

6) It concerns me that the work of... seems to lack initiative. Every time there is no clear instruction from New York, almost nothing is done. It is known and explained in many places, and in various *seforim*, that the purpose of learning is to become a person of action oneself, and not to remain in a state of *Netzach, Hod, Yesod* alone—even though, specifically, *Netzach, Hod, Yesod* are what sustain the entire body, including the head and the brain within the head.

I have received a letter indicating that he is joining the second category, and may it be G-d’s will that he succeed in all his affairs.

With blessings for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah*, and looking forward to hearing good news from you and your family, may they live and be well,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1821

1821

B"H, 6 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the congregants and the gabbaim at their head, of the Lubavitch Shul,
Toronto, Ont.

Greetings and Blessings!

A kosher mikveh is the foundation upon which the Jewish people stand in the matter of taharah, and it is the holiest merit to take part in it, each person according to his best abilities.

I was pleased to hear the good news that in your city you are in the midst of building a mikveh and the matter is already close to completion. Surely you will agree that a shul in general, and a shul of Anash Lubavitch in particular, must justify its name with a significant contribution to such a cause. I am certain that each of the gabbaim and members will participate according to their highest abilities—both by contributing themselves and by influencing friends and acquaintances to take part—and the Ribono shel Olam does not remain a debtor.

With the blessing of Kesivah V’chasimah Tovah to each one individually—awaiting good news.

## 1822

1822

B"H, 7 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the venerable Rabbi and Chassid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, etc.,
Rabbi Avraham Sander, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letters of the 15th and 16th of Menachem Av, and the one preceding them: please accept my apology for the delay in my response until now. During these days of mercy, forgiveness, and favor of the month of Elul in which we now find ourselves, I am certain you will forgive the aforementioned.

I will address your points one by one.

1) Regarding your observation that in *Likutei Torah*, in the discourses on the Red Heifer (*Parah Adumah*), it is implied that the casting of the scarlet wool (*tola'as shani*) hints that just as the worm’s power is only in its mouth, this serves as a rectification for the "defective mouth" of the heifer: Seemingly, however, it is proven and explicitly stated there that the scarlet wool rectifies not the mouth of the heifer, but the mouth of the "worm" of the opposing side (see there, page 57b, and elsewhere).

2) Nevertheless, your observation that the heifer’s mouth is "defective" is correct. This is based on what is stated in *Maseches Shabbos* (100b): "An animal whose mouth is bad—it is a heifer" (the fact that it is written there that a donkey also has a "bad mouth" does not cause harm to others, as is proven there). It is also worth noting *Bamidbar Rabbah*, beginning of *Parshas Balak*: "The ox’s power is in its mouth... what it grazes has no sign of blessing."

3) It is self-understood that this does not contradict at all what you wrote in your letter regarding the heifer’s mouth, based on what is observed in reality—that nails and the like are found inside them—as is known from the statement of Rashi in several places: "Like a hammer that shatters the rock."

4) Regarding what you wrote concerning the *Shelah*—that the matter of the "Cushite woman" whom Moshe took refers to the Babylonian Talmud, "He has made me dwell in darkness"—and your question as to why specifically the Babylonian Talmud and not the Jerusalem Talmud: It appears you are referring to the *Shelah* in his introduction to the section *Beis Chochmah* (16b) and in *Maseches Shevuos* (197b and onwards).

Based on what is understood there, the precision here is that it refers to the Oral Torah and not the Written Torah, which comes primarily to exclude (and not the Jerusalem Talmud). The essence of the Oral Torah is the Babylonian Talmud, in which the debates and pilpulim are more abundant. In it, the distinction between the Oral Torah and the Written Torah is emphasized more—that in the Oral Torah, many explanations are added, etc.—which is also more pronounced in the Babylonian Talmud than in the Jerusalem Talmud (this is explained at length, according to the teachings of Chassidus, in *Shaarei Orah* by the Mitteler Rebbe, in the discourse for the 25th of Kislev, and in the *Hemshech* of Rosh Hashanah 5666).

It should also be noted—and through this, the connection of Moshe specifically to the Babylonian Talmud becomes even more clarified—that according to the aforementioned distinction between the Babylonian and Jerusalem Talmuds, in the Babylonian, the questions, pilpul, and contradictions are more abundant, whereas in the Jerusalem Talmud, one arrives immediately at the point of the matter. This is based on the words of our Sages (*Nedarim* 38a) that the *pilpula* (sharp dialectic) of Torah was given specifically to Moshe Rabbeinu.

5) Regarding your writing that you found a new insight—the reason why Rabbeinu Gershom is specifically called *Meor HaGolah* (Light of the Exile): I have already seen this matter at the end of the book *Likutei Minhagim* (41b), in the *Hashmatos* (omissions) section, in the name of Rabbi Michelsohn of Plonsk (and later Warsaw), in the name of a great scholar.

6) You need not apologize for writing interpretations and explanations on matters of Torah, for this is our *avodah* and our request: to contribute our share to His Torah.

With the blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah* for you, your wife, and all your household, may they live.

***

**Rabbi Avraham Sander:** Nemtzov. Further letters to him: above, Vol. 5, 1557, and in the references noted there.

## 1823

B"H, 7 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the congregants and the Gabbaim of the Kehal Chassidim Synagogue
Manchester
May Hashem grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

A few days ago, I received a copy of your letter, and I was pleased to see that you properly appreciate the work and activities of the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, G-d-fearing and learned, etc., Rabbi Shmuel Rhein, shlita, shochet u-bodek, for your community. This demonstrates that you take an interest in his work and relate to it internally, and that you wish to maintain a closer connection with us, which is expressed in your desire to send him here as your representative.

I hope that, like every living thing, your positive sentiments will continue to grow and will permeate through the members of the shul into their homes and all their activities. This is the essence of our Torah and religion, which do not relate only to a portion of the day, leaving one unable to discern Yiddishkeit during the remaining time. Rather, it is a Torah of **life** from the Living G-d, which encompasses one’s entire life from the first moment until the last moment, after one hundred and twenty good years. It is not merely being a Jew in shul, while davening and learning, but also at home, in the street, in the office, etc., as we say twice every day: "When you sit in your house and when you walk on the way," etc.

Regarding your actual proposal that Rabbi Shmuel Rhein make a trip here, based on what he has written to me regarding his state of health, I calculate that the rigors of travel and the change in habits, food, drink, and general lifestyle, as well as the excitement (even if it is for a joyous reason), would be too much of a strain for him. Surely he has already shared with you my letter to him, which is in accordance with the above.

I wish to thank you for the good intention to send your representative, especially coming from a community that carries the name "Kehal Chassidim" with pride. A good thought is joined to the deed, and as the Alter Rebbe (Tanya, Chapter 16) notes regarding the Sages' expression "is joined to the deed"—that there must be a deed as well, even if it is far removed from the thought—I hope that there will be a deed on your part as well. That is to say, the positive results that this visit would have brought you will be realized in practice, even though the thought itself did not come to fruition.

I conclude with a wish for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* to all the members of your shul and their families, for each and every one with whatever they need in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessing.

## 1824

B.H., 7 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and accomplished, engaged in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Mordechai HaKohen, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

... 2) I was very pleased to hear that you are fixing the mikveh in your camp according to the instructions of the Rebbe (Rashab), of blessed memory. I have already written to express my thanks to the bochur, Mr. [Name], for his help in this matter. It is not worthwhile to prolong the process more than necessary; since they have agreed to proceed according to his instructions, one must take advantage of the positive momentum.

3) Regarding the additional stringencies you asked about: recently, it was brought to my attention that the tiles used to cover the walls and floor of the mikveh come in two types: a) those with a hollow backing (a cavity), and b) those without a hollow backing, even if they are very small. Although I have not seen anyone be particular about this until now, since they are made for construction, nevertheless, since it was pointed out to me that some say the cavity serves to hold the cement (which allows the tiles to adhere better), if it is easy to do so, it is worth obtaining the small tiles that do not have a hollow backing.

4) Regarding what you wrote in your letter, that you will not allow the old mikveh to be demolished until the new one is completed: seemingly, it would be worthwhile to make an effort so that the old mikveh also remains kosher and properly maintained. The benefit of this would be having two kosher mikvaos in the city. May the Ribono shel Olam grant us that through this "arousal from below" in increasing purity in the world, we will merit, very soon, the fulfillment of the prophecy, "And I will sprinkle pure water upon you," for "the Mikveh of Yisrael is Hashem."

5) Surely you have already received the regards from Mr. Tzipel, may he live, and I am interested to know how he delivered them. While he was here, I spoke with him regarding matters of chinuch and the building of the mikveh in your community. I also told him, in response to his question, that in my opinion, as long as there is hope to improve the state of Yiddishkeit in your camp without resorting to controversy and forming a separate community, one should distance oneself from that as much as possible.

6) I asked Mr. Tzipel to convey my regards to anash upon his return to your camp (and as is known from the Rebbe, my father-in-law, of blessed memory, anash refers to every Jew who observes Torah and mitzvos; and it is also known from our Sages' interpretation of the verse (Makkos 24a), "He who does these shall never falter"—that this applies even to one who observes a single thing). It would be appropriate to urge him to organize some sort of gathering or farbrengen to deliver my regards. Consequently, this could serve as a sort of introduction, during which they could draw others among those gathered into communal activity, especially regarding the mikveh, about which I spoke with him specifically, and he promised me that he would do what he can in this matter.

With the blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah* for you, your wife, and all your offspring, may they live.

## 1825

B"H, 7 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, involved in communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Yaakov, may he live, Shochet and Bodek

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Eikev, and thank G-d that you are well. Surely by now, you have received the personal regards from here, from Mr. Tzipel, may he live. It would be appropriate for you to ensure that he fulfills my request to organize a sort of gathering or farbrengen to convey the regards from me. Consequently, this can serve as a sort of introduction, during which you will be able to draw in (arientziehen) others among those gathered to communal activity, especially regarding the matters of chinuch and the mikveh. I spoke with the aforementioned individual specifically about these, and he promised me that he would do as much as he can in this regard. I am writing to the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, etc., Rabbi M. Hakohen Perlov, may he live, regarding this as well, and surely you will consult with one another on how to carry this out so that it will have the greatest benefit...

Regarding what you wrote that you were asked: Why is it that in the Siddur of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, in the "V'shamru" before the Maariv prayer of Shabbos Kodesh, the word "le'olam" is written with a vav, even though in the Chumash it is written without a vav? In the Siddur Shaar HaKollel, which is the most accurate, it is written "le'olam" without a vav, as it should be. In general, it has not yet been clarified whether these pesukim and the like were also written out in the Siddur of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe that was printed during his lifetime, or if he merely indicated that one should recite "V'shamru," etc...

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*, and awaiting good tidings.

#### ***1825***

**Rabbi Yaakov, may he live:** Ginsburg. Another letter to him—see above, 1720.

## 1826

B"H, 7 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the distinguished and G-d-fearing chossid, who toils in the needs of the community, etc.,
Rabbi Shlomo Zalman, may he live,

Greetings and blessings!

... Regarding your question as to whether it is possible to institute that the chazzan begin before the amud by reciting "Vayidaber, etc." for Mincha every day, and on Erev Shabbos by reciting "Hodu" and "Pischu Eliyahu," so that all those praying will recite this: This is certainly a proper thing to do, in order to guard against forgetfulness, etc., and such an innovation is a Torah obligation.

With blessings for proper health, success in communal and personal matters, and to be inscribed and sealed for a good year, for him and for his household, may they live.

**Rabbi Shlomo Zalman:** Hecht. Additional letters to him — see above, letter 1626, and the references in the footnotes there.

## 1827

B"H, 7 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished philanthropist, R' Chaim Yaakov, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I was pleased to have the opportunity to speak with you by telephone and to personally convey my wishes that Hashem grant you long life, good and pleasant years, and proper health—in connection with your undertaking the great mitzvah of helping to build a house for *chinuch hakasher* on the foundation of holiness, upon the holy land.

Now that your contribution has arrived and has been handed over to be transformed into the actualization of this objective, I take this opportunity to reiterate the blessing that it should also descend from potential into actuality.

For in general, all blessings exist within the Jewish people in potential; however, the ultimate purpose is for the blessings of Hashem to descend here below into actuality. This is also connected to the concept of the *yeridas haneshamah* below, from the highest heights to the deepest depths. This is true for the Jewish people in general, and it is true for each individual in particular.

Consequently, just as your *tzedakah* has now been put into actual practice to be realized in life, I wish you that the Divine blessings for this great mitzvah should also descend into actual reality—for long life, good and pleasant years, proper health, and all that is needed in both material and spiritual matters, for him, his wife, and their household, may they live.

In the hope of hearing good news from you always, all the days, and with the blessing of *Kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for him, his wife, and their household, may they live.

#### ***1827***

**R' Chaim Yaakov:** Holman. Another letter to him—above, Vol. 4, 1863.

## 1828

1828

B"H, 7 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed brothers, R' Moshe and R' Yosef, may they live,

Shalom u'Bracha!

Following our telephone conversation, I would like to express my satisfaction with the interest you have shown in the matter of undertaking to donate the second half of the sum required for the building in our Holy Land, for which your worthy father, may he live and be well, has already donated the first half.

I believe it is unnecessary to elaborate on the importance and necessity of this matter, which is certainly self-evident to you.

I would only like to emphasize two points:

Our Sages, of blessed memory, state that the merit of a mitzvah is attributed to those who complete it. This means that by your father, may he live and be well, having carried out the first half of the project and your completing it with the second half, you thereby take a share in your father's portion as well.

At the same time, this also strengthens the participation of your father, may he live and be well, in that the entire project will be in the name of the Holman family.

And since a building in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt speedily, that is connected to chinuch al taharas hakodesh is among those things that are eternal, both in gashmius and in ruchnius, I am certain that you will gladly contribute the second half, and thereby secure for the entire Holman family, may they live, the great and eternal zechus associated with this, especially in these days of the month of Elul, the month of mercy and favor.

I hope that you will gladden me with the good news regarding your positive decision.

With the blessing of Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah for you and your families, may they live.

#### ***1828***

**R' Moshe and R' Yosef:** Holman.

## 1829

B"H, 7 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter from Tuesday, Parshas Shoftim—about which I had become somewhat concerned, as a long time had passed without any word from you.

Regarding your announcement of the Bar Mitzvah of your son, may he live and be well, I hereby bless him that from the age of thirteen for mitzvos, he should grow to the age of fifteen for Gemara, and so on. May you and your wife, may you live and be well, derive from him much nachas—Yiddishe nachas and Chassidishe nachas. It is known from our Sages, "If one says, 'I have labored and found,' believe him; if one says, 'I have not labored and found,' do not believe him." Consequently, the privilege and the obligation rest upon you to do everything in your power to ensure that your son, may he live and be well, becomes a Chassid. The beginning of this is that he should go into exile to a place of Torah, to study in a yeshiva where they study Torah with yiras shamayim.

You conclude your letter by mentioning that you are also a shaliach tzibbur. It is surely unnecessary to remind you of the good custom of Yisrael—and even of the gedolei Yisrael who were shluchim tzibbur—to review and go over the prayers and piyutim before Rosh Hashanah and Yom Kippur, including the meaning of the words and the drashos of our Sages. Especially since you write that you belong to a distinguished lineage, as you mentioned in your letter regarding your marriage into the lineage of the Chozeh of Lublin, there must also be, in this regard, matters appropriate to the themes of hisorerus found in the teachings of Chassidus.

With blessings for a kesiva v’chasima tova.

## 1830

1830

B"H, 7 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to hear that you are the executor of the will of... and that you are making every possible effort to ensure that the inheritance designated for a yeshiva goes toward a building for Yeshivas Tomchei-Tmimim.

Beyond the fact that Yeshivas Tomchei-Tmimim is a unique institution where one studies both the revealed Torah and the inner dimensions of Torah—and is the only one of its kind in this regard—it also provides the opportunity to better fulfill what our Sages, of blessed memory, have said: it is a mitzvah **to fulfill** the words of the deceased. For since one cannot fulfill the will exactly as written, one must fulfill it in a manner as close and as appropriate as possible to the words of the deceased, a"h. As is well known, Yeshivas Tomchei-Tmimim was founded in **Russia**, later moved to **Poland**, and subsequently here.

Consequently, this is also consistent with the words of the deceased.

It is surely unnecessary to elaborate on the great merit of spreading Torah—both the revealed Torah and the inner dimensions of Torah. Since you have been appointed the executor of this will, it is a sign that you are **worthy** of having this merit and **capable** of bringing it to fruition. I would only like to emphasize two points:

First, in the mitzvah of Talmud Torah specifically, time is of the essence, because every day that passes cannot be filled by the following day, as the second day has its own obligation of Talmud Torah.

Second, even though you are merely the intermediary and the funds come from another, since the possibility of accelerating this good deed or delaying it lies in your hands, the extent of the action is yours, and the merit thereof is immeasurable. The sooner you bring this matter to a successful conclusion, the greater the merit.

I will be pleased to hear the good news that the matter of the will is being carried out as quickly as possible, even if there are other executors, for you have assistance from Above, as the Gemara says: "One who comes to purify himself is assisted."

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*, and awaiting good news.

## 1831

1831

B"H, 7 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter from 26 Menachem Av, along with the *pidyon nefesh* enclosed within it, which I will read at an auspicious time at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

I was pleased to read in your letter that you have increased the time you set aside for regular study in both *nigleh* and *Chassidus*. You would do well to also establish a time for studying *Chassidus* before *Shacharis*. Regarding what you write—that an obstacle to your spiritual state is your weak health—if you mean weakness in spirituality, that is true. But if you mean physical weakness, I do not agree that this is the case. I only wish that you would exert yourself in spiritual matters to the extent that it does not affect your physical health; that would be more than enough. As our Sages have said, the Holy One, blessed be He, only makes demands according to the strength of the Jewish people, and the Holy One, blessed be He, Himself rules in His holy Torah that the body must be healthy, for a healthy body is one of the ways of Hashem.

Regarding the *tikkun* you ask about: first and foremost, you should have memorized at least a few chapters of *Tehillim*, a few chapters of *Mishnayos*, and a few chapters of *Tanya*. When you are walking in the street, in a permitted and appropriate place, you should recite them by heart, or at the very least, contemplate them in your thoughts. In addition to this, until the upcoming 19 Kislev, you should give a few coins to *tzedakah* before *davening*, and in general, increase your engagement with the letters of Torah and *tefillah*.

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* and for finding suitable arrangements for your future, in both spiritual and material matters.

## 1833

1833

B”H, 7 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I received your letter with pleasure—though it lacked the date of writing—along with a copy of a letter from my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

It is known from the Zohar and the writings of the Arizal that thirty days before a passing, the process already begins. Consequently, on the day that letter was written, it was already within those thirty days—that is, at the beginning of his ascent to the higher worlds—which naturally adds to the preciousness and great value of the letter. I was pleased that you focused on the moral lesson that can be learned from this: the closeness of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, to all his students and those connected to him. It is known what is explained in Midrash Rabbah (Shemos 2:2) that this is how they tested Moshe Rabbeinu to see if he was worthy of being a shepherd and leader of Israel—by his special concern for the outcast.

I was distressed by what you wrote in your letter, that the opportunity has not yet arisen to travel to order a sheitel. It is surprising that you are delaying this matter so much, especially since you are aware of what is explained in many places in Chassidus—and which is also understood by human logic—that in every single moment one can acquire an entire world, or G-d forbid, the opposite. If so, every moment that passes without you acting on this matter means that you had the potential to build a world—that is, to draw down through this an addition of holiness in all the worlds, as is understood from Igeres HaTeshuvah by the Alter Rebbe, Chapter 12—and due to negligence, it was not done. However, one does not cry over the past; in any event, you must now hasten as much as possible in this, and this is also the reason I am sending this letter via special delivery.

Surely you are aware that there is a special fund at Machne Israel for gemach for such matters, and the repayment terms are favorable. If this was the delay until now, it is a pity that you did not disclose it, as the matter could have been arranged long ago. In any event, you should now hasten in this as is fitting. It is known from our Sages that alacrity leads to [the other stages of spiritual growth], and in the sequence of things, they conclude (Avodah Zarah 20b) that ultimately one attains Ruach HaKodesh.

With blessings for success in your influence in your new position, as well as your old one, to imbue them with a spirit of yiras shamayim, and with blessings for a kesivah v’chasimah tovah.

#### ***1833***

**Sheitel:** See also above, letter 152, and the references in the notes there.

## 1833

[7 Elul 5712]

...I was pleased by your interest in the state of the *shochet* affairs in your camp, although I was very distressed by the events and matters that are not as they should be, which you mention in your letter. It seems that your intention there is regarding the *Shulchan Aruch*.

Surely these days will provide an opportunity to speak with a few more of *anash* who are able to intervene in this, and I hope that eventually, it will be possible to rectify the situation, little by little. It goes without saying that I will not mention that the initial report came from you. May Hashem grant you success in your studies and in your holy work, without any obstacle, *chas v'shalom*. It is also well known how our Sages interpret the word *v'shachat* (and he shall slaughter) as *v'mashach* (and he shall draw out). Just as, on the literal level, the purpose of *shechita* is to prepare the meat of the animal or bird to be elevated from the level of *chai* (living) to the level of *medaber* (speaking—since it becomes the blood and flesh of a human), so too should this be performed in a spiritual sense: to draw down and elevate the *nefesh habehamis* to the level of *adam* (man), which is related to *adameh l'elyon* (I will be like the Most High). This is as written in the *Shelah*, page 20b, and in the *Sefer Asarah Maamaros*, *Maamar Em Kol Chai*, Part 2, Section 33.

#### 1833

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 12, p. 141.

## 1834

B"H, 7 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished scholar, etc., Moreinu Harav Menachem Mendel, may he live, a shochet and bodek.

Peace and blessing!

...I will take this opportunity—since, according to the teachings of the Baal Shem Tov, every matter, even the smallest detail, occurs through Divine Providence—that I have received your first letter, to awaken and encourage you. Relying on the words of our Sages (Sifra, beginning of Parshas Tzav), "One only encourages those who are already diligent," I wish to emphasize the absolute necessity for every single Jew to influence their surroundings to draw the hearts of Israel closer to our Father in Heaven in every possible way. Experience proves that the heart of a Jew is sensitive, and the matter depends only on the one who awakens it, as our Sages said, "Words that come from the heart enter the heart."

Especially as I see from your signature that you are a shochet and bodek, it is well known that our Sages said, "The term *v'shachat* (and he shall slaughter) implies *v'mashach* (and he shall draw)." Just as the slaughter, in its literal sense, renders the meat of an animal or bird fit for human consumption and transforms it into the blood and flesh of the human—meaning that the meat is elevated from the level of *chai* (living/animal) to the level of *medaber* (speaking/human)—so too is your role in the spiritual sense: to draw out the *nefesh habehamis* of the sons and daughters of Israel who are in your surroundings and to "render them fit" so that they may rise to the level of *adam* (human), which is related to the phrase "I will be like the Most High" (*adameh l'elyon*), as is written in the *Shelah*, page 20b, and in the *Sefer Asarah Maamaros*, *Maamar Em Kol Chai*, Part 2, Section 33.

With blessings for a *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah*.

***1834***

**Moreinu Harav Menachem Mendel:** Zuckerman.

## 1835

1835

B"H, 10 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter—undated—in which you describe everything you went through during the war years and the miracles that Hashem Yisbarach performed for you. I am even more pleased that you understand that these were open miracles and Hashgacha Pratis. I hope that the lesson to be learned from this will remain with you for your entire life, for long, good days and years, so that you will always remember and keep before your eyes that Hashem Yisbarach leads not only the great world in general, but also every detail of each of us in all the particulars of his life. Consequently, one must arrive at the decision and recognition that the only path leading to true happiness is the study of Torah and the fulfillment of mitzvos with yiras shamayim. May Hashem Yisbarach help you to be able to easily incorporate your resolutions into your daily life.

Regarding your question as to whether you should continue your studies... which you have already begun, or take on a farm in Kfar Chabad:

My opinion on this is that, since you write that you have already been studying... for several months, you should finish it and settle in Kfar Chabad. If you do not have enough work in that field in the village, then it is worthwhile for you to also have a farm, and your profession can serve as a supplement to that. In any case, you must continue to live among anash in the village, which will be for your success in both gashmius and ruchnius.

Surely you are participating in the shiurim that are taught publicly in the village, and you are also keeping the three daily shiurim that my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, instituted in Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, as is well known.

With the blessing of kesivah v'chasimah tovah for a good and sweet year.

## 1836

B"H, 10 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

...Regarding your complaint about the situation at the yeshiva in your camp: I have already written to you several times, and I have also told you this in person, that the matter of *marah shechorah* (melancholy) should be utilized for persistence in Torah study, but absolutely not in regard to communal work. It is distracting both to the person experiencing the *marah shechorah* and to those assisting him and working alongside him. Without a doubt, since my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, sent you... the power of the Sender is with you. Do not say that this is not such an easy place; surely you would also admit that in comparison to the powers of the Sender, one should not be discouraged. Especially since in your camp you see success through *hashgacha pratis* in many, many matters, and a yeshiva the likes of which does not exist in other places.

As for the many details that have not yet been rectified, there are two possible reasons for this: 1) Because the order of *kedusha* is "little by little I will drive them out." 2) Perhaps those working in the yeshiva and the administrators have not yet achieved *zichu*—meaning *zichuch* (refinement) and *birur* (clarification)—and consequently, the channels were obstructed for a **brief** moment. Through simple *teshuvah*—that is, keeping the *shiurim* in Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya, *tevilas Ezra*, and the like—the channels will naturally be straightened and opened, and success will come in its fullness...

Awaiting good news, and signing with a blessing for a *kesiva v'chasima tova*.
