## 1838

B"H, 12 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter of the 17th of Menachem Av, in which you write that you are preparing to publish a book...

You have enclosed the maamarim you delivered at the hesped for my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, and on the day marking the completion of the thirty days since his passing, and you request my haskamah.

Now, it is not my practice or custom to provide haskamos for books, especially seforim of drush.

I have said before that, on one hand, one does not debate matters of drush. In halacha, everyone must aim for the absolute truth of the psak din. This is not the case in drush. Yet, on the other hand, since in halacha only the practical psak din is at stake, it is not as critical whether one’s fear of Heaven preceded one’s wisdom, as is explained in various places. In the time of the galus, and especially in the ikvesa d'meshicha, it is possible for Torah study to occur not for its own sake, yet the halacha still aligns with the truth. (This is unlike the time of the Beis Hamikdash and the period shortly thereafter, when the proof that the halacha follows a particular opinion was specifically because **Havayah** was with him—He was, is, and will be as one—which is above nature, whereas the name Elokim is numerically equivalent to hateva [nature]. Therefore, in that respect, it is possible for both these and those to be the words of the living **Elokim**.) This is not the case in matters of drush, where, since the intended effect is to arouse fear of Havayah our G-d, the result of every drush must be consistent with that goal.

One may note the Shulchan Aruch of our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, Orach Chayim, section 429, at the end of the section: "And now... we expound upon the aggadah related to the day." See also there, section 529, Kuntres Acharon. It is also well known what the Sifri says: "If you wish to know the One who spoke and the world came into being, study aggadah."

Regarding what you write in the content of your maamarim about my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe: may your strength be bolstered for your precision and for your efforts among those who eulogized him. For the tzaddikim are like their Creator, and especially the Nesi’ei Hador—the extension of Moshe in every generation—of whom it is said, "I stand between Havayah and you." Just as the Holy One, blessed be He, is the ultimate of knowledge—that we cannot truly know Him—and yet, at the same time, the Name of Heaven is familiar to all (and this is explained in Torah Or, Parshas Vayeira 14b, which states: "Therefore, even infants know that there is a G-d who is present," etc.—see there, that this is specifically through the Maor [the Luminary]), a similar concept applies to the tzaddikim and Nesi’ei Hador: it is impossible to reach their ultimate depth, yet at the same time, "even infants know," etc.

As you requested, when I was at the tziyun of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, I mentioned you and your family, may they live, for whatever they need, as written in your letter. May the Almighty grant each and every one of us the merit to hear only good news, always, all the days.

With the blessing of Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah.

Enclosed are your four maamarim.
Enclosed is the sicha from Shabbos Mevarchim.

## 1839

1839

B"H, 13 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to your letter from the beginning of the month of Elul, some of your questions have already been addressed in my previous letter, which I trust was received in due time, and I await confirmation of its receipt. The questions contained therein will be answered as well.

2) Regarding what you wrote concerning your registration in Lod: Since you add in your letter that the school of the Agudas Yisrael stream, which had 138 students, has only just closed, you must be extremely careful not to give the impression that you are the ones responsible for this, even if there is no basis for such a claim—and certainly if there is any basis for this concern. As for what was suggested to you—that you manage the studies without publicity—I do not understand how the Talmud Torah there will be sustained. If they provide you with the necessary resources, at least unofficially, even then, since it is unofficial, who knows if they will follow through on their word? It is obvious that once you begin, you will be obligated to continue, and there is no room for excuses that "so-and-so is a man of his word." Since this Talmud Torah requires very significant resources, you must calculate whether, with such resources, it is possible to achieve greater things elsewhere.

3) In accordance with the above, and regarding my approach in all my letters to the Reshet administration—to avoid controversy and the interpretation of ulterior motives—my stance regarding the yeshiva in Meron is also understood. Beyond the fact that a yeshiva in general does not belong to the Reshet—and perhaps their intention was not for it to be under the Reshet, but rather among Chabad institutions in general—since until now it belonged, according to your letter, to Mizrachi, even if they now say they will hand it over willingly, one cannot know what a day may bring. It is highly probable that if they see the matter succeeding, they will come with demands, claims, and grievances, etc. We have already seen such cases where, initially, they said they would not object, but later, when it was close to fruition or even after the matter was finalized, they raised a clamor and complained. It goes without saying that if it is possible to encourage the directors of the yeshiva to strive for its development, the matter of the Talmud Torah is of the utmost importance, but do not take the yeshiva upon your shoulders. This is especially true since it seems they are using you for publicity, claiming that you are going to "conquer" the entire country and its education system. As our Sages of blessed memory said, "The barrel was clear..." [implying the danger of arrogance].

4) If, as mentioned above, your question was not on behalf of the Reshet or one of our yeshivos, please convey my opinion on this to the people involved.

5) Regarding your question as to whether the Talmud Torah of Kfar Chabad should be part of the Reshet: I do not understand why changes should be made. Since until now it has been together with the yeshiva of the Kfar, and this is also how it appears on their letterheads—meaning it has already been publicized that it is a yeshiva and Talmud Torah together—one should not remove it from its established status. The same applies to the Talmud Torah of Lod, which until now served, as I recall, as a sort of preparatory school for the Lod yeshiva.

6) I was very pleased that this time everyone signed the letter. I wish to interpret this as proof and a sign that peace dwells among you. Surely, the teaching of our Sages of blessed memory will be fulfilled, that this is the "vessel that holds blessing"—the blessing of the Ribono shel Olam, which is connected with success that transcends the natural order.

With the blessing of success in your holy work and a *Kesiva V'chasima Tova*.

## 1840

1840

B”H, 13 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn

To the Administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Lod,
May they live,

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letters dated 13 and 22 Menachem Av. Regarding the information I just received from Paris, they spoke there with Dr. Shapira, who said that he has already spoken with Mr. Pasman regarding the vocational school, and he will raise the matter once again (apparently Mr. Pasman was abroad, and he spoke with him there). It appears that the Joint will handle the vocational school for them and for... and if the matter is arranged properly on their end, there is hope that they will have priority. It seems the Joint does not have a budget large enough to provide all the necessary means for a vocational school, so they will provide it little by little; naturally, whoever they favor will surely be the first to receive it. I await good news.

2) Regarding what I wrote about maintaining the image of your Yeshiva—to ensure it is known as a Yeshiva and not a Talmud Torah—what prompted this concern is: a) It appears from the lists added recently that the age of the students is very young. b) What I heard, that there is an idea to bring the Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Talmud Torah under your administration. Therefore, I expressed my opinion on this: that even in normal years, and especially when one is being watched with seven eyes, one must be careful not to give anyone cause to say that the Talmud Torah is the main focus and the study of Gemara is minimal in quantity, which consequently serves as evidence regarding the quality as well—and a word to the wise is sufficient. You are surely correct in your argument that it is easier to influence various types of children if you begin to educate them with the desired education at a young age, but there has always been a distinction between what is ideal and what is possible, and therefore, in this situation as well, one must take that into account. It goes without saying that I do not mean that you should, G-d forbid, dismiss the students who have already been accepted, nor is it my opinion that you should not accept young students at all, but rather only older ones. My intention is only this: that the increase in quality, and even the increase in quantity, should be among students who testify that this is a Yeshiva. The details of this depend on the local conditions, and therefore you must decide this each time. May Hashem grant you success so that you may aim for the true intention, and may there be success in this beyond the natural order.

3) On this occasion, I wish to emphasize once again the great importance of your work with the children from Yemen; the benefits of this are beyond measure.

4) During these days, the activist Mr. Yitzchak Elmalich from Casablanca, along with Rabbi Toledano from Meknes and others, will surely be traveling to Eretz Yisrael (may it be rebuilt and established)—with the intention of returning. The aforementioned are very G-d-fearing and are working for the benefit of the Oholei Yosef Yitzchok institutions in Morocco... You should certainly show them your institution. It is worthwhile to honor them, as our Sages have said, "It is a mitzvah to publicize those who perform a mitzvah." You should surely consult with Agudas Chabad regarding this, so that the matter is arranged in a way that will bring the greatest benefit.

5) You surely already have an update regarding the construction of the shack on the roof. I was pleased to see in your letter that a beginning of expansion—*breitkeit*—is felt. In addition to the above, you requested a loan for building materials as well; when you expand the vessel below, you will certainly be influenced accordingly from Above.

6) When you have news, please inform me, and thank you in advance.

With blessings for success in your holy work and with a *Kesivah V’chasimah Tovah*.

P.S. Enclosed is a segment from the *Maamar* of the Rebbe Rashab for *Shabbos Mevarchim* Elul; you should certainly publicize it among the students in an appropriate manner.

## 1841

B"H, 13 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the Administration of the Yeshiva in Kfar Chabad,
in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established,
May Hashem preserve them and may they live.

Peace and Blessing!

I received your letter with pleasure, in which you inform me that on the bright day of 18 Elul—the birthday of our holy master, the Baal Shem Tov, founder of the general teachings of Chassidus, and the birthday of our holy master, the Alter Rebbe, founder of the Chabad teachings of Chassidus—you are preparing to hold the dedication ceremony for the Yeshiva building in Kfar Chabad. My joy was even greater upon reading the conclusion of your letter, that in recent times Hashem has increased your borders with students. Surely, this increase in quantity will also lead to an increase in quality, as is known from our Sages: "A thousand enter for Mikra, a hundred emerge for Mishnah, from a hundred for Mishnah ten emerge for Talmud, and from ten for Talmud one emerges for Hora'ah."

Especially in your Yeshiva, which is founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory—where the revealed Torah and the hidden Torah, which is the Torah of Chassidus, are united as two lights—this is also the unification of the thousand who enter for Mikra. Mikra in Asiyah, meaning that it descends even into Asiyah, just as in the simple interpretation, Mikra refers to simple matters; and the one who emerges for Hora'ah is the ultimate perfection, to arrive at the truth **in its absolute sense**. Regarding this it is said that "Hashem is with him," that the Halacha follows his opinion in every place. Hashem—He was, He is, and He will be as one—is above nature and its limitations, yet He is drawn down specifically into nature. Halacha in physical matters means the unification of Asiyah in Torah with Atzilus in Torah, Mikra and Kabbalah. As is understood from all this in Likutei Torah, in the beginning of the three parshiyos, page 3a.

May it be the will of Hashem to bestow success upon the Yeshiva, its students, and its administration, that their minds and hearts be refined a thousand times over to understand and grasp the revealed Torah and Chassidus, and to serve as a beacon to spread the light of Torah and the "light within the Torah" to the entire surrounding area.

With the blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year to the administration of the Yeshiva, its students, and all those participating in the gathering, they and all their households, may they live. And through the spreading of the wellsprings outward, may we all merit together the complete Redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days.

With blessing.

## 1842

1842

B”H, 13 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from Erev Shabbos Parshas Teitzei, in which you write... that you cannot endure the great suffering that you have undergone, etc., etc.

These words of yours are truly surprising. Have you forgotten, in such a short time, the state you were in a year ago and thereafter—both regarding your circumstances, etc., and regarding your health, etc., etc.? Even though, regarding the Ribono shel Olam, everything is possible—for He has the power to grant many times over, and every Yid has reason to hope for this, since all Yidden are children of kings—elaboration on this is surely unnecessary. As is known, the *kal v’chomer* cited in Chassidus: if Nevuchadnetzar was granted a kingdom for three generations because of three steps, then how much more so [for a Yid]—*az a Yid ken men zich nit ois-tzaalen* [for a Yid, one cannot calculate the reward]. But together with this, one must not, chas v’shalom, forget the miracles and wonders that are performed for each and every one of us, and you are included in this as well. Elaboration on this is surely unnecessary.

You will surely spend the appropriate amount of time in Eretz Yisrael, tichyeh v'tizkeh, and contemplate the possibility of relocating there for yourself and for your family, shichyu. May it be the will of Hashem that He guide you on a path of success, for you and for your family, shichyu, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings for a *Kesivah V’chasimah Tovah*,

**M. Schneerson**

## 1843

B"H, 13 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter from 3 Elul, I was pleased to read that you have recognized several positive qualities in his personality that align with what you are looking for in a young man to marry, and that you also hope there may be other qualities in him that have not yet been revealed to you.

It is correct, as you write, that in a matter such as this, there must also be a certain positive feeling, and not merely a calculation based on intellect. It is also understood that since one is building an entire home—a *binyan adei ad*—the home must be unified in all matters, not only in matters of intellect. On the other hand, however, it is not always easy to clarify where the deliberation stemming from intellect ends and the deliberation stemming from emotion begins. For many times, even when it seems that it is only a matter of intellect, there is in truth a large part—and perhaps even the decisive part—of emotion involved. My hope is that after you meet with him a few more times, you will be able to clarify this for yourself: that it is not only intellect involved in the matter, but emotion as well.

In accordance with the above, if it is clear that for the time being there is no feeling at all in the matter, then it would seem that a decision is still premature. But if emotion is also participating in this, then may it be the will of Hashem that it should be with success, and at a good and auspicious time.

Surely you will also take into account that after a relatively short period of time, the aforementioned will be traveling to his parents—may they live and be well—and therefore, it is not worthwhile to continue the matter if there is no necessity for it.

In any event, I am sure you will reply to this letter of mine. May it be the will of Hashem that He guide you on the path leading to your success and happiness, both materially and spiritually.

## 1844

B"H, 13 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, G-d-fearing and distinguished, etc.,
Rabbi Ephraim Eliezer, may he live, HaKohen

Peace and blessing!

Enclosed, as you requested some time ago, is the Kuntres for 18 Elul, as well as the excerpt from the sicha regarding "Shabbos Mevarchim: The month of Elul is the month of mercy," which I am sure will be of interest to you, and also regarding practical application.

I hereby also acknowledge receipt of your two letters. Regarding your observation that the heart (*lev*) is sometimes referred to in the masculine and sometimes in the feminine, it is a known rule that "for anything that lacks a spirit of life, you may refer to it as masculine or feminine" (Responsa of Dunash on Rav Saadia Gaon, section 150). Time does not permit an elaboration on this, and there will be another opportunity for this in the future.

I was pleased to receive the regards from you via the travelers, and I was happy to hear their account of your participation in bringing the matter to fruition. Relying on the statement of our Sages that "a mitzvah is attributed to the one who completes it" (Tanchuma, Eikev, cited in Rashi), I am confident that you will endeavor to bring the matter to actual completion—meaning, that the check be written and signed—and the sooner, the better, especially in this month of mercy. See Iggeres HaKodesh, section 21: "And the alacrity of Avraham Avinu, peace be upon him, is what stands forever," etc. The connection to the Kohanim, in particular, is understood from what is written in Likkutei Torah at the end of Parshas Korach.

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for you and, through you, to the donor, may he live. I await good news.

***

**1844**

**Rabbi Ephraim Eliezer, may he live:** Yalles. Additional letters to him appear above in 1529, and in the notes referenced there.

## 1845

1845

B"H, 14 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter of 5 Elul, in which you write that you have already been discharged from the hospital and are back at home, and that your health has improved significantly. May Hashem help that it should continue to improve further, and may you be able to report good news in ruchnius as well.

Regarding what you write—that you have taken it upon yourself to enter the camp of Chabad, both internally and externally, and to accept the p'sak din of the Tzemach Tzedek regarding the *tzelem Elokim* and not to remove the *yud-gimmel tikunei dikna*—which, as is explained in Zohar, Kabbalah, and Chassidus, are the spiritual channels through which Hashem draws down additional blessing in all that one requires—I say to you *yashar kocho v’cheilo* for this decision. *Habah letaher mesay'in oso* (one who comes to purify himself is assisted), and you will certainly have *siya d'shmaya* (assistance from Above) not to be affected by those who mock. This is the foundation and beginning of all four sections of the Shulchan Aruch; in the very first section, Shulchan Aruch Orach Chaim, in the very first siman and seif, it states: "And do not be ashamed before those who mock." May Hashem help you that your situation of *parnassah* should improve very soon. And may Hashem fulfill the days of your wife’s pregnancy, *tichyeh*, properly and easily, and may she give birth to a healthy child with ease.

With blessings for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah*.

P.S. Enclosed is a script for your personal needs.

## 1846

1846

B"H, 14 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

Your *pidyon nefesh* on behalf of [name] has been received. When I am at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, I will mention him for a speedy recovery. May Hashem grant that he be able to bring me good news regarding the improvement of his health. You should encourage him to keep a checked *mezuzah* near his bed that is *kosher*—naturally, it should be in a double covering since he is in the hospital. He should also have the *mezuzos* in his home checked, as well as his *tefillin* and the *tzitzis* of his *tallis gadol* and *tallis katan*. He should also take upon himself—without a vow—to observe the three daily *shiurim* established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, for every person, which are *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*, as is known. If speaking is difficult for him at this time, then, if the doctors agree, he may recite them in his thoughts. I will await good news from you. Surely the wife of the aforementioned [name] sets aside *tzedakah* every *Erev Shabbos* and *Erev Yom Tov* before lighting the candles, for the *kupah* of Rabbi Meir Baal HaNes.

Enclosed is the *kuntres* for 18 Elul and a segment of the *sicha* from *Shabbos Mevarchim* the month of Elul, the month of mercy. I am certain you will publicize them in an appropriate manner so that they reach the widest possible circles.

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*.

#### ***1846***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 19, p. 443.

## 1847

B"H, 14 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Mushka, may she live, wife of the late R' Gershon, of blessed memory, Wolfsohn

Blessings and peace!

Your letter and the check that your husband, of blessed memory, left for tzedakah in accordance with my decision, have been received. The check has been turned over to support our **"Oholei Yosef Yitzchak Lubavitch"** institutions, and a receipt is enclosed.

These institutions, which bear the name of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, perform vital work in various parts of the world: in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt, in Europe, North Africa, Australia, and so on. They provide Jewish children, both boys and girls, with a Torah-true education, and often with material assistance as well, wherever it is needed. The merit of taking part in this work is beyond measure.

As you are aware of the good work your husband, of blessed memory, did for the Lubavitcher institutions, I am certain that you will use your influence on your children, may they live, to maintain the family tradition. Through this, you will keep open the channels through which the Ribono shel Olam sends blessing and success, long life, and nachas—Jewish nachas—from the children, may they live.

With the blessing of Kesiva V’chasima Tova.

## 1848

1848

B"H, 18 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To our brothers and sisters, the sons and daughters of Israel,
Wherever they may be,
May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and blessing!

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I send to all our brothers and sisters, the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be, may Hashem grant them life, a blessing for the year: that you be inscribed and sealed for a good and sweet year.

At the end of the Sabbatical year, this year, we are reminded of this mitzvah—a strong pillar and great honor in our religion—the mitzvah of **Hakhel**, when all the people, men, women, **and children**, would gather in the holy place, may it be rebuilt speedily in our days, to hear the section regarding the acceptance of the Kingdom of Heaven, the acceptance of the yoke of mitzvos, the acceptance of the covenants of Torah, and the proclamation to the masses of "You shall surely tithe."

And even though we are commanded at all times and at every hour to educate our sons and daughters to keep the way of Hashem, at the end of the Sabbatical year we are commanded in this with greater intensity and added inspiration. As it is said: "And their children, who have not known, may hear and learn to fear Hashem."

And I am certain that during the Days of Awe and the days of the festival of Sukkos—the days of Hakhel, which are coming upon us for good—every rabbi, every leader, every person involved in communal needs, and everyone whose words are heeded—

And words that come from the heart—a heart that is sensitive, which exists in **every single man and woman of Israel**—enter the hearts of the listeners—

Will arouse the members of their community and their surroundings toward Torah and fear of Heaven with greater intensity and greater strength, and especially to support, strengthen, and expand the kosher educational institutions—education of Talmud Torah with fear of Heaven—**and to gather and bring** the sons and daughters to be educated in them, to be "a shoot of My planting, the work of My hands, in which I glory."

And it is my hope that this inspiration and influence will continue and be effective throughout the entire year.

And because of this, may the Almighty grant us the complete Redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, to perform and fulfill the mitzvah of Hakhel in the dwelling of our glory, speedily in our days, amen, may it be His will.

Blessing and being blessed with a good inscription and sealing for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters,

**Menachem Mendel son of Chana**
**Schneerson**

## 1849

1849

B"H, 18 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To our brothers and sisters, the sons and daughters of Israel,
wherever they may be,
May Hashem grant them life.

Peace and Blessing!

On the threshold of the new year, the year 5713, which is approaching for us and for all of Israel for good, I send my blessing for a good and sweet year to all our brothers and sisters, the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be, may Hashem grant them life.

The year 5712, the year of Shemitah, is passing, and these days remind us of the great mitzvah, which is "a firm pillar and a great honor for our religion," the mitzvah of **Hakhel**, when the entire nation — men, women, and **children** — would gather during Chol Hamoed Sukkos in the holy place, the Beis Hamikdash, may it be rebuilt speedily in our days by Moshiach Tzidkeinu, to hear select portions of the Torah, portions that speak of the acceptance of the yoke of Heaven, the acceptance of the yoke of mitzvos, and in particular the mitzvah of tzedakah (*Aser Te'aser*).

And although Jews are always, in all times, commanded to educate Jewish children in the path of Torah and mitzvos, the mitzvah of Hakhel awakens us and reminds us of this with particular intensity.

In these days, at the end of the past year and the beginning of the coming year, every father and mother in Israel, every Rav and leader, every activist and person of influence, should make the serious resolution in the spirit of the mitzvah of Hakhel — not only for the coming days of the Yomim Noraim and Sukkos, the days of Hakhel, but for the entire year — to gather and bring Jewish children in large numbers into the yeshivos, Talmud Torahs, and educational institutions of pure holiness; and through tzedakah with an open hand, to strengthen and secure the existence of kosher educational institutions for Jewish children, boys and girls, everywhere,

To raise them in the spirit of yiras shamayim, ahavas Hashem, ahavas haTorah v'hamitzvos, and ahavas Yisrael.

In the merit of this, may Hashem Yisbarach grant us the merit that we may very soon be able to fulfill the mitzvah of Hakhel in the Beis Hamikdash in Jerusalem, rebuilt by Moshiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days.

Blessing you and being blessed with a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year in both material and spiritual matters,

**Menachem Mendel ben Chana**
**Schneerson**

#### ***1849***

Printed in Likutei Sichos, Vol. 9, p. 408.

## 1850

1850

By the grace of Hashem, 19 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the administration of Agudas Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily,
To the administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily,
May Hashem keep them alive.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your reports from the 19th and 20th of Menachem Av, your letters from the 26th and 29th of Menachem Av, and the attachments thereto. Furthermore, a letter has now been received from the administration of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim in Tel Aviv. It is very strange that there is no word regarding the results of receiving the shipment of goods sent from here. I do not know how to respond here, and this is also a matter of concern for the future.

2) I will begin with what is most pressing at this time: since we have entered the month of Elul, and surely the time has come for the necessary preparations for the month of Tishrei, you should certainly proceed to draft a detailed plan of action, divide the tasks, and organize the work among everyone in a way that there will be assistance and completion from one to the other. In general, as has been the custom in many places in recent years, you should organize two types of activities: one type, in many locations, **and also** the second type, in one central location with a large gathering. Surely, with the participation of representatives of all the professions and institutions, you will arrange the matter in the most effective way.

3) It goes without saying that this does not in any way negate working in other places as well, beyond those locations where there is already a large number of people—may they increase.

4) I believe I have already written in response to someone’s question that if there is a way to broadcast on the radio, it is the right thing to do. It is simple that, to begin with, the text of the broadcast must be reviewed by a committee of people suitable for this.

5) Regarding the dissemination of Chassidus: in my opinion, it is not the role of Agudas Chabad and Tzeirei Agudas Chabad to station people **sent from their center** in all locations in order to receive a salary and to stir up the local people—**permanently**. Rather, the main thing is the effort to find in every single place a person (or committee) who will take upon themselves the management of the work pertaining to that place, as well as the study of Chassidus in public, etc. Only in an entirely exceptional case should people be hired to travel from one place to another, *ratzo v'shov*, and act there in accordance with the Agudas Chabad plan of action (unless there are insufficient means to organize the first type of work, which makes it necessary to adopt the second type of work; however, even then, **the good of the matter** requires that the one acting on the spot be one of the local residents, and only occasionally, whether rarely or frequently, should a guest or someone to stir things up come from another place).

6) In response to the question of whether to print, in a newspaper or bulletin or the like, any *reshimos* and letters from the Rebbe, my father-in-law, that have not been printed until now: this will introduce confusion and also a lack of precision in the publication of the *maamarim* and *sichos*, etc., of the Rebbe, my father-in-law. Therefore, **according to his instruction**, this is to be concentrated here, since here it is possible to check the transcripts more precisely and compare them to what is found in other places, etc. Therefore, one should only think about such matters that have already been printed, and even regarding those, one should ask beforehand, since even in those that are printed, there are matters that were subject to a later revision, even though the first version did not move from its place.

7) If the renovation of the *mikveh* in Haifa is approximately 100-200 Lira at their expense, perhaps it is worth doing, although in general it is a matter of wonder that in a city like Haifa they are in need of your help?!...

With the blessing of *Ksivah V'chasimah Tovah*,

#### ***1850***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 23, p. 2, and completed according to the secretariat's copy.

**Whether to print:** See above, letter 1744.

## 1851

B"H, 22 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the participants of the farbrengen on the auspicious day of Chai Elul,
The birthday of the Baal Shem Tov and the Alter Rebbe,
In the city of Toronto,

I was pleased to receive your notification regarding your farbrengen on the past auspicious day of Chai Elul. It is my firm hope that this past day will infuse vitality into the present and the future, in accordance with the saying of the early Chassidim, cited in the sicha of the Rebbe Rayatz—Chai Elul 5705—"Chai Elul is the day that brought and brings life into Elul." The concept of Elul has already been explained, albeit briefly, in the introduction to the Kuntres Chai Elul 5711—Kuntres 94. May Hashem inscribe and seal each and every one of the participants, together with their entire households, for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

Blessing you with all that is good.

## 1852

1852

B"H, 22 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

To my dear friend, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and learned, engaged in communal needs, etc.,
R' Azriel Zelig, may he live.

Peace and Blessing!

... 4) Enclosed is the *kuntres* for Chai Elul, as well as a section from the *maamar* for the 18th of Elul. Surely you will publicize them in an appropriate manner.

5) Regarding your long-standing question concerning the custom of *kohanim* to visit the graves of *tzaddikim*, and your request for my opinion on the matter:

One should examine the *Sdei Chemed*, Part *Asifas Dinim*, *Ma'areches Eretz Yisrael*, entry *Aveilus*, *Rosh Hashanah*, as well as *Pe'as HaSadeh* there. He cites many *Acharonim*, and most of them, if not all, are stringent in this regard. This is also the implication of the ruling of the Chabad community, as is evident from the *teshuvah* of the Maharil of Yanovitch (brother of the Alter Rebbe) printed in one of the issues of *HaTamim* (Issue 6, p. 38) regarding the partition they erected in Haditch around the grave. It is also noted in the books cited by the *Sdei Chemed* that, nevertheless, many are lenient in this, especially *Chassidim* regarding their *Nesi'im*. Even so, I am not comfortable with this, due to the aforementioned *teshuvah* of the Maharil. Furthermore, I was told that in Lubavitch, at the *Ohel*, there were markers serving as a partition, indicating that *kohanim* may approach up to that point and no further.

6) Regarding the *Ohel* of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe: It has been arranged that around the grave there is a partition ten *tefachim* high, and the *kohanim* stand at a distance of four *tefachim* from the grave—and the partition as well. Furthermore, since the *Ohel* is located within a cemetery, the *kohanim* arrive there in a closed vehicle, which has the status of an *ohel*. And an *ohel* that is "thrown" (moved) in such a case is considered an *ohel*, since the requirement of distancing four *amos* from a cemetery is only a Rabbinic decree according to all opinions.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and your family, may they live, with the blessing of *Kesivah V'Chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for success.

***1852***

Printed in *Likkutei Sichos*, Vol. 21, p. 316, and completed based on the secretariat's copy.

**R' Azriel Zelig:** Slonim. Additional letters to him appear above, Vol. 4, 807, and in the references noted there.

## 1853

1853

B"H, 22 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and refined, involved in communal needs, etc.,
R' Alexander Sender, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I received with pleasure your letter of 3 Tavo, in which you write that you are continuing your work of "collecting physicality" for the Yeshiva—whereby, as a result, the physicality becomes spirituality—and "sowing spirituality," and that you also strive, while at home, to influence your surroundings, etc.

Regarding what you conclude in your letter—that often the thought occurs to you, and you say to yourself, "Who am I to preach morality?"—it is a well-known principle from our Sages that "were it not for Hashem’s help, one could not overcome [his evil inclination]." Consequently, it is not you who is preaching, nor is it you who is offering moral instruction; rather, it is the delivery of words of truth, taken from the Torah of truth.

In particular, a Chossid who stands in hiskashrus to our Nasi, my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, is merely fulfilling a shlichus. As such, the power of the Sender is with him. My revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, has sufficiently broad shoulders to carry out his mission in every place and at every time, through every person—provided that the shaliach remains in connection with the Sender.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and to your family, may they live, with the blessing of *Kesivah v’Chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both physicality and spirituality.

With blessing.

#### 1853

**R' Alexander Sender:** Menkin.

## 1854

B"H, 22 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
Mr. Kahanov, may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to learn from the administration of the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established, regarding your favorable attitude toward them and the assistance you provided them when needed.

The great value of this matter surely requires no elaboration. It is well known that there is a difference between influencing adults and influencing children: a slight deviation from the correct path when influencing adults is, in the ordinary course of things, but a small matter. Not so in the education of the younger generation; even a small change is liable to cause great damage when they grow up. Man is like the tree of the field, and we see that a small change in the seed affects the essential growth of the tree, both in its quality and its quantity.

And if at all times special attention to the education of the younger generation was necessary, how much more so in these days, after the terrible destructions, may Hashem spare us, in which a significant portion of the Jewish people was destroyed, both in quantity and in quality. Consequently, the importance of each and every son and daughter of Israel is many times greater, and likewise, the merit of everyone who participates in improving the state of education is greater—especially education that connects the younger generation with the tradition of our ancestors and our past, which exists eternally in the present and in the future. These are the foundation of the existence of the Jewish people throughout the duration of our exile, until the coming of Mashiach Tzidkeinu, speedily in our days.

I extend double thanks for your assistance in the past, and I request that you continue to provide your help to the administration of the Reshet Oholei Yosef Yitzchok Lubavitch in their time of need; surely you will do everything within your ability and means in this regard.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and your family, may they live, with the blessing of *Kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

With respect and blessing.

## 1855

1855

B"H, 22 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I have received your letter of [date], in which you describe your biography and the difficulties you have faced since the passing of your husband, a"h. You conclude your letter by noting that, thank Hashem, your son-in-law, daughter, and family conduct themselves in a good way. May Hashem Yisbarach help you to derive from them true Yiddishe nachas.

The custom is that in a prayer or request to Hashem Yisbarach, one mentions the name in Lashon HaKodesh along with the mother's name. I would suggest that you send me the names of all your family members as they are called in Lashon HaKodesh, along with the mother's name for each of them. I will then mention them during a time of favor at the Tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, ztzuklalleh"h, nbg"m, zy"a.

Since you write that you operate a kosher guest house, it is very important that you have various seforim available so that the guests can learn about Torah and yiras shamayim. It goes without saying that these seforim should be in a language suitable for the type of guests who visit your guest house.

It is also important to have the mezuzos in your home checked to ensure they are all kosher. It is surely unnecessary to remind you of the good custom of kosher Yiddishe daughters to give tzedakah before lighting candles every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov, and it is certain that your daughter does this as well.

With wishes to you and your entire family for a kesivah v'chasimah tovah for a good and sweet year,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,

**The Secretary**

## 1859

B"H, 22 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 17 Elul, in which you write regarding the various offers you have concerning a position, including an offer from the Tomchei Temimim Yeshiva in Paris.

Since you have such an offer, I do not understand why you need to search in other vineyards, at a time when Hashem has provided you with an opportunity to be a guardian of my vineyard. It is well known that in such matters, more than one does for the institutions of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the institution does for those who work for its benefit—both in spiritual and material matters—by involving them in its work. Especially since the environment there is also as it should be, you will naturally be able to ascend in Torah and avodah, in accordance with the words of our Sages, "We ascend in matters of holiness."

As we approach the new year, which is coming upon us and all of Yisrael for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings.

## 1,857

B"H, 22 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I have been informed by his brother, the distinguished avreich, our friend... [may he live and be well], that he has been in the army for nearly a year. Surely, he remembers the rock from which he was hewn wherever he may be. It is my hope that he sometimes reflects on the possibility that he has a specific shlichus to bring to the environment where he has been sent and is now located. While there is no one among us who can say with absolute certainty that a specific matter is one’s designated shlichus, it is very often the case that there are details which, in all likelihood, fall within a person’s specific mission. Furthermore, since he is a scion of a family such as his—a tradition passed down from generation to generation of those who sacrificed themselves for Torah and mitzvos—it is highly probable that it is also his duty, in the environment where he is now, to explain to them the truth and light of Torah and the traditions of Israel. Surely, with the appropriate effort, he will find the right words to convey this, and may Hashem grant him success.

As we approach the New Year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby extend to him my blessing: a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings,

1858

1858

B"H, 22 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 14 Elul, in which you inform me of your birthday on Friday, 6 Tishrei, and ask for the appropriate conduct for this day:

You should certainly receive an aliyah to the Torah. During the day, you should seclude yourself for some time, as explained in *Hayom Yom* for 11 Nissan. During this time of *hisbodedus*, you should contemplate the year that has passed and awaken yourself to good resolutions for the coming year. Furthermore, you should give *tzedakah* before *davening* Shacharis and Mincha. If possible, you should endeavor to review a *maamar* of *Chassidus* before a group, whether large or small. Naturally, all of the above should be done without any ostentation.

Since you mention in your letter that you have made errors in your review of the chapters of *Tanya*—which, as explained in the letter of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (in *Kitzurim L'Tanya*), is the Written Torah of the teachings of *Chassidus*—you must strive to correct these errors. You should begin this immediately upon receiving this letter, in such a way that by your birthday, you will have corrected a significant portion of them.

You conclude your letter by stating that, for various reasons, you have begun *davening* on Shabbos close to 2:00 PM. This report does not please me at all. One should not establish such practices as a fixed custom. There is an obvious difference between starting early and finishing late, versus starting at 2:00 PM by design. You should consult with the elders of *anash* in your location, and they will provide you with guidance on how to rectify this so that you are not forced to shorten the necessary preparation for the *avodah* of *tefillah*, nor the *tefillah* itself. In any case, you must not begin your *davening* after midday.

Regarding what you wrote—that your *hisbonenus* is worth nothing—it is understood that this is not at all appropriate, and one should not speak this way. You are contemplating matters of the Torah of the Living G-d, which were transmitted to us by our holy *Nesi'im*, whose words are alive and endure forever. Ultimately, they accomplish their effect, whether in this incarnation or another (as explained in *Heichaltzu* to the students—for Chanukah—that in another incarnation, one can be in the state of *b'chayim chayuso* when one transforms from one extreme to the other). Therefore, G-d forbid, one should not dismiss such matters as "nothing" simply because their effect is not yet visibly apparent. It is also understood that this does not contradict what is explained in many places regarding the lowliness of the one contemplating, because the greatness of the *hisbonenus* does not stem from his own strength or power, as explained in *Kuntres Uma'ayon* and elsewhere.

You surely have a fixed *shiur* in *Chassidus*, both for *girsa* (reading) and *iyun* (in-depth study). It is appropriate to remind you to keep the three daily *shiurim* that are incumbent upon every soul, as established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe: *Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*, as is well known.

As we approach the new year, which is coming upon us and all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

## 1859

B"H, 22 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

Peace and Blessing!

... 2) Regarding your question as to what my intention is in the study of Chassidus: whether it is a matter of avodah that stirs the heart—it is well known in many places in the sichos of our Rebbeim that the essence of study, and especially the study of Chassidus, is a matter of avodah. However, this does not mean that one must study only maamarim that explain matters of avodah, for even from matters of haskalah (intellectual conceptualization) one can find a connection to avodah. It is impossible to give general instructions on this, as it depends on the individual’s talents, his available time, etc. But a matter that applies to everyone is that there must be study of both the intellectual matters in the teachings of Chassidus and the matters of avodah. The way one divides the time—how much to study matters of avodah and how much for matters of haskalah—depends on the nature of the individual. Surely, when you consult with the elders of anash who know you, they will show you the correct path for this. Furthermore, I would like to reiterate what I have written to several of anash in the past: that in general, the study of Chassidus must also include the aspect of studying for the sake of deep analysis (iyun) and for the sake of covering ground (girsa), in order to know, at the very least in a general way, the matters of Chassidus. There is no contradiction here to what is explained in several places, for one must not be a "chitzon" (externalist); Chabad demands inwardness (pnimiyus), especially in the study of Chassidus. For even the study for the sake of girsa should not be done in an external way, but rather in the manner explained regarding the study of the Torah Shebichtav (Written Torah), and similarly in the study of the Tanya: that the greatest of the great cannot reach its ultimate depth, yet even the smallest of the small can grasp at least a portion of the simple meaning.

3) Regarding your question as to whether what you study with your students—Chumash with Rashi, not from the weekly parsha—fulfills the set shiur established by the takanah of our Rebbe, the Rayatz: this is not the case. For the study of the weekly parsha is in accordance with the saying of the Alter Rebbe, that "one must live with the times" (see also the sicha of Shabbos Mevarchim, 8 Elul of this year). Therefore, in the Hayom Yom calendar, which was edited in its time by our Rebbe, the Rayatz, there is a shiur of the weekly parsha marked for every day that must be studied on that day.

4) Your pidyon nefesh was received, and G-d willing, I will read it at the tziyun of our Rebbe, the Rayatz, at an auspicious time.

And approaching the New Year, which is coming upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and your family, may they live, with the blessing of *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessing.

## 1860

B"H, 22 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and blessings!

I received your letter from Parshas Tavo with pleasure, and I was pleased to read that you knew my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Rebbe Rashab, may he rest in Eden. My hope is that this is not merely a memory, but that it exerts an influence upon you to elevate your spirit, raising yourself above the materiality of this physical world and all that fills it—a world full of kelipos and sitra achra. As our Sages of blessed memory have said, "The main thing is not the study, but the deed."

Regarding what you write—that it is difficult to fulfill the necessary activities at this time—you are correct in your words. However, it is known from our Sages that the Ribono shel Olam only demands according to our strength. We must begin to fulfill our shlichus in this world, and when we do so without ulterior motives and with a whole heart, then Hashem grants success beyond the natural order. This is similar to the story related by our Sages in Koheles Rabbah at the beginning: When Rabbi Chanina ben Dosa saw the people of his city bringing burnt offerings and peace offerings, and he was unable to bring anything due to his great poverty, he found a stone in the ruins of his city. He chiseled and polished it and said, "It is incumbent upon me to bring this to Yerushalayim." However, he did not have the means to hire workers to transport it. The Ribono shel Olam summoned angels in the form of men who agreed to transport it for a small fee, but they stipulated, "On the condition that you place your hand and finger with us." Seemingly, it is difficult to understand why they said he must place his finger, since they were the ones doing the transporting. But this is according to the aforementioned principle: one must open an aperture as small as the eye of a needle. That is, one must begin the avodah, even if, on the face of it, according to human intellect, one does not see how the matter will be brought to fruition. If one does this truly and sincerely, one succeeds. See there in the Chiddushei HaRashash; this applies to each and every one of us, in every place and at every time.

I trust you are aware of the three daily shiurim for every person, established by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, may the merit of the righteous protect us: Chumash, Tehillim, and Tanya. I hope you are strengthening yourself in them, as these shiurim draw an added measure of vitality and strength from the living Elokus for the Bnei Yisrael who cleave to Him, of whom it is said, "You who cleave to Hashem your G-d are all alive today."

As we approach the new year, which is coming upon us and all of Yisrael for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and your family, may they live: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters.

With blessings.

## 1861

B"H, 22 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 10 Elul, in which you write about your experiences and also that you are easily agitated and that [unwanted] thoughts enter your mind, etc.

In general, one must divert one's attention from this. It goes without saying that you must do what the doctor instructs, but that is only regarding matters connected to the power of action. However, to dwell on these things is not our way. When you divert your attention from this, you will certainly be healthier and will have more time to succeed in your personal matters, as well as in your participation in the activities of Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established.

It would be appropriate for you to memorize a few chapters of Mishnayos and a few chapters of Tanya—naturally, in a way that does not strain you. When you feel that you are becoming agitated or that unwanted thoughts are entering your mind, you should at that moment think of a few Mishnayos and a few lines of Tanya. A little light dispels a great deal of darkness, especially when the light is from the *Maor* of Chassidus, and when the darkness is a perceived—imaginary—darkness.

I have received your *pidyon nefesh* for the upcoming Rosh Hashanah, and I will read it—*bli neder*—at a time of favor at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

As we approach the new year, which is coming upon us and upon all of Israel for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you: a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings.

## 1862

B"H, 22 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn.

Greetings and Blessings!

In response to your letter of 15 Elul, I was pleased to read that your health has improved and that you have already begun teaching your shiurim in public again. May it be the will of Hashem that your condition continues to improve, and may you share good news regarding this.

You conclude your letter by mentioning that you have decided to daven as a shaliach tzibbur during the Yomim Nora'im that are approaching us for good, and that you will also have a choir to assist you somewhat. Surely you will endeavor, to the extent possible, to minimize the strain. You are familiar with the two interpretations in our Sages' words, "with all your strength": either literally, or [referring to] your intent. It is understood that the second interpretation is more appropriate in terms of spirituality, and consequently, it is better in terms of physicality as well.

Your pidyon nefesh has been received, and I will read it, bli neder, at the tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

As we approach the new year, which is coming upon us and all of Yisrael for good and for blessing, I hereby express my blessing to you and your family, may they live, with a blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, both physically and spiritually.

With blessings for proper health, in particular.

## 1863

1863

B"H, 24 Elul, 5712

The esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, the G-d-fearing, the distinguished, who sits in judgment, leader of his community with integrity, etc., Moreinu Harav Dovid, may he live and be well, Tzafaro

Peace and blessing!

I have just received the shocking news of the passing of your father, Rabbi Yismach, of blessed memory. I hereby offer you my condolences; may Hashem comfort you, lengthen your days and years in goodness and pleasantness, and may you know no more sorrow.

Regarding the matter of passing and comforting mourners, I will briefly note what I have said in the past: that Creation is a **descent and a Seder Hishtalshelus** from above to below, and the intent is that there should subsequently be an ascent after ascent from below to above. Since this is the Divine intent, it **is actually accomplished** in practice; from the moment the descent was completed, a constant ascent began, as our Sages of blessed memory stated that Tzaddikim and Talmidei Chachamim have no rest, neither in this world nor in the World to Come, for they go from strength to strength.

And the verse states, "A Tzaddik falls seven times and rises," meaning that the fall is for the sake of the rising and the ascent that follows. This fall and descent is necessary, as is explained at length in many places, that between a previous level and a more exalted level that follows it, there must be a state of bitul in between. Since this descent is a necessary preparation for an ascent to a more exalted level, in truth, it is not a descent at all, but rather a part of the more exalted ascent.

So it is with the general matter of passing and mourning: Regarding the departed, the passing is a matter of "and to the dust you shall return" for the sake of the more exalted ascent that follows; regarding the mourners—may they be separated for a good life—the matter of mourning, which is a state of mochin d'katnus, is also for the sake of an ascent to a more exalted level that follows.

And may the prophecy be fulfilled speedily in our days: "He will swallow up death forever, and Hashem will wipe away tears from off all faces."

With blessings for a kesivah v'chasimah tovah.

#### ***1863***

**What I have said:** To those comforting him on the passing of his brother—see above, Letter 1506, and the references in the notes there.

## 1864

B"H, 27 Elul, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of Yeshivas Lod
To the Administration of Yeshivas Toras Emes
May Hashem preserve them and grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

I trust you have received my previous letters and have responded to them.

Although I have already conveyed this through the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing and accomplished, who engages in communal needs, etc., Rabbi M. Gurary, I am nonetheless writing to put these matters on record:

It has long been my desire and wish to ascertain the talents and merits of the yeshiva students, both in the study of Nigleh and in the study of Chassidus. This was the practice in all Lubavitcher yeshivos for a long time, where from time to time they would conduct examinations for the students, and the custom was to hold these examinations during the bein hazmanim period.

Therefore, I propose and request that such examinations be conducted in the yeshivos in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established.

It is understood that these examinations will be private, meaning without inviting people from the outside, etc.

The examiners will consist of two committees: a committee for examination in Nigleh, and a committee for examination in Chassidus. Each of these two committees will include the *mashpia* of Nigleh or Chassidus from Yeshivas Lod and Yeshivas Toras Emes, plus one additional person upon whom both shall agree.

It is understood that this examination concerns only the students of the upper classes and those who study independently.

It is also understood that this examination does not replace the examinations required for advancing students from one class to another, as it is intended only for the highest classes, as mentioned above, in order to know the true standing of the students and their talents in Nigleh of Torah and in Chassidus.

It is my hope that you will utilize the days of the upcoming month of Tishrei for this, as surely the regular schedules are not maintained as strictly during that time anyway. May it be the will of Hashem that this be successful.

I trust you will confirm receipt of this letter immediately, and that you will also hasten to appoint the members of the committees and inform me of this as soon as possible.

I have also requested the administration of Agudas Chassidei Chabad to organize these matters and to mediate between the two yeshivos. It is unnecessary to note that it would be appropriate for all examinations to be completed within the month of Tishrei.

Awaiting good news, and signing with the blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah* and success in your holy work.

#### ***1864***

**I have conveyed:** See letter 1789 above.

## 1865

[Late Elul 5712]

...Regarding Yom Kippur — one should certainly conduct oneself according to the instructions of expert physicians, for this is the opinion of our Torah, the Torah of life — not only in the World to Come, but also in this world. And if it is according to a doctor’s instruction, then one **recites a blessing** over this eating, for the purpose of blessings is the drawing down of **Elokus** and the elevation of the sparks, which are accomplished specifically through eating, and cannot be achieved through thoughts and intentions alone.

#### 1865

Published in Likkutei Sichos, Vol. 21, p. 306.

## 1886

1886

B”H, end of Elul, 5712
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished Rabbi, the Chassid, the G-d-fearing man, who occupies himself with communal needs, etc.,
Rabbi Shmuel, may he live, HaLevi

Greetings and blessings!

As we approach the coming year, may it be for good and for blessing for all of Israel, I hereby wish to express my blessings for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year, in both material and spiritual matters. May you have success with your students in elevating them on the path that leads to the House of G-d, and may you have much Chassidishe *nachas* from all your children, may they live, for long, good years—good in every sense of the word.

With blessings for good in both material and spiritual matters,

**M. Schneerson**

#### ***1886***

**Rabbi Shmuel:** Levitin. Another letter to him—see above, Vol. 4, 1222.
